## Learning Guide: Understanding the IT Business and Ethics

This guide provides a structured overview of key concepts related to IT Business, Strategy, and Planning.

### I. The Concept of IT Business

This section introduces fundamental definitions, components, and frameworks essential to understanding the IT business landscape.

**01. The Concept of IT Business: A Summary**

*   **A) Definition of IT Business:**
    *   What is IT business? [Essential definition, scope, and key characteristics.]
    *   Examples of activities and services typically classified as IT business.
*   **B) The Alignment of Business and IT:**
    *   Why is aligning business goals with IT strategy crucial? [Importance, benefits.]
    *   Key challenges and best practices for achieving business-IT alignment.

**02. IT Business Ecosystem**

*   **A) IT Business and the Hype Cycle:**
    *   **Hype Cycle:** [Brief explanation: A graphical representation of the maturity, adoption, and social application of specific technologies.]
    *   How emerging technologies evolve through different phases (e.g., Innovation Trigger, Peak of Inflated Expectations, Trough of Disillusionment, Slope of Enlightenment, Plateau of Productivity).
    *   Implications for IT business strategy and investment.
*   **B) IT Ecosystem:**
    *   **IT Ecosystem:** [Brief explanation: A network of interconnected IT organizations, technologies, services, and users that interact to create value.]
    *   Key participants and their roles (e.g., vendors, customers, partners, developers).
*   **C) Components of an IT Business Ecosystem:**
    *   Core elements that constitute a functional IT ecosystem (e.g., technology platforms, infrastructure, applications, data, human capital, governance).

**03. IT Resources and Management Activities for IT Business**

*   **A) The Concept of IT Resources:**
    *   **IT Resources:** [Brief explanation: Tangible and intangible assets related to information technology that an organization uses to achieve its objectives.]
    *   Categorization of IT resources (e.g., hardware, software, network, data, human resources, financial capital related to IT).
*   **B) The Role of IT Resources:**
    *   How IT resources support business operations, innovation, and competitive advantage.
    *   The strategic importance of effective IT resource utilization.
*   **C) Management Activities and Structure for IT Business:**
    *   Key processes involved in managing IT resources (e.g., planning, acquisition, deployment, maintenance, security, optimization).
    *   Organizational structures typically used for IT management.

**04. The IT Business Value Chain**

*   **A) Overview of the Value Chain:**
    *   **Value Chain:** [Brief explanation: A set of activities that a firm operating in a specific industry performs in order to deliver a valuable product or service to the market.]
    *   Primary activities (e.g., inbound logistics, operations, outbound logistics, marketing, service) and support activities (e.g., procurement, technology development, HR management, firm infrastructure).
*   **B) Company-wide Integration of the Value Chain Model and IT:**
    *   How IT facilitates and enhances activities across the entire value chain.
    *   Examples of IT's role in improving efficiency, reducing costs, and increasing value.
*   **C) Value Chain Model and IT Specialized Companies:**
    *   How the value chain concept applies to companies whose primary business is IT (e.g., software developers, IT service providers).
    *   Unique aspects of value creation in IT-centric organizations.
*   **D) Expansion of the Value Chain Model:**
    *   Extensions or adaptations of the traditional value chain model to account for networked economies, digital platforms, and ecosystem thinking.

### II. IT Business Strategy

This section focuses on the development, analysis, and establishment of strategic plans for IT within an organization.

*   **B) The Elements of a Strategy Plan:**

**03. IT Business Environment Analysis**

*   **A) External Environment Analysis:**
    *   Methods for analyzing factors outside the organization that impact IT strategy.
    *   **PESTEL Analysis:** [Brief explanation: Political, Economic, Social, Technological, Environmental, Legal factors.] How each factor influences IT.
    *   **Porter's Five Forces:** [Brief explanation: Threat of new entrants, bargaining power of buyers, bargaining power of suppliers, threat of substitute products/services, intensity of rivalry.] How these apply to the IT industry.
    *   Market trends, competitive landscape, regulatory changes.
*   **B) Internal Environment Analysis:**
    *   Methods for analyzing factors within the organization that impact IT strategy.
    *   **SWOT Analysis:** [Brief explanation: Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, Threats.] Application to IT capabilities and resources.
    *   Assessment of current IT infrastructure, applications, human resources, processes, and budget.
*   **C) Consolidated Internal and External Environment Analysis:**
    *   How to integrate findings from both external and internal analyses to identify strategic options and priorities for IT.
    *   Bridging the gap between organizational capabilities and market demands.

*   **B) Framework of IT Governance:**

*   **A) Overview of EA (Enterprise Architecture):**

*   **B) ISP Deployment Procedure:**
    *   Key phases and activities involved in conducting ISP (e.g., business analysis, IT assessment, strategic IT roadmap development, portfolio planning).

## IT Business Learning Guide

This guide extracts essential information and key concepts from the original text (Pages 7-11) to help you study IT Business effectively.

### I. The Concept of IT Business

#### 1. IT Business Fundamentals

*   **Define IT Business:** Understand what IT business encompasses.
*   **Business-IT Alignment:** Explain how business strategies and IT strategies are harmonized.

#### 2. IT Business Ecosystem

*   **Hype Cycle in IT Business:** Understand the Gartner Hype Cycle and its relevance to IT business technologies.
*   **Define IT Ecosystem:** What constitutes an IT ecosystem.
*   **IT Business Ecosystem Components:** Identify the various parts of an IT business ecosystem.

#### 3. IT Resources & Management Activities

*   **Define IT Resources:** What are IT resources (e.g., hardware, software, people, data)?
*   **Role of IT Resources:** Explain the importance and function of IT resources.
*   **IT Business Management Activities & Structure:** Describe typical management activities and organizational structures for IT business.

#### 4. The IT Business Value Chain

*   **Value Chain Overview:** Understand Porter's Value Chain concept.
*   **Company-Wide IT-Value Chain Integration:** How IT integrates across a company's entire value chain.
*   **Value Chain in IT-Specialized Companies:** Specific application of the value chain model in companies focused on IT.
*   **Expansion of the Value Chain Model:** How the value chain concept can be extended or adapted.

---

### II. IT Business Strategy

#### 1. Establishing an IT Business Strategy

*   **Strategy Establishment Concept:** Define what it means to establish a strategy.
*   **Elements of an IT Strategy Plan:** List the key components of an IT business strategy document.
*   **Strategy Setting Process:** Outline the steps involved in developing an IT business strategy.

#### 2. IT Business Environment Analysis

*   **External Environment Analysis:** Methods for analyzing factors outside the organization (e.g., market trends, competitors, technology advancements).
*   **Internal Environment Analysis:** Methods for analyzing factors within the organization (e.g., resources, capabilities, culture).
*   **Consolidated Analysis:** How to combine internal and external findings (e.g., SWOT analysis).

---

### III. Understanding IT Business Planning

#### 1. IT Governance

*   **Concept of IT Governance:** Define IT governance – how IT decisions are made and controlled.
*   **IT Governance Framework:** Understand common frameworks (e.g., COBIT, ITIL) that guide IT governance.
*   **IT Governance Process:** Describe the steps and activities within IT governance.
*   **Key Focus Areas of IT Governance:** Identify critical areas like risk management, value delivery, resource management, and performance measurement.

#### 2. Enterprise Architecture (EA)

*   **Overview of EA:** Define Enterprise Architecture – a master blueprint of an organization's IT assets.
*   **EA Conceptual Diagram & Components:** Understand the typical structure and key components (business, data, application, technology architectures).
*   **The EA Framework:** Explore common EA frameworks (e.g., TOGAF, Zachman).

#### 3. Information Strategic Planning (ISP)

*   **Overview of ISP:** Define Information Strategic Planning – aligning information systems with business objectives.
*   **ISP Deployment Procedure:** Outline the steps to implement ISP.
*   **Key Output of ISP Deployment:** Identify the deliverables resulting from ISP (e.g., IT master plan, project portfolio).

---

### IV. Understanding IT Business Adoption

#### 1. IT Business Adoption Process

*   **IT Business Ordering Process:** Steps involved in acquiring or requesting IT business solutions.
*   **SW Adoption Process (ISO/IEC 12207):** Understand the international standard for software lifecycle processes.
*   **Tailoring Process:** Adapting standard processes or solutions to specific organizational needs.

#### 2. IT Business Adoption Methods

*   Explore various methodologies for adopting new IT business solutions.

#### 3. IT Business Outsourcing Service

*   **Overview of IT Business Outsourcing:** Define outsourcing – delegating IT functions to external providers.
*   **Outsourcing Adoption Process:** Steps to select, contract, and manage outsourcing relationships.
*   **Forms of Outsourcing:** Differentiate types like onshore, offshore, nearshore, BPO (Business Process Outsourcing), ITO (Information Technology Outsourcing).
*   **Considerations for Adopting Outsourcing:** Key factors to evaluate before outsourcing (e.g., cost, risk, control, expertise).

---

### V. Understanding the IT Business Process

#### 1. Component Elements for IT Business Process Execution

*   **People & Organization:** The role of human resources and organizational structure in executing IT processes.
*   **Business Process:** Define what a business process is in an IT context.

#### 2. Examples of IT Business Processes

*   Illustrate various types of IT business processes.

#### 3. Methods of Executing IT Business Processes

*   **IT Business Process Management (BPM):** Define BPM – managing and optimizing business processes using IT.
*   **IT Business Process Information Management:** How information is managed and flows within IT business processes.

#### 4. IT Business Process Improvement Techniques

*   **Business Process Reengineering (BPR):** Radical redesign of business processes.
*   **Process Innovation (PI):** Introducing new or significantly improved processes.
*   **Six Sigma:** A data-driven methodology for eliminating defects and improving quality.
*   **TRIZ (Theory of Inventive Problem Solving):** A problem-solving methodology based on observed patterns of invention.
*   **SERVQUAL:** A framework for measuring service quality.
*   **Statistical Process Control (SPC):** Using statistical methods to monitor and control a process.

---

### VI. Understanding IT Business Services

#### 1. General-Purpose Work Support Systems (Enterprise Solutions)

*   **Enterprise Solution:** Define software packages that support an organization's core business functions.
*   **Types of Enterprise Solutions:** List common categories.
*   **Business Strategy & Enterprise Solutions:** How these solutions support and enable business strategies.
*   **Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP):** Integrated management of core business processes.
*   **Supply Chain Management (SCM):** Managing the flow of goods and services.
*   **Customer Relationship Management (CRM):** Managing interactions with current and potential customers.
*   **Product Lifecycle Management (PLM):** Managing a product's entire lifecycle from conception to disposal.

#### 2. IT Business Decision-Making Support Systems

*   **Enterprise Data Warehouse (EDW):** A central repository of integrated data for reporting and analysis.
*   **Decision Support System (DSS):** Systems that aid in decision-making by analyzing data.
*   **Business Intelligence (BI):** Technologies and strategies for data analysis and presentation of actionable information.

#### 3. IT Service Management

*   **Overview of IT Service Management:** Define ITSM – managing the end-to-end delivery of IT services to customers.
*   **ITIL (Information Technology Infrastructure Library):** A widely adopted framework for ITSM.
*   **Service Level Agreement (SLA):** A contract outlining the level of service expected from a provider.
*   **Service Level Management (SLM):** Activities to ensure IT services meet agreed-upon service levels.

---

### VII. Understanding IT Business Performance Evaluation

#### 1. Financial Performance Evaluation

*   **Overview:** Assessing an organization's financial health and efficiency.
*   **Types of Financial Performance Evaluation Techniques:** Common methods like ratio analysis, ROI, payback period.

#### 2. Balanced Scorecard (BSC) Technique

*   **Overview of BSC:** A strategic performance management framework.
*   **Component Elements of BSC:** Key aspects included in a BSC.
*   **Four Perspectives of BSC:**
    *   **Financial:** How do we look to shareholders?
    *   **Customer:** How do customers see us?
    *   **Internal Business Process:** What must we excel at?
    *   **Learning & Growth:** Can we continue to improve and create value?

#### 3. Balanced IT Performance Evaluation Technique (IT-BSC)

*   **Overview of IT-BSC:** Adapting the BSC specifically for IT performance measurement.
*   **Component Elements of IT-BSC:** Specific metrics and perspectives for IT.

#### 4. Management of Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)

*   **Overview of KPI:** Define Key Performance Indicators – measurable values demonstrating how effectively a company is achieving key business objectives.
*   **KPI Establishment Procedure:** Steps to identify, define, and implement KPIs.
*   **Precautions When Deriving KPI:** Considerations to ensure effective and meaningful KPIs.

#### 5. Goal Management System

*   Understand the concept and implementation of systems designed to set, track, and achieve organizational goals.

## Pages 10-14


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text outline:

---

## IT Business & Service Management: Learning Guide

This guide covers essential concepts in IT business process management, IT services, performance evaluation, environmental transformation, latest services, and professional ethics.

---

### **V. IT Business Process Information Management**

This section focuses on managing information within IT business processes and techniques for improvement.

#### **05 IT Business Process Improvement Techniques**
Techniques used to optimize and enhance IT-related business processes:

*   **A) Understanding BPR (Business Process Reengineering)**
    *   **Definition:** Fundamentally rethinking and radically redesigning business processes to achieve dramatic improvements in critical contemporary measures of performance such as cost, quality, service, and speed.
*   **B) Understanding PI (Process Innovation)**
    *   **Definition:** The creation of new, more efficient, or effective ways of doing things, or significant improvements to existing processes. It often involves applying new technologies or methods.
*   **C) Understanding Six Sigma**
    *   **Definition:** A data-driven methodology for eliminating defects in any process – from manufacturing to transactional and beyond. It aims to improve process output quality by identifying and removing the causes of errors and minimizing variability.
*   **D) Understand TRIZ (Theory of Inventive Problem Solving)**
    *   **Definition:** A methodology based on systematic analysis of patterns of invention and evolution in technology. It provides tools and techniques for creative problem-solving and innovation, particularly in technical fields.
*   **E) Understanding SERVQUAL (Service Quality)**
    *   **Definition:** A multi-dimensional research instrument designed to capture consumer expectations and perceptions of service quality. It measures quality across dimensions like tangibles, reliability, responsiveness, assurance, and empathy.
*   **F) Understanding SPC (Statistical Process Control)**
    *   **Definition:** A method of quality control that uses statistical methods to monitor and control a process. Its goal is to ensure that a process operates efficiently and produces more specification-conforming products with minimal waste.

---

### **VI. Understanding IT Business Services**

This section explores various IT business services, including enterprise solutions and decision support systems.

#### **02 IT Business General-Purpose Work Support System**
These are comprehensive software systems designed to integrate and manage various aspects of an enterprise's operations.

*   **A) Enterprise Solution**
    *   **Definition:** Integrated software packages that support the core business processes of an organization, covering areas like finance, human resources, manufacturing, and supply chain.
*   **B) Types of Enterprise Solutions**
    *   Common examples include ERP, SCM, CRM, and PLM systems (detailed below).
*   **C) Business Strategy and Enterprise Solution**
    *   **Concept:** Enterprise solutions are crucial tools for implementing and supporting an organization's overall business strategy by streamlining operations, improving data flow, and enhancing decision-making.
*   **D) Understanding ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning)**
    *   **Definition:** A suite of integrated software applications that an organization can use to manage and integrate the core business processes in real-time, mediated by software and technology. This includes finance, HR, manufacturing, supply chain, and services.
*   **E) Understanding SCM (Supply Chain Management)**
    *   **Definition:** The management of the flow of goods and services, from the origin of raw materials to the delivery of the final product to the consumer. It involves optimizing supply-side activities to maximize customer value and achieve a sustainable competitive advantage.
*   **F) Understanding CRM (Customer Relationship Management)**
    *   **Definition:** A technology for managing all your company's relationships and interactions with customers and potential customers. The goal is to improve business relationships to grow your business. It focuses on sales, marketing, and customer service.
*   **G) Understanding PLM (Product Lifecycle Management)**
    *   **Definition:** The process of managing the entire lifecycle of a product from its conception, through design and manufacture, to service and disposal. PLM integrates people, data, processes, and business systems, providing a product information backbone for companies and their extended enterprise.

#### **03 IT Business Decision-Making Support System**
Systems designed to aid managers and executives in making informed business decisions.

*   **A) Understanding EDW (Enterprise Data Warehouse)**
    *   **Definition:** A central repository of integrated data from one or more disparate sources. It stores current and historical data and is used for creating analytical reports for workers throughout the enterprise.
*   **B) Understanding the DSS (Decision Support System)**
    *   **Definition:** An interactive computer-based system that gathers and presents data from a wide range of sources to help management make decisions. It provides information, models, and analytical tools to support semi-structured and unstructured decision-making tasks.
*   **C) Understanding BI (Business Intelligence)**
    *   **Definition:** A set of strategies and technologies used by enterprises for the data analysis of business information. BI technologies provide historical, current, and predictive views of business operations, often delivered through reporting, dashboards, and analytical tools.

#### **04 Understanding IT Service Management (ITSM)**
A framework for managing the delivery of IT services to customers.

*   **A) Overview of IT Service Management**
    *   **Definition:** A discipline for managing information technology (IT) systems and services with a focus on delivering value to customers. It involves designing, delivering, managing, and improving IT services.
*   **B) Understanding ITIL (Information Technology Infrastructure Library)**
    *   **Definition:** A widely adopted framework of best practices for IT service management. ITIL provides a comprehensive set of concepts and practices for managing IT services to meet business needs.
*   **C) Understanding the SLA (Service Level Agreement)**
    *   **Definition:** A contract between a service provider and a customer that defines the level of service expected from the provider. It outlines metrics, responsibilities, and penalties for non-compliance.
*   **D) Understanding SLM (Service Level Management)**
    *   **Definition:** The process within ITIL that involves continually negotiating, monitoring, and managing IT services to ensure they meet agreed-upon business requirements and service levels as defined in SLAs.

---

### **VII. Understanding IT Business Performance Evaluation**

This section covers various techniques for evaluating the performance of IT businesses, from financial metrics to strategic scorecards.

#### **02 Financial Performance Evaluation Technique**
Methods used to assess the financial health and efficiency of an IT business.

*   **A) Overview of Financial Performance Evaluation**
    *   **Concept:** Analyzing financial statements and data to gauge the profitability, efficiency, solvency, and stability of an organization.
*   **B) Types of Financial Performance Evaluation Techniques**
    *   Includes ratio analysis (e.g., profitability, liquidity, solvency ratios), trend analysis, and comparisons to industry benchmarks.

#### **03 Balanced Scorecard (BSC) Technique**
A strategic performance management framework.

*   **A) Overview of the BSC Technique**
    *   **Definition:** A strategic planning and management system that organizations use to translate their vision and strategy into action. It provides a balanced view of organizational performance beyond just financial metrics.
*   **B) Component Elements of BSC**
    *   Includes objectives, measures, targets, and initiatives.
*   **C) Four Perspectives of BSC**
    *   **Financial:** How do we look to shareholders? (e.g., profitability, revenue growth)
    *   **Customer:** How do customers see us? (e.g., customer satisfaction, market share)
    *   **Internal Business Processes:** What must we excel at? (e.g., operational efficiency, quality)
    *   **Learning and Growth:** How can we continue to improve and create value? (e.g., employee skills, innovation)

#### **04 Balanced IT Performance Evaluation Technique (IT-BSC)**
Applying the Balanced Scorecard framework specifically to IT performance.

*   **A) Overview of IT-BSC**
    *   **Definition:** An adaptation of the traditional Balanced Scorecard to measure the performance of an IT department or IT services, linking IT objectives directly to business strategy.
*   **B) Component Elements of IT-BSC**
    *   Similar to BSC, but tailored for IT, with perspectives such as:
        *   **Corporate Contribution:** How IT contributes to business value.
        *   **Customer Orientation:** How IT meets user needs.
        *   **Operational Excellence:** How efficient and reliable IT processes are.
        *   **Future Orientation:** How IT prepares for future needs and innovation.

#### **05 Management of Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)**
Tools for measuring organizational and individual performance.

*   **A) Overview of KPI**
    *   **Definition:** Quantifiable measures used to evaluate the success of an organization or a particular activity in meeting its objectives. KPIs are critical for tracking performance against strategic goals.
*   **B) KPI Establishment Procedure**
    *   Typically involves defining objectives, identifying relevant metrics, setting targets, collecting data, and regular review.
*   **C) Precautions to Take When Deriving KPI**
    *   Ensure KPIs are **SMART** (Specific, Measurable, Achievable, Relevant, Time-bound), aligned with strategic goals, and not too numerous or complex.

#### **06 Goal Management System (MBO - Management by Objectives)**
A strategic management model that aims to improve the performance of an organization by clearly defining objectives that are agreed to by both management and employees.

*   **A) Key Perspectives of MBO**
    *   Focus on setting measurable goals, employee participation, and regular performance reviews.
*   **B) The Main Reasons Why Enterprises Are Adopting MBO**
    *   To improve employee motivation, align individual goals with organizational goals, enhance communication, and increase accountability.
*   **C) Component Elements of MBO**
    *   Goal setting, action planning, self-control, and periodic reviews.

---

### **VIII. IT Business Environmental Transformation and Response**

This section explores changes in the IT business environment and how enterprises adapt.

#### **01 Trends of Change in the IT Business Environment**
*   **A) Understanding the Transformation of the IT Business Environment**
    *   **Concept:** The continuous evolution of technology, market demands, regulatory landscape, and global competition significantly impacts the IT sector. Trends include digital transformation, cloud computing, AI, big data, and cybersecurity challenges.

#### **02 Enterprises’ Response to Changes in the IT Business Environment**
Strategies and activities businesses undertake to adapt and thrive amidst environmental shifts.

*   **A) IT Business Innovation Activities**
    *   **Concept:** Developing new products, services, processes, or business models leveraging emerging IT. This includes R&D, adopting new technologies (e.g., AI, blockchain), and fostering a culture of continuous improvement.
*   **B) IT Business Integration and Expansion**
    *   **Concept:** Strategies like mergers, acquisitions, partnerships, and global market expansion to increase market share, diversify offerings, and gain competitive advantage in a dynamic IT landscape.

---

### **IX. Latest IT Business Service**

This section highlights contemporary IT business services and underlying infrastructure.

#### **01 Latest Web and Mobile Service**
*   **A) Latest Web Technologies**
    *   **Concept:** Modern web development trends including progressive web apps (PWAs), single-page applications (SPAs), real-time communication (WebSockets), serverless architecture, and advanced JavaScript frameworks (e.g., React, Angular, Vue.js).
*   **B) Mobile Service**
    *   **Concept:** Services delivered via mobile devices, encompassing mobile applications, location-based services, mobile payments, and responsive web design, driven by smartphone penetration and ubiquitous connectivity.

#### **02 Smart Business Infrastructure**
*   **A) Convergent Infrastructure**
    *   **Definition:** An IT system that groups multiple components into a single optimized computing package. It combines servers, storage, networking, and virtualization into a pre-integrated unit, simplifying deployment and management.
*   **B) Smart Infrastructure**
    *   **Definition:** An infrastructure (e.g., smart cities, smart grids, smart buildings) that leverages IoT devices, sensors, data analytics, and AI to monitor, manage, and optimize operations automatically, improving efficiency, sustainability, and quality of life.

#### **03 Latest IT Business Services**
*   **A) Latest SW Centered IT Business Services**
    *   **Concept:** Services primarily driven by software innovations, such as Software-as-a-Service (SaaS), Platform-as-a-Service (PaaS), serverless computing, AI-as-a-Service, blockchain services, and advanced analytics platforms.
*   **B) Latest IT Business Services that Are H/W Centered**
    *   **Concept:** Services heavily relying on advanced hardware, including edge computing (processing data closer to the source), specialized AI hardware (GPUs, TPUs), quantum computing, advanced robotics, and sophisticated IoT devices.

---

### **X. Professional Ethics of IT Business**

This section addresses the ethical principles and codes of conduct crucial for IT professionals and businesses.

#### **01 Understanding the Concept of Professional Ethics**
*   **A) Concept of Professional Ethics**
    *   **Definition:** A set of moral principles that govern the behavior of professionals in their work. It dictates how professionals should act in certain situations, often setting a higher standard than personal ethics.
*   **B) Professional Ethics of IT Business**
    *   **Concept:** Specific ethical considerations for IT professionals, addressing issues like data privacy, intellectual property, system security, algorithmic bias, responsible AI development, and the impact of technology on society.

#### **02 Ethical Principles and Code of IT Business**
*   **A) Code of Ethics Related to ICT Technology**
    *   **Concept:** Formal guidelines or statements adopted by professional organizations or companies outlining acceptable ethical behavior and decision-making for individuals working with Information and Communication Technologies (ICT). Examples include principles of honesty, integrity, confidentiality, competence, and public safety.

---

### **XI. Privacy**

This section covers the understanding and protection of personal information.

#### **01 Understanding of Personal Information**
*   **A) Concept of Personal Information**
    *   **Definition:** Any information that relates to an identified or identifiable living individual. This includes names, addresses, identification numbers, online identifiers, and factors specific to the physical, physiological, genetic, mental, economic, cultural, or social identity of that individual.
*   **B) Relevant Domestic Laws and Regulations Related to Personal Information Protection**
    *   **Concept:** Legal frameworks within a specific country (e.g., GDPR in Europe, CCPA in California, PIPA in Korea) designed to protect individuals' personal data, regulating its collection, processing, storage, and sharing.
*   **C) Foreign Policy Related to Personal Information Protection**
    *   **Concept:** International agreements or national laws of other countries that impact how personal data is handled across borders, especially for global businesses.

#### **02 Ex Ante and Ex Post Response Method for Personal Information Infringement**
Strategies for preventing and responding to personal information breaches.

*   **A) Proactive Measures for Personal Information Controllers (Ex Ante)**
    *   **Concept:** Preventive actions taken *before* an incident occurs, such as implementing robust security systems, data encryption, access controls, privacy impact assessments, staff training, and developing clear privacy policies.
*   **B) Follow-up Measures for Personal Information Controllers (Ex Post)**
    *   **Concept:** Reactive actions taken *after* an incident, including breach notification to affected individuals and authorities, forensic investigation, data recovery, impact mitigation, and reviewing/improving security protocols to prevent future incidents.

---

### **XII. Copyright and Industrial Property Protection**

This section explores intellectual property rights, specifically copyright and industrial property.

#### **01 Understanding of Intellectual Property Rights (IPR)**
*   **A) Definition of Intellectual Property Rights**
    *   **Definition:** Legal rights that protect creations of the mind. They grant creators exclusive rights over their inventions, literary and artistic works, designs, and symbols, names, and images used in commerce.
*   **B) Types of Intellectual Property Rights**
    *   Includes copyrights, patents, trademarks, and trade secrets.

#### **02 Understanding of Copyright**
*   **A) Definition and Classification of Copyright**
    *   **Definition:** A legal right granted to the creator of original literary, dramatic, musical, and artistic works, including software and databases. It grants exclusive rights to reproduce, distribute, perform, display, or license their work.
    *   **Classification:** Can be economic rights (e.g., reproduction, distribution) and moral rights (e.g., right of attribution, integrity).

#### **03 Understanding of Industrial Property Rights and New Intellectual Property Rights**
*   **A) Concept of Industrial Property Rights**
    *   **Definition:** A branch of intellectual property that deals with inventions (patents), trademarks, industrial designs, and geographical indications. It primarily protects the functional and commercial aspects of creations.
*   **B) Concept of New Intellectual Property Rights**
    *   **Definition:** Emerging forms of intellectual property protection that address challenges posed by new technologies, such as protection for semiconductor chip layouts, plant varieties, and database rights.

#### **04 Understanding of Unfair Competition Prevention and Trade Secret Protection**
*   **A) Concept of Unfair Competition Prevention**
    *   **Definition:** Laws and regulations aimed at preventing deceptive or unlawful business practices that harm competitors or consumers. This includes protection against false advertising, product disparagement, and unauthorized use of business reputation.
*   **B) Concept of Trade Secret Protection**
    *   **Definition:** Legal measures to protect confidential business information that provides a competitive edge. This includes formulas, practices, designs, instruments, or compilations of information that are not generally known or reasonably ascertainable by others (e.g., Coca-Cola formula, Google's search algorithm).

---

### **XIII. Ethical Issues of the Latest IT Business Services**

This section focuses on the ethical challenges posed by cutting-edge IT services.

#### **01 Major Ethical Issues of the Latest IT Business Services**
*   **A) Ethical Issues of the Latest IT Business Services**
    *   **Concept:** Concerns arising from advanced technologies like AI, big data, IoT, and gene editing. These include:
        *   **Algorithmic Bias:** AI systems perpetuating or amplifying societal biases.
        *   **Privacy Erosion:** Extensive data collection and surveillance.
        *   **Job Displacement:** Automation impacting employment.
        *   **Autonomous Decision-Making:** Accountability and control of AI systems.
        *   **Digital Divide:** Unequal access to technology and its benefits.
        *   **Misinformation and Disinformation:** Spread of false content online.
        *   **Environmental Impact:** Energy consumption of data centers and hardware.
        *   **Security Risks:** Vulnerabilities in interconnected systems.

---

**Learning Guide: Understanding IT Business and Ethics**

This guide covers the fundamental concepts, trends, and practical examples related to IT business.

---

**1. Introduction to IT Business**

*   **Evolution of IT's Role:**
    *   **Past:** IT was seen as an auxiliary (supportive) tool for business processes.
    *   **Present:** Digital technologies are deeply integrated into daily life and core corporate business processes.
*   **Key Areas to Understand:** To fully grasp IT business, it's essential to understand:
    *   The concept and characteristics of IT business.
    *   The **IT business ecosystem** (network of organizations and individuals involved).
    *   The **IT business value chain** (activities involved in delivering value through IT).

---

**2. The Concept of IT Business**

*   **Definition:** An IT business involves:
    1.  Developing a strategy and plan for adopting IT.
    2.  Integrating IT into core business processes.
    3.  Delivering IT services that generate company earnings.
*   **IT Business Lifecycle:** This is a continuous process:
    1.  **Strategy & Planning:** Define IT business strategy and detailed plans.
    2.  **Adoption:** Implement the planned IT business.
    3.  **Process Execution:** Run IT-enabled business processes.
    4.  **Service Delivery:** Generate IT business services (which produce earnings).
    5.  **Performance Evaluation:** Continuously assess performance.
    6.  **Correction & Improvement:** Adjust or enhance the IT business based on evaluation.
*   **Impact of Environment:**
    *   Businesses operate in dynamic environments influenced by politics, economy, society, culture, and technology.
    *   IT integration, especially with the latest technologies, is crucial for optimizing management and guiding the evolution of the IT business to maximize corporate value.

---

**3. Case Study: Alibaba's Success Factors**

Alibaba, a Chinese e-commerce giant, exemplifies successful IT business strategy.

*   **Background:** Founded in 1999 by Jack Ma, Alibaba grew from a small online B2B platform to a leading global e-commerce and fintech corporation.
*   **Key Success Factors (against competitors like eBay):**
    1.  **No Transaction Fees:** Unlike many competitors, Alibaba's core online shopping malls did not charge transaction fees. Profits came from advertising and search services.
    2.  **Innovative Logistics System:** Developed an efficient system capable of delivering goods across China's vast territory in just 1-2 days.
    3.  **Trusted Payment Service (Alipay):** Introduced a secure electronic payment service, "Alipay," which built trust in China's e-commerce market by ensuring reliable transactions.
    4.  **Customer-Centric Services:** Actively met customer demands, such as enabling "chat-purchase" where customers could negotiate product prices online before buying.
    5.  **Strong Leadership and Vision:** CEO Jack Ma's strategic vision inspired employees, fostering dedication and driving aggressive growth.

*   **Lesson Learned:** Alibaba demonstrates that effective strategy, customer focus, and operational innovation (price, quality, service) are paramount for success in the IT business.

---

## Pages 16-20


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide

This guide condenses essential information about IT business concepts, evolution, strategic alignment, and the impact of new technologies.

---

### 1. Understanding the IT Business

**A. What is IT Business?**
*   **Definition:** All activities strategically integrating Information Technology (IT) into a company's processes to achieve its business objectives.
*   **Purpose:** To maximize corporate value by optimizing management through IT integration and utilizing the latest technologies.

**B. Evolution of the IT Business Concept**
*   **20th Century:** IT (computers) primarily used in dedicated computing rooms, limited integration into daily work.
*   **1990s:** With web technology, computers became more common in general work environments.
*   **21st Century:**
    *   IT permeates all industries, leading to a digital-centered lifestyle.
    *   IT plays a key role in business processes and enterprise-wide decision-making.
*   **Around 2005:** The concept of "IT business" gained recognition, especially in industries where IT was critical to products.
*   **Post-2010:** IT became tightly merged with business processes to gain competitive advantage. Decision-makers recognized IT's crucial role in acquiring high-quality data in a dynamic environment.
*   **Concept Shift:** From "IT utilization" (IT as a mere tool) to "IT integration" (IT and business closely merged).

**C. IT Business Lifecycle**
An ongoing cycle to develop and deliver IT business services:
1.  **Strategy & Planning:** Develop a strategy and plan for adopting IT business.
2.  **Adoption:** Begin the process of integrating IT.
3.  **Process:** Execute the IT business operations.
4.  **Service:** Deliver IT business services that generate earnings.
5.  **Evaluation & Improvement:** Continuously evaluate performance and correct/improve the direction of the IT business.
*This cycle is perpetual, integrating IT into the company's core business.*

**D. The IT Business Ecosystem**
The IT business environment is a competitive and collaborative landscape involving five core industries:
*   **C (Contents):** Digital information and media.
*   **P (Platform):** Operating systems, online services, or frameworks that host applications.
*   **N (Network):** Communication infrastructure (e.g., internet providers).
*   **D (Device):** Hardware used to access IT services (e.g., smartphones, computers).
*   **S (Security):** Technologies and practices to protect IT systems and data.

---

### 2. Strategic Alignment of Business and IT

**A. Importance of Alignment**
*   IT is not just a tool; it's interdependent with business strategy and objectives.
*   This interdependence strengthens a company's business model competitiveness and creates new business value.

**B. Business-IT Alignment Defined**
*   It's how IT application programs, IT infrastructure, and the IT organization support and realize a company's business strategy and processes.

**C. Strategic Alignment Model (SAM)**
This model illustrates the strategic links between business and IT using two main dimensions:
1.  **Strategic Fit:** Focuses on the harmony between internal and external factors.
    *   **External Focus:** Aligning business strategy with the external business environment.
    *   **Internal Focus:** Aligning organizational structure and processes with internal management.
2.  **Functional Integration:** Focuses on the interplay between business and IT.
    *   **Business:** Relates to business strategy and business processes.
    *   **IT:** Relates to IT strategy, IT infrastructure, and IT processes.

*To achieve strategic alignment, these four areas (Business Strategy, IT Strategy, Organizational Infrastructure & Processes, IT Infrastructure & Processes) must complement each other.*

---

### 3. Impact of New Technologies: The Hype Cycle

**A. Gartner Hype Cycle**
*   A diagram released annually by Gartner, showing changes in the expected industrial economic value and impact of new IT technologies over time.
*   It helps understand the lifecycle and maturity of emerging technologies.

**B. Phases of the Hype Cycle**
1.  **Innovation Trigger:**
    *   New technologies are first introduced.
    *   Early public interest and expectations are high.
2.  **Peak of Inflated Expectations:**
    *   Hype and publicity reach their maximum.
    *   Expectations often exceed the technology's actual capabilities, creating an "inflated bubble."
3.  **Trough of Disillusionment:**
    *   The "bubble bursts" as technologies fail to meet exaggerated expectations.
    *   Interest wanes, and investment may decrease.
4.  **Slope of Enlightenment:**
    *   A period of revival where the technology's true potential and practical applications become clearer.
    *   Expectations climb steadily again, based on real-world use cases.
5.  **Plateau of Productivity:**
    *   The technology achieves mainstream adoption.
    *   Its benefits are widely demonstrated, and it generates steady, reliable value.

---

### 4. Case Study: Alibaba's Success in IT Business

**A. Background**
*   Founded in 1999 by Jack Ma and 17 friends as an online B2B shopping mall for Chinese SMEs.
*   Grew rapidly with a $20 million investment from Softbank in 2000.
*   Expanded into C2C (Taobao), online department store (Tmall.com), and electronic payment (Alipay).
*   Became a world leader in online shopping and FinTech.

**B. Key Success Factors (CSFs) for Alibaba**
1.  **No Transaction Fees:** Profits generated through advertising and search services instead of direct transaction fees.
2.  **Innovative Logistics & Trust:**
    *   Developed a logistics system for 1-2 day delivery across vast China.
    *   Used "Alipay" to build trust in China's often unreliable e-commerce environment.
3.  **Customer-Centric Approach:**
    *   Supported "chat-purchase" allowing customers to negotiate prices before buying.
    *   Aggressively met diverse customer requirements.
4.  **Visionary Leadership:**
    *   CEO Jack Ma's vision and strategy inspired employee dedication and effort.

**C. Core Competitiveness Elements Demonstrated by Alibaba**
*   **Price:** Competitive pricing facilitated by their business model.
*   **Quality:** Delivering reliable services (e.g., logistics, payment).
*   **Customer-Friendly Services:** Meeting specific user needs (e.g., chat-purchase).
*   **Strong Leadership & Strategy:** A clear vision driving the organization.

---

Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# IT Business & Ethics: Learning Guide

## I. IT Business Integration & Alignment

### A. Concept of IT Business
*   IT is more than a tool or support function; it's a concept deeply interdependent with business strategy and objectives.
*   This interdependence:
    *   Strengthens a company's business model competitiveness.
    *   Creates new business value.

### B. Business and IT Alignment
1.  **Interdependence:**
    *   Corporate business (strategy, data management, processes) and IT systems (applications, infrastructure, network) are mutually dependent.
    *   **Alignment:** IT application programs, infrastructure, and organization support and realize a company's business strategy and processes.
2.  **Strategic Alignment Model (2-Dimensional Diagram):**
    *   **Strategic Fit:** Focuses on external (business environment) and internal (management structure) aspects.
    *   **Functional Integration:** Focuses on business and IT integration.
    *   *Visualized as: Business Strategy ↔ IT Strategy & Strategic Compatibility ↔ Functional Integration.*
3.  **Four Complementary Areas for Strategic Alignment:**
    *   Business Strategy
    *   IT Strategy
    *   Organizational Infrastructure and Processes
    *   IT Infrastructure and Processes
    *   *Each area has its own scope, capabilities, governance, infrastructure, processes, and technology.*

## II. IT Business Ecosystem

### A. The Hype Cycle (Gartner)
*   **Definition:** A diagram showing the evolution of expected industrial economic value and impact of new IT technologies over time. Released annually by Gartner.
*   **Purpose:** Helps understand current and future technological trends to aid company growth and IT business incorporation.
*   **Five Phases:**
    1.  **Innovation Trigger:** New technologies are first introduced, generating high expectations.
    2.  **Peak of Inflated Expectations:** Hype exceeds actual capabilities, leading to unrealistic expectations.
    3.  **Trough of Disillusionment:** The "bubble bursts" as technologies fail to meet overblown expectations.
    4.  **Slope of Enlightenment:** Expectations stabilize and start climbing steadily again as the technology improves and real-world applications emerge.
    5.  **Plateau of Productivity:** The technology matures, generates steady value, and becomes widely adopted.

### B. Evolution of the IT Ecosystem
*   IT technology advances create a vast ecosystem of interacting and competing technologies.
1.  **Key Revolutions:**
    *   **Information Revolution (1980s):** Driven by personal computers and telecom networks.
    *   **Smart Revolution (2000s onwards):** Mobile devices, smartphone-based wireless internet, phone, and computing services converged, accelerating IT industry convergence and "smartification" across industries (e.g., education, automobiles, medicine).
2.  **Hyper-Connected Society:**
    *   Driven by advancements in sensor and network technologies.
    *   Evolution: **M2M** (Machine-to-Machine) → **IoT** (Internet of Things) → **IoE** (Internet of Everything).
    *   Connects humans to humans, humans to objects, and objects to objects, linking humans, objects, spaces, data, and services.
3.  **Core Technologies for Hyper-Connected Society:**
    *   **ICBM:**
        *   **I**oT (Internet of Things)
        *   **C**loud Computing
        *   **B**ig Data
        *   **M**obile
4.  **IT Ecosystem Components (C-P-N-D-S):**
    *   The IT ecosystem's center is shifting from hardware devices to platforms and contents, increasing software importance.
    *   **C - Contents:**
        *   Increased consumption of mobile content due to mobile technology (e.g., music, video, e-books).
        *   Smartphone-centered mobile environment allows diverse content use anywhere, anytime.
        *   New content distribution ecosystems are emerging, focused on mobile users.
    *   **P - Platform:**
        *   Evolution from individual services by single operators to common platforms with multiple providers.
        *   Shift from closed platforms to open platforms.
        *   Trend towards using shared common platforms rather than building proprietary ones (e.g., Apple, Google, Kakao service frameworks).
    *   **N - Network:**
        *   Smart revolution (smartphones, tablets, smart TVs) significantly increased network traffic.
        *   Next-generation smart services (smart homes, smart cars) and numerous IoT devices generate massive amounts of data traffic.
    *   **D - Device:**
        *   Wearable devices (e.g., smartwatches like Samsung Galaxy Gear, smart glasses like Google Glass) have intensified competition and collaboration among device makers.
        *   The number of smartphones and tablet PCs connectable to smart devices is increasing.
    *   **S - Security:** (Mentioned as a component, but specific characteristics are not detailed in the provided text.)
    *   *Note: Destructive innovations like 3D printing and unmanned vehicles lead the IT ecosystem and improve competitiveness through open innovation and customized business models.*

### C. Major IT Paradigm Changes (Five Trends)
1.  **Change from HW to SW Platform:**
    *   IT ecosystem shifts from devices (Hardware) to platforms and contents (Software).
    *   Software and platforms are now key drivers for value creation and national industry growth.
2.  **Change from IT Convergence to Smart Convergence:**
    *   Smart mobile-based IT convergence expands into traditional major industries (e.g., finance, healthcare).
    *   Fintech (Finance + Technology) has emerged as a significant new growth area.
3.  **ICBM-based Hyper-Connected Society:**
    *   The foundation of the hyper-connected society is ICBM (IoT, Cloud, Big Data, Mobile).
    *   This paradigm creates increased opportunities for economic growth.
4.  **Rapid Changes in the IT Technology Environment:**
    *   Emergence of "real sensation environment" technologies like virtual reality (VR), blending real and virtual worlds.
    *   Rise of "destructive innovations" such as 3D printing and unmanned vehicles, which can disrupt existing markets.
5.  **IT Business Transformation of Competition:**
    *   Growth is increasingly driven by small and medium-sized creative IT venture companies.
    *   Competitiveness is built through open innovation and the spread of demand-customized business models.

---

## IT Business and Ethics: A Learning Guide

This guide covers the essentials of the IT business landscape, key trends, ecosystem components, and resource management.

---

### 1. The Hyper-Connected Society and IT Ecosystem

The world is transforming into a **hyper-connected society**, where humans, objects, spaces, data, and services are all interconnected. This evolution spans from **M2M (Machine to Machine)** communication to the **IoT (Internet of Things)** and ultimately to the **IoE (Internet of Everything)**.

**Key Characteristics:**
*   IT technology connects:
    *   Humans to humans
    *   Humans to objects
    *   Objects to objects
*   **IT Ecosystem (C-P-N-D-S):** The foundational elements of this society.
    *   **C**ontents
    *   **P**latforms
    *   **N**etworks
    *   **D**evices
    *   **S**ecurity

**Ecosystem Shift:**
*   The focus is moving from hardware **devices** to **platforms** and **contents**.
*   **Software** is becoming increasingly important.
*   **Smart mobile-based IT convergence** is expanding into traditional industries (finance, healthcare).
*   **Destructive innovations** (e.g., 3D printing, unmanned vehicles) are driving competition through open innovation and customized business models.

**Core Technology: ICBM**
The hyper-connected society is powered by **ICBM technology**:
*   **I**nternet of Things (IoT)
*   **C**loud Computing
*   **B**ig Data
*   **M**obile

---

### 2. Key Trends in IT Paradigm Change

The IT landscape is undergoing significant shifts in five major areas:

1.  **From HW to SW Platforms:**
    *   IT ecosystem focus shifts from devices (hardware) to platforms and contents (software).
    *   Software and platforms are critical for value creation and industrial growth.
2.  **From IT Convergence to Smart Convergence:**
    *   Smart mobile-based IT convergence expands to traditional sectors (industries, finance, medical).
    *   **Fintech** (Financial Technology) has emerged as a major growth area.
3.  **ICBM-based Hyper-Connected Society:**
    *   IoT, Cloud, Big Data, and Mobile technologies create new economic growth opportunities.
4.  **Rapid Changes in the IT Technology Environment:**
    *   Emergence of "real sensation" technologies like virtual reality.
    *   Rise of destructive innovations that disrupt existing markets (e.g., 3D printing, unmanned vehicles).
5.  **IT Business Transformation of Competition:**
    *   Growth driven by small, creative IT venture companies.
    *   Competitiveness built through **open innovation** and **demand-customized business models**.

---

### 3. Components of an IT Business Ecosystem (C-P-N-D-S)

These five components characterize the modern IT ecosystem:

*   **Contents (C):**
    *   Mobile technology increases mobile content consumption.
    *   Smartphones enable users to access diverse content anytime, anywhere.
    *   New content distribution models prioritize mobile users.
    *   *Examples:* Games, Music, Video, E-books.
*   **Platform (P):**
    *   Evolving from single-operator services to common platforms where multiple providers participate.
    *   Shift from **closed platforms** (proprietary) to **open platforms**.
    *   Trend: Using shared common platforms instead of building individual ones.
    *   *Examples:* Apple App Store, Google Play, Facebook, Kakao.
*   **Network (N):**
    *   The "smart revolution" (smartphones, tablets, smart TVs) significantly increases network traffic.
    *   Next-generation services (smart homes, smart cars) generate large volumes of diverse traffic.
    *   IoT devices and sensors in the hyper-connected society produce massive data traffic.
    *   *Examples:* SK Telecom, KT, LG U+.
*   **Device (D):**
    *   Wearable devices (e.g., smartwatches, smart glasses) lead to fierce competition and collaboration among manufacturers.
    *   The number of smartphones and tablet PCs connecting to smart devices is growing.
    *   *Examples:* Smartphones, Tablets, PCs, McIntosh.
*   **Security (S):**
    *   Increasing sophistication of cyber threats (e.g., cyber terrorism, hacktivism) leads to more damage, especially to national infrastructure.
    *   Response strategy shifts from post-attack investigation to **early prevention** and **real-time resolution**.
    *   *Examples:* DDoS response, Attack detection, PIMS (Personal Information Management System), ISMS (Information Security Management System).

---

### 4. IT Resources and Management Activities

#### A) Concept of IT Resources

**IT Resources** include the people, processes, software, and hardware essential for running an IT business.

*   **Components of IT Resources:**
    *   **IT Support Systems:** Systems that support or manage IT businesses.
        *   *Examples:* **ERP** (Enterprise Resource Planning), **SCM** (Supply Chain Management), **PLM** (Product Lifecycle Management).
    *   **IT Management Systems:** Systems for managing IT services.
        *   *Example:* **ITSM** (Information Technology Service Management).
*   **Nature:** IT resources continuously evolve to maximize IT business results, adapting to changing technologies and times.
*   **IT Resource Management System:** Manages the entire lifecycle of IT resources (planning, development, application, operation, management, disposal). It tracks resource specifications and the business performance gains achieved by using them.

#### B) Role of IT Resources

IT resources provide three main benefits to an IT business:

1.  **Improved Production Efficiency:**
    *   Companies use IT to monitor customer patterns and manage inventory in real-time.
    *   *Example:* Wal-Mart's RetailLink system allows suppliers direct access to sales data, maximizing sales and competitive advantage.
2.  **Creation of New Business Values:**
    *   IT applications create entirely new business models and markets.
    *   *Examples:* Apple's iTunes transformed music distribution; E-commerce created online markets, open markets, and social commerce.
3.  **Expansion of Global Business:**
    *   IT resources enable global cooperative work, opening new markets and reducing costs, labor, and time for international expansion.
    *   *Examples:* Videoconferencing improves decision-making speed; Intranet systems facilitate information exchange across borders.

#### C) Management Activities and Structure for IT Business

IT business management follows a cyclical process:

**1. Cyclical Management Activities (PDCA Cycle):**

*   **P - Planning:**
    *   Identify opportunities and issues.
    *   Set IT business goals and scope.
    *   Create an IT business plan linking business objectives with IT.
*   **D - Do (Execution):**
    *   Design and implement the IT business solution.
    *   Collect operational data.
*   **C - Check:**
    *   Analyze IT business operational results.
    *   Monitor business and IT performance indicators.
    *   Verify the correlation between business and IT performance.
*   **A - Action (Corrective Action):**
    *   Identify necessary improvements.
    *   Adjust or modify IT solutions to better support the business.
    *   Repeat the cycle, returning to the Planning phase.

**2. Management and Control Structure:**

*   **Operational Support:** IT service and IT infrastructure provide support to enable business processes to achieve IT business results.
*   **Performance Metrics:** New IT business performance indicators are derived from:
    *   **IT QoS** (IT operational support service quality)
    *   Organizational business performance results.
*   **Decision Support:** These indicators are sent to the IT division. IT business management then supports decisions, adjustments, and investments in IT service and infrastructure to ensure target performance levels are met.

## Pages 25-29


This learning guide transforms the provided text (Pages 25-29) into a concise, study-friendly format.

---

# **IT Business & Ethics: Learning Guide (Pages 25-29)**

---

## **1. The Expanding Role of IT in Business Value**

Information Technology (IT) is fundamental for modern businesses, driving efficiency, creating new values, and enabling global expansion.

*   **Boosting Production Efficiency & Sales:**
    *   IT allows for continuous adjustments to inventory levels based on real-time customer purchasing data.
    *   **Example:** Wal-Mart's **RetailLink system** provides suppliers direct access to sales data, improving inventory management, maximizing sales, and creating a significant competitive advantage.
*   **Creating New Business Values:**
    *   IT enables the formation of entirely new business models and value propositions.
    *   **Examples:**
        *   **Apple's iTunes Store:** Revolutionized music distribution from physical to digital, becoming a major growth driver for the company.
        *   **E-commerce:** Created virtual online markets, leading to new concepts like open markets and social commerce, changing traditional commerce.
*   **Expanding Global Business:**
    *   IT facilitates global cooperative work environments, allowing companies to explore new international markets.
    *   It challenges traditional views on the costs, labor, and time required for global expansion.
    *   **Examples:**
        *   **Videoconferencing systems:** Enhance decision-making speed and efficiency across dispersed teams.
        *   **Intranet systems:** Enable instant information exchange globally, overcoming time and space constraints, giving competitive advantages to international businesses.

## **2. Managing IT Business: The PDCA Cycle**

IT business management uses a cyclical process, the **PDCA cycle** (Plan, Do, Check, Act), to ensure IT initiatives are aligned with business goals and continuously improved.

*   **Plan (P):**
    *   Identify opportunities and issues related to IT business.
    *   Set clear goals and define the scope for IT initiatives.
    *   Establish an IT business plan that strategically links IT with overall business objectives.
*   **Do (D):**
    *   Design and implement the IT business solution or project.
    *   Collect operational data generated by the implemented IT solution.
*   **Check (C):**
    *   Analyze the results and outcomes of the IT business operations.
    *   Monitor key performance indicators (KPIs) for both business and IT.
    *   Verify the correlation and impact of IT performance on business results.
*   **Action (A):**
    *   Identify necessary improvements or adjustments based on the analysis from the "Check" phase.
    *   Modify the IT solution or processes to better support the business.
    *   The cycle then repeats, returning to the "Planning" phase for continuous refinement and renewal.

### **2.1 IT Business Management and Control Structure**

*   **Purpose:** To ensure IT services and infrastructure effectively support business processes to achieve desired IT business outcomes.
*   **Process:**
    1.  **IT Service & Infrastructure Support:** Provide operational support.
    2.  **Business Process:** The core activities that utilize IT.
    3.  **Performance Metrics:**
        *   **IT Service Quality (IT QoS):** Measures the quality of IT operational support.
        *   **Business Performance Results:** Measures the overall performance of the organization.
        *   These combine to form **IT-business performance metrics**.
    4.  **IT Business Management:** Analyzes these metrics and IT QoS to make informed decisions, adjustments, and investments in IT service and infrastructure, ensuring target performance levels are met.

## **3. The IT Business Value Chain**

The value chain model is a critical management theory for analyzing business activities and understanding a company's competitive advantage. It breaks down an enterprise into **key (primary) activities** and **support activities**.

### **3.1 Traditional vs. E-commerce Value Chains**

The structure of the value chain differs significantly based on the business model:

*   **Traditional Manufacturing Company Value Chain:**
    *   **Key Activities:** Warehousing, operation (production), shipment, marketing & sales, customer service.
    *   **Support Activities:** Corporate infrastructure, HR management, technology development, purchasing activities.
*   **E-commerce Company Value Chain:** (Focused on digital and electronic processes for efficiency)
    *   **Key Activities:** Procurement, zero-inventory production, third-party logistics, network sales, online services.
    *   **Support Activities:** Integrated information platform and network infrastructure, Internet recruitment, online management of suppliers.

### **3.2 The Evolving Role of IT in the Value Chain**

The perception of IT's role in the value chain has changed dramatically:

*   **Past View (Pre-mid-2000s):** IT was largely considered a "back-office support activity," separate from a company's main operations.
*   **Current View (Post-2000s, especially Post-2010):**
    *   **Company-Wide IT Integration:** IT is now integrated into *all* key and support activities across the entire company. It is a critical factor in every aspect of primary operations.
        *   **Example:** A hypermarket cannot operate competitively without IT to manage inventory, display products, and collect customer data in real-time. This highlights a fundamental **convergence** of the value chain model with IT.
    *   **IT-Specialized Companies:** For businesses whose core model is e-business or Internet-based (e.g., Amazon.com, Interpark), IT is inseparable from both their key and support activities. Their entire value chain is inherently IT-driven.
    *   **Expansion of the Value Chain Model:** This pervasive integration means our understanding of the traditional value chain must expand.
        *   IT integration drives significant **structural changes** within organizations (e.g., eliminating unnecessary decision-making steps via intranet systems, fostering more horizontal organizations by distributing information widely).
        *   The utilization of IT is now seen as having a decisive impact on an entire organization's structure and competitive advantages, representing a **new concept of the value chain model**.

## **4. Recent Trends & Major Issues: IT Business Strategy**

Developing an effective IT business strategy is crucial for companies to achieve their missions and objectives within complex internal and external environments.

*   **Strategic Importance:** Setting the right strategy is particularly critical for the modern IT business, which involves deep integration of IT with business processes.
*   **Key Areas of Focus:** As the domain of IT business expands, there is growing interest in:
    *   Methods for establishing robust IT business strategies.
    *   Techniques for analyzing the business environment (e.g., **SWOT analysis**) as a prerequisite for strategy formulation.
*   **Future Learning:** This topic involves exploring current and future models for IT business strategies, implementation methods, and various environmental analysis tools.

---

### **Learning Objectives:**

1.  Explain the concept and significance of an IT business strategy.
2.  Describe models and methods for analyzing the business environment to effectively formulate IT business strategies.

### **Keywords:**

IT business strategy formulation, IT business environment analysis.

---

## Pages 28-32


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## **IT Business & Ethics: Strategy & Value Chain**

### **1. IT's Evolving Role in the Business Value Chain**

The traditional Value Chain Model, which outlines a company's key and support activities, is fundamentally transformed by IT.

*   **Company-wide IT Integration:**
    *   IT is no longer just for "back-office" functions.
    *   It's integrated into *all* key and support activities of a company's value chain.
    *   **Example:** A hypermarket uses IT for real-time inventory, customer behavior analysis, and purchase history tracking to stay competitive.
*   **IT-Specialized Companies:**
    *   For e-businesses or Internet businesses (e.g., Amazon.com, Interpark), IT is the core.
    *   Their key and support activities are inseparable from IT; a new perspective on the value chain is needed.
*   **Expansion of the Value Chain Model:**
    *   Our understanding of the value chain must adapt to IT's dual role:
        1.  IT integrated *into* existing business processes.
        2.  IT *as* the main business itself.
    *   **Impact of IT Integration:**
        *   Drives structural changes within companies.
        *   Eliminates unnecessary processes (e.g., through intranet information systems).
        *   Transforms hierarchical organizations into more horizontal ones by sharing information more broadly.
        *   IT's impact creates a "new" value chain concept that influences organizational structure and competitive advantage.

### **2. IT Business Strategy: Introduction**

**IT Business Strategy** is about finding the most effective way to achieve a company's mission and objectives by integrating IT and business processes, considering both internal and external environments.

*   **Key Focus:** Establishing strategies and analyzing the environment before formulation.
*   **Learning Objectives:**
    1.  Explain IT business strategy.
    2.  Explain business environment analysis models for IT strategy formulation.
*   **Keywords:** IT business strategy formulation, IT business environment analysis.

### **3. Practical Example: Dell Computers' SWOT Analysis (Mid-1990s)**

Dell used **SWOT analysis** (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, Threats) to develop its IT business strategy.

*   **Strengths (Internal):**
    *   Ability to sell directly to consumers.
    *   Ability to design components to lower manufacturing costs.
    *   Lower prices than competitors.
*   **Weaknesses (Internal):**
    *   No relationships with local computer dealerships.
*   **Opportunities (External):**
    *   Consumer demand for one-stop shopping.
    *   Consumers had good computer knowledge and knew what they wanted.
    *   The Internet emerged as a powerful marketing tool.
*   **Threats (External):**
    *   Competitors (Compaq, IBM) had superior brand power and quality reputation.
    *   Competitors had strong relationships with local dealerships.
*   **Dell's Strategy based on SWOT:**
    *   **Leveraged Strengths & Opportunities:** Assembled and sold custom-built computers directly to customers (initially phone, then Internet).
    *   **Addressed Weaknesses & Threats:** Eliminated dependence on local dealer networks, directly counteracting competitor advantages in that area. Built high-quality, tailored PCs shipped immediately, neutralizing brand/quality threats.

### **4. Phases of IT Business Strategy**

Developing an IT business strategy involves two main phases:

**Phase 1: Establishment of IT Business Strategy**
*   Defining the strategy's general concept, elements, and process.

**Phase 2: Analysis of the IT Business Environment**
*   Involves analyzing external, internal, and then consolidated environments.

    *   **A. External Environment Analysis:**
        *   **Macro-External (PEST Technique):** Analyzes broad external factors:
            *   **P**olitical
            *   **E**conomic
            *   **S**ocial
            *   **T**echnical
        *   **Micro-External (Porter's 5-Forces Industry Structure Analysis):** Analyzes competitive forces within an industry:
            *   Bargaining power of suppliers
            *   Bargaining power of buyers
            *   Threat of new entrants
            *   Threat of substitute products or services
            *   Intensity of rivalry among existing competitors
        *   **Marketing/Competitive Market Analysis:**
            *   **4P Technique:** Product, Price, Place, Promotion.
            *   **3C Technique:** Company, Customers, Competitors.
    *   **B. Internal Environment Analysis (McKinsey 7S Method):**
        *   Analyzes 7 interconnected internal elements:
            *   **S**hared Values, **S**trategy, **S**tructure, **S**ystems, **S**taff, **S**tyle, **S**kills.
    *   **C. Consolidated Environment Analysis:**
        *   **SWOT Analysis:** Combines external opportunities/threats with internal strengths/weaknesses.
        *   **BCG Matrix:** Used with SWOT to select business development strategies based on an IT business's growth potential and market share (e.g., Stars, Cash Cows, Question Marks, Dogs).

### **5. Establishing an IT Business Strategy: Detailed View**

**A. Concept of Strategy Establishment:**
*   Defining strategies to fulfill an organization's mission.
*   Requires analysis of current status and a clear direction for change.
*   Must align with strategies at all organizational levels.
*   The output (strategic plan) provides overall direction for Enterprise Architecture (EA), process improvement, risk management, and portfolio management.

**B. Elements of a Strategy Plan:**

| Element              | Description                                                                     |
| :------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Basic Information**  | Company's mission, objectives/goals, quantitative performance results.           |
| **Current Status Model** | The "As-Is" state: current internal/external environment, business principles, values. |
| **Future Goal Model**  | The "To-Be" state: the vision and specific goals for the future.                |
| **Implementation Strategy** | The roadmap or actions to achieve the future goals and mission.                 |

**C. Strategy Development Process (As-Is to To-Be):**
1.  **Evaluate Current (As-Is) Model:** Understand the company's present state.
2.  **Present Future (To-Be) Model:** Define the desired future state and goals.
3.  **Develop Implementation Strategies:** Create plans to transform the company from the As-Is to the To-Be model.

**D. Interdependence of Strategy Elements (Simplified Flow):**

*   **Mission:** The organization's highest purpose and achievement.
*   **Vision:** Future aspirations and goals, guided by the mission.
*   **Goals/Objectives:** Specific, measurable targets derived from the vision.
*   **Implementation Strategies/Initiatives:** Actions and plans to achieve objectives and vision.
*   **Performance Index/Measures:** Metrics used to track progress and success in realizing goals.
