## Pages 31-35


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text, designed for study.

---

## IT Business Strategy & Environment Analysis: Learning Guide

This guide covers the core concepts of establishing an IT business strategy and analyzing its environment.

### 1. Overview of IT Business Strategy Phases

An IT business strategy involves two main phases:
1.  **Strategy Establishment:** Defining the strategy itself.
2.  **Environment Analysis:** Understanding the context.

**Key Analysis Techniques:**
*   **External Environment:**
    *   **Macro-environment:** PEST (Political, Economic, Social, Technical)
    *   **Micro-environment:** 5-Force industry structure, 4P/3C marketing analysis
*   **Internal Environment:** McKinsey 7S Method
*   **Consolidated Environment:** SWOT Analysis, BCG Matrix

### 2. Establishing an IT Business Strategy

The IT business environment constantly changes, so IT strategies must be continuously updated. The goal is to align the organization and its business with the environment to increase survival chances and achieve targets.

#### A) Concept of Strategy Establishment

*   **Definition:** The process of defining strategies to fulfill an organization's mission.
*   **Purpose:**
    *   Explains current status and suggests directions for change.
    *   Ensures alignment with strategies of individual business units.
    *   Provides direction for company-wide activities (e.g., Enterprise Architecture, risk management).
*   **Output:** A Strategic Plan document.
*   **Hierarchy:** Corporate strategy cascades down to mid-level and operational goals.

#### B) Elements of a Strategy Plan

Strategy development typically involves evaluating the **current (As-Is) model**, setting **future goals (To-Be model)**, and formulating **implementation strategies** to bridge the gap.

| Element               | Description                                                               |
| :-------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Mission**           | The organization's core purpose or main business; not time-bound.         |
| **Vision**            | The ideal future the company aspires to; achieved by executing the mission. |
| **Goals**             | Measurable, high-level targets that support the mission.                  |
| **Objectives**        | Specific, quantifiable, low-level targets indicating goal achievement.      |
| **Principles**        | Core values or constraints guiding how targets are achieved.               |
| **Enablers**          | External environments or internal strengths that help achieve goals.      |
| **Barriers**          | External environments or internal weaknesses that hinder goal achievement. |
| **Strategy**          | The approach taken to achieve the mission, objectives, and goals.           |
| **Strategic Plan**    | A document outlining the strategy and factors influencing it.              |
| **Initiatives**       | Sets of activities performed to implement a strategy.                       |
| **Actions**           | Specific, time-constrained procedures to achieve objectives, assigned to people. |
| **Performance Index** | The target value used to measure progress toward a goal.                   |

#### C) Strategy Setting Process

The strategy setting process is cyclical and involves four phases:

1.  **Strategy Analysis**
2.  **Strategy Selection**
3.  **Strategy Implementation & Management**
4.  **Feedback** (leading back to Analysis for review)

##### 1. Strategy Analysis

*   **Purpose:** Collect information needed for business decisions.
*   **Key Distinction:**
    *   **Internal Environment:** Can be controlled and improved by the company.
    *   **External Environment:** Difficult to control, requiring adaptive strategies.

    **Components of Strategy Analysis:**
    *   **External Environment Analysis:**
        *   **Macro-environment:** Broad factors like political, economic, social, technological. (PEST analysis is used here).
        *   **Micro-environment:** Industry-specific competitive environment where the company acquires resources and sells products/services.
    *   **Internal Environment Analysis:** Focuses on a company's internal elements, processes, resources, organization, and internal changes.
    *   **Consolidated Environment Analysis:**
        *   A comprehensive look at both external and internal factors together.
        *   **SWOT Analysis:** A key tool that examines:
            *   **S**trengths & **W**eaknesses (internal factors)
            *   **O**pportunities & **T**hreats (external factors)

##### 2. Strategy Selection

*   **Purpose:** Choose the best future direction for the company based on the analysis results.
*   **Critical Point:** Flawed analysis leads to poor strategy selection. A thorough review of analysis results is essential.
*   **Process:**
    1.  Generate a list of alternative strategic directions.
    2.  Evaluate each alternative against established standards (considering resource needs and solutions to key issues).
    3.  Select the most appropriate alternative as the strategic direction.

##### 3. Strategy Implementation & Management

*   **Action:** Adopt and put the chosen strategic alternative into effect.
*   **Key Managerial Issues:**
    *   Resource viability for execution.
    *   Readiness of company culture and structure.
    *   Change management for strategy realization.
    *   Strategy realization path and development method.
    *   Steering group readiness within the company.
    *   Influence over internal/external stakeholders.
*   **Monitoring & Adaptation:**
    *   Continuously monitor strategy progress.
    *   Provide feedback from implementation back to the analysis phase.
    *   Be prepared for unexpected events: internal/external environments can change, requiring a review of the strategy analysis to ensure continued validity.

### 3. IT Business Environment Analysis

#### A) External Environment Analysis

##### 1. PEST Analysis

*   **Purpose:** Analyzes the external **macro-environment** by identifying Political, Economic, Social, and Technological (PEST) opportunity and threat factors.
*   **Method:** Brainstorm characteristics of the target market (country/region) across these four dimensions.

## Pages 34-38


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business Strategy & Environment Analysis

This guide covers the process of setting business strategies and analyzing the internal and external environments that influence them.

---

### Section 1: The Strategy Setting Process

The strategy-setting process ensures a company plans and executes its future direction effectively. It involves four main phases:

1.  **Strategy Analysis:** Investigating basic company information and studying its current (As-Is) state.
2.  **Strategy Selection:** Establishing the future (To-Be) model and the strategy to achieve it.
3.  **Strategy Implementation & Management:** Adopting and putting the strategy into effect, making adjustments as needed.
4.  **Feedback:** Continuous monitoring and feeding information back to the analysis phase to ensure ongoing relevance.

---

### Section 2: Strategy Analysis Explained

**Purpose:** To collect information vital for making sound business decisions.

**Key Environments:**

*   **Internal Environment:** Elements within the company's control (e.g., resources, processes). Can be improved directly.
*   **External Environment:** Conditions outside the company's direct control (e.g., market trends, regulations). Requires adaptive strategies.

**Analysis Types:**

1.  **External Environment Analysis:**
    *   Examines conditions outside the company.
    *   **Macro-environment:** Broad factors influencing multiple industries (e.g., political, economic, social, technological).
    *   **Micro-environment:** Industry-specific environment where the company competes for resources and sales (competitive environment).

2.  **Internal Environment Analysis:**
    *   Focuses on internal elements, processes, resources, organizational structure, and internal changes.

3.  **Consolidated Environment Analysis:**
    *   Combines both external and internal factors for an integrated view.
    *   **SWOT Analysis:** A crucial tool for this. It identifies:
        *   **S**trengths (Internal)
        *   **W**eaknesses (Internal)
        *   **O**pportunities (External)
        *   **T**hreats (External)

---

### Section 3: Strategy Selection

**Purpose:** To choose the optimal future direction for the company based on insights from the Strategy Analysis phase.

**Key Steps:**

1.  **Review Analysis Results:** Thoroughly examine the information from the strategy analysis. Flawed analysis leads to poor strategy choices.
2.  **Identify Alternatives:** Generate a list of potential strategic directions, each with different resource requirements and solutions.
3.  **Evaluate & Choose:** Assess each alternative against established evaluation standards and select the most appropriate strategic direction.

---

### Section 4: Strategy Implementation & Management

**Purpose:** To execute the chosen strategy and oversee its progress.

**Key Aspects:**

*   **Execution:** Adopt and put the selected strategic alternative into effect.
*   **Managerial Issues:** Be prepared for challenges related to:
    *   Resource availability and viability.
    *   Company culture and structural readiness for change.
    *   Change management processes.
    *   Strategy realization path and development methods.
    *   Steering group readiness within the company.
    *   Influence over internal and external stakeholders.
*   **Monitoring & Feedback:** Continuously track strategy progress. Status updates are fed back to the analysis phase to inform future decisions.
*   **Adaptation:** If unexpected external or internal changes occur after initial analysis, re-evaluate the strategy to ensure its continued validity.

---

### Section 5: IT Business Environment Analysis Methods

These are specific tools used for detailed environmental analysis.

#### A) External Environment Analysis Methods

1.  **PEST Analysis (Macro-environment)**
    *   **Purpose:** To analyze macro-external political, economic, social, and technological factors that present opportunities or threats.
    *   **Process:** Brainstorm characteristics of the target market country/region.
    *   **Categories & Examples:**
        *   **P**olitical: Government stability, legislation (employment, regulation), tax policy, trade, environmental laws.
        *   **E**conomy: Economic growth, unemployment, inflation, interest rates, labor costs, globalization impact, disposable income.
        *   **S**ociety, Culture: Population demographics, education, health, social mobility, job market attitudes, social taboos.
        *   **T**echnology: Impact of new technologies (e.g., internet), communication costs, remote work, R&D, technology transfer.
    *   **PESTLE/PESTEL:** Includes Legal (L) and Environmental (E) factors in addition to PEST.

2.  **Porter's Five Forces Analysis (Micro-environment)**
    *   **Purpose:** To analyze the structure of the industry and establish strategies for competitive advantage.
    *   **Focus:** Industry structure analysis from five perspectives:
        *   **Competitive Rivalry:** How intense is competition? (Product differentiation, fixed costs, industry growth, surplus equipment).
        *   **Bargaining Power of Suppliers:** How much leverage do suppliers have? (Supplier's market share, volume, tech superiority, product importance).
        *   **Bargaining Power of Buyers:** How much leverage do customers have? (Price sensitivity, purchase volume, buyer importance).
        *   **Threat of New Entrants:** How easy is it for new companies to join the market? (Entry barriers, product differentiation, new entrant financial resources, market penetration).
        *   **Threat of Substitutes:** How likely are customers to switch to alternative products/services? (Changes in consumer needs, price competitiveness of substitutes, impact of replacement).

3.  **3C & 4P Analysis Method (Micro-environment)**
    *   **Purpose:** To analyze the industry market, used broadly for marketing and competitive environment analysis.
    *   **3C's (Customer, Company, Competition):**
        *   **Customer Analysis:** Estimate market size & growth, identify target customers, product positioning, and demand hierarchy.
        *   **Company Analysis:** Examine internal/external environment, strengths/weaknesses (often with SWOT), and use for goal setting & strategy development.
        *   **Competitor Analysis:** Identify current/potential competitors using market analysis, financial data, and business portfolios.
    *   **4P's (Product, Price, Place, Promotion):**
        *   **Product Analysis:** Examine design, brand, characteristics, performance, quality.
        *   **Price Analysis:** Analyze product price, discounts, demand-price relationship, competitor pricing, and price flexibility.
        *   **Place Analysis:** Analyze sales region, distribution, logistics, and inventory levels.
        *   **Promotion Analysis:** Analyze advertising, promotion, marketing, and customer communication strategies.

#### B) Internal Environment Analysis Methods

1.  **7S Analysis Method**
    *   **Purpose:** To analyze a company's internal environment, diagnose its health, and identify its core competency components.
    *   **Origin:** Developed by McKinsey consulting firm.
    *   **Seven "S" Components:** The model defines 7 core components starting with 'S'.
        *   **Shared Values:** Analyze the ideals, mission, and core beliefs universally shared among organization members.
        *   **Strategy:** Analyze the company's goals, vision, and the budget, organization, and human resources required to achieve them.
        *   **System:** Analyze processes, techniques, regulations, and policies for managing people and making decisions.
        *   **Structure:** Analyze the organizational form, workforce structure, division of departmental responsibilities, and coordination systems.
        *   *(The provided text describes only these four of the seven 'S' components.)*

---

## Pages 37-41


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# Business Environment Analysis Learning Guide

This guide covers key frameworks for analyzing a company's external, internal, and combined environments.

---

## 1. External Environment Analysis

### A. Porter's Five Forces Framework

**Purpose:** An industry structure analysis model to understand the forces shaping an industry and how companies can respond to threats.

**The Five Forces (and their key factors):**

1.  **Bargaining Power of Suppliers:**
    *   **Factors:** Supplier's market share, volume supplied, technological superiority, importance of supplied product.
2.  **Bargaining Power of Buyers:**
    *   **Factors:** Purchaser's price sensitivity, amount purchased, importance of a purchaser.
3.  **Threat of New Entrants:**
    *   **Factors:** Entry barriers, product differentiation, financial resources of new entrants, market penetration level, brand recognition.
4.  **Threat of Substitutes:**
    *   **Factors:** Changes in consumer needs, price competitiveness of substitutes, impact of replacement.
    *(Note: The fifth force, "Rivalry among existing competitors," is usually included in Porter's model but not detailed in the provided text.)*

---

### B. 3C and 4P Analysis Method

**Purpose:** A micro-external environmental analysis method used to analyze an industry's market, crucial for marketing products/services and understanding the competitive environment.

**1. The 3C's:**

*   **Customer Analysis:**
    *   Identify target customers, product positioning, and customer demand.
    *   Estimate market size and market growth rate.
*   **Company Analysis:**
    *   Examine the company's internal and external environment, strengths, and weaknesses (often linked with SWOT analysis).
    *   Used for setting company goals and developing strategies.
*   **Competitor Analysis:**
    *   Identify current and potential competitors.
    *   Use market analysis, financial data, and business portfolios.

**2. The 4P's (Marketing Mix):**

*   **Product Analysis:**
    *   Analyze design, brand, characteristics, brand power, performance, and quality.
*   **Price Analysis:**
    *   Analyze product price, discount conditions, demand vs. price levels.
    *   Compare prices to competitors and examine price flexibility.
*   **Place Analysis (Distribution):**
    *   Analyze sales region, distribution channels, logistics, and inventory levels.
*   **Promotion Analysis:**
    *   Analyze advertising, promotional activities, marketing strategies, and customer communication.

---

## 2. Internal Environment Analysis

### A. McKinsey 7S Analysis Method

**Purpose:** An internal environmental analysis technique to diagnose a company by identifying its core competency components. It defines these components using 7 items starting with 'S'.

**The 7 S's:**

1.  **Shared Values:** Ideals and mission shared by organizational members; values emphasized and universally shared.
2.  **Strategy:** Company's goals and vision; assessment of budget, organization, and human resources needed to achieve the strategy.
3.  **System:** Processes and techniques for managing people and making decisions; includes regulations and policies.
4.  **Structure:** Organizational form, workforce structure, division of responsibilities between departments, and coordination systems.
5.  **Staff:** Capabilities, qualities, and expertise levels of staff; including strengths/weaknesses and environment for demonstrating capabilities.
6.  **Style:** Management and operational style of the company; leadership exhibited and organizational culture.
7.  **Skills:** Organizational operations and management skills; employee skills needed to run the company and core competencies.

**Key takeaway:** The 7S elements are dynamic and interconnected. Weakness in one area can impact others. A company must manage its 7S comprehensively to achieve business goals.

---

## 3. Consolidated Internal & External Environment Analysis

### A. SWOT Analysis

**Purpose:** A framework for analyzing a company's **internal strengths (S)** and **weaknesses (W)** alongside **external opportunities (O)** and **threats (T)**. Used primarily for establishing strategies, especially overall company strategy and marketing activities.

**Framework:**
The analysis results are often mapped into a matrix:

| Strategic Direction | Opportunities (O) | Threats (T) |
| :------------------ | :---------------- | :---------- |
| **Strengths (S)**   | SO Strategy       | ST Strategy |
| **Weaknesses (W)**  | WO Strategy       | WT Strategy |

**Evolution & Value:**

*   **Historically:** Often based on abstract insights and theoretical arguments, leading to limited practical implications.
*   **Today (Renewed Attention):** With the integration of IT and Business Intelligence (BI), SWOT analysis is enhanced by high-quality, data-backed information.
    *   This provides objective and predictive results.
    *   Improved data quality leads to better company strategies, especially when quantified numerical data is analyzed from multiple angles.

---

### B. BCG Matrix (Boston Consulting Group Matrix)

**Purpose:** A market analysis technique used to evaluate a company's portfolio of products and business services, or even a single company/department. It helps in marketing and sales planning.

**Structure:** A two-dimensional matrix evaluating products/services based on:

*   **Vertical Index:** Market Growth (external environment)
*   **Horizontal Index:** Market Share (internal environment)

**The Four Quadrants:**

1.  **Dog:**
    *   **Characteristics:** Low market share, low growth potential.
    *   **Strategy:** Consider exiting the business.
2.  **Question Mark (?):**
    *   **Characteristics:** Low market share, high growth potential.
    *   **Strategy:** Requires investment to increase market share, with uncertain future.
3.  **Star (*):**
    *   **Characteristics:** High market share, high growth potential.
    *   **Strategy:** Requires continuous investment to maintain growth and position.
4.  **Cash Cow:**
    *   **Characteristics:** High market share, low growth potential.
    *   **Strategy:** Generates high cash flows with low investment; profits can fund other areas.

---


---

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business Strategy & Governance

This guide covers key strategic analysis tools and essential concepts in IT business planning and governance.

---

### Section 1: Strategic Analysis Tools

#### 1.1 SWOT Analysis

**Purpose:** A framework used to establish overall company strategy.

*   **Traditional Use:**
    *   Primarily for marketing activities.
    *   Based on abstract insights, not concrete data.
    *   Often seen as theoretical, lacking practical implications for strategy execution.
*   **Modern Relevance (with IT & Business Intelligence):**
    *   **Renewed Value:** Business Intelligence (BI) integration has revitalized SWOT.
    *   **Data-Driven:** Now enhanced by high-quality, quantified data.
    *   **Results:** Provides objective and future-predictive analysis.
    *   **Benefits:** Huge impact on marketing and overall company processes, leading to improved strategy quality.

#### 1.2 BCG Matrix (Boston Consulting Group Matrix)

**Purpose:** A market analysis technique to evaluate a company's portfolio of products and business services. Can also evaluate a single company or department.

*   **Dimensions:**
    *   **Vertical Index:** Market Growth (External Environment)
    *   **Horizontal Index:** Market Share (Internal Environment)
*   **Four Quadrants:**
    *   **Question Mark (?):**
        *   **Characteristics:** Low market share, high growth potential.
        *   **Action:** Requires investment to increase market share.
    *   **Star (*):**
        *   **Characteristics:** High market share, high growth potential.
        *   **Action:** Needs continuous investment to maintain growth.
    *   **Dog:**
        *   **Characteristics:** Low market share, low growth potential.
        *   **Action:** Consider exiting the business.
    *   **Cash Cow:**
        *   **Characteristics:** High market share, low growth potential.
        *   **Action:** Generates high cash flows with low investment.

---

### Section 2: IT Business Planning & Governance

**Learning Objectives:**
*   Explain IT governance.
*   Explain Enterprise Architecture (EA).
*   Explain Information Strategy Planning (ISP).

**Key Concepts:** IT Governance, Enterprise Architecture (EA), Information Strategy Planning (ISP)

#### 2.1 Overview of IT Business Planning

*   **Starting Point:** Understanding company vision, goals, strategies, and tasks.
*   **Main Activities:** Enterprise Architecture (EA) and Information Strategy Planning (ISP).
*   **Goal:** Plan from a macro perspective to prevent indiscriminate and overlapping development activities in IT business.
*   **Management:** IT Governance provides control over EA and ISP implementation.

#### 2.2 IT Governance

**Concept:** A system for controlling and managing a company's IT, similar to corporate governance.

*   **Aim:**
    *   Align IT resources with company goals and strategies.
    *   Contribute to realizing business targets.
*   **Mechanism:** Defines roles, responsibilities, and creates a control/management structure for IT performance and risks.
*   **Key Roles:**
    *   Controls EA and ISP implementation.
    *   Secures linkage between IT business strategy and IT values.
    *   Provides risk management, resource management, and performance measurement systems.

#### 2.3 Enterprise Architecture (EA)

**Concept:** A foundational plan-based informatization strategy.

*   **Purpose:** To prevent or eliminate overlapping and indiscriminate IT development efforts.
*   **Process (Example):**
    1.  Inspect and reengineer current business processes.
    2.  Establish mid-to-long-term plans for:
        *   Job responsibilities (stakeholders)
        *   Applications
        *   Data
        *   Technologies
*   **Management:** Often supported by an Enterprise Architecture Management System (EAMS) for continuous upgrades, helping close the gap between strategy and IT business.

#### 2.4 Information Strategy Planning (ISP)

**Concept:** The process of developing informatization strategies at the division level.

*   **Purpose:**
    *   Derive detailed requirements for individual systems.
    *   Set up systems for efficient calculation and verification of business scope, schedules, and budgets.
*   **Integration with EA:** Uses current EA information to prevent overlapping and indiscriminate development activities.
*   **Recent Trend:** Public sector RFPs (Requests for Proposal) often require detailed specifications; ISP helps companies produce these.

---
This guide summarizes the core information from pages 40-44, making it easier to study and understand.

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business Planning & Governance

This guide summarizes essential concepts related to IT Business Planning, focusing on Enterprise Architecture (EA), Information Strategic Planning (ISP), and IT Governance.

---

### 1. IT Business Planning Overview

*   **Starting Point:** IT business activities begin with establishing a **strategy**, followed by **planning**.
*   **Main Planning Activities:**
    *   **Enterprise Architecture (EA):** A blueprint for the entire enterprise's IT business.
    *   **Information Strategic Planning (ISP):** A plan for developing informatization strategies at the division level.
*   **Purpose of EA & ISP:** To plan from a macro perspective, preventing **indiscriminate** (unplanned) and **overlapping** IT development activities.
*   **IT Governance's Role:** Provides control over EA and ISP implementation, links IT business strategy with IT values, and manages risk, resources, and performance.
*   **Output Utilization:** These plans are used for IT business deployment, process/service operation, and performance evaluation.

---

### 2. IT Governance

#### 2.1. Concept & Purpose

*   **Definition:** A system for controlling and managing a company's IT, similar to corporate governance.
*   **Aim:**
    *   Align IT resources with company goals and strategies to achieve business targets.
    *   Define roles and responsibilities within the organization.
    *   Establish a control and management structure for IT performance and risks.
*   **Key Idea:** Ensures IT is used properly and contributes effectively to business objectives.

#### 2.2. Framework (COBIT 5)

**COBIT 5 (Control Objects for Information and Related Technology 5)** is a widely recognized IT governance framework. It separates governance and management processes.

*   **Governance Area (5 Processes):** Focuses on evaluating, directing, and monitoring IT.
    *   **EDM 1:** Establish the governance framework and measurement standards.
    *   **EDM 2:** Provide profits (value).
    *   **EDM 3:** Minimize IT-related risks.
    *   **EDM 4:** Optimize IT resource usage and risks.
    *   **EDM 5:** Ensure transparency for stakeholders.
*   **Management Area (4 Phases):** Focuses on building, running, and monitoring IT activities.
    *   **APO (Align, Plan, Organize):** Planning phase (linking, planning).
    *   **BAI (Build, Acquire, Implement):** Deployment phase (deploying, acquiring, configuring).
    *   **DSS (Deliver, Service, Support):** Operation phase (transferring, servicing, supporting).
    *   **MEA (Monitor, Evaluate, Assess):** Monitoring phase (monitoring, evaluating, reviewing).
*   **Standards Link:** The IT governance framework is linked to the international standard **ISO/IEC 38500**, which provides principles for evaluating, directing, and monitoring IT use.

#### 2.3. IT Governance Process

The IT governance process follows a four-stage cycle:

1.  **Planning Stage:**
    *   Links business goals with IT.
    *   Sets IT goals and establishes structures for organizing IT activities.
    *   Defines rules for resource use, risk management, governance structure, and performance measurement.
2.  **Operations Stage:**
    *   Monitors IT resources, IT risks, and overall IT management.
    *   Measures IT performance against set target levels.
3.  **Evaluation Stage:**
    *   Evaluates the **IT value** (earnings and costs) from future business opportunities delivered by IT.
    *   IT value includes strategic, economic, risk management, technical, social, and quality benefits.
    *   Calculated by subtracting business and potential risk costs from business opportunities.
4.  **Feedback Stage:**
    *   Based on evaluation results, corrective measures are taken to improve IT governance activities and processes.

#### 2.4. Key Focus Areas of IT Governance

These five areas align with a company's strategies:

1.  **Strategic Alignment:** Ensures IT governance supports strategic decisions and aligns with company strategy (e.g., through **EA**).
2.  **IT Value Delivery:** Optimizes IT integration with business processes to achieve IT business goals (e.g., **Backbone systems**, **IT Compliance**).
3.  **Risk Management:** Manages risk factors to ensure continuity of IT business (e.g., **DRS** - Disaster Recovery System, **BCP** - Business Continuity Plan).
4.  **Resource Management:** Organizes and manages IT resources to promptly respond to business requirements (e.g., **ITAM** - IT Asset Management).
5.  **Performance Measurement:** Establishes an IT-centered system to evaluate the performance of IT business activities (e.g., **BSC** - Balanced Scorecard, **IT ROI** - Return on Investment).

---

### 3. Enterprise Architecture (EA)

#### 3.1. Definition

*   **EA (Enterprise Architecture):** A comprehensive blueprint that clearly defines an enterprise's IT business.
*   **Purpose:**
    *   Make IT business understandable for stakeholders.
    *   Help the enterprise achieve its strategic goals and information resource management objectives.
*   **US OMB Definition:** "A blueprint that defines the current state of the relationship between information technology and an enterprise (as well as the activities carried out by the enterprise) and the state that the enterprise must strive for in the future."

#### 3.2. Need for EA

*   **Problem:** Without proper macro-level planning for IT systems, enterprises face:
    *   **Redundant systems:** Multiple systems performing similar functions.
    *   **Inability to collaborate:** Systems and departments cannot work together effectively.
*   **Consequence:** Falling into the **"IT Productivity Paradox"** – continuous adoption of IT systems without seeing actual benefits like increased corporate profits.
*   **Solution:** EA provides the necessary planning to avoid these issues, ensuring IT investments deliver tangible value and support strategic objectives.

---


---


## Pages 46-50


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text, designed for quick study.

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide

This guide covers key concepts in IT Governance, Enterprise Architecture (EA), and Information Strategic Planning (ISP).

---

### 1. IT Governance

**Definition:** IT Governance refers to the principles and frameworks used to evaluate, direct, and monitor how companies utilize IT.

**A. IT Governance Process**
This process consists of four stages:

1.  **Planning Stage**
    *   **Goal:** Link business strategy with IT, set IT goals.
    *   **Activities:** Establish structures, rules for IT activities, resource use, risk management, governance structure, and performance measurement.

2.  **Operations Stage**
    *   **Goal:** Monitor and manage IT activities.
    *   **Activities:** Monitor IT resources, IT risks, IT management, and IT performance. Set targets for performance and measure their achievement.

3.  **Evaluation Stage**
    *   **Goal:** Assess the value delivered by IT.
    *   **Activities:** Evaluate IT value, considering strategic, economic, risk management, technical, social, and quality benefits. Calculate IT value by subtracting business and potential risk costs from business opportunities.

4.  **Feedback Stage**
    *   **Goal:** Improve IT governance based on evaluation.
    *   **Activities:** Implement corrective measures and improvements to IT governance activities and related jobs.

**B. Key Focus Areas of IT Governance**
These five areas link IT to company strategies:

1.  **Strategic Alignment**
    *   **Focus:** Aligning IT with company strategy; ensuring IT decisions support business direction.
    *   **Method:** Enterprise Architecture (EA)

2.  **IT Value Delivery**
    *   **Focus:** Optimizing IT integration with business processes to achieve IT business goals.
    *   **Method:** Backbone systems, IT Compliance

3.  **Risk Management**
    *   **Focus:** Managing IT-related risk factors to ensure business continuity.
    *   **Method:** Disaster Recovery System (DRS), Business Continuity Plan (BCP)

4.  **Resource Management**
    *   **Focus:** Organizing and managing IT resources to quickly respond to business requirements.
    *   **Method:** IT Asset Management (ITAM)

5.  **Performance Measurement**
    *   **Focus:** Establishing an IT-centered system to evaluate performance of IT business activities.
    *   **Method:** Balanced Scorecard (BSC), IT Return on Investment (IT ROI)

---

### 2. Enterprise Architecture (EA)

**A. Overview of EA**

*   **Definition:** EA is a blueprint that clearly explains an enterprise's IT business to stakeholders. Its purpose is to help the enterprise achieve its strategic goals and information resource management objectives. It defines the current and desired future state of the relationship between IT and the enterprise.

*   **Need for EA:**
    *   **Problem:** Without macro-level planning, rapid adoption of information systems can lead to redundant systems, lack of collaboration, and the "IT Productivity Paradox" (adopting IT without seeing increased profits).
    *   **Solution:** EA provides an overall view of the business and creates close working relationships between different information resources, preventing these issues.

**B. Conceptual Diagram and Components of EA**

*   **Conceptual Flow:**
    `Enterprise Business Strategy` ↔ `IT Strategy`
    ↓
    `Enterprise Architecture (EA)`
    ↓
    `Business Architecture (BA)` | `Application Architecture (AA)` | `Data Architecture (DA)` | `Technical Architecture (TA)`

*   **Components of an EA:** EA is an act and instrument of IT governance. Its key components are:
    1.  **IT Governance:** (As defined above) Manages the process of aligning IT with business goals.
    2.  **Business Architecture (BA)**
        *   **Focus:** Designing how people, processes, and information interact based on business strategy and environment analysis.
        *   **Reference Model:** Performance Reference Model (PRM)
    3.  **Application Architecture (AA)**
        *   **Focus:** Identifying information needed for jobs, defining activities for processing/managing it. Creating standards for application functions and environments.
        *   **Reference Model:** Service Component Reference Model (SRM)
    4.  **Data Architecture (DA)**
        *   **Focus:** Identifying required documents, designing data models by understanding relationships between all information, data, and data structures.
        *   **Reference Model:** Data Reference Model (DRM)
    5.  **Technology Architecture (TA)**
        *   **Focus:** Defining criteria for selecting infrastructure and other technologies that support business and data applications. Also defines technical support services.
        *   **Reference Model:** Technology Reference Model (TRM)
    6.  **Standard Profile (SP)**
        *   **Focus:** A sub-structure of TA that defines the detailed list of technologies (e.g., JAVA architecture version: JDK 2.0).

**C. EA Frameworks**
These are leading frameworks for establishing an EA:

1.  **Zachman Framework**
    *   **Description:** Most frequently used. Defined as a matrix using views (perspectives) and descriptions.
    *   **5 Perspectives:** Planner, Owner, Designer, Builder, Subcontractor.
    *   **6 Descriptions:** Data, Function, Network, People, Time, Motivation.

2.  **TOGAF (The Open Group Architecture Framework)**
    *   **Description:** Open framework focusing on interoperability between companies.
    *   **Components:** Architecture Development Method (ADM) cycle, Technology Reference Model (TRM), and a Standards Information Point (SIP) database. Uses a building block approach.

3.  **FEAF (Federal Enterprise Architecture Framework)**
    *   **Description:** Developed by the U.S. CIO Council. Manages all Zachman framework content.
    *   **Components:** Eight components, 4-step progressive structure. Defines five reference models (Business, Performance, Data, Service Component, Technology). Forms the basis of Japan's EA framework. Includes AS-IS (current state) and TO-BE (future state) gap analysis for implementation.

---

### 3. Information Strategic Planning (ISP)

**A. Overview of ISP**

*   **Definition:** "Information Strategy Plan." It presents a vision for the information system and management structure needed to support an enterprise's mid-to-long term goals and business plan. Essentially, it's a rough sketch for the direction of long-term information system deployment.

**B. ISP Deployment Procedure**

1.  **Initial Analysis:**
    *   Analyze the company's external and internal environment using tools like SWOT, 5-Force, 7S, and 4C.
    *   Analyze the information environment, including technology requirements, trends, and new technology applications.

2.  **Current Operations Analysis:**
    *   Analyze the company's current operations, focusing critically on **business processes**.
    *   Examine existing information systems.
    *   Identify stakeholder requirements and areas for improvement.

3.  **Benchmarking:**
    *   Review earlier cases in similar industries to identify missing or distorted information and refine the plan.


---


## Pages 49-53


Here's a simplified learning guide extracted from the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: Enterprise Architecture (EA) & Information Strategic Planning (ISP)

### 1. Enterprise Architecture (EA) Reference Models

Reference models provide guidance for developing different aspects of an EA.

*   **Application Architecture (Service Component Reference Model - SRM):**
    *   Extracts information needed for tasks.
    *   Defines activities for processing/managing information.
    *   Creates standards for application development functions, characteristics, and environment.
    *   Identifies necessary documents for business model activities.
*   **Data Architecture (Data Reference Model - DRM):**
    *   Designs data models by understanding relationships between information, data, and structures.
*   **Technology Architecture (Technology Reference Model - TRM):**
    *   Defines criteria for selecting infrastructure to support business, data, applications, and other technologies.
    *   Defines technical support services.
*   **Standard Profile:**
    *   Defines a detailed technology list for the Technology Architecture (e.g., JAVA architecture version: JDK 2.0).

**Purpose of Reference Models:**
*   Provide early reference cases from similar industries/sectors to guide EA deployment.
*   **Government EA Reference Model:** Used for government-wide EA, also as a reference for departmental EAs.
    *   **Note:** Government-wide EA includes **Security Architecture** in addition to the four above.

### 2. EA Frameworks

Frameworks provide structured approaches for establishing an Enterprise Architecture. Key frameworks include:

*   **Zachman Framework:**
    *   **Most often used** for establishing an EA.
    *   Defined as a matrix using "view" and "perspective."
    *   **5 Perspectives:** Planner, Owner, Designer, Builder, Subcontractor.
    *   **6 Ways of Describing Each Perspective:** Data, Function, Network, People, Time, Motivation.
*   **TOGAF (The Open Group Architecture Framework):**
    *   An open framework focused on **interoperability between companies**.
    *   **Components:**
        *   Architecture Development Method (ADM) cycle.
        *   Technology Reference Model (TRM).
        *   Standards Information Point (SIP) - a database of summarized standards.
    *   Uses a "building block" concept to resolve component-level problems.
*   **FEAF (Federal Enterprise Architecture Framework):**
    *   Developed by the U.S. CIO Council (1998).
    *   **Structure:** 8 components and a 4-step progressive structure.
    *   Manages all Zachman Framework model contents.
    *   **Defines 5 Reference Models:** Business Reference Model (BRM), Performance Reference Model (PRM), Data Reference Model (DRM), Service Component Reference Model (SRM), Technology Reference Model (TRM).
    *   These models are interrelated and based on the Zachman Framework.
    *   Forms the basis of Japan's EA framework.
    *   Includes an approach for each segment, implementation plan, and AS-IS/TO-BE gap analysis.

### 3. Information Strategic Planning (ISP)

#### A) Overview of ISP
*   **Definition:** Information Strategic Plan. Often referred to as "ISP establishment."
*   **Purpose:** To define a **vision for the information system and management structure** that supports an enterprise's mid-to-long-term goals and business plan. It's a rough sketch of IT system deployment direction for long-term objectives.

#### B) ISP Deployment Procedure
1.  **Environment Analysis:**
    *   **Company Environment:** Analyze external/internal factors using tools like SWOT, 5-Force, 7S, 4C.
    *   **Information Environment:** Review technology requirements, trends, and new technology application feasibility.
2.  **Current Operation Analysis:**
    *   Analyze existing business processes to identify problems and areas for improvement.
    *   Analyze existing information systems.
    *   Gather stakeholder requirements and improvement agenda.
    *   **Benchmarking:** Compare with similar industries to correct missing/distorted information.
3.  **Informatization Plan:** Use analysis results to determine improvement directions, develop improved procedures, and create an informatization plan.

#### C) Basic Composition of ISP (Key Activities by Step)

| Step                      | Activity                               | Details                                                                                                                              |
| :------------------------ | :------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **1. Analysis**           | Management Environment Analysis        | Identify opportunities & threats (internal/external environment). Determine CSF (Critical Success Factors) & OIR (Official Information Required). |
|                           | Information Technology Environment Analysis | Study IT trends, analyze new IT application feasibility, identify informatization requirements.                                      |
|                           | Work Analysis                          | Analyze organizational role & work structure; identify current problems & improvement areas.                                         |
|                           | Information System Analysis            | Analyze current IT systems & resource management; identify problems & needed improvements.                                           |
|                           | Benchmarking                           | Conduct benchmarking from work & IT system viewpoints.                                                                               |
|                           | Gap Analysis                           | Identify business process & IT infrastructure requirements from early cases; study gaps with company's requirements; determine improvement direction. |
| **2. Future Model Design** | Future Business Process Design         | Establish a plan for improving business processes (ideal future model, new processes).                                               |
|                           | Establishment of Information Strategy  | Establish informatization vision, goals, execution strategy; define rules for IT system deployment, technology, and management.      |
|                           | Information System Future Structure Design | Establish an ideal application service/IT-based structure for strategic IT system deployment.                                        |
|                           | Information Resource Management System Design | Organize resource management for efficient operation of the established IT system.                                                    |
|                           | Establishment of Business Process Improvement Plan | Establish business process based on a future model.                                                                                  |
| **3. Deployment Plan**    | Establishment of Information System Deployment Plan | Establish execution strategy, implementation system, schedule, investment budget, and evaluate investment benefits.                  |
| **4. Detailed Cost**      | Development Service                      | Calculate development costs for each item.                                                                                           |
|                           | Equipment Purchase                       | Details of technical specifications, quantity, amount for SW/HW.                                                                     |
|                           | Maintenance and Repair during Operations | Cost of post-deployment operations, maintenance, disposal.                                                                           |
|                           | Calculation of Function Score            | Calculate function scores needed for deployment.                                                                                     |
| **5. Feasibility Analysis** | Economic Feasibility Analysis          | Conduct economic analysis (B/C, NPV, etc.).                                                                                          |
|                           | Alternative Analysis                     | Analyze at least 2 alternatives for changes in business volume/cost, business development approach.                                  |

#### D) Key Output of ISP Deployment
*   **Most Valuable Output:** A blueprint for a future process model and a set of activities for achieving company goals.
*   **Typical Outputs:**
    *   **Analysis Stage:**
        *   Report on business management environment analysis (strategic direction, environment).
        *   Report on enterprise status analysis (business process problems, improvement areas).
        *   Report on IT analysis (IT system problems, improvement areas).
    *   **Strategy Establishment Stage:**
        *   Informatization goal model specification form (new information model).
        *   Master plan for building the "To-Be" work system (complete ISP, define & prioritize projects).

### 4. Comparison of ISP and EA Concepts

| Category       | ISP (Information Strategic Planning)                                                               | EA (Enterprise Architecture)                                                                                    |
| :------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Objectives** | Link management strategy with informatization strategy; introduce new IT.                      | Blueprint for seamless integration of business and information resources.                                        |
| **Scope**      | Informatization strategy; can be company-wide, service, or departmental.                         | Architectures for technology (ITA), business (BA), application (AA), data (DA), etc., company-wide.             |
| **Main Activities** | - Analysis of business management environment, IT trends, tasks, IT system structure. <br> - Establishment of IT strategy & management system. <br> - Design future task handling process & IT system. <br> - Establish To-Be roadmap. | - Establish ITA direction & guidelines, reference models (BRM, SRM, DRM, TRM/SP, PRM). <br> - Analyze AS-IS architecture (BA, AA, DA, TA, SA). <br> - Establish TO-BE architecture (BA, AA, DA, TA, SA). <br> - Establish implementation plan & ITA management system. |
| **Key Outputs** | - Reports on analysis (business environment, IT trends, job/IT system). <br> - IT vision & strategy. <br> - Implementation agenda & roadmap. | - Company-wide architecture vision, rules, architecture matrix. <br> - Current & target architecture (BA, AA, DA, TA, SA). <br> - Plan for target architecture implementation. |

**Key Relationship:**
*   ISP deals with plans that fall within the scope of EA but are **more microscopic** and focused on the **informatization strategy**.
*   EA is deployed under a company's target architecture, aligning IT direction with management strategy using the latest IT.

**EA Management:**
*   EA must be managed to **respond quickly to changes** in the business management environment.
*   It needs to be **flexible** for quick implementation of company agendas through continuous updating.
*   The EA roadmap must be **shared** across the organization.

---

## Pages 52-56


This learning guide condenses the original text (Pages 52-56) into essential, easy-to-understand information.

---

## **IT Business & Ethics: Strategy, Adoption, and Outsourcing**

### **1. Information Strategy Planning (ISP) & Enterprise Architecture (EA)**

Understanding how IT initiatives are planned and integrated within an organization.

#### **1.1 Information Strategy Planning (ISP)**

*   **Purpose:** To link a company's management strategy with its information technology (IT) strategy and introduce new IT solutions. It's about planning *how* to use IT to achieve business goals.
*   **Scope:** Can be applied company-wide, to a specific service, or a department. It is more focused and "microscopic" compared to EA, concentrating on the IT informatization strategy itself.
*   **Key Activities:**
    *   Analyzing the business management environment (organization, stakeholders, customers).
    *   Analyzing the latest IT trends.
    *   Analyzing current business tasks and processes.
    *   Analyzing the existing information system structure.
    *   Establishing the new IT strategy and an information management system.
    *   Designing future business processes and information systems (the "To-Be" state).
    *   Creating a "To-Be" roadmap for implementation.
*   **Key Outputs:**
    *   Reports on business environment and IT trend analysis.
    *   Reports on job/information system analysis.
    *   Defined IT vision and strategy.
    *   An implementation agenda and roadmap.

#### **1.2 Enterprise Architecture (EA)**

*   **Purpose:** To create a blueprint for seamless integration of all business and information resources. It aligns IT direction with the overall management strategy.
*   **Scope:** Broader and more "macro-level" than ISP. It covers various architectures across the enterprise:
    *   **BA (Business Architecture):** How the business operates.
    *   **AA (Application Architecture):** How applications support business processes.
    *   **DA (Data Architecture):** How data is structured and managed.
    *   **TA (Technology Architecture):** The underlying technology infrastructure.
    *   **SA (Security Architecture):** How systems are secured.
*   **Key Activities:**
    *   Establishing direction and guidelines for IT Architecture (ITA).
    *   Establishing reference models (e.g., Business, Service, Data, Technical, Performance Reference Models).
    *   Analyzing the current ("AS-IS") architecture across all domains (BA, AA, DA, TA, SA).
    *   Establishing the target ("TO-BE") architecture for all domains.
    *   Developing an implementation plan.
    *   Establishing an ITA management system.
*   **Key Outputs:**
    *   Company-wide architecture vision, rules, and architecture matrix.
    *   Documentation of the current and target architectures (BA, AA, DA, TA, SA).
    *   A plan for implementing the target architecture.
*   **Key Characteristic:** EA must be flexible and continuously updated to respond quickly to changes in the business environment, ensuring the company's agenda is quickly implemented and shared.

#### **1.3 ISP vs. EA: Summary**

| Category    | Information Strategy Planning (ISP)                               | Enterprise Architecture (EA)                                                                  |
| :---------- | :---------------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Objective** | Links management & IT strategy; introduces new IT.                | Blueprint for business & IT resource integration; aligns IT with management strategy.           |
| **Scope**   | More focused on *informatization strategy*; microscopic within EA. | Broader target architecture (Business, Application, Data, Technology, Security); company-wide. |
| **Focus**   | Planning *how* IT will support goals.                            | Defining *what* the overall IT and business structure should look like.                       |

---

### **2. Key Considerations for IT Business Adoption**

When a company decides to implement an IT business solution, several crucial decisions arise.

*   **In-house Development vs. Outsourcing:** Deciding whether to develop solutions using internal resources or to hire external companies.
*   **Package Products vs. Custom Development:** If outsourcing, choosing between off-the-shelf software packages or building a custom system from scratch.
*   **Strategic Importance:** These decisions must enable the company to adapt to environmental changes quickly and ensure the long-term success of the IT business.
*   **Organizational Readiness:** Effective IT business adoption requires a proper organizational structure and processes for managing the building and operation of information systems.

#### **Keywords for Study:**
*   IT business adoption method
*   IT business adoption procedure
*   IT business outsourcing

---

### **3. Recent Trends & Issues: The Split Order Process**

*   **Problem Context (Public Sector Example):** Historically, poor planning and design of information systems (especially in the public sector) led to excessive work changes, cost overruns, and a lack of awareness/expertise regarding IT system benefits.
*   **Regulatory Measures:** Legislation now requires detailed **RFP (Request for Proposal)** and a **PMO (Project Management Office)** program for IT business deployment to improve outcomes.
*   **The "Split Order Process":** A government initiative to prevent irresponsible work changes and unfair subcontracting structures.
    *   **Core Idea:** Separates the **planning/design** phase from the **deployment/development** phase.
    *   **Planning/Design Phase:** Focuses on detailed requirement analysis, including:
        *   **ISP (Information Strategy Plan)**
        *   **ISMP (Information System Master Plan)**
        *   **Basic Design (Logical Design)**
    *   **Deployment/Development Phase:** Involves:
        *   **Detailed Design (Physical Design)**
        *   **System Development (Coding)**
        *   **Testing**
*   **Significance:**
    *   Promotes more meticulous and systematic planning and design.
    *   Helps overcome the "invisibility of software" by making requirements clearer upfront.
    *   Highlights how frequent requirement changes impede IT business success, encouraging upfront clarity.

---

### **4. IT Business Adoption Process**

The method by which a company acquires or develops IT systems or services.

*   **Alignment:** IT business adoption must align with the company's overall IT strategy and plans.
*   **Customization:** The methods and procedures should be tailored to the organization's size and its external environment.
*   **Core of IT:** Since the core value of IT is often implemented in software, the success of software development is critical for successful IT business adoption.
*   **Standardization:** The **Software Development Lifecycle (SDLC)**, specifically following standards like **ISO/IEC 12207**, should be used for software development post-adoption.

#### **4.1 IT Business Ordering Process**

This process defines the steps for the "orderer" (the department/person needing the IT solution) and involves external "suppliers" or internal "developers."

*   **Orderer:** The department or person responsible for defining and issuing requirements.
*   **Developer/Supplier:** The company's internal IT department or an external IT outsourcing expert.
*   **Key Activities within the Ordering Process:**
    1.  **Concept Definition & Detailed Specification of Requirements:** Clearly outlining what is needed.
    2.  **Preparation of RFP (Request for Proposal):** Document inviting potential suppliers to propose solutions.
    3.  **Evaluation of Proposal & Contract Signing:** Assessing proposals and formalizing the agreement.
    4.  **Monitoring of Project:** Overseeing the project's progress.
    5.  **Handover and Completion of Project:** Receiving the final solution and closing the project.
*   **Benefits of using this process:**
    *   Clearly defines activities for both the orderer and the supplier/contractor.
    *   Enhances the success rate of the IT service business.
    *   Provides a structured means of communication between parties.
    *   Adds visibility to the IT deployment process.

---

### **5. IT Outsourcing**

Engaging external expert resources to manage or perform IT-related functions.

*   **Benefits:**
    *   Improves a company's competitiveness by leveraging specialized external expertise.
    *   Allows the company to focus on its core business activities.
*   **Considerations for Outsourcing:** Should primarily be considered for non-core areas or processes of the company.
*   **Risks/Challenges:**
    *   **Lock-in:** Potential dependency on the outsourced vendor, which can be:
        *   **Work-related:** Difficulty in changing vendors due to embedded processes or knowledge.
        *   **Technology-related:** Dependence on specific technologies or systems controlled by the vendor.
    *   **Mitigation:** Regulatory measures are often needed to address and manage these lock-in risks.

---


---


## Pages 55-59


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT Business Adoption & Management: A Study Guide

This guide covers essential concepts for understanding and implementing IT business adoption processes, focusing on challenges, standard procedures, and methods.

---

### 1. Challenges in IT Business Adoption & Government Initiatives

**Key Problems:**
*   **High Costs:** Significant additional costs in public sector IT projects due to excessive work changes.
*   **Poor Planning:** Inadequate planning and design of information systems.
*   **Lack of Awareness/Expertise:** People often don't understand the benefits of IT systems or lack the necessary expertise.

**Government & Legislative Responses:**
*   **Mandatory Requirements:** Legislation now requires issuing a **Detailed RFP** (Request for Proposal – a document inviting proposals from potential suppliers) and implementing a **PMO Program** (Project Management Office – a department that defines and maintains standards for project management within an organization) for IT businesses.
*   **"Split Order Process" Initiative:**
    *   **Goal:** Prevent irresponsible work changes and eliminate unfair subcontracting practices.
    *   **How it Works:** Divides an IT project into two distinct phases:
        1.  **Planning/Design Phase:** Focuses on detailed requirement analysis, including:
            *   **ISP (Information Strategy Plan):** A long-term plan for an organization's information systems.
            *   **ISMP (Information System Master Plan):** A comprehensive plan for developing and implementing IT systems.
            *   **Basic Design (Logical Design):** Outlines the system's abstract structure and functionality.
        2.  **Deployment/Development Phase:** Focuses on implementation:
            *   **Detailed Design (Physical Design):** Specifies the concrete implementation details of the system.
            *   **System Development (Coding):** Writing the actual software code.
            *   **Testing:** Verifying the system works as intended.

**Benefits of the Split Order Process:**
*   Enables more meticulous and systematic planning/design.
*   Helps overcome the "invisibility of software" (difficulty in perceiving software changes).
*   Increases understanding of how frequent requirement changes impede IT projects.

---

### 2. Overview of IT Business Adoption

**Core Principles:**
*   **Strategic Alignment:** IT business adoption must align with a company’s overall IT strategy and plans.
*   **Adaptability:** Adoption methods and procedures should be tailored to the organization's size and external environment changes.
*   **Software is Key:** The core value of IT lies in software; successful software development is crucial for successful IT business adoption.

**Role of IT Outsourcing:**
*   **Benefits:** Improves company competitiveness by leveraging external expert resources, especially for non-core areas.
*   **Challenges:** Risk of work-related and technology-related "lock-in" (dependency on the external provider), which requires regulatory measures.

**IT Business Adoption Process Components:**
*   Uses a company's **ordering process** combined with the **SW Development Life Cycle (SDLC)** standard **ISO/IEC 12207**.
*   **Orderer (Acquirer):** Department or person responsible for issuing requirements.
*   **Developer (Supplier):** Company's internal IT department or an external expert/outsourcing partner.

---

### 3. The IT Business Ordering Process

**Purpose:** Defines the activities and tasks of the orderer (client) and guides the deployment of IT systems, software, or services. It aims to enhance success rates by providing clear communication and predictability.

**Key Stages:**
1.  **Plan Order:**
    *   **Activities:** Describe the system, define requirements & detailed specifications, create an ordering plan.
    *   **Outputs:** Ordering plan, status analysis, requirements specification.
2.  **RFP Preparation:**
    *   **Activities:** Document proposal requirements, describe constraints, establish supplier selection procedures & standards.
    *   **Outputs:** Request for Proposal (RFP), contracting terms & conditions, supplier evaluation criteria.
3.  **Proposal Evaluation & Contracting:**
    *   **Activities:** Issue tender notice, evaluate proposals, select supplier, negotiate, sign contract.
    *   **Outputs:** Tender notice, proposal evaluation results, contract.
4.  **Supplier Monitoring:**
    *   **Activities:** Review & approve project execution plan, inspect supplier's contract fulfillment.
    *   **Outputs:** Project execution plan, contract implementation inspection report.
5.  **Acquisition & Completion:**
    *   **Activities:** Select inspection manager, prepare acquisition plan, conduct inspection & acquisition test, finalize project acquisition & completion.
    *   **Outputs:** Acquisition plan, test results report, acquisition & project completion report.

---

### 4. ISO/IEC 12207: Software Adoption Lifecycle Standard

**What it Is:** An international standard that provides a standardized and systematic process for acquiring, supplying, developing, operating, and maintaining software.

**Structure:** Consists of three main processes, each with detailed procedures.
*   **Scope:** Defines *what* processes, activities, and tasks apply to software adoption/development, but *not* the specific naming, form, or content of outputs.
*   **Enhancement:** Can be used with **SPICE** (Software Process Improvement and Capability Determination) or **CMMI** (Capability Maturity Model Integration) to learn *how* to implement the processes effectively.

**A. Basic Lifecycle Processes:** (5 sub-processes focusing on core software activities)
1.  **Acquisition:** Defines activities of the software acquirer (client) for systems, outputs, and services.
2.  **Supply:** Defines activities of the software supplier (developer) to the acquirer.
3.  **Development:** Defines activities of the software developer and the development team.
4.  **Operation:** Defines activities of the operator providing operational services.
5.  **Maintenance:** Defines activities of the manager providing maintenance services.

**B. Support Lifecycle Processes:** (8 sub-processes that support other processes and contribute to quality/success)
1.  **Documentation:** Activities for recording outputs throughout the lifecycle.
2.  **Configuration Management:** Managing and tracking configuration details.
3.  **Quality Assurance:** Checking requirements fulfillment and plan compliance.
4.  **Verification:** Checking software output from the **developer's perspective**.
5.  **Validation:** Checking software output from the **user's perspective**.
6.  **Joint Review:** Comprehensive evaluation of output and progress.
7.  **Audit:** Examining software's compatibility with plans and contracts.
8.  **Problem Resolution:** Analyzing and resolving problems encountered in the basic lifecycle.

**C. Organization Lifecycle Processes:** (4 sub-processes configuring the underlying organizational structure, not specific to a project)
1.  **Management:** Basic management activities, including project management.
2.  **Infrastructure:** Defines the basic structure for the lifecycle process.
3.  **Improvement:** Activities for process improvement by stakeholders or the organization.
4.  **Training:** Activities for providing trained staff.

---

### 5. Tailoring Process

**Definition:** The process of optimizing a software development methodology or adoption procedure by eliminating activities and tasks that are not applicable or deemed unnecessary for a specific context.

**Purpose:** To adapt the adoption procedure, method, and outputs to accommodate internal and external requirements changes. It is particularly critical for unit-level projects to create the best software adoption environment.

**Important Considerations:**
*   **Reasons for SW Adoption:** Scope of work (e.g., finance, telecom), stakeholder needs, project goals, and direction.
*   **Timetable and Scope:** Overall scope of adoption, interfacing parts, project timeline, selection of methodology and outputs.
*   **Environment:** Regulations, laws, IT compliance, security measures, and internal/external environment response strategy.
*   **Application Technology:** Software application framework, base technology, and inspection of its utilization.

---

### 6. IT Business Adoption Methods

There are two primary methods for adopting an IT business:

**A. In-house Development:**
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   Uses internal personnel to set up and develop information systems.
    *   System is highly customized to internal requirements.
    *   Accumulates internal know-how.
*   **Pros:** High degree of control, tailored to specific user needs, builds internal expertise.
*   **Cons:** Higher adoption costs, success is not guaranteed, can be time-consuming.

**B. Package Purchase:**
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   Adopting a pre-existing, standardized software package.
    *   Benefits from know-how gained from previous implementations of the package.
    *   System has typically undergone many tests and verifications.
*   **Pros:** Reduces uncertainty about success, shorter adoption period, relatively low initial cost, built on advanced, standardized processes (improves work efficiency).
*   **Cons:** Less customizable, potential for higher maintenance costs in the long run, may not perfectly fit unique internal requirements.

---


---


## Pages 58-62


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text, designed for efficient study.

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide (Pages 58-62)

### I. Core IT Lifecycle Processes

These define the fundamental activities in software and IT services.

*   **Development:** Activities of software developers, defining software output and team tasks.
*   **Operation:** Activities of operators providing operational services.
*   **Maintenance:** Activities of maintenance managers providing maintenance services.

#### A. Support Lifecycle Process

*   **Purpose:** Supports other processes, contributing to output quality and success.
*   **Key Sub-processes (8 total):**
    *   **Documentation:** Recording outputs generated during the lifecycle.
    *   **Configuration Management:** Managing configurations and details.
    *   **Quality Assurance:** Checking fulfillment of requirements and plan compliance.
    *   **Verification:** Verifying software output from the developer's perspective.
    *   **Validation:** Checking software output from the user's perspective.
    *   **Joint Review:** Evaluating output and progress comprehensively.
    *   **Audit:** Examining software compatibility with plans and contracts.
    *   **Problem Resolution:** Analyzing and resolving problems found in the basic lifecycle.

#### B. Organization Lifecycle Process

*   **Purpose:** Configures the underlying organizational structure for business, independent of specific projects or contracts.
*   **Key Sub-processes (4 total):**
    *   **Management:** Basic management activities, including project management.
    *   **Infrastructure:** Defines the basic structure of the lifecycle process.
    *   **Improvement:** Activities carried out by stakeholders or participating organizations.
    *   **Training:** Activities for providing trained staff.

#### C. Tailoring Process

*   **Definition:** The process of eliminating activities and tasks that are not applicable or unnecessary in the lifecycle.
*   **Purpose:** Optimizing software adoption procedures, methods, and outputs, especially for unit-level projects, to accommodate changing requirements.
*   **Important Considerations:**
    *   **Reasons for SW adoption:** Work scope, stakeholder considerations, establish goals.
    *   **Timetable and Scope:** Project timeline, scope of adoption, interfacing parts, select methodology.
    *   **Internal/External Environment:** Regulations, laws, IT compliance, security measures, response strategy.
    *   **Application Technology:** SW application framework, base technology, utilization inspection.

### II. IT Business Adoption Methods

There are two primary methods for adopting an IT business, often used in a hybrid approach.

#### A. In-House Development

*   **Definition:** Companies use internal personnel to set up and develop information systems.
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   **Goal:** Actively reflects a company’s internal requirements.
    *   **Manpower:** Centered on own company manpower.
    *   **Dependency:** Know-how accumulates internally; user requirements are satisfied.
    *   **Advantages:**
        *   Full reflection of user needs.
        *   Accumulates internal know-how.
        *   Company information/processes can be guarded.
        *   Scope of adoption is easily adjusted.
    *   **Disadvantages:**
        *   Higher adoption costs.
        *   Success not guaranteed.
        *   Deployment costs are relatively high.
        *   Scope of work improvements is relatively narrow.

#### B. Package Purchase

*   **Definition:** Adopting a pre-developed system (software package).
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   **Goal:** Uses advanced processes and cases.
    *   **Manpower:** Uses experts on the package.
    *   **Dependency:** Risk of technology dependence.
    *   **Advantages:**
        *   Easy absorption of industry know-how.
        *   System has undergone many tests, reducing uncertainty.
        *   Short adoption period.
        *   Relatively low initial cost.
        *   Work processes can be innovated.
        *   Advanced management processes can be integrated.
    *   **Disadvantages:**
        *   Maintenance costs tend to increase.
        *   Company's confidential information could be leaked.
        *   Company's internal processes may need to be altered to meet package requirements.

#### C. Hybrid Approach

*   **Trend:** Companies increasingly use a hybrid approach.
*   **Method:** In-house development for the overall approach, combined with packaged products for specific component technologies.
*   **Benefits:** Reduces costs and risks.

### III. IT Business Outsourcing Service

#### A. Overview

*   **Purpose:** To respond quickly to changing environments, allowing companies to focus on core competencies.
*   **Strategy:**
    *   **In-house:** For strategic areas or processes where the company has a competitive edge.
    *   **Outsource:** For non-strategic or weak areas, subcontracting work to external experts or third-party companies.
*   **Definition:** Subcontracting IT resources, IT management, and IT operations to external providers.

#### B. Adoption Process

1.  **Preparation/Identification:** Identify core competencies and select tasks to be outsourced.
2.  **Select Target Tasks:** Choose specific tasks for outsourcing.
3.  **Select Outsourcing Company:** Choose the best vendor.
4.  **Negotiations & Contracting:** Sign a contract; crucial to agree on **Service Level Index (SLI)** management.
5.  **Contract Control Phase:** Manage and improve performance, transfer technology, build experience database.
6.  **Transition & Implementation:** Realistic management and clear handover.

#### C. Forms of Outsourcing

*   **Total Outsourcing:**
    *   **Description:** Entire IT functionality outsourced to a single vendor.
    *   **Pros:** Clear accountability, improved efficiency.
    *   **Cons:** Lack of competition can lead to monopolistic issues.
*   **Selective Outsourcing:**
    *   **Description:** Selected functions or job units outsourced to multiple vendors.
    *   **Pros:** Price and quality improvements due to vendor competition.
    *   **Cons:** Accountability issues when problems occur, communication difficulties for exact requirements.
*   **IT Subsidiary Company Outsourcing:**
    *   **Description:** IT functionality outsourced to a subsidiary company specializing in IT.
    *   **Pros:** Improved communication and unity among employees.
    *   **Cons:** Increased associated costs, risk to parent company if subsidiary is not profitable.
*   **Co-Sourcing:**
    *   **Description:** IT planning, strategy, and service activities are separated.
    *   **Pros:** Advantages in rapidly evolving environments, addresses some total outsourcing problems.
    *   **Cons:** Coordination may be needed if there's a gap between strategy and performance.

#### D. Considerations for Adopting Outsourcing

*   **Continuous Oversight:** Requires continuous monitoring of the vendor using standards like **eSCM** (e-Sourcing Capability Model) and **ISO/IEC 20000** (IT Service Management).
*   **Security & Quality:** Establish a security system to prevent information leaks; continuously monitor and manage service levels for optimal quality.
*   **Business Process Outsourcing (BPO):** If outsourcing a whole or part of a business process (not just a specific job category), BPO should be adopted.

#### E. Issues and Considerations (Summary Table)

| Category    | Problems                                                               | Considerations                                                                     |
| :---------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Management** | - Weak control over subcontractors <br/> - Dependency on vendor <br/> - Difficulty in accumulating know-how <br/> - Inter-company disputes <br/> - Increased management costs | - Set up control system using **IT Governance** <br/> - Evaluate from **BSC** (Balanced Scorecard) viewpoint <br/> - Set up evaluation system using standards (eSCM, ISO20000) |
| **Contracts** | - Unclear scope and R&R (Roles & Responsibilities) <br/> - Uncertainty over estimated costs <br/> - Difficulty in awarding bonus points and imposing sanctions | - **SLA** (Service Level Agreement) for level agreement and management <br/> - Set up plan for change management <br/> - Adopt systematic method for cost estimation |
| **Operations** | - Security concerns over corporate information <br/> - Insufficient fulfillment of requirements | - Set up security training program and control system <br/> - Set up technology transfer process <br/> - Set up service quality management |

---
