## Pages 61-65


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide derived from the provided text:

---

## IT BUSINESS OUTSOURCING & PROCESS INNOVATION: Learning Guide

### Section 1: IT Business Outsourcing

#### A. Adoption Process
When a company decides to outsource IT functions, the process typically involves these phases:

1.  **Preparation Phase:**
    *   Identify your company's core competencies.
    *   Select specific IT tasks or operations to be outsourced.
2.  **Selection Phase:**
    *   Choose the best outsourcing vendor/company.
3.  **Negotiation & Contracting Phase:**
    *   Negotiate terms and sign a contract.
    *   **Crucial Point:** Achieve a clear agreement with the vendor on how **Service Level Indicators (SLIs)** will be managed.
4.  **Control Phase:**
    *   Manage the contract and oversee performance.
    *   Continuously improve performance.
5.  **Transition & Implementation Phase:**
    *   Transfer necessary technology and build experience.
    *   Ensure clear handover management for a smooth transition.

#### B. Forms of IT Business Outsourcing
IT outsourcing can take four main forms, each with its own characteristics:

1.  **Total Outsourcing**
    *   **Description:** The entire IT functionality is handed over to a single vendor.
    *   **Pros:** Clear accountability, improved job handling efficiency.
    *   **Cons:** Lack of competition can lead to monopolistic issues.
2.  **Selective Outsourcing**
    *   **Description:** Specific functions or job units are subcontracted to multiple vendors.
    *   **Pros:** Competition among vendors can improve price and quality.
    *   **Cons:** Potential accountability issues if problems arise, difficulties communicating exact requirements to multiple vendors.
3.  **IT Subsidiary Company Outsourcing**
    *   **Description:** IT functionality is outsourced to a subsidiary company established specifically for IT services.
    *   **Pros:** Improved communication and unity due to a shared sense of solidarity among employees.
    *   **Cons:** Increased associated costs, risk to the parent company if the subsidiary is not profitable.
4.  **Co-Sourcing**
    *   **Description:** IT planning, strategy, and service activities are separated, often with the client and vendor sharing responsibilities.
    *   **Pros:** Advantages in rapidly evolving environments, can partially address issues of total outsourcing.
    *   **Cons:** May require coordination if there's a gap between strategy and performance.

#### C. Considerations When Adopting Outsourcing
Companies face various challenges during IT outsourcing. Key considerations include:

1.  **General Oversight:**
    *   **Continuous Oversight:** Essential to monitor the outsource vendor using standards like **eSCM** (e-Sourcing Capability Model) and **ISO/IEC 20000** (IT Service Management standard).
    *   **Security:** Establish robust security systems to prevent corporate information leakage.
    *   **Service Quality:** Continuously monitor and manage service levels to ensure optimal quality.
    *   **BPO (Business Process Outsourcing):** If an entire business process (or a significant part) is outsourced, adopt BPO.

2.  **Specific Issues & Solutions (Table Summary):**

| Category    | Common Problems                                        | Key Considerations/Solutions                                                                                                        |
| :---------- | :----------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Management** | Weak control over subcontractors, increased vendor dependency, inter-company disputes, higher management costs. | Set up a control system using IT governance. Evaluate from a Balanced Scorecard (BSC) viewpoint. Use evaluation systems like eSCM/ISO20000. |
| **Contracts** | Unclear scope and Roles & Responsibilities (R&R), uncertain estimated costs, difficulty awarding bonuses/sanctions. | Use **Service Level Agreements (SLA)** for clear level agreement and management. Plan for change management. Adopt systematic cost estimation methods. |
| **Operations** | Security concerns for corporate information, difficulty accumulating internal know-how, insufficient fulfillment of requirements. | Implement a security training program and a security control system. Establish a technology transfer process. Set up a service quality system. |

---

### Section 2: Recent Trends & Process Improvement

#### A. Optimizing IT Business Processes
*   **Goal:** Companies must optimize IT business processes to respond quickly to environmental changes.
*   **Evolution:** Processes become more optimized over time, with changes in the business environment acting as a key factor.
*   **Identifying Issues:** Continuous monitoring of process **bottlenecks** is crucial for improvement.
*   **Solutions:** Companies use **BPR (Business Process Reengineering)** or **PI (Process Innovation)** to rectify bottleneck issues.

#### B. The Human Element in Process Innovation
*   **Challenge:** The most challenging aspect of BPR/PI is gaining the support and conviction of a company's own employees.
*   **Reason:** Employees are both the operators of processes and the subjects of any innovations.
*   **Success Factors:**
    *   Ceaseless persuasion.
    *   Creating an atmosphere where employees feel they can share in the company's growth.

#### C. Learning Objectives
By studying this material, you should be able to:
1.  Explain the constituent elements of the IT business process.
2.  Explain various methods of improving the IT business process.

#### D. Keywords
*   **BPM:** Business Process Management
*   **BAM:** Business Activity Monitoring
*   **BRE:** Business Rule Engine
*   **ILM:** Information Lifecycle Management
*   **IRM:** Information Rights Management
*   **BPR:** Business Process Reengineering (fundamental rethinking and radical redesign of business processes to achieve dramatic improvements)
*   **PI:** Process Innovation (often used interchangeably with BPR or as a broader term for significant process improvement)
*   **6 Sigma:** A set of techniques and tools for process improvement.
*   **Trees:** (Context unclear, but likely refers to decision trees or problem-solving methodologies)
*   **Servqual:** A service quality measurement scale.
*   **SPC:** Statistical Process Control

---

### Section 3: Case Studies in Process Innovation

#### A. BPR Case Study: Starbucks
**Context:** In 2008, Starbucks faced a significant economic downturn and a more than 50% drop in sales.

**BPR Initiatives (Transformation Strategy):**
1.  **Leveraging Technology:** Integrated wireless technology and mobile digital platforms into its business.
2.  **Customer-Centric Innovations:**
    *   Customer analysis showed 1/3 of customers used smartphones.
    *   Introduced a smartphone app-based payment system (prepaid/rechargeable cards).
    *   Created "Starbucks Digital Network" with Yahoo, offering free Wi-Fi, Wall Street Journal articles, and iTunes music downloads.
3.  **Internal Process Efficiency (Lean Manufacturing Principles):**
    *   Formed a "Lean Team" to benchmark Toyota's lean manufacturing methods.
    *   Redesigned barista workstations to eliminate unnecessary bending.
    *   Minimized customer waiting times and reduced drink preparation time.
4.  **Employee Work Environment:**
    *   Built a smart work environment with wireless technology to maximize employee efficiency.
    *   Enabled employees to work from any store nationwide, increasing regional managers' store visit times by ~25%.

**Results:**
*   Significant cost savings through new operating methods and customer services.
*   Starbucks recovered its profitability and maintained growth.

#### B. PI Case Study: Korea Workers’ Compensation & Welfare Service (COMWEL)
**Context:** From 2010-2011, COMWEL undertook a large-scale Process Innovation (PI) project to build an advanced administration system.

**Keys to PI Success (for COMWEL and generally):**
*   **Company-Wide Consensus:** PI requires agreement from top management to working-level staff.
*   **Best Practices:** Application and full internalization of best practices within the organization.
*   **Systematic Management:** COMWEL's success became a benchmark for other public institutions, despite their conservative nature.

**Motivation:**
*   To achieve "job efficiencies through process innovation."
*   To improve the quality of public services despite limited human resources.

**COMWEL's PI Process:**
1.  **Internal Analysis:** Began with internal discussions to identify areas most in need of improvement.
2.  **Process Diagnosis:** Conducted "AS-IS" (current state) process diagnosis consulting.
3.  **Selection:** Studied end-to-end processes for each job and selected those requiring PI.
4.  **Requirements Gathering:** Identified and extracted requirements from the working level.
5.  **System Implementation:** Used gathered information to set up:
    *   **BPM (Business Process Management):** For managing business processes.
    *   **PKMS (Process-based Knowledge Management System):** For managing knowledge related to processes.
    *   **EID (Enterprise Information Display) system:** For displaying enterprise information.
6.  **Prioritization & Systemization:** Systemized 25 out of 50 core processes that were expected to yield the greatest impact.
7.  **Continuous Improvement Cycle:** PI was continuously performed through a framework of: Process Establishment → Monitoring → Improvement Activities → Process Establishment.

**Benefits/Results:**
*   **Improved Public Service:** Eliminated unnecessary procedures and simplified complex ones.
*   **Enhanced Information Access:** When users search for data, the system provides increasingly relevant information as data accumulates.
*   **Better Management:** Management could quickly identify business unit plans and core information, allowing for rapid modification of strategies and reduction of risks.

---

## Pages 64-68


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text.

---

## IT Business and Ethics: A Learning Guide

This guide focuses on understanding IT business processes, their components, and how they drive innovation and competitiveness.

---

### 1. Case Study: Starbucks' IT-Driven Transformation (Page 64)

**Context:** Starbucks, a global coffee chain, faced a significant sales drop (>50%) during the 2008 economic downturn. They leveraged IT to transform their business.

**Key Strategies & Innovations:**

*   **Customer Analysis:** Identified that over 1/3 of customers were smartphone users.
*   **Mobile Digital Platform Integration:**
    *   **Smartphone App-Based Payment:** Customers could pay using prepaid or rechargeable cards via a mobile app.
    *   **Starbucks Digital Network (with Yahoo):** Offered free WiFi, free Wall Street Journal articles, and free iTunes downloads to customers in stores.
*   **Internal Business Process Efficiency:**
    *   **Lean Team:** Formed to benchmark Toyota's "lean manufacturing" methods.
    *   **Operational Improvements:** Minimized barista bending, reduced coffee waiting times, and shortened drink preparation times.
    *   **Smart Work Environment:** Utilized wireless technology to maximize employee efficiency.
        *   Employees could work from any store nationwide.
        *   Increased regional manager store visiting times by ~25%.
*   **Outcome:** Recovered profitability and sustained growth by using IT to create new customer services and optimize operations.

---

### 2. Case Study: COMWEL's Process Innovation (PI) (Page 65)

**Context:** The Korea Workers’ Compensation & Welfare Service (COMWEL) successfully implemented a large-scale Process Innovation (PI) project to enhance public services.

**What is Process Innovation (PI)?**
*   A comprehensive approach to improving business processes.
*   **Requires:** Company-wide consensus (from top management to staff), application of best practices, and full internalization within the organization.
*   **Challenge:** Often difficult for conservative public institutions to implement.

**COMWEL's PI Goals & Approach:**
*   **Goal:** Improve public service quality despite limited human resources.
*   **Process:**
    1.  **Internal Discussions:** Identified areas most needing improvement.
    2.  **AS-IS Process Diagnosis:** Analyzed existing processes.
    3.  **End-to-End Job Study:** Examined entire workflows for each job.
    4.  **Process Selection:** Chose processes for PI implementation.
    5.  **Requirements Gathering:** Identified needs at the working level.
    6.  **System Implementation:** Set up:
        *   **BPM (Business Process Management):** For managing business processes.
        *   **PKMS (Process-Based Knowledge Management System):** For managing process-related knowledge.
        *   **EID (Enterprise Information Display) system:** For displaying enterprise information.
    7.  **Systematization:** Completed for 25 out of 50 core processes with the highest expected impact.
    8.  **Focus:** Eliminated unnecessary procedures and simplified complex ones to improve public service.
*   **Continuous Improvement Framework:** Process establishment → Monitoring → Improvement activities → Process establishment.

**Benefits of COMWEL's PI:**
*   **Improved User Experience:** System provides more relevant information to user queries (relevancy increases with data).
*   **Enhanced Management:** Reduced risks by enabling quick modification of management strategies and providing an "at-a-glance" view of business plans and key information across all units.

---

### 3. Summary of Lessons Learned & Core Elements (Page 66)

#### 3.1. What are IT Business Processes?
*   A combination of tools and procedures for companies to conduct their activities.
*   **Key components:** People, organizations, and job processes.
*   **Importance:** Tied to core enterprise management and crucial for competitiveness.

#### 3.2. Key IT Business Process Tools:
*   **BPM (Business Process Management):** Manages all business processes.
*   **BAM (Business Activity Monitoring):** Monitors processes to identify bottlenecks and issues.
*   **BRE (Business Rule Engine):** Manages the specific rules that govern business process tasks.
*   **BPR/PI (Business Process Reengineering / Process Innovation):** Tools for radical or incremental innovation and improvement of processes.
*   **Outcome:** These tools interact dynamically, leading to continuous process improvements and enhancing a company's ability to respond quickly to internal and external changes.

#### 3.3. Component Elements for IT Business Process Execution:

*   **A. Business Model:**
    *   **Definition:** A strategic blueprint guiding an organization's structure, processes, and systems to create value.
    *   **Core Areas:** Customers, order fulfillment, infrastructure, and business feasibility analysis.

*   **B. Business Execution:**
    *   **Goal:** Achieve agility in a dynamic business environment.
    *   **Requirements:**
        *   Integrated core business processes across departments for flexibility.
        *   Strong underlying assets: core competencies, finance, human resources.
        *   Infrastructure for rapid decision-making.
        *   Basic operational elements: people, job systems, and business management tools.

*   **C. People and Organization:**
    *   **People:** Individuals participating as members.
    *   **Organization:** A consciously created system by two or more people. It divides, consolidates, and connects jobs.
    *   **Purpose:** To fulfill common objectives (communication, collaboration) while maintaining internal/external balance, effectiveness, and efficiency.
    *   **Function:** Allocates human resources by dividing functions and responsibilities to achieve agreed-upon objectives effectively.

---

### 4. Business Process Details & Examples (Page 67-68)

#### 4.1. Understanding the Business Process

*   **Enterprise:** A formal organization aiming for profit by selling goods/services at prices higher than production costs.
*   **Business Functions:** Interrelated activities defined by specific business rules.
*   **Business Rules:** Determine *when, how, in what order,* and *which rules* apply to business activities. They significantly influence an organization's management, performance, and value creation.
*   **Business Process:** The step-by-step method and work involved in organizing tasks within an enterprise.

#### 4.2. Common Business Processes by Enterprise Function (Examples):

| Enterprise Function       | Business Processes (Examples)                                                               |
| :------------------------ | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Manufacturing & Production** | Product assembly, Quality inspections, Raw material list production, Ordering/procurement, Production planning, BOM management |
| **Sales & Marketing**     | Customer identification, Product sales, Customer product management, Distribution, Cost estimation, Prepayment/borrowing |
| **Finance/Accounting**    | Issuance of bonds, Payment settlement, Process payment, Tax invoice issuance, Financial statement production, Cost management |
| **HR Management**         | Recruitment, Appointment, Tardiness/absenteeism management, Employee welfare, Performance evaluation, Wage management |

#### 4.3. Example of an IT Business Process: Multifunctional Printer Repair Service (Page 67-68)

This example illustrates a typical service process flow, involving multiple departments and actions.

1.  **Customer Request:** Customer experiences a printer problem and contacts the customer center.
2.  **Service Assignment:** Customer center determines if a site visit is needed and assigns service personnel.
3.  **Scheduling Visit:** Service personnel contacts the customer, clarifies symptoms, and schedules a visit.
4.  **On-site Repair:** Service personnel visits, examines, and repairs the printer.
5.  **Completion & Confirmation:** Customer signs to confirm repair completion.
6.  **Billing & Revenue (for paid repairs):**
    *   Customer is billed for repairs, generating revenue for the company.
    *   Sales amount and service fee are settled.
    *   A tax invoice is issued and delivered to the customer.
    *   Customer makes the payment.
7.  **Accounting:** Received payment is deposited, and accounts receivable are credited.

**Outcomes of this Process:**
*   Provides essential customer services.
*   Generates profits for the enterprise.

**Job Domains Involved:** Service, Accounting, Materials, and Revenue (Sales).

**Key Takeaway:** Most business processes require continuous improvement and flexible adaptation to changes in the business environment. Organizations must constantly identify and eliminate waste and bottlenecks to ensure quick job processing.

---


---

Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text, designed for efficient study.

---

# Learning Guide: Business Processes and IT Management

## 1. Business Processes: The Foundation of an Enterprise

*   **Enterprise Definition:** A formal organization focused on making profits by selling goods or services for more than their production costs.
*   **Enterprise as Functions:** Can be seen as a collection of interconnected business activities (functions) governed by **business rules** to achieve specific objectives.
    *   **Business Rules:** Dictate *when, how, in what order, and which* actions apply. They heavily influence an organization's management, performance, and value creation.
*   **Business Process Definition:** The documented method and organization of work within an enterprise.

### Common Business Processes by Function:

| Function                      | Key Business Processes                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| :---------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Manufacturing & Production** | Product assembly, quality inspections, raw material list production, ordering & procurement management, production planning management, Bill of Materials (BOM) management.                                          |
| **Sales & Marketing**         | Customer identification, customer product management, product sales, distribution management.                                                                                                                         |
| **Finance/Accounting**        | Cost estimation, prepayment/borrowing management, issuance of bonds, settlement of payment, process payment, tax invoice issuance, production of financial statements, cost management.                                |
| **HR Management**             | Recruitment, appointment, tardiness & absenteeism management, employee welfare management, performance evaluation, wage management.                                                                                       |

### Example: An IT Business Service Process (Printer Repair)

This shows a typical service lifecycle:
1.  **Customer Problem:** A customer's printer isn't working.
2.  **Service Request:** Customer contacts the customer center for repair.
3.  **Personnel Assignment:** If an on-site visit is needed, the center assigns service personnel.
4.  **Visit Scheduling:** Personnel contacts the customer to understand symptoms and arrange a visit time.
5.  **Repair & Confirmation:** Personnel visits, diagnoses, repairs the printer, and gets the customer's signature as confirmation.
6.  **Billing & Payment:**
    *   For paid repairs, the customer is billed, creating revenue for the company.
    *   A tax invoice is issued and sent to the customer.
    *   The customer pays, and the payment is processed (crediting accounts receivable).
*   **Outcomes:** This process enables customer service and generates profits.
*   **Involved Departments:** Service, Accounting, Materials, and Revenue (Sales).
*   **Key Principle:** Business processes need continuous improvement and flexibility to adapt to changing environments. Waste and bottlenecks must be constantly identified and addressed.

---

## 2. Methods of Executing IT Business Processes

### A) IT Business Process Management (BPM)

*   **Overview:** A core technique for optimizing and automating business processes within IT.
    *   **Related Concepts:**
        *   **BAM (Business Activity Monitoring):** Used to identify and manage bottlenecks.
        *   **BRE (Business Rule Engine):** Manages and executes business rules and process flows.
*   **BPM Definition:** The consolidated management, optimization, and automation of the flow of people, information, resources, and tasks in IT business processes. It's vital for business performance and requires a logical, structured approach that can actively respond to changes.

#### BPM Design Stages:

1.  **Process Definition:** Define core processes, identify rules, analyze processes, and establish measurement methods.
2.  **Process Execution, Operation:** Run and manage processes according to guidelines, ensuring seamless connections (person-to-person, person-to-system, system-to-system).
3.  **Monitoring Control:** Track job completion times, performance quality, and execution progress in real-time. Maintain records of monitoring.
4.  **Process Improvement:** Identify and compare Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) for process performance. Conduct simulations to find improvements, and continuously repeat the execution and improvement cycle.

### B) Business Activity Monitoring (BAM)

*   **Definition:** A technique to optimize IT business processes. It monitors processes in real-time to detect bottlenecks and identify risk factors early.
*   **Function:** Leverages extended **Business Intelligence (BI)** techniques for real-time analysis to monitor and manage process flow.

#### BAM Base Technologies:

*   **Business Intelligence (BI):** Analyzes key business process indicators (KPIs).
*   **Data Warehouse:** Collects and analyzes statistical data to identify risks in business processes.
*   **BPM (Business Process Management):** Analyzes business events and guides process improvements.
*   **System Infrastructure:** Manages the network and integrated system; used for collecting, analyzing, visualizing data, and processing events.

### C) Business Rule Engine (BRE)

*   **Definition:** A technique for effectively managing, automating, and optimizing processes by formalizing complex business rules and process flows.
*   **Need:** Essential due to the increasing volume and complexity of information in IT business processes. Rule-based management is needed for service improvements and cost savings.
*   **Benefits:** Helps enterprises proactively manage changes and reduce operating costs for business processes.

#### BRE Component Elements:

*   **Rule Manager:** Develops and manages business rules, handles the process lifecycle, and manages the rule repository.
*   **Rule Service:** Acts as a server for the rule engine, providing interfaces between processes, distributing rules, and offering rule services.
*   **Rule Monitoring:** Supports process improvement, rule performance tuning, analysis, and statistical functions.
*   **Rule Repository:** A storage location for all business rules.

---

## 3. IT Business Process Information Management

*   **Context:** As IT business processes become more complex and require rapid adaptation to changes, systematic management of the data they generate is increasingly important.
*   **Methods:** Data generated by IT business processes can be managed using **Information Life Cycle Management (ILM)** or **Information Resource Management (IRM)**.

### A) Information Life Cycle Management (ILM)

*   **Definition:** A series of processes for categorizing and managing storage media based on the changing value of data throughout its entire life cycle.
*   **Purpose:** To reduce data management costs and systematically manage data, especially as data volume grows and its value changes over time.

#### ILM Constituent Elements:

1.  **Management Policies Category:**
    *   **IT Governance:** Provides guidelines for data generation, storage, and disposal.
    *   **IT Compliance:** Ensures adherence to legal, regulatory, and policy standards.
    *   **Enterprise Data Management Policy:** Specific policies related to the organization's Enterprise Architecture (EA) and Data Architecture (DA) systems and data operations.
2.  **Technology Elements Category:**
    *   **1st Storage:** For high-utilization, high-value data; uses high-performance, expensive storage solutions.
    *   **2nd Storage:** For lower-utilization, lower-value data; uses low-performance, low-priced storage solutions.
    *   **Data Archiving:** Technology that periodically archives data and processes it automatically.
    *   **Backup:** Storing data separately using tape libraries or affordable disks, following a defined backup policy.

### B) Information Resource Management (IRM)

*   **Definition:** The efficient and integrated management of all IT resources.
*   **Purpose:** To prevent redundant investments in IT resources and increase the Return on Investment (ROI).
*   **Scope:** Manages a wide range of IT resources, including human resources, IT equipment, budgets, and IT outputs.

---


---


## Pages 70-74


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT Business Monitoring, Management, and Improvement Techniques

This guide covers key concepts related to monitoring, managing, and improving IT business processes.

---

### **Section 1: IT Business Monitoring & Management**

#### **1.1 Business Activity Monitoring (BAM)**

*   **What it is:** A technique that monitors business processes in real-time to identify bottlenecks and recognize risks in advance.
*   **Purpose:** Uses advanced business intelligence (BI) for real-time analysis and manages process flow for Business Process Monitoring (BPM).
*   **Base Technologies:**
    *   **Business Intelligence (BI):** Analyzes key business process indicators.
    *   **Data Warehouse:** Collects and analyzes statistical data to identify risks.
    *   **Business Process Management (BPM):** Analyzes business events and suggests process improvements.
    *   **System Infrastructure:** Manages the network and integrated system, collects, analyzes, and visualizes data and events.

#### **1.2 Business Rule Engine (BRE)**

*   **What it is:** A technique to manage, automate, and optimize processes by formalizing complex business rules and process flows.
*   **Why it's needed:** Addresses the increasing volume of information and complexity of process flows, enabling rule-based management.
*   **Benefits:** Helps enterprises proactively manage changes, reduce operating costs, and improve services.
*   **Component Elements:**
    *   **Rule Manager:** Develops and manages business rules, handles the process lifecycle, and manages the rule repository.
    *   **Rule Service:** Acts as a server for the rule engine, provides interfaces between processes, and distributes implemented rules.
    *   **Rule Monitoring:** Supports process improvement, performance tuning, and provides analysis/statistical functions.
    *   **Rule Repository:** A storage location for business rules.

---

### **Section 2: IT Business Process Information Management**

As IT business processes become more complex and respond rapidly to changes, systematized data management is crucial. This is achieved through ILM or IRM.

#### **2.1 Information Life Cycle Management (ILM)**

*   **What it is:** A series of processes for managing storage media by separating data based on its changing value throughout its life cycle.
*   **Purpose:** To reduce data management costs and systematically manage data as its volume increases but its value changes over time.
*   **Constituent Elements:**
    *   **Management Policies:**
        *   **IT Governance:** Provides guidelines for data generation, storage, and disposal.
        *   **IT Compliance:** Ensures adherence to legal, regulatory, and policy standards.
        *   **Enterprise Data Management Policy:** Defines data operation policies, often related to Enterprise Architecture (EA).
    *   **Technology Elements:**
        *   **1st Storage:** High-performance, expensive storage for high-utilization, frequently accessed data.
        *   **2nd Storage:** Lower-performance, less expensive storage for data with relatively low utilization and value.
        *   **Data Archiving:** Technology for periodic, automatic archiving of data.
        *   **Backup:** Separate storage (e.g., tape library, affordable disk) for data protection.

#### **2.2 Information Resource Management (IRM)**

*   **What it is:** The efficient and integrated management of all IT resources.
*   **Goals:**
    *   Prevent redundant IT investments.
    *   Increase returns on IT investments (ROI).
    *   Manage diverse IT resources, including human resources, equipment, budgets, and outputs.
*   **Why it's needed:** Addresses the growing complexity and scale of enterprise information systems and the need for systematized management.
*   **Function:** Provides a common standard and management system for all informatization procedures (planning, development, performance evaluation).
*   **Relationship with Enterprise Architecture (EA):** IRM provides the framework for information resources to EA, while EA gives IRM guidelines for enterprise resource schemes. They complement each other.
*   **IRM Process for EA (Key Activities & Outputs):**
    *   **Information Resource Planning:** Develop strategies and objectives.
        *   *Output:* Information resource management plan.
    *   **Set up Organization Structure:** Form teams and committees, appoint chief architect.
        *   *Output:* Team organization chart, work assignment chart.
    *   **Set up Architecture:** Define AS-IS (current state) and To-BE (future state) architectures, plan conversion.
        *   *Output:* Architecture analysis report, conversion plan.
    *   **Utilize Architecture:** Implement investment plans, develop and use information resources.
        *   *Output:* Utilization guidelines.
    *   **Architecture Maintenance:** Continuously update and manage the architecture, evaluate its link to information resources.
        *   *Output:* Report on information resource utilization.
    *   **Evaluation of Information Resource Management:** Assess performance, develop improvement plans.
        *   *Output:* Evaluation report.

---

### **Section 3: IT Business Process Improvement Techniques**

Enterprises constantly seek to improve business processes for competitiveness, efficiency, and developing new business models.

#### **3.1 Business Process Reengineering (BPR)**

*   **Origin:** Introduced by Professor Michael Hammer in 1990 to address declining competitiveness by rethinking fundamental business processes.
*   **Concept:** A technique for **fundamentally redesigning business processes** to achieve **radical improvements** in performance indicators like cost, quality, service, and speed.
*   **Four Attributes of BPR:**
    *   **Basic:** Addresses core problems, questions the fundamental purpose of tasks, and identifies inefficiencies.
    *   **Zero Base:** Designs entirely new ways of performing tasks by abandoning existing procedures.
    *   **Dramatic Improvement:** Aims for absolute, radical innovation, not gradual enhancements.
    *   **Process:** Focuses on improving task processes, not just jobs, workers, or organizational structures, to internalize business values.
*   **Implementation Procedure:**
    1.  **Set Corporate Objectives:** Define vision and redesign goals (e.g., reduce costs, save time, improve quality).
    2.  **Select Target Process:** Identify and prioritize key processes for redesign.
    3.  **Understand Current Process:** Analyze how the selected process currently operates and evaluate its performance.
    4.  **Select Process Goals:** Link corporate vision to specific improvement goals for the process.
    5.  **Design Improved Process:** Create a new process design to achieve the selected goals, and pilot a prototype.
    6.  **Develop Change Model:** Address potential resistance from employees or technological issues.
    7.  **Implement:** Transition from the old process to the new, improved one, including strategies for risk reduction.
    8.  **Operate:** Run the new prototype and establish quality control management.

#### **3.2 Process Innovation (PI)**

*   **Origin:** Introduced by David Port in 1993.
*   **Concept:** Activity focused on improving the business environment to maximize corporate value by eliminating unnecessary elements (in processes, organization, and IT) and rebuilding effective business processes.
*   **BPR vs. PI:**
    *   Similar to BPR but places **greater emphasis on the integration of information technology**.
    *   Aims to build a structure that can respond to changes by making processes more customer-centric, improving information, logistics, and value flows.
    *   Internationally, BPR is widely used; in South Korea, PI gained popularity, often used in a broader sense than BPR (e.g., with ERP deployments).
*   **Example of PI Implementation Procedure (integrates IT):**
    1.  **AS-IS Analysis:** Analyze current systems, processes, and human resources; set Critical Success Factors (CSFs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs).
    2.  **PI To-BE Process Design:** Design the future-state process, focusing on achieving the defined CSFs and KPIs.
    3.  **Organization/Strategy (Information Strategy Plan - ISP):** Establish IT strategies aligned with business goals; develop mid-term and long-term information system plans and an IT architecture roadmap.
    4.  **Implementation (Detailed Plan):** Create a detailed plan for establishing the integrated information system.
    5.  **Deployment:** Step-by-step deployment of the integrated information system (e.g., ERP, CRM).

---

## Pages 73-77


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: Business & IT Process Improvement Concepts

This guide covers Business Process Reengineering (BPR), Process Innovation (PI), Six Sigma, and TRIZ.

---

### A) Understanding Business Process Reengineering (BPR)

**1. Concept of BPR**
*   **Origin:** Introduced by Professor Michael Hammer (MIT, 1990) to address declining U.S. product competitiveness (price and quality) by fixing issues in overall business processes.
*   **Definition:** A technique for fundamentally redesigning business processes to achieve radical improvements in performance indicators like cost, quality, service, and speed.
*   **Four Attributes of BPR:**
    *   **Basic:** Addresses fundamental problems and inefficiencies in an enterprise's operations.
    *   **Zero Base:** Designs new ways of performing tasks by abandoning existing procedures. It's about starting fresh, not improving existing methods.
    *   **Dramatic Improvement:** Aims for radical, not gradual, improvements. Used when absolute innovation is needed.
    *   **Process:** Focuses on task processes, not specific jobs, workers, or organizational structures, to internalize processes that drive business value.

**2. BPR Implementation Procedure**
1.  **Set Corporate Objectives:** Establish goals aligned with the corporate vision (e.g., reduce costs, save time, improve quality).
2.  **Select Target Process:** Identify key processes, define their scope, and prioritize them through strategic evaluation.
3.  **Understand Current Process:** Analyze how the selected process currently operates and evaluate its performance level.
4.  **Select Process Goals:** Choose specific improvement goals for the process, linking them to the corporate vision.
5.  **Design Improved Process:** Create a new process to achieve the selected goals, and pilot a prototype.
6.  **Develop Change Model:** Address potential resistance (company, technology) and plan the transition.
7.  **Implement:** Transition from the current process to the improved one, implementing risk reduction strategies.
8.  **Operate:** Run the new prototype and transition to ongoing quality control management.

---

### B) Understanding Process Innovation (PI)

**1. Concept of PI**
*   **Definition:** Activity aimed at improving the business environment to maximize corporate value by eliminating unnecessary elements and rebuilding effective business processes.
*   **Origin:** Introduced by David Port (1993) in his paper "Process Innovation."
*   **Relationship to BPR:** Similar to BPR, but with a **greater emphasis on the integration of information technology (IT)**.
*   **Objective:** Build a customer-centric structure that can respond to changes in the business environment by improving current processes, information flow, logistics, and values.
*   **Regional Context:** While BPR is widely used internationally, PI gained popularity in South Korea (e.g., Samsung Electronics, POSCO's ERP adoption) and is used in a broader sense there.

**2. PI Implementation Procedure (with IT integration)**
*   PI is often implemented with IT deployment, typically through **Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP)** or Customer Relationship Management (CRM) integration.
*   **Typical Flow:**
    1.  Improve and redesign enterprise systems, processes, and workforce.
    2.  Establish an informatization (IT implementation) plan based on improved systems/processes.
    3.  Deploy a system (e.g., ERP, CRM) capable of executing the plan.
*   **Detailed Steps (as per Fig. 25):**
    *   **Analysis:** Analyze AS-IS (current) processes, systems, and human resources. Set Critical Success Factors (CSF) and Key Performance Indicators (KPI).
    *   **PI To-Be Process Design:** Design the future (To-Be) process focusing on achieving CSF/KPI based strategies.
    *   **Organization & IT Strategy:** Establish IT strategies aligned with business strategies, including mid/long-term information system plans and an IT architecture roadmap.
    *   **Implementation:** Develop a detailed plan to establish an integrated information system and deploy it step-by-step.

**3. Relationship between PI and ERP**
*   PI improves systems, processes, and workforce, laying groundwork for data and process integration. This is followed by building the integrated system.
*   **Two Approaches:**
    1.  Adopting ERP *through* PI.
    2.  Using ERP to *accelerate* PI implementation.
*   Regardless of the approach, a strategic adoption plan tailored to the enterprise's circumstances is crucial.

**4. PI and Change Management**
*   **Challenge:** After innovative process improvements, organizations need time to adapt, leading to a temporary drop in productivity.
*   **Importance:** Successful PI projects require effective management of expectations, resistance, insecurity, and motivation at each project stage.
*   **Key Success Factors:**
    *   Strong support from top management.
    *   Company-wide consensus on the need for change.
    *   Choosing the right technique for the situation and goals.
    *   Clear goals and plans for implementation.
    *   Leveraging capable internal/external talent.
    *   Motivated, high-energy environment.
*   **Key Stumbling Blocks:**
    *   Resistance to change.
    *   Lack of strong leadership/support.
*   **Leadership Role:** CEO and leaders must display strong leadership, share the vision, organize resources for change, encourage participation, and help individuals/teams adapt to the new environment.
*   **Outcome:** Successful change management is vital for stable PI establishment and project success.

---

### C) Understanding Six Sigma

**1. Overview of Six Sigma**
*   **Definition:** A quality innovation movement and methodology.
*   **Origin:** Started by Motorola in 1987.
*   **Goal:** Achieve a defect rate of less than three defects per one million products (a "6 Sigma" quality level) by analyzing and quantifying causes of inefficiencies.
*   **Three Pillars:** Statistical measurement, business strategy, and philosophy (transforming work methods).

**2. Characteristics of Six Sigma**
*   Emphasizes **statistical measurement** and objective quantification of process innovations.
*   An **enterprise-wide** process innovation activity, not limited to specific departments.
*   Ultimate goal is to improve **customer value and satisfaction**.
*   Fosters a **passionate organizational culture** where all members continuously pursue improvements.

**3. Six Sigma Hierarchy**
*   **Champion:**
    *   **Qualifications:** Executive with leadership skills.
    *   **Role:** Suggests Six Sigma vision/philosophy, disseminates concepts, oversees implementation, provides resources.
*   **Master Black Belt:**
    *   **Qualifications:** Practical experience and knowledge.
    *   **Role:** Provides Black Belt/Green Belt training, teaches Six Sigma concepts and methodology.
*   **Black Belt:**
    *   **Qualifications:** Manager/assistant manager level, knowledgeable in statistics.
    *   **Role:** Operates Six Sigma projects, provides entry-level/Green Belt training.
*   **Green Belt:**
    *   **Qualifications:** Sufficient job-related knowledge and experience.
    *   **Role:** Acts as an expert in project execution, applies Six Sigma techniques at work.

**4. Six Sigma Implementation Methodology**
*   Two main programs:
    *   **Design Program (DMADV):** For designing new processes or products, or redesigning existing ones. Focuses on **preventing errors and defects**.
        *   **D**efine: Establish design goals based on user requirements.
        *   **M**easure: Select critical quality factors.
        *   **A**nalyze: Assess design feasibility, analyze for best design.
        *   **D**esign: Develop detailed agenda, optimize design, plan verification.
        *   **V**erify: Test the design and verify product development application.
    *   **Manufacturing Program (DMAIC):** For improving existing products and processes. Focuses on **reducing defects and preventing recurrence**.
        *   **D**efine: Define the problem, set goals, estimate Critical to Quality (CTQ).
        *   **M**easure: Select measurement items, establish methods, analyze current status.
        *   **A**nalyze: Analyze problem's causal relationship, determine root cause.
        *   **I**mprove: Derive optimal methods to eliminate root cause and improve manufacturing.
        *   **C**ontrol: Prevent recurrence, maintain improved condition, analyze improvement effects.

---

### D) Understanding TRIZ

**1. Overview of TRIZ**
*   **Definition:** A systematic methodology for solving invention problems.
*   **Origin:** Developed in the Soviet Union by Genrich Altshuller in the 1940s.
*   **Basis:** Altshuller analyzed 50,000 "creative" patents out of 1.5 million worldwide, discovering common rules and patterns in inventions.

**2. Four Important Discoveries (Key Insights from Altshuller's Analysis)**
*   **Definition of Invention Problem:** An invention problem always contains at least one contradiction.
*   **Level of Invention:** There are 5 distinct levels of invention.
*   **(Implied, but not explicitly detailed in the text):** Other discoveries would relate to patterns of evolution of technical systems and specific inventive principles. The text only provides two from the table, so we stick to those.

---

## Pages 76-80

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business & Ethics (Key Methodologies)

### Introduction to Process Innovation (PI)
For **Process Innovation (PI)** to succeed:
*   **Leadership:** Executives must drive change, share the vision, and actively participate.
*   **Organization:** Activities and resources must be organized; strategies developed.
*   **Participation:** Leaders should encourage stakeholder involvement and responsibility.
*   **Adaptability:** The organization's ability to adapt to change is critical for project success.

---

### C) Understanding Six Sigma

**1. Overview**
*   **Definition:** A quality innovation movement started by Motorola in 1987.
*   **Goal:** Achieve a defect rate of less than 3.4 defects per million products (known as the "6 Sigma" quality level) by analyzing and quantifying inefficiencies.
*   **Three Main Pillars:**
    1.  Statistical measurement
    2.  Business strategy
    3.  Philosophy (transforming how work is performed)

**2. Characteristics**
*   **Statistical Measurement:** Emphasizes quantification and objective measurement for process innovation.
*   **Enterprise-Wide:** Applies across the entire organization, not limited to specific departments.
*   **Customer-Focused:** Aims to improve value and satisfaction for customers.
*   **Culture of Improvement:** Strives for an organizational culture where all members continuously participate in improvements.

**3. Six Sigma Hierarchy**
Different roles with specific qualifications and responsibilities:
*   **Champion:**
    *   **Qualification:** Company executive with leadership skills.
    *   **Role:** Suggests Six Sigma vision, disseminates concepts, oversees implementation, provides resources.
*   **Master Black Belt:**
    *   **Qualification:** Possesses both practical experience and knowledge.
    *   **Role:** Provides training for Black Belts and Green Belts, teaches Six Sigma methodology.
*   **Black Belt:**
    *   **Qualification:** Manager/assistant manager level, knowledgeable in statistics and their application.
    *   **Role:** Operates Six Sigma projects, provides entry-level/Green Belt training.
*   **Green Belt:**
    *   **Qualification:** Sufficient job-related knowledge and experience.
    *   **Role:** Expert in Six Sigma project execution, applies Six Sigma techniques.

**4. Six Sigma Implementation Methodology**
Two main programs, each with a distinct focus and methodology:

*   **Design Program (DMADV)**
    *   **Purpose:** Designing new products/processes or redesigning existing ones to **prevent errors and defects** and surpass customer expectations.
    *   **Steps:**
        *   **D**efine: Establish design goals based on user requirements.
        *   **M**easure: Select factors critical to quality.
        *   **A**nalyze: Assess design feasibility, develop best design.
        *   **D**esign: Optimize detailed design, plan verification.
        *   **V**erify: Test the design and verify its application in product development.

*   **Manufacturing Program (DMAIC)**
    *   **Purpose:** Improving existing products and processes to **reduce defects** and **prevent recurrence**.
    *   **Steps:**
        *   **D**efine: Define the problem, set goals, estimate Critical To Quality (CTQ).
        *   **M**easure: Select items for measurement, establish methods, analyze current status.
        *   **A**nalyze: Determine the root cause of the identified problem.
        *   **I**mprove: Derive optimal methods to eliminate the root cause and improve manufacturing.
        *   **C**ontrol: Prevent recurrence, maintain improved conditions, analyze improvement effects.

---

### D) Understanding TRIZ

**1. Overview**
*   **Definition:** A systematic methodology for solving invention problems.
*   **Origin:** Developed by Genrich Altshuller in the Soviet Union (1940s) by analyzing 50,000 creative patents.
*   **Four Important Discoveries:**
    1.  Invention problems always involve at least one contradiction.
    2.  There are 5 levels of invention.
    3.  There are 40 principles concerning the type of invention.
    4.  There are 8 rules concerning technology system evolution.

**2. Types of TRIZ Contradictions**
TRIZ classifies contradictions into two main types:

*   **Physical Contradiction:**
    *   **Meaning:** A single variable needs two opposite values at the same time (e.g., an object needs to be both hot and cold).
    *   **Solution:** Mainly solved using the **principle of separation** (in time, space, scale, or condition).
*   **Technical Contradiction:**
    *   **Meaning:** Two variable characteristics conflict with each other (e.g., making a product stronger makes it heavier).
    *   **Solution:** Solved with 40 inventive principles, contradiction matrix, 76 standard solutions, 8 laws of technology evolution, and natural science effects.

**3. Utilization of TRIZ in Business Management**
TRIZ is effective in both engineering and management:
*   **Management Support:** Quickly resolves management difficulties/contradictions, saves time/money, approaches issues from an engineering perspective, avoids compromises, and resolves fundamental problems.
*   **Innovation Support:** Secures innovativeness by resolving fundamental problems.
*   **Thinking Management:** Develops a business management technique where thinking processes are internalized, providing a rational decision-making system.
*   **Fusion Management:** Creates synergies by combining TRIZ with other sectors/techniques.

---

### E) Understanding SERVQUAL

**1. Overview**
*   **Definition:** A technique to analyze the gap between the service quality *expected* by users and the *actual* service quality provided by an enterprise.
*   **Purpose:** Helps prioritize the relative importance of service attributes (as perceived by the user), allowing enterprises to provide service based on these priorities.
*   **Origin:** Proposed by Parasuraman, Zeithaml, and Berry in 1985.

**2. The 5 Dimensions of SERVQUAL**
SERVQUAL is built around five core dimensions:
*   **Tangibles:** Physical facilities, equipment, staff attire, visual appearance of data.
*   **Reliability:** The service company's ability to perform the promised service dependably and accurately.
*   **Responsiveness:** The attitude, behavior, and willingness associated with customer response and prompt service provision.
*   **Assurance:** An employee's ability to communicate knowledge, good manners, trust, and confidence.
*   **Empathy:** The attention, effort, and consideration given to customers by a service company.

**Note:** These 5 dimensions can be further subdivided into 10 categories for detailed investigation and evaluation:
1.  Tangibles
2.  Reliability
3.  Responsiveness
4.  Competence
5.  Courtesy
6.  Credibility
7.  Safety
8.  Accessibility
9.  Communication
10. Customer Understanding

---

### F) Understanding SPC (Statistical Process Control)

**1. Overview**
*   **Full Name:** Statistical Process Control.
*   **Definition:** A management technique that uses statistical data and analysis to repeatedly improve a process and maintain high rates of satisfactory quality production.
*   **Purpose:** Allows enterprises to control the condition of a product during production, conduct engineering analysis of defect causes, and establish the best rectification methods.

**2. Effects of SPC**
*   **Uniform Quality:** Produces goods of uniform quality within a narrow distribution range.
*   **Reduced Variation:** Reduces process variations.
*   **Process Stability:** Stabilizes each process.
*   **Zero-Defect Foundation:** Lays the groundwork for producing zero-defect goods.
*   **Productivity & Profit:** Enhances productivity, leads to significant cost reductions, and contributes to higher profits.

**3. Constituent Elements of SPC**
*   **Deviation:**
    *   **Description:** An attribute indicating product quality; refers to the distribution of values around a central point or its trend.
    *   **Causes:** Occurs due to **common causes** (inherent, normal variation) or **assignable causes** (specific, identifiable issues).
*   **Process Management & Capability:**
    *   **Description:** Managerial ability to reduce deviation.
    *   **Goal:** Keep deviations within allowable product ranges by continuously eliminating common and assignable causes.
*   **Distribution & Statistics:**
    *   **Description:** Schematic diagram showing deviation trends.
    *   **Goal:** Minimize "spraying" (variation) by continuously managing common causes and removing assignable causes.
*   **Data Collection Instruments:** Work logs, checklists, inspection device data.
*   **Statistical Techniques for Analysis:** Control chart, histogram, scatter plot, Pareto diagram, cause-effect diagram.

---


---

# IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide

This guide covers key concepts in service quality, process control, and IT business management.

---

## 1. SERVQUAL: Service Quality Dimensions

**SERVQUAL** is a framework used to assess service quality, based on customer perceptions. It comprises 5 core dimensions, which are often expanded into 10 categories for more detailed analysis.

### The 5 Core SERVQUAL Dimensions:

1.  **Tangibles:** Physical facilities, equipment, attire, physical appearance of data.
2.  **Reliability:** Ability to perform the promised service dependably and accurately.
3.  **Responsiveness:** Willingness to assist customers and provide prompt service.
4.  **Assurance:** Employees' ability to convey knowledge, good manners, trust, and confidence.
5.  **Empathy:** Attention, effort, and consideration given to customers.

### 10 Categories for Detailed SERVQUAL Evaluation:

These categories provide a more granular view for investigations and evaluations:

1.  **Tangibles:** Physical facilities, equipment, employees, outward appearance of data.
2.  **Reliability:** Ability to perform a promised service in a trustworthy and accurate manner.
3.  **Responsiveness:** Readiness to assist users and provide quick services.
4.  **Competence:** Possession of the necessary technology and knowledge for service provision.
5.  **Courtesy:** Courtesy, respect, consideration, and friendliness of front-line workers.
6.  **Credibility:** Trustworthiness and honesty of the service provider.
7.  **Safety:** Absence of risk likelihood and doubt.
8.  **Accessibility:** Ease of access and convenience.
9.  **Communication:** Communicating with users in an easy-to-understand language and actively listening.
10. **Customer Understanding:** Making an effort to understand what customers want.

---

## 2. Statistical Process Control (SPC)

**SPC** stands for **Statistical Process Control**. It is a management technique that uses statistical data and analysis to control and improve processes, especially in manufacturing, to ensure consistent product quality.

### Key Aspects of SPC:

*   **Statistical:** Relies on statistical data and analysis.
*   **Process:** Focuses on a given product's quality specifications and process capability.
*   **Control:** Allows businesses to manage product conditions during production.

### Objectives & Effects of SPC:

*   **Continuous Improvement:** Repeatedly improves processes.
*   **Maintain Quality:** Sustains high rates of satisfactory quality goods.
*   **Defect Analysis:** Conducts engineering analysis of defect causes to find solutions.
*   **Uniform Quality:** Aims to produce goods of uniform quality within a narrow range.
*   **Reduce Variation:** Minimizes process variations.
*   **Stabilize Processes:** Establishes foundations for producing zero-defect goods.
*   **Cost Reduction:** Enhances productivity, leading to significant cost savings and higher profits.

### Constituent Elements of SPC:

1.  **Deviation:**
    *   Indicates product quality attributes.
    *   Refers to the distribution of values around a central point or the trend of this value.
    *   Occurs due to **common causes** (inherent to the process) or **assignable causes** (specific, identifiable issues).
2.  **Process Management & Capability:**
    *   Managerial ability to reduce deviations.
    *   Aims to keep deviations within an allowable range by repeatedly eliminating common and assignable causes.
3.  **Distribution & Statistics:**
    *   Schematic diagram showing deviation trends.
    *   Goal: Minimize distribution range by continuously managing common causes and eliminating assignable causes.

### Tools Used in SPC:

*   **Data Collection Instruments:** Work logs, checklists, inspection device data.
*   **Statistical Techniques:** Control charts, histograms, scatter plots, Pareto diagrams, cause-effect diagrams.

---

## 3. Recent Trends in IT Business Services

The IT business landscape emphasizes customer-centricity and integrated operations.

### Key Trends:

*   **Customer-Centric Quality:** Service quality is defined by customer requirements. Understanding customer needs is paramount.
*   **Integrated Value Chains:** IT business services are interconnected, involving customers, partner companies (suppliers), and other stakeholders. Integrated analysis across the entire value chain is crucial.
*   **End-to-End Process Management:** The trend is towards operating the entire "purchase-production-sales-post management" cycle as a single, connected process, rather than fragmented operations.
*   **Continuous Quality Control:** Quality control must extend from the very beginning to the very end of a service, including supplier services.
*   **Systematic Information Flow:** Effective management of information flow between general-purpose internal systems (e.g., ERP) is vital for continuous quality control.

---

## 4. Core IT Business Systems

IT business services are supported by various systems, enhancing competitiveness and innovation.

### A. Enterprise Solutions (General-Purpose Work Support Systems)

**Enterprise Solutions** are information systems that support management activities to maximize business efficiency and gain competitive advantages. They are not just tools but crucial enablers for business survival and growth.

*   **Definition:** A collective term for information systems that support management activities to maximize business efficiency and competitive advantages.
*   **Value:** Depends on how business processes are defined and not solely on system functions.
*   **Scope:** Includes IT planning, job-specific solutions, system building, and ongoing maintenance.

**Key Enterprise Solution Systems:**

*   **ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning):** Integrates all facets of an operation, including product planning, development, manufacturing processes, sales, and marketing.
*   **SCM (Supply Chain Management):** Manages the flow of goods, data, and finances related to a product or service, from raw materials to delivery.
*   **CRM (Customer Relationship Management):** Manages all interactions with current and potential customers to improve business relationships.

These systems help enterprises maintain close customer relationships by analyzing their needs.

### B. Decision-Making Support Systems

These systems aid decision-makers in maximizing business value.

*   **DSS (Decision Support System):** Computerized systems used to support decision-making activities in an organization or a business.
*   **BI (Business Intelligence):** Uses strategies and technologies for data analysis of business information.
*   **EDW (Enterprise Data Warehouse):** The backbone for DSS and BI. It collects internal and external data for analysis, providing a unified source of truth for decision-making.

---

## 5. IT Service Management (ITSM)

**ITSM** is a management technique for the systematic management of IT services. It focuses on delivering IT services that meet user needs and improve service quality.

### Key Aspects of ITSM:

*   **Frameworks:** Leverages frameworks like **ITIL (IT Infrastructure Library)** for defining IT service processes and activities.
*   **Standards:** Can be combined with international standards like **ISO/IEC 20000** to improve and enhance IT service quality.
*   **Service Levels:** Requires defining and managing **Service Levels** in advance to ensure user satisfaction.
    *   **SLA (Service Level Agreement):** A contract that defines the level of service expected from a vendor.
    *   **SLM (Service Level Management):** The process of managing service levels to ensure they meet agreed-upon targets and satisfy customers.

### Practical Application Example (Company K):

Company K, a trading company, adopted ITSM to:

*   **Improve Quality:** Enhance the quality of IT resource maintenance and repair.
*   **Stabilize Operations:** Stabilize IT infrastructure operation.
*   **Advanced Processes:** Deploy advanced operational processes.

**Implementation with ITIL:**

*   **ITIL-based Processes:** Implemented to improve operational efficiency.
*   **Transparent Management:** Real-time monitoring of service levels.
*   **Supplier Management:** Effective management of suppliers to preserve high service quality.
*   **Malfunction Prevention:** Strategies for preventing malfunctions and real-time monitoring/analysis of key logs.

**Tools & Benefits:**

*   **Visualization:** Introduced event/performance management, configuration management, malfunction management, report management, and a **dashboard** for help desk operations.
*   **Dashboard:** Visualizes server malfunction status by type and severity, enabling instant awareness and quick response to IT service issues.
*   **Rapid Response:** Quickly communicated malfunctions to managers.
*   **Knowledge Base:** Built a knowledge database of malfunctions to prevent recurrence.
*   **Service Level Management (SLM):** Used ITSM to conduct SLM systematically, contributing to comprehensive service level evaluation and building customer trust.

## IT Business & Ethics: A Study Guide

### 1. Understanding IT Service Management (ITSM)

**What is ITSM?**
IT Service Management (ITSM) is a management technique for systematically managing IT services to ensure quality, stability, and efficiency.

**Why implement ITSM? (Company K Example)**
*   **Purpose:** Improve quality of IT resource maintenance & repair, stabilize infrastructure, deploy advanced operational processes.
*   **Key Principles/Criteria (using ITIL global standard):**
    *   Implement ITIL-based processes for operational efficiency.
    *   Transparent management and real-time monitoring of service levels.
    *   Effective supplier management to preserve high service quality.
    *   Strategies for preventing malfunctions and monitoring/analyzing logs.
*   **Tools/Visualizations:**
    *   Event/performance management
    *   Configuration management
    *   Malfunction management
    *   Report management
    *   Help desk dashboard (reports server malfunction status by type/severity)
*   **Benefits:**
    *   Quick response to malfunctions.
    *   Building a knowledge database (DB) to prevent future issues.
    *   Systematic Service-Level Management (SLM) for comprehensive evaluation and customer trust.

### 2. Core Components of IT Business Services

IT business services are broadly categorized into:

1.  **General-Purpose Work Support Systems:**
    *   Assist in performing business tasks.
    *   **Components:**
        *   **ERP** (Enterprise Resource Planning)
        *   **SCM** (Supply Chain Management)
        *   **CRM** (Customer Relationship Management)
    *   **Purpose:** Help maintain close relationships with customers by analyzing their needs.

2.  **Decision Support Systems:**
    *   Assist decision-makers in making informed choices.
    *   **Components:**
        *   **BI** (Business Intelligence) unit
        *   **DSS** (Decision Support System)
    *   **Backbone:** **EDW** (Enterprise Data Warehouse) – collects and analyzes internal and external data.

3.  **IT Service Management (ITSM):**
    *   A management technique for IT services.
    *   **Frameworks:** Leverages **ITIL** (IT Infrastructure Library) for defining processes and activities.
    *   **Standards:** Used with international standards like **ISO/IEC 20000** to improve IT service quality.
    *   **Key for Satisfaction:** Requires pre-defined service levels and effective service level management (SLM).

### 3. Enterprise Solutions

**What are Enterprise Solutions?**
*   **Definition:** A collective term for information systems that support management activities to maximize business efficiency and gain competitive advantages.
*   **Evolution:** From simple business support tools to critical tools for survival in competitive environments.
*   **Scope:** Encompasses IT planning, job-specific solutions, and maintenance for operating IT systems.
*   **Value:** Depends on how well it aligns with and defines business processes and activities, not just system functions.
*   **Focus:** Maximizing business efficiency, improving productivity, and strengthening competitiveness.

**Key Roles/Benefits of Enterprise Solutions:**

*   **Optimize Business Operations:** Maximize profits by reducing time and costs.
*   **Innovate Business Processes:** Enable and facilitate work process innovations and rebuilding.
*   **Improve Quality:** Apply IT to product quality improvement, identify issues from data.
*   **Strengthen Customer-Supplier Relationships:** Secure loyal customers (CRM), reduce costs & ensure smooth delivery (SCM).
*   **Improve Decision Making:** Provide real-time market data to executives for timely, accurate decisions.
*   **Secure Competitive Advantages:** Achieve operational excellence, develop new products/models, strengthen relationships.
*   **Shorten Time to Market:** Use technologies (e.g., CAD/CAM) to reduce product development times.

**Types of Enterprise Solutions:**

| Solution Acronym | Full Name / Description                                                                                                                              | Key Function / Purpose                                                                          |
| :--------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **ERP**          | **Enterprise Resource Planning:** An integrated management system for optimal operation of enterprise-wide resources.                               | Optimizing, distributing, deploying, and operating an enterprise's entire resources.             |
| **SCM**          | **Supply Chain Management:** Integrates and manages the flow of products, services, and information across the supply chain.                          | From customer orders to material procurement, production, and delivery; optimizes processes.    |
| **CRM**          | **Customer Relationship Management:** Processes and information systems for enhancing corporate image and brand value.                               | Timely delivery of products/services based on accurate customer understanding and needs analysis. |
| **PLM**          | **Product Lifecycle Management:** Product-centered information system.                                                                              | Supports product development and collaborative utilization of product information.              |
| **HRM**          | **Human Resource Management:** Information support system for HR management activities.                                                             | Recruitment, job assignment, education, promotion, resignation.                                 |
| **KM**           | **Knowledge Management:** Set of activities for collecting, generating, and utilizing employee knowledge resources.                                  | Information system for supporting/managing these knowledge activities.                          |
| **EIS**          | **Executive Information System:** Information system that effectively aggregates management information and analyzes problems.                        | Provides support for rapid decision-making to executives.                                       |
| **SEM**          | **Strategic Enterprise Management:** (Implied, mentioned in figure)                                                                                 | Maximizing shareholder value.                                                                   |
| **EP**           | **Employee Portal:** (Implied, mentioned in figure)                                                                                                 | Provides a central access point for employees to information and applications.                  |

### 4. Business Strategy & Enterprise Solutions

*   **Strategic Alignment:** Enterprise solutions must be organically linked (customer communication, product management, process integration) to efficiently execute business strategies and achieve goals.
*   **Adaptability:** Companies must adopt and tailor solutions to fit changing environmental conditions and strategic goals for survival.
*   **Essential Deployment:** A core set of solutions are universally needed or developed by enterprises, sometimes due to IT compliance requirements.
*   **Solutions & Strategy:** Enterprise solutions are adopted to fulfill specific strategic items:
    *   **SCM:** Collaboration with business partners
    *   **CRM:** Customer communication
    *   **PLM:** Product information
    *   **ERP:** Process integration
    *   **KM:** Knowledge management
    *   **SEM:** Shareholder value maximization

### 5. Deep Dive: Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP)

**Definition of ERP:**
A system that integrates an enterprise's various management resources into a single system to maximize overall productivity.

**Goals & Benefits:**
*   Maximize enterprise-wide business efficiency by integrating key business processes and sharing information.
*   Provides integrated work support and systematic linking of different business aspects.
*   Contributes to efficient data sharing and increased organizational flexibility.

**Key Characteristics of ERP:**

*   **Integration:** Designed to flawlessly connect related business operations (finance, accounting, manufacturing, sales, marketing, service) with zero redundancies.
*   **Flexibility:** Customizable and configurable by users and businesses to suit unique operational needs.
*   **Openness:** Built on international standards with an open structure, allowing integration with diverse platforms, hardware, and software.
*   **International:** Supports multiple languages and manages local data (e.g., tax items, address systems, currencies) for multinational corporations.

**Configuration & Operational Flow (Example: Order Processing):**

ERP systems organize most operational functions (purchasing, production, distribution, marketing, sales, service, finance, accounting, HR) ensuring interdependencies and balanced resource distribution.

1.  **Customer Order:** Sales representative enters the order into the ERP system.
2.  **Data Communication:** Finalized order data (quantity, delivery location/time) is communicated to relevant departments.
3.  **Raw Materials:** Data on raw materials (procurement time, quantity, price) is sent to relevant departments to meet the order.
4.  **Production:** The factory produces the order on schedule.
5.  **Production Data:** Production data is entered into ERP and transmitted to the shipping department.
6.  **Delivery:** Shipping delivers goods to the customer on the desired date.

The ERP system provides an environment where these complex operations can take place organically and efficiently.
