---

# Enterprise Solutions Learning Guide

This guide covers key enterprise solutions: Supply Chain Management (SCM), Customer Relationship Management (CRM), and Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP).

---

## Part 1: Business Strategy & Enterprise Solutions Overview

### 1.1 What are Enterprise Solutions?
Enterprise solutions are systems designed to help businesses execute strategies and achieve goals efficiently. They link communication, product management, and process integration.

### 1.2 Why are Enterprise Solutions Needed?
*   Businesses operate in a constantly changing environment.
*   They need to respond nimbly to survive and adapt strategies.
*   Adopting solutions that meet strategic goals and IT compliance is crucial.

### 1.3 Key Enterprise Solutions & Their Purpose
| Enterprise Solution | Purpose                       |
| :------------------ | :---------------------------- |
| **SCM**             | Collaboration with partners   |
| **CRM**             | Customer communication        |
| **PLM**             | Product information           |
| **ERP**             | Process integration           |
| **SEM**             | Shareholder value maximization|
| **EP**              | Employee portal               |

**Key Idea:** Enterprise solutions are adopted to fit specific business strategies and their detailed objectives.

---

## Part 2: Understanding ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning)

### 2.1 Definition of ERP
ERP is a system that **integrates various management resources** (finance, HR, production, etc.) of an enterprise into a single system to **maximize overall productivity and efficiency**.

**Goal:** To maximize enterprise-wide business efficiency by integrating key business processes and enabling information sharing.

**Benefits:**
*   Integrated work support across business operations.
*   Systematic linking of different business aspects.
*   Efficient data sharing.
*   Increased organizational flexibility.

### 2.2 Characteristics of ERP

*   **Integration:** Connects all related business operations (finance, accounting, manufacturing, sales, service) without redundancies.
*   **Flexibility:** Customizable settings to suit unique business operations and user needs.
*   **Openness:** Based on international standards, designed with an open structure to integrate with diverse platforms, hardware, and software.
*   **International:** Supports multiple languages and manages local data (e.g., tax items, addresses, currencies) for multinational corporations.

### 2.3 Configuration of ERP
ERP organizes most operational functions of an enterprise, ensuring interdependencies and balanced resource distribution.

**Example Flow:**
1.  Customer places an order.
2.  Sales enters order into ERP.
3.  Order data (quantity, delivery, timing) is communicated to relevant departments.
4.  Data on raw materials (procurement, price, quantity) is sent to production.
5.  Factory produces the order; production data is entered into ERP.
6.  Production data transmitted to shipping.
7.  Shipping delivers goods to customer.
ERP provides the environment for these operations to happen organically.

**Core Components of ERP (as per Fig. 30):**
*   **Integrated Business Process:** Supports diverse business processes and dynamic interlinking of operational modules.
*   **Integrated Database:** Enterprise-wide resource database, shared across different business areas.
*   **Best Practice / Management Techniques:** Adopts standard operating processes and includes Business Process Redesign (BPR) functions.

**Key Modules/Functions often found in ERP:**
*   **Customer Management:** Purchase, Distribution, Customer, Promotion, Cost estimation.
*   **HR Management:** HR, Education, Attendance, Salary, Absenteeism.
*   **Finance & Accounting:** Bond rights, Fund management, Cost management, General account ledger, Profitability analysis.
*   **Manufacturing, Production & Service Delivery:** Production, Material, Price, Sales, Order, Service management.

### 2.4 ERP Deployment Procedure
Deployment should be viewed as business innovation, not just system introduction. It requires analyzing existing processes, identifying improvement points, and undergoing radical transformation through Process Innovation (PI). CEO support is critical for success.

**Typical Steps:**

1.  **Project Launch:**
    *   Write project plan.
    *   Write quality assurance plan.
2.  **Analysis:**
    *   Analyze current and future processes.
    *   Conduct gap analysis (differences between current and future).
    *   Draw up gap response plan.
    *   Provide package/module/language education.
3.  **Design:**
    *   Set up processes, functions, and master data.
    *   Define interface and prototyping.
    *   Design additional development.
    *   Design data codes.
    *   Establish test plan and interface design.
4.  **Development:**
    *   Develop functions.
    *   Perform unit-level testing.
    *   Perform regression testing (connection between existing and new modules).
    *   Conduct outside link (interface) integrated test.
5.  **Implementation:**
    *   Perform data conversion.
    *   Provide training on system usage.
    *   Carry out a pilot operation.

### 2.5 ERP Deployment Strategy
There are three main approaches:

| Method                  | Description                                                  | Strengths                                         | Weaknesses                                                    |
| :---------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------ | :------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Big Bang**            | All modules and functions deployed simultaneously across all operational areas. | Easy integration of the package itself, easy implementation. | Projects tend to be large-scale, difficult project management.  |
| **Phased (Functional)** | ERP modules deployed by function and in phases.              | Little resistance to changes.                     | Additional programs may be needed to link to existing systems. |
| **Phased (Place of Business)** | ERP system deployed in phases at each business location, then expanded. | Good use of human resources (recycled in phases). | Project prolongation, high likelihood of redundant work.       |

**ERP Vendors & Considerations:**
*   **Leading Foreign Solutions:** SAP ERP, Oracle ERP.
*   **Leading Domestic Solutions:** Younglimwon ERP, Douzone ERP.
*   **Advantages of Commercial ERP:** Standardized processes.
*   **Disadvantages of Commercial ERP:** Difficult to customize for unique enterprise environments.
*   **Important Check:** Ensure compliance with IFRS (International Financial Reporting Standards), which are global accounting standards.

---

## Part 3: Understanding SCM (Supply Chain Management)

### 3.1 Concept of SCM
SCM refers to **Supply Chain Management solutions**.

**Supply Chain:** Encompasses the entire process from order placement, raw material supply, production, distribution network, to final delivery to the customer.

### 3.2 The Bullwhip Effect (The Biggest Problem in Supply Chains)
*   **Definition:** A phenomenon where a small change in end-consumer demand causes a sudden and significantly expanded demand upstream in the supply chain.
    *   **Example:** If a consumer orders 10 items, the retailer might order 12 "just in case," the wholesaler 15, and the manufacturer 20.
*   **Consequences:**
    *   Overstocked supply chain.
    *   Wasted resources, unnecessary investments in manpower and facilities.
    *   Distorted demand and increased variance at each step upstream.
    *   High risks for raw material suppliers.
    *   Inefficiency across the entire supply chain due to demand imbalance.
    *   Results in surplus orders, excess inventory, and overinvestment.

### 3.3 Goal and How SCM Works
**Goal of SCM:** To maximize efficiency by rectifying the bullwhip effect and eliminating waste throughout the supply chain.

**How it Works:**
*   Supply chain players cooperate to manage materials, funds, and information.
*   It links and integrates the flow of all goods, services, and values (purchasing, manufacture, allocation, distribution) from suppliers to end customers.

**Effects of SCM:**
*   Shortened lead time.
*   Reduced uncertainties and variabilities.

**Overall:** SCM is a management technique focused on optimizing inventory management and other supply chain decisions.

---


---


## Pages 88-92


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text, designed for study purposes.

---

## IT Business and Ethics: ERP, SCM, and CRM Learning Guide

This guide covers ERP Deployment Strategies, Supply Chain Management (SCM), and Customer Relationship Management (CRM).

---

### **1. ERP Deployment Strategy**

ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning) systems can be deployed using three main approaches:

**A. Deployment Approaches**

1.  **Big Bang Method:**
    *   **Description:** All ERP modules and functions are deployed simultaneously across the entire enterprise.
    *   **Strengths:** Easy integration of the package itself, simpler project management for integration.
    *   **Weaknesses:** Large-scale projects, difficult overall project management.
2.  **Phased and Function-Based Approach (Functional Approach):**
    *   **Description:** ERP modules are deployed in phases, separated by their functions (e.g., finance module first, then HR).
    *   **Strengths:** Less resistance to change within the business due to gradual deployment.
    *   **Weaknesses:** Requires additional programs to link with existing systems during phased rollout.
3.  **Phased and Place of Business Approach (Place of Business Approach):**
    *   **Description:** ERP is deployed in phases at individual business locations (e.g., one branch first, then others). Deployment expands horizontally once stable.
    *   **Strengths:** Efficient use of human resources as they can be recycled across phases.
    *   **Weaknesses:** Risk of project prolongation and redundant work.

**B. ERP Solutions**

*   **Vendors:** Both domestic (e.g., Younglimwon ERP, Douzone ERP) and foreign global vendors (e.g., SAP ERP, Oracle ERP) offer solutions. In-house development is also possible.
*   **Commercial Products:** Offer advantages of standardized processes, but customization to specific enterprise environments can be difficult.
*   **Key Consideration:** When adopting, check for compliance with **IFRS (International Financial Reporting Standards)**, which are global accounting standards.

---

### **2. Understanding Supply Chain Management (SCM)**

**A. Concept of SCM**

*   **Supply Chain:** The entire process from order placement, raw material supply, production, distribution, to final customer delivery.
*   **The Bullwhip Effect:**
    *   **Problem:** A phenomenon where small changes in end-consumer demand lead to dramatically increasing demand fluctuations further up the supply chain (e.g., small consumer order leads to larger orders from retailer to wholesaler, then to manufacturer, then to parts suppliers).
    *   **Impact:** Distorted demand, increased variance at each step, huge risks for upstream suppliers, inefficiency, surplus orders, excess inventory, and overinvestment.
*   **SCM Goal:** To maximize efficiency by rectifying the bullwhip effect and eliminating waste throughout the supply chain.
*   **SCM Mechanism:** Players in the supply chain cooperate, managing materials, funds, and information to link and integrate all goods, services, and value flows (purchasing, manufacture, allocation, distribution) from suppliers to end customers.
*   **Benefits:** Shortened lead times, reduced uncertainties and variabilities, optimized inventory.

**B. Functions of SCM**

SCM has three core functions that form a positive feedback cycle for continuous improvement:

1.  **Supply Chain Planning (SCP):**
    *   **Description:** Establishes optimal plans for daily supply chain operations.
    *   **Examples:** Demand forecasting, global production plans, transportation/delivery plans, distribution allocation plans.
2.  **Supply Chain Execution (SCE):**
    *   **Description:** Enhances efficiency of field logistics.
    *   **Examples:** Warehousing, product transport/delivery management, order management, distribution management. Uses digital tools like barcodes and RFID.
3.  **Supply Chain Visibility:**
    *   **Description:** Monitors the supply chain, identifies costs and performance, looks for anomalies, and provides preventive functions by recommending corrective actions.

**C. SCM vs. ERP Comparison**

| Category            | SCM                                        | ERP                                                              |
| :------------------ | :----------------------------------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Key Viewpoint**   | Planning and decision-making               | Work process-centered                                            |
| **Data Handling**   | Process-centered                           | Transaction-centered                                             |
| **Major Functions** | Demand forecasting, order management, planning, distribution, warehouse management | Purchasing, production, raw materials, finance, accounting, sales, HR management |
| **Industrial Sector** | Manufacturing and distribution             | Manufacturing, public organizations, finance                     |
| **Enterprise Size** | Even small manufacturers benefit (e.g., reduced inventories) | Mainly operated by conglomerates; SMEs should consider ROI     |
| **Benefits**        | Production planning, demand forecasting considering sales opportunities, inventory management | Faster work processing, labor cost savings                       |

**D. SCM Deployment Effects**

*   **Improved Customer Satisfaction:** Increased transportation/delivery capacity, reduced inventory, reduced customer order processing time due to adherence to delivery schedules.
*   **Reduced Costs:** Lower logistics costs.
*   **Improved Efficiency:** Standardized work, reduced product delivery time, improved fund flow.
*   **Example (Dell Computer):** Reduced inventory from 8 weeks to 12-15 days by linking information between customers, company, and suppliers in real time.

---

### **3. Understanding Customer Relationship Management (CRM)**

**A. Concept of CRM**

*   **Definition:** A management strategy system that studies customer tendencies and requirements in advance to create desired products and develop effective marketing strategies.
*   **Why CRM is Essential Today:**
    *   Customers are highly informed about products/services.
    *   Higher customer expectations and churn rates.
    *   Enterprises need customer-centric structures, diverse customer interface channels, and customer management strategies that lead to better earnings.
*   **Implementation:** Requires analyzing customer behavior and consumption patterns, consolidating internal/external data, and deriving insights (e.g., using Big Data analysis).

**B. Customer Life Cycle and CRM Goal**

Enterprises manage customers through their entire life cycle:

*   **Acquisition:** Target responsive potential customers with focused marketing.
*   **Retention/Growth:** Strategically manage purchasing and high-value (loyal) customers. Categorize customers by personality, type, and interests to provide tailored services and marketing.
*   **CRM Goal:** To maximize **Customer Lifetime Value (CLV)** – the total value a customer generates throughout their relationship with the enterprise, rather than just temporary profits from individual transactions.

**C. Official Definition of CRM (Gartner)**

*   "A strategy for optimizing corporate sales and expanding the customer base by creating and supporting relationships with profitable customers."
*   **Essentially:** It's a management technique that integrates and analyzes customer-related data (internal and external) to provide findings to customer points of contact, enabling continuous delivery of desired products/services based on accurate customer understanding, ultimately maximizing CLV and profitability.

**D. CRM Classification**

From a process perspective, CRM collects, analyzes, and provides meaningful information. It can be classified into three types:

1.  **Analysis CRM:**
    *   **Description:** Gathers information from customer interactions, derives meaningful insights, and supplies them to the enterprise.
2.  **Operations CRM:**
    *   **Description:** Uses the insights from Analysis CRM as the backbone for marketing, servicing, and sales activities.
3.  **Collaboration CRM:**
    *   **Description:** Focuses on enterprise interactions with customers through a diverse range of communication channels.

---

## Pages 91-95

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Key Concepts

### 1. SCM vs. ERP

| Category           | SCM (Supply Chain Management)                        | ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning)                       |
| :----------------- | :--------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Key Viewpoint**  | Planning and decision-making for the supply chain.   | Work process-centered within the enterprise.             |
| **Data Handling**  | Process-centered.                                    | Transaction-centered.                                    |
| **Major Functions**| Demand forecasting, order/purchasing/distribution/warehouse management. | Purchasing, production, raw materials, finance, accounting, sales, HR. |
| **Industrial Sector**| Manufacturing and distribution.                      | Manufacturing, public organizations, finance.            |
| **Enterprise Size**| Even small manufacturers can benefit (e.g., reduced inventory). | Mainly for conglomerates. SMEs should consider ROI.      |
| **Benefits**       | Integrates sales opportunities into production/demand planning, improves inventory management. | Faster work processing, labor cost savings.              |

---

### 2. SCM Deployment Effects

*   **Goal:** Real-time information linkage between customer, company, and component suppliers.
*   **Benefits:**
    *   **Reduced Inventory:** Significant reduction in supply stock (e.g., Dell reduced from 8 weeks to 12-15 days).
    *   **Improved Customer Satisfaction:** Increased delivery capacity, reduced order processing time, strict adherence to schedules.
    *   **Reduced Logistics Costs.**
    *   **Improved Fund Flow Efficiency:** Standardized work, reduced product delivery and order processing times.

---

### 3. Understanding CRM (Customer Relationship Management)

*   **Definition:** A management strategy system to understand customer tendencies and requirements, enabling product creation and effective marketing strategies.
*   **Why CRM is Essential Today:**
    *   Customers have more product/service knowledge.
    *   Higher customer expectations and churn rates.
    *   Businesses need customer-centric structures, diverse interaction channels, and profit-driven customer management.
*   **Method:** Enterprises analyze customer behavior and consumption patterns, consolidating internal/external data to derive insights (e.g., using Big Data).

#### Customer Life Cycle in CRM

CRM helps manage customers through stages to maximize their **Customer Lifetime Value (CLV)** – the total value generated throughout their relationship, not just individual transactions.
*   **Potential Customer:** Shows initial interest.
*   **Responsive Customer:** Reacts to marketing efforts.
*   **Purchasing Customer:** Buys products.
*   **High-Value Customer:** Highly loyal and profitable.
*   **Low-Value Customer:** Less profitable or loyal.
*   **Lost Customer:** No longer engaging with the business.
*   **Forced-Departure Customer:** The company terminates interaction.

#### Definition of CRM (Gartner)
*   **Core Idea:** A strategy to optimize sales and expand the customer base by creating and supporting relationships with profitable customers.
*   **Process:** Integrates and analyzes customer data (internal and external) to provide findings to customer contact points, enabling effective interactions. This ensures customers receive desired products/services based on accurate understanding, maximizing CLV and profitability.

#### CRM Classification

CRM is typically classified into three types for better understanding:

1.  **Analysis CRM:**
    *   **Concept:** Gathers and analyzes data from customer interactions to derive meaningful insights for the enterprise. Often linked to a **Data Warehouse (DW)**.
    *   **Components:** Enterprise-wide DW, Data Mining, OLAP (Online Analytical Processing).
    *   **Considerations:** Providing analysis techniques to identify customer needs, building a knowledge base, ensuring data reliability.

2.  **Operational CRM:**
    *   **Concept:** Uses insights from Analysis CRM to support customer management at contact points, integrating marketing, service, and sales activities. Automates front-office business processes.
    *   **Components:** Marketing information management, Campaign system, SFA (Sales Force Automation), Customer service system.
    *   **Considerations:** Integrating processes across channels, unified management of customer contact history, rapid development of business functions, access to back-office systems.

3.  **Collaboration CRM:**
    *   **Concept:** Manages customer interaction channels. Facilitates improved communication and task consolidation between customers, the company, and internal departments.
    *   **Components:** Call Center, Mobile collaboration system, eCRM (electronic CRM).
    *   **Considerations:** Diversifying channels, providing a uniform service across all channels.

*   **Overall Goal:** While categorized for understanding, CRM's ultimate aim is to deeply understand customer minds, requiring robust data analysis, business support systems, and diverse interaction channels.

#### Configuration of the CRM System

*   **Information Flow:** Starts and ends at the **customer point of contact (channel)**.
*   **Role of Channels:** Collects **VoC (Voice of Customer)** and communicates internal process results back to the customer. This makes channels crucial for identifying CRM components.
*   **Key Components:**
    *   **Customer Data Warehouse:** Central storage for all customer data; used by all CRM elements.
    *   **OLAP & Data Mining:** Tools for diverse customer analysis, identifying relationships, and supporting decision-making (e.g., customer acquisition).
    *   **Campaign System:** Develops tailored services and recommends profitable business directions.
    *   **Channel System:** Provides 1:1 or 1:N marketing support (e.g., call centers, email, direct mail).
    *   **Sales Force Automation (SFA):** Supports sales staff with planning, management, performance evaluation, and direct sales activities.
    *   **Customer Service System:** Uses VoC for customer service and product maintenance (A/S).

#### Effects of CRM Deployment

*   **Improved Customer Relationships:** Increases loyalty and prevents customer churn.
*   **High-Quality Services:** Provides tailored services by analyzing customer tastes.
*   **Increased Sales:** Induces linked sales and upstream sales.
*   **Competitive Edge:** Builds differentiated policies for products and services based on customer insights.

| Benefit Area                | Specific Advantages                                       |
| :-------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Marketing Opportunity**   | - Attracts new customers, invigorates existing base.      |
|                             | - Increases earnings and customer lifetime values.        |
|                             | - Enables effective marketing based on customer life cycle. |
| **Marketing Management**    | - Develops products meeting customer requirements and market changes. |
|                             | - Improves products based on market reactions/results.    |
| **Customer Service**        | - Strengthens customer loyalty.                           |
|                             | - Manages customer satisfaction and service effectively.  |
| **Customer Channel Management** | - Secures optimal channels meeting customer requirements. |
|                             | - Minimizes customer management costs.                    |

---

### 4. Understanding PLM (Product Lifecycle Management)

*   **Definition:** A solution that uniformly manages a product's entire lifecycle, from design drawings to final product and post-sales services.
*   **Goal:** Increase product added value and reduce costs throughout the process.
*   **Detailed Definition:** A support system that integrates and manages all product-related information (drawings, documents, CAD/CAM, parts, design changes, process information) generated across the enterprise's product development and manufacturing lifecycle.
*   **Configuration:**
    *   PLM includes not only initial product planning but also **post-sales services** provided to customers.
    *   Its key role is managing an individual product's complete cycle from planning to sale.
    *   Requires organic support from other work support systems.
    *   Visualizing the product's entire life cycle helps understand PLM components.

---

---

## IT Business Systems: CRM, PLM, and Decision Support

This guide covers essential IT business systems: Customer Relationship Management (CRM), Product Lifecycle Management (PLM), and Enterprise Data Warehousing (EDW) as a foundation for Decision Support Systems.

---

### Section 1: Customer Relationship Management (CRM)

**What is CRM?**
CRM is a system designed to manage and analyze customer interactions and data throughout the customer lifecycle. Its goal is to improve business relationships with customers, assist in customer retention, and drive sales growth.

**Key Idea:** Customer points of contact (channels) are critical for collecting customer feedback (VoC - Voice of Customer) and communicating back.

**Components of a CRM System:**

*   **Customer Data Warehouse:** Central storage for all customer data, used by all CRM elements for fetching, updating, and adding information.
*   **OLAP & Data Mining:** Tools for advanced analysis of customer data to understand relationships, support decision-making, and help with customer acquisition.
    *   **OLAP (Online Analytical Processing):** Allows users to analyze data from different perspectives.
    *   **Data Mining:** Discovers patterns and insights from large datasets.
*   **Campaign System:** Provides services tailored to customer needs and recommends profitable business directions.
*   **Channel System:** Supports 1:1 or 1:N marketing through call centers, emails, and direct mails.
*   **Sales Support System:** Uses customer information for sales planning, customer management, performance evaluation, and direct sales staff support.
*   **Customer Service System:** Leverages VoC for customer service support and product maintenance.

**Benefits of CRM Deployment:**

*   **Improved Customer Relationships:** Prevents customer churn and increases loyalty.
*   **Enhanced Service Quality:** Analyzes customer tastes to provide high-quality, tailored services.
*   **Increased Sales:** Induces linked sales (cross-selling) and upstream sales (up-selling).
*   **Competitive Advantage:** Builds a strong position through differentiated products and services.
*   **Marketing Opportunities:** Attracts new customers, invigorates existing ones, increases earnings and customer lifetime value.
*   **Effective Marketing Management:** Develops products based on customer requirements, observes market reactions, and strengthens loyalty.
*   **Optimized Customer Channels:** Secures the best channels, minimizes customer management costs.

---

### Section 2: Product Lifecycle Management (PLM)

**What is PLM?**
PLM is a solution for managing the entire lifecycle of a product, from its initial design concept through production, service, and disposal. Its aim is to increase a product's added value and reduce costs.

**Definition:** PLM is a support system that integrates and manages all product-related information (e.g., drawings, documents, CAD/CAM data, parts info, design changes, process info) generated throughout an enterprise's product development and manufacturing lifecycle.
*   **CAD/CAM (Computer-Aided Design/Manufacturing):** Software used for designing and manufacturing products.

**Configuration of PLM:**
PLM manages the entire product cycle, from planning to post-sales services. It requires integration with other business systems.

**Key PLM Components:**

*   **Project Management:** Manages schedules, outputs, and tasks for product development.
*   **Drawing Management:** Handles drawing approval, information, revisions, and viewing.
*   **Design Change Management:** Manages processes for Engineering Change Requests (ECR) and Engineering Change Notices (ECN), and component revisions.
*   **BOM Management:** Links to CAD, manages Bill of Materials (BOM) revisions, generates and approves Engineering BOM (EBOM) and Manufacturing BOM (MBOM).
*   **Technology Management:** Manages listing, correction, and revision of technology documents; links to related information.
*   **Product Information Management:** Manages model, product, and goods codes, product specifications, and related outputs.
*   **Security Management:** Ensures document/drawing encryption, leakage prevention, security level settings, and Digital Rights Management (DRM)/Data Loss Prevention (DLP).

**PLM Trends:**

*   **Evolution:** Started in the 1990s as storage for engineering design information.
*   **Consolidation:** Moved towards centralizing scattered information, standardizing development processes, and implementing workflow-based change management for efficiency.
*   **Integration:** Current trend involves consolidating PLM by integrating it with **ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning)** and **MDM (Master Data Management)** solutions for enterprise-wide data management.
*   **Future:** Expansion into "social PLM" by linking with external data.

---

### Section 3: IT Business Decision-Making Support Systems

**The Need for Decision Support:**
In today's fast-changing business environment, enterprises need quick, rational decisions based on vast amounts of internal and external information. Manual analysis of large datasets is impractical, leading to a high demand for systems that can support complex, time-sensitive analyses.

**Main Decision Support Systems:**

1.  **Decision-Making Support System (DSS):**
    *   **Purpose:** Used for decisions requiring quantitative analysis.
    *   **Examples:** Analyzing Return on Investment (ROI), break-even points.

2.  **Business Intelligence (BI) System:**
    *   **Purpose:** Enables agile responses by monitoring the business environment and detecting changes.
    *   **Method:** Achieves this through discovery, extraction, and analysis of business data.

**Understanding Enterprise Data Warehouse (EDW)**

The EDW is a fundamental component underpinning enterprise data analytics, including DSS and BI.

**What is EDW?**
EDW is a system that integrates internal and external data to address user information analysis requests by subject matter. It acts as the backbone infrastructure for all enterprise data.
*   **Evolution:** Initially focused on internal data; now integrates both internal and external information for forecasting.

**Why is EDW Necessary?**

*   **Uniformity of Viewpoint:** Consolidates all critical internal and external information into master data for consistent organizational understanding.
*   **Strategic Forecasting:** Provides sufficient forecasting capability for strategic choices and responding to changing user requirements and business environments.
*   **Resource Integration:** Helps integrate information resources and reorganize management systems to prevent data duplication.

**Characteristics of the EDW:**

1.  **Subject-Oriented:**
    *   Structures the system around specific topics for analysis (e.g., customers, products), rather than daily transactions.
    *   Extracts and integrates relevant internal and external data.

2.  **Integrated:**
    *   Combines data from various sources.
    *   Ensures different data formats are converted and expressed in a uniform format during extraction.

3.  **Time-Variant:**
    *   Data accuracy is preserved over time.
    *   Time elements (day, week, month) are properly reflected, allowing for historical analysis.

4.  **Non-volatile:**
    *   Once data is recorded, its properties generally do not change to maintain analytical consistency.
    *   Stored data is typically read-only and is not deleted unless specific rules or events require it.

**Configuration of EDW:**

*   **Macro View:** Encompasses the entire process: collecting, transforming, loading data from operational systems; analyzing data to meet requirements; and visualizing results to assist decision-making.
*   **Micro View:** Refers specifically to the repository where the data is stored.

---


---


## Pages 97-101

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business Decision-Making Support Systems

This guide covers essential concepts related to Product Lifecycle Management (PLM), Enterprise Data Warehouses (EDW), Decision Support Systems (DSS), and Business Intelligence (BI).

---

### 1. Product Lifecycle Management (PLM)

**What it is:**
*   A centralized system that consolidates information related to product and project development.
*   Helps manage increasing complexity in product development.

**Key Functions:**
*   **BOM Management:** Manages the **Bill of Materials** (a complete list of raw materials, parts, and assemblies needed to build a product).
*   **Development Process Standardization:** Ensures consistent processes across projects.
*   **Workflow-based Change Management:** Manages changes efficiently through defined workflows.

**Benefits:**
*   Maximizes product development efficiency.

**Modern Trends:**
*   **Integration:** PLM is increasingly integrated with **ERP (Enterprise Resource Planning)** and **MDM (Master Data Management)** solutions.
    *   **ERP:** Software that integrates core business processes (e.g., finance, HR, supply chain).
    *   **MDM:** Manages consistent master data across the enterprise.
*   **Enterprise-wide Data Management:** Aims to manage reference data from an entire organizational perspective.
*   **Future:** Expansion into "Social PLM" by linking with external data.

---

### 2. IT Business Decision-Making Support Systems

Businesses need accurate and timely information to make rational decisions, especially in fast-changing environments. Manual analysis of large data volumes is impractical, leading to the need for specialized systems.

**Two Leading Systems:**
1.  **Decision Support System (DSS):** Focuses on quantitative analysis for specific decisions (e.g., ROI, break-even points).
2.  **Business Intelligence (BI):** Monitors the business environment, detects changes, and provides insights for agile responses through data discovery, extraction, and analysis.

---

### 3. Enterprise Data Warehouse (EDW)

The EDW is a foundational data repository for enterprise data analytics, underpinning both DSS and BI.

**A. Definition of EDW:**
*   A system that integrates internal and external enterprise data.
*   Organizes data by "subject matter" to fulfill user information analysis requests.
*   Requires robust infrastructure to support enterprise data across all business aspects.

**B. Evolution:**
*   Initially focused on internal data.
*   Now evolving into a forecasting system that integrates both internal and external information.

**C. Necessity for EDW:**
*   **Uniform Viewpoint:** Consolidates all enterprise information (internal & external) into master data for a consistent organizational perspective.
*   **Forecasting & Strategy:** Enables diverse data analyses to support strategic choices and adapt to changing user requirements and business environments.
*   **Data Integrity:** Integrates information resources and reorganizes management systems to prevent data duplication.

**D. Characteristics of EDW:**
*   **Subject-Oriented:** Structures the system around specific topics for data analysis, not daily transactions. Extracts and integrates internal/external data. Standardizes data formats.
*   **Integrated:** Combines data from various sources into a consistent format.
*   **Time Variant:** Stores data reflecting specific time elements (day, week, month) while maintaining accuracy over time.
*   **Non-volatile:** Once data is stored, its properties do not change. Data is primarily read-only and is not deleted unless specific rules dictate.

**E. Configuration of EDW:**
*   **Macro Perspective:** The entire process of collecting, transforming, loading, analyzing, and visualizing data for decision support.
*   **Micro Perspective:** Refers specifically to the central repository where data is stored.
*   **Process:** Transaction data from legacy systems is stored in the Data Warehouse, then analyzed and visualized using BI solutions.

---

### 4. Decision Support System (DSS)

**A. Concept of DSS:**
*   An interactive system designed to support decision-makers during the decision-making process.
*   Assists in solving **semi-structural** (partially defined) and **non-structural** (complex, undefined) problems.
*   **Core Elements:** Enterprise data (internal/external) and analytical models for processing quantitative data.

**B. Characteristics of DSS:**
*   **Resolves Non-structural Problems:** Primarily assists CEOs and middle managers with complex issues.
*   **Easy-to-Use User Interface:** Provides interactive interfaces that are user-friendly.
*   **Improves Decision-Making Effectiveness:** Focuses on finding optimal solutions rather than just processing efficiency.
*   **Model and Database Support:** Offers various tools like financial/statistical models, simulations, and statistical techniques to solve complex problems.

**C. Configuration of DSS:**
*   Comprises a **Document System**, a **Model System**, and a **Knowledge System**.
*   Users interact through a **User Interface** to access information and manage data/models.

**D. Constituent Elements of DSS:**
*   **Database Management System:** Stores all corporate activity data (financial, accounting, marketing, production, HR) used as basic decision data.
*   **Model Base Management System:** Analytical tools (e.g., statistical, forecasting, linear planning, simulation models) developed to solve similar types of problems consistently, improving efficiency and accuracy.
*   **Knowledge Base System:** Provides qualitative information to support unstructured decision-making problems that are hard to quantify.
*   **User Interface Management System:** The communication channel between the decision-maker and the DSS, ensuring flexibility, performance, and convenience.

**E. DSS Data Models:**
*   Provide a framework for analyzing data to support rational decisions.
*   Continuously developed and improved, with a recent trend towards integrating **AI (Artificial Intelligence)** for better forecasting.

**Types of DSS Data Models:**
*   **What-if Analysis:** Examines how changes in one variable impact another, useful for testing assumptions about uncertain future situations.
*   **Sensitivity Analysis:** Observes how changes in one or two input variables affect other variables in an equation model.
*   **Goal-seeking:** Determines the values of variables needed to achieve a predefined goal.
*   **Optimization Analysis:** Finds the optimal value(s) for target variables under specific constraints.

---

### 5. Business Intelligence (BI)

**A. Concept of BI:**
*   A set of processes to improve business decisions and performance by summarizing, analyzing, and using enterprise data and information.
*   While DSS is often for high-level decision-makers, BI is designed to be adopted by regular employees for everyday decision support.
*   **"Intelligence" (Hans Luhn, IBM, 1958):** The ability to understand relationships between facts to achieve a desired goal.
*   **Evolution:** BI evolved from DSS, with analysis technologies like **Data Warehouses** and **OLAP (Online Analytical Processing)** developing in the late 1980s based on DSS principles.
    *   **OLAP:** Enables users to easily extract and view data from different business perspectives.

**B. Key Purpose:**
*   To improve the quality of business management decisions and overall business performance through comprehensive data analysis.

---


---


## Pages 100-104


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide (Pages 100-104)

## 1. Decision Support Systems (DSS)

**What is DSS?**
*   A system focused on improving the **effectiveness** of decision-making, aiming for optimal solutions.
*   Helps solve complex problems by providing financial/statistical models, simulations, and analytical tools.

**DSS Configuration & Components:**

A DSS is made up of interactive systems:
1.  **Database Management System:**
    *   Stores core corporate data (financial, accounting, marketing, production, HR).
    *   This data serves as the foundation for decision-making.
2.  **Model Base Management System:**
    *   An analytical tool designed to consistently solve similar problems.
    *   Uses quantified models (statistical, forecasting, linear planning, simulation) to increase problem-solving efficiency and accuracy.
3.  **Knowledge Base System:**
    *   Provides qualitative information to support solving unstructured decision problems that are difficult to quantify.
4.  **User Interface Management System:**
    *   The communication window between the decision-maker and the DSS.
    *   Ensures flexibility, performance, and user convenience.

**How DSS Works:**
*   Users access the knowledge system through the user interface to get information for decisions.
*   Users also access the model and database systems for management tasks.

**DSS Data Models:**
*   Provide a framework for data analysis, helping decision-makers make rational choices.
*   Continuously developed and improved, with increasing use of **Artificial Intelligence (AI)** for better forecasting.

**Types of DSS Data Models:**
*   **What-if Analysis:** Examines how changes in one variable impact another (e.g., "What if sales increase by 10%?"). Useful for testing assumptions.
*   **Sensitivity Analysis:** Observes how changes to one or two variables affect other variables within an equation model.
*   **Goal-seeking:** Determines the variable values needed to achieve a specific goal (e.g., "What sales volume do we need to hit a profit target?").
*   **Optimization Analysis:** Finds the best (optimal) value for one or more target variables given certain constraints.

---

## 2. Business Intelligence (BI)

**What is BI?**
*   A set of processes that improve business decisions and performance by summarizing, analyzing, and using enterprise data and information.
*   Evolved from DSS, extending decision support to regular employees, not just top decision-makers.
*   **Intelligence:** The ability to understand relationships between facts to achieve desired goals (Hans Luhn, IBM, 1958).

**BI Configuration & Key Operations:**
BI systems collect, analyze, and visualize data, organically linked to decision support.

1.  **ETL (Extraction, Transformation, Load):**
    *   Processes data from various sources (databases, applications, web services).
    *   Ensures consistency and compatibility, especially for **OLTP (Online Transaction Processing)** data.
2.  **Data Storage:**
    *   **Data Warehouse:** Centralized repository for integrated data.
    *   **Data Mart:** Smaller, focused data store for specific business functions or departments, allowing multi-dimensional analysis.
3.  **Analysis Tools:**
    *   Perform various analyses (e.g., **OLAP - Online Analytical Processing** for multidimensional expert analysis).
4.  **Visualization:**
    *   **Dashboards:** Key BI component, providing visual presentations of key metrics (charts, simulations, statistical analysis) for quick insights.

**Benefits of BI:**
*   **Decision Makers:** Get visual analyses of key management metrics.
*   **Field Managers:** Use multidimensional analytical tools (OLAP) for expert-level insights.

**Types of BI:**

| Classification   | Main Business Focus                   | Key Users                 | Measurement Target                                        | Frequency                  | Types of Data           |
| :--------------- | :------------------------------------ | :------------------------ | :-------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------- | :---------------------- |
| **Strategy BI**  | Realizing long-term goals and targets | CEO, decision-makers      | Tracking feedback on strategic plans                      | Monthly, quarterly, annually | Past data, forecast data |
| **Analysis BI**  | Analyzing info/data for corporate goals | Task supervisor, analyst  | Tracking and analyzing feedback on strategy execution     | Daily, weekly, monthly     | Past data, forecast data |
| **Operations BI** | Managing daily business operations    | Task specialist, operator | Personalized BI for supervisors for performance insights | On the spot, any time      | Present/working hours   |

**BI Dashboard:**
*   A crucial data visualization tool for intuitive decision-making.
*   Displays the status of key quantified metrics and performance indicators (e.g., sales, costs, profits, risks) on a single screen.
*   Helps decision-makers quickly identify areas needing attention.
*   Easily customizable and integrates with tools like spreadsheets and real-time data analysis.

---

## 3. IT Service Management (ITSM)

**What is ITSM?**
*   A systematized method for managing IT services and their quality.
*   Based on best practices outlined in **ITIL (IT Infrastructure Library)**.
*   Can be outsourced depending on business needs.

**Key Concepts & Relationships:**

*   **ITIL (IT Infrastructure Library):** The standard model (best practice) for IT service management. ITSM uses ITIL as its foundation.
*   **SLA (Service Level Agreement):** A formal agreement between a service provider and a customer that defines the level of service expected. An IT service is delivered only after an SLA is signed, which then becomes the standard for measuring service quality.
*   **SLM (Service Level Management):** The process of systematically managing IT services to ensure agreed-upon service levels (defined in the SLA) are met.
*   **CSR (Customer Service Request):** The process through which users formally request IT services.

**How ITSM Works:**
1.  **Agreement:** An SLA is signed, setting the service level between the user and service supplier.
2.  **Request:** Users submit IT service requests via the CSR process.
3.  **Delivery & Management:** IT services are delivered at the agreed-upon level, and their quality is systematically managed using SLM based on the SLA standards.

**Leading Standards in ITSM:**
*   **eSCM (eSourcing Capability Model):** An international quality assessment model for service providers to objectively evaluate their capabilities in delivering IT services. It guides IT service implementation across all business phases.
*   **ISO/IEC 20000:** An international standard for IT service management, also rooted in ITIL.


---

---

## Learning Guide: Business Intelligence & IT Service Management

### 1. Business Intelligence (BI) Fundamentals

**What is BI?** Business Intelligence involves using data to make better business decisions.

#### 1.1 Types of Business Intelligence (BI)

| Classification | Main Business Focus           | Key Users                     | Measurement Target               | Frequency                  | Types of Data           |
| :------------- | :---------------------------- | :---------------------------- | :------------------------------- | :------------------------- | :---------------------- |
| **Strategy BI**    | Realizing long-term goals & targets | CEO, Decision Makers          | Feedback on strategy plans       | Monthly, Quarterly, Annually | Past data, Forecast data |
| **Analysis BI**    | Analyzing info/data for corporate goals | Task Supervisors, Analysts    | Feedback on strategy execution   | Daily, Weekly, Monthly     | Past data, Forecast data |
| **Operations BI**  | Managing daily business operations  | Task Specialists, Operators   | Personalized performance insights| On-the-spot, Any time      | Present/Working hours data |

#### 1.2 The BI Dashboard

*   **Definition:** A data visualization tool that displays the status of key quantified metrics and performance metrics for an enterprise on a single screen.
*   **Purpose:** Helps decision-makers quickly identify areas needing attention (e.g., sales, costs, profits, risks) and make fast, intuitive judgments.
*   **Features:**
    *   Easy to customize screen configuration.
    *   Supports integration with tools like spreadsheets and real-time data analysis.
*   **Importance:** One of the most critical BI functions for facilitating quick, intuitive decision-making.

### 2. IT Service Management (ITSM)

#### 2.1 Overview of ITSM

*   **Definition:** A systematized method for managing IT services and ensuring their quality. Commonly referred to as ITSM.
*   **Core Concepts & Relationships:**
    *   **ITIL (IT Infrastructure Library):** The standard model or "best practice" framework that ITSM uses for guidance.
    *   **IT Outsourcing:** ITSM functions can be outsourced to external service providers.
    *   **SLA (Service Level Agreement):** A formal agreement signed between a service provider and a customer, defining the specific level of IT service to be delivered. It serves as the standard for measuring service quality.
    *   **SLM (Service Level Management):** The systematic process of managing IT services to ensure they meet the agreed-upon standards defined in the SLA.
    *   **CSR (Customer Service Request):** The process customers use to request an IT service.
*   **Leading Standards Associated with ITSM (Rooted in ITIL):**
    *   **eSCM (eSourcing Capability Model):** An international quality assessment model used by service providers to objectively evaluate their quality and capabilities in delivering IT services. It guides IT service implementation across all business phases.
    *   **ISO/IEC 20000:** An international standard that specifies the requirements for IT service management activities. It was developed from the BS15000 certification.

### 3. IT Infrastructure Library (ITIL)

#### 3.1 Definition of ITIL

*   **What it is:** A comprehensive framework of "best practices" for IT service management. It compiles proven approaches to guide organizations in delivering efficient and effective IT services.
*   **Origin:** Developed by the Central Computer & Telecommunications Agency (CCTA) of the UK in the late 1980s for public agency users.
*   **Purpose:** To provide standard guidelines for managing IT services, helping organizations clearly understand their IT service framework and achieve business objectives.
*   **Status:** An intellectual property and registered trademark managed by the British government, widely recognized as a de-facto global standard for IT service management.

#### 3.2 History of ITIL

*   **Version 1 (1980s):** Developed to address the British government's reliance on IT, published as a collection of specialized IT service documents.
*   **Version 2 (2000-2001):** Introduced with a focus on two main areas: Service Delivery and Service Support.
*   **Version 3 (2007/2011):** Announced in 2007 (known as ITIL 2007 edition) and improved in 2011. It introduced a "lifecycle approach" and a stronger focus on business value.

#### 3.3 ITIL v2 Process Areas (Key Elements)

ITIL v2 primarily focused on two core areas:

*   **1. Service Delivery:** Focuses on the strategic and tactical aspects of planning and providing IT services.
    *   **Service Level Management:** Manages and ensures service quality as dictated by SLAs.
    *   **Capacity Management:** Estimates required resources and manages transaction loads.
    *   **Availability Management:** Ensures the continuity and control of IT services.
    *   **Financial Management:** Manages the quantitative costs and income associated with IT services.
    *   **IT Service Continuity Management:** Manages efforts for disaster recovery and service resilience.
*   **2. Service Support:** Focuses on the day-to-day operational support of IT services.
    *   **Service Desk:** The single point of contact for users to report incidents, problems, and inquiries.
    *   **Incident Management:** Manages and evaluates the impact and resolution of service malfunctions.
    *   **Problem Management:** Investigates the root causes of incidents and applies emergency measures to solve them.
    *   **Change Management:** Manages and controls changes to IT services, programs, and infrastructure.
    *   **Configuration Management:** Manages information about IT assets and their configurations.
    *   **Release Management:** Manages the planning, building, testing, and deployment of approved products and services.
*   **Other Mentioned Areas:** Business Perspective (e.g., business continuity, outsourcing), and ICT Infrastructure Management (e.g., network, operations, system management).

#### 3.4 ITIL v3 Process (Lifecycle Approach)

ITIL v3 evolved from v2 by:
*   Becoming a **business value model**.
*   Supporting **IT governance** (a previous deficiency).
*   Extending IT service management to **all business areas**.
*   Strengthening service support and delivery, and incorporating requirements from ISO/IEC 20000.
*   **Goal:** To align IT with business strategies through a lifecycle perspective and continuously improve IT services.

ITIL v3 consists of **five process areas** that form a continuous, repeated lifecycle for service improvement:

*   **1. Service Strategy:**
    *   **Purpose:** To define the strategic perspective of IT service management, ensuring IT services are aligned with business objectives.
    *   **Key Activities:** IT service strategy planning, organization and relationship specification, IT investment management, understanding customers, prioritizing competition and investment, HR management, compliance with external requirements.
*   **2. Service Design:**
    *   **Purpose:** To design new or changed IT services to meet business requirements and strategic objectives.
    *   **Key Activities:** Negotiation and contract drafting based on requirement analysis, designing service solutions (applications, systems, processes), evaluating alternative solutions, and procuring preferred solutions.
*   **3. Service Transition:**
    *   **Purpose:** To build, test, and deploy new or changed services into the live operational environment.
    *   **Key Activities:** Release planning and preparation, building/testing/piloting services, establishing and preparing a transition plan, managing the transition/adoption/disposal of services, service verification and testing, transition review and termination.
*   **4. Service Operation:**
    *   **Purpose:** To deliver and support IT services efficiently and effectively in the live environment, ensuring services meet customer expectations.
    *   **Key Activities:** Customer request processing and communication management, event/incident/problem management, service level metrics management, monitoring efficiency (e.g., safety, accessibility management).
*   **5. Continual Service Improvement (CSI):**
    *   **Purpose:** To continuously improve the effectiveness and efficiency of IT services and processes across all lifecycle stages.
    *   **Key Activities:** Participating across strategy/design/implementation phases, analyzing service reports and identifying trends, establishing performance evaluation baselines, implementing the **PDCA Model** (Plan-Do-Check-Action cycle), operating service improvement programs, and providing feedback to earlier lifecycle phases.
    *   **Note:** ITIL v3 strengthened the performance evaluation (ROI) area significantly compared to v2.

---

## Pages 106-110

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide (Pages 106-110)

### 1. ITIL v3 Process Overview

ITIL v3 (Information Technology Infrastructure Library Version 3) is a framework that evolved from ITIL v2 to provide a business value model for IT service management. It supports IT governance and extends service management across all business areas.

**Key Features of ITIL v3:**
*   **Lifecycle Approach:** Follows a continuous improvement cycle.
*   **Business Value-Centered:** Focuses on delivering value to the business.
*   **Strengthens Performance Evaluation (ROI):** Addresses a deficiency in v2.
*   **Incorporates ISO/IEC 20000 Requirements.**
*   **Uses PDCA Model:** Plan-Do-Check-Action for continuous improvement.

**The 5 Core ITIL v3 Process Areas (Lifecycle):**

1.  **Service Strategy:**
    *   **Purpose:** Define IT service strategy, align with business goals.
    *   **Key Activities:** Planning IT services, organization/relationship specification, IT investment management, understanding customers, setting competitive priorities, HR management, compliance.

2.  **Service Design:**
    *   **Purpose:** Design new or changed services to meet business requirements.
    *   **Key Activities:** Requirement analysis, negotiation/contract drafting, service solution design, evaluating alternatives, procuring preferred solutions, designing applications, systems, and processes.

3.  **Service Transition:**
    *   **Purpose:** Build, test, and deploy services into the live environment.
    *   **Key Activities:** Release planning/preparation, build/test/pilot services, establish transition plans, transition/adoption/disposal, review and termination, service verification.

4.  **Service Operation:**
    *   **Purpose:** Deliver and support services effectively and efficiently.
    *   **Key Activities:** Customer request processing, communication management, event/incident/problem management, service level metrics management, safety/accessibility management.

5.  **Continual Service Improvement (CSI):**
    *   **Purpose:** Improve IT services and processes over time.
    *   **Key Activities:** Participating in strategy/design/implementation phases, service report analysis, trend identification, establishing performance baselines, operating improvement programs, feedback across all lifecycle phases.

### 2. ITIL v2 vs. ITIL v3 Comparison

| Feature             | ITIL Version 2                               | ITIL Version 3                                                                                                   |
| :------------------ | :------------------------------------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Volumes**         | 8 (Core: Service Support, Delivery)          | 5 major + additional volumes (Introduction & Dic)                                                                |
| **Processes**       | 1 function + 10 processes                    | 5 major processes                                                                                                |
| **Usage**           | Best Practice, ISO 20000 Guideline (Part II) | Best Practice, Framework + Standard expansion, ISO 20000 revision                                                |
| **Key Points**      | Book of best practices, service level-centric  | More libraries, business value-centered (IT Governance), Lifecycle Approach, Continual Service Improvement       |
| **Limitations (v2)** | Lacked IT service-wide support, weak business alignment, inadequate IT governance, gap with current processes (SOA, BSM). |                                                                                                                  |
| **Improvements (v3)** |                                              | Presents IT service lifecycle & business-driven services, design/execution/improvement model, links to SOA, BRM, IT operation. |

### 3. Understanding Service Level Agreement (SLA) & Related Concepts

**SLA (Service Level Agreement):**
*   An agreement between an IT service provider and its customers.
*   Defines the scope, items, form, performance, measurement methods, and price of the provided service.
*   Crucial for managing expectations and preventing conflicts.

**SLM (Service Level Management):**
*   The framework for continuously monitoring, changing, and managing SLAs.
*   Ensures agreed service quality and works to improve service levels and customer confidence.

**SOW (Statement of Work):**
*   A work statement that specifies the detailed requirements of a service or work described in the SLA or for a project.

**Effects of SLA Deployment:**
*   **Seamless Communication:** Facilitates dialogue between consumers and suppliers.
*   **Prevention of Conflicts:** Narrows expectation gaps and provides a basis for resolution.
*   **Objective Evaluation:** Enables quantitative assessment of service quality.
*   **Continuous Control:** Establishes a system for managing and controlling services.

### 4. Component Elements of an SLA & Metrics

An SLA sets target levels, provides measurement standards, and defines reporting for service levels.

**SLA Component Elements:**

1.  **Service Level Metrics:** Quantitatively judge service levels for each service area (e.g., uptime, response time).
2.  **Service Level Objectives (SLO):** Establish target and minimum service levels. Can include penalties for underperformance and incentives for exceeding targets.
3.  **Service Level Measurements:** Define how metrics are measured (interval, team, frequency).
4.  **Service Level Reports:** Specify the format and method for reporting service levels.

**Examples of SLA Metrics (also called "Service Level Items" or "Configuration Items"):**

*   **Application System:** On-time processing rate, program revision rate, system response speed/time, number of malfunctions.
*   **Hardware (HW):** System operation rate, backup compliance, malfunction handling rate, number of HW malfunctions, disk usage.
*   **Network:** Line failure rate, network availability/utilization, troubleshooting compliance.
*   **Service Desk:** Call processing rate, number of calls handled, call waiting rate, help desk system availability, employee absenteeism.
*   **Security:** User request processing rate, customer profile accuracy, security training sessions, personal information inspection count.
*   **Strategy:** Number of suggestions received, compliance with training plans.

### 5. Understanding Service Level Management (SLM)

SLM is a core ITIL process that manages service level objectives (SLOs) within an SLA and notifies of any infringements. It's essential for managing IT service levels.

**Component Elements of SLM:**

1.  **Service Catalog:** A document listing all available services and their metadata.
2.  **SLA (Service Level Agreement):** The written contract on agreed IT service levels.
3.  **SLO (Service Level Objectives):** The specific list of IT services covered by the SLA and their target levels.
4.  **OLA (Operational Level Agreement):** An internal agreement between departments within a service supplier to ensure effective communication and management of the SLA.
5.  **Service Quality Plan:** An internal plan detailing everything required to ensure agreed service levels.
6.  **Service Report:** Periodic assessment of SLA violations.
7.  **SLM Engine:** An automated system to measure metrics, automate reports, and monitor services in real-time.

**Operating Criteria for SLAs and SLMs:**
*   Evaluation criteria must be **specific, quantitative, and objective.**
*   Criteria must be **verified.**
*   Ensure **seamless baseline setting** and **smooth management of changes.**

## Pages 109-113

---

## Learning Guide: Service Level Management and IT Business Performance

### 1. Service Level Agreements (SLA)

An **SLA (Service Level Agreement)** is a formal contract between a service provider and a customer. It defines the service to be provided, the expected level of service, and the responsibilities of both parties.

*   **Key Benefits of SLAs:**
    *   **Seamless Communication:** Acts as a clear communication tool between customers and service suppliers.
    *   **Conflict Prevention:** Reduces the gap between customer expectations and actual service, providing a framework for dispute resolution.
    *   **Objective Evaluation:** Allows for quantitative and objective measurement of service quality.
    *   **Continuous Control:** Provides a structured system for managing and monitoring services.

*   **Core Components of an SLA:**
    *   **Service Level Metrics:** Quantitative measures used to judge service levels (e.g., uptime, response time).
    *   **Service Level Objectives (SLOs):** Specific target levels and minimum acceptable levels for each metric. These often include penalties for underperformance and incentives for exceeding targets.
    *   **Service Level Measurements:** Details how metrics are measured (e.g., measurement intervals, responsible team, frequency).
    *   **Service Level Reports:** Specifies the format and method for reporting service levels to stakeholders.

*   **Examples of SLA Metrics (Service Level Items / Configuration Items - CIs):**
    These metrics cover various aspects of IT services:
    *   **Application Systems:** On-time processing rates, system response speed, number of malfunctions.
    *   **System Hardware (HW):** System operation rate, backup compliance, malfunction handling rate.
    *   **Network:** Line failure rate, network availability, utilization rate.
    *   **Service Desk:** Call processing rate, call waiting rate, help desk system availability.
    *   **Security:** Immediate processing rate for IT requests, security training sessions, personal information inspection frequency.
    *   **Strategy:** Number of suggestions received, compliance with training plans.

### 2. Service Level Management (SLM)

**SLM (Service Level Management)** is a core process within ITIL (Information Technology Infrastructure Library). It ensures that the agreed-upon service quality levels are consistently delivered, boosting customer confidence and driving continuous service improvement.

*   **Purpose:** SLM manages the **Service Level Objectives (SLOs)** specified in an SLA and identifies any infringements of the agreement. It's crucial for effective IT service level management.

*   **Key Elements of SLM:**
    *   **Service Catalog:** A document listing all available IT services with their descriptions.
    *   **Service Level Agreement (SLA):** The formal, written contract outlining mutually agreed IT service levels.
    *   **Service Level Objectives (SLO):** The specific IT services and their performance targets covered by the SLA.
    *   **Operational Level Agreement (OLA):** Internal agreements between different departments within the service provider. These OLAs ensure internal teams can effectively support the overall SLA.
    *   **Service Quality Plan:** An internal plan detailing all requirements to ensure agreed-upon service levels are met.
    *   **Service Report:** Periodic assessments that track compliance with the SLA and report any violations.
    *   **SLM Engine:** An automated system designed to measure service level metrics, generate reports, and monitor service performance in real-time.

*   **Critical Considerations for SLA & SLM Operations:**
    *   **Evaluation Criteria:** Must be specific, quantitative, and objective.
    *   **Verifiability:** Criteria should be easy to verify.
    *   **Baseline & Change Management:** Establish clear baselines and manage any changes smoothly.
    *   **Clear Responsibilities:** Define responsibilities for each item to prevent potential disputes.
    *   **Automated Tools:** Utilize reliable, automated management tools to streamline task execution.

### 3. IT Business Performance Evaluation

This process reviews how IT contributes to an organization's overall growth and success.

*   **Evolution of Evaluation:**
    *   **Historically:** Focused primarily on **financial aspects**, quantifying IT's direct impact on earnings. This approach was limited.
    *   **Currently:** Expanded to **comprehensive evaluations** that include both financial and **non-financial aspects**. This includes factors like enhancing corporate image, improving employee morale, and boosting job satisfaction.

*   **Key Principle:** A critical aspect is aligning individual employee performance goals with the broader enterprise performance goals.
    *   This requires strong communication among employees.
    *   Organizations must effectively balance "top-down" (management-set) and "bottom-up" (employee-driven) goal setting.

*   **Key Terms:**
    *   **Financial Performance Evaluations:** Assessing IT's impact on financial results.
    *   **BSC (Balanced Scorecard):** A strategic performance management framework.
    *   **IT-BSC (IT Balanced Scorecard):** A BSC specifically adapted for IT organizations.
    *   **KPI (Key Performance Indicator):** Measurable values that demonstrate how effectively a company is achieving key business objectives.
    *   **MBO (Management by Objectives):** A management model aiming to improve performance by clearly defining objectives that are agreed to by both management and employees.

### 4. Case Study: Korean Intellectual Property Office (KIPO) BSC Implementation

**Background:** KIPO aimed to improve patent administration and create customer-oriented services, with a vision to promote technology innovation and protect intellectual property. As a public institution, they needed to balance public benefit with financial considerations.

**Solution:** In 2005, KIPO implemented a **Balanced Scorecard (BSC) system** to link individual employee performance targets directly to KIPO's five strategic organizational objectives.

*   **KIPO's 3-Phase BSC Implementation Process:**

    1.  **Phase 1 (Late 2004): Establishing the Strategic Framework**
        *   **Defined:** Mission, vision, and strategic goals for the organization.
        *   **Derived:** 19 Key Success Factors (KSFs) and 32 Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) to achieve these goals.
        *   **Completed:** Strategic framework for the office.
        *   **Communicated:** Department-level performance goals, KSFs, and KPIs.
        *   **Formalized:** Job performance agreements signed between the commissioner, bureau/department heads, and team managers based on these metrics.

    2.  **Phase 2 (Early 2005): Individual Performance Alignment & HR Integration**
        *   **Designed:** Individual-level performance management model, aligning with the organizational BSC.
        *   **Distributed:** Organizational performance indicators to individual employees, ensuring their goals reflected the broader organizational scores.
        *   **Established:** An individual performance and competency evaluation system to motivate employees.
        *   **Integrated:** Linked individual performance evaluation results more closely to the compensation system, shifting towards a performance-centered HR policy.

    3.  **Phase 3 (April-June 2005): Information System Deployment**
        *   **Implemented:** A dedicated information system for performance management, using a "best solution."
        *   **Established:** A strategic operational system to continuously monitor strategy execution and enable rapid responses to changes.
