## Pages 112-116


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide derived from the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business Performance Evaluation & Ethics

### 1. Introduction to IT Business Performance Evaluation

*   **Purpose:** To review IT's contribution to enterprise growth.
*   **Evolution:**
    *   **Past:** Focused primarily on **financial aspects** (easy to quantify).
    *   **Present:** Expanded to a **comprehensive evaluation** covering:
        *   **Financial aspects**
        *   **Non-financial aspects:** Corporate image enhancement, employee morale/satisfaction.
*   **Key Challenge:** Aligning individual performance goals with enterprise performance goals. This requires effective communication.

### 2. Overview of IT Business Performance Evaluation Techniques

Effective IT business performance evaluation ensures IT investments align with business strategy and provides feedback. The main techniques are:

1.  **Financial Performance Evaluation:** Focuses on quantitative financial benefits.
2.  **Balanced Scorecard (BSC) Assessment:** Complements financial evaluation by adding qualitative and non-financial perspectives.

*   **Key Tools:**
    *   **Key Performance Indicators (KPI):** Measures the level of goal attainment.
    *   **Management by Objectives (MBO):** System for setting objective levels for employee skill development.

### 3. Financial Performance Evaluation Technique

**A. Overview**

*   **Nature:** Traditional, quantitative, uses "currency" as a common unit. Also called "quantitative performance evaluations."
*   **Purpose:**
    *   Shareholders and managers prioritize financial results.
    *   Provides a quick understanding of the management situation.
*   **Limitations:**
    *   **Result-oriented:** Tends to ignore the process of achieving results.
    *   **Low employee motivation:** Not a great booster for morale due to its abstract nature.
    *   **Abstract figures:** Difficult to convey meaning accurately to all organizational members.

**B. Types of Financial Performance Evaluation Techniques**

These techniques assess financial performance over a specific period or at a specific point in time.

| Technique                 | Description                                                                                             |
| :------------------------ | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **ROI** (Return on Investment) | Ratio of net effect to total cost. Used to assess investment feasibility. Does *not* estimate payback time. |
| **NPV** (Net Present Value)   | Relationship between cost and effect of present value, considering discount rate. Reflects future net profits and monetary value over time. Risks should be considered separately. |
| **IRR** (Internal Rate of Return) | Revenues from investments against cash flows. Expresses expected annual revenues to judge risk reduction. Does *not* consider investment size or payback period. |
| **PP** (Payback Period)       | Time taken for cumulative effect to exceed cumulative cost and reach the break-even point. Shows when revenue is generated, *not* how much. |

### 4. Balanced Scorecard (BSC) Technique

**A. Overview of the BSC Technique**

*   **Definition:** A balanced performance evaluation technique that assesses both financial and non-financial performances.
*   **Origin:** Introduced in 1992 by Harvard Business School Professor Robert Kaplan and consultant David Norton.
*   **Why BSC?**
    *   Traditional systems focused too much on financial indicators, making systematic strategy execution difficult.
    *   Necessity to consider non-financial evaluations.
*   **Purpose:**
    *   Maintains a balance between indicators.
    *   Concretizes and links strategies.
    *   Improves communication within the organization.

**B. Characteristics of BSC**

*   **Balance Between Indicators:**
    *   Considers multiple perspectives (beyond just financial).
    *   Balances short-term vs. long-term views.
    *   Balances leading (predictive) vs. trailing (historical) indicators.
*   **Concreteness of Strategy:**
    *   Secures strategy clarity through **KPIs**.
    *   Aims for company-wide optimization, not just partial.
    *   Aligns feasible strategies with correct business directions.
*   **Connectivity of Strategy:**
    *   Establishes **causal relationships** between strategies.
    *   Links core strategies after focused selection.
*   **Internal Communication Tool:**
    *   Builds executive capability using detailed KPIs.
    *   Serves as a common language across the organization.

**C. Component Elements of BSC**

BSC evaluates performance from four perspectives and includes elements to manage and achieve enterprise goals.

| Component Element  | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| :----------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Perspective**    | The four core viewpoints: Financial, Customer, Process, Learning & Growth.                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| **CSF**            | **Critical Success Factors:** Factors absolutely essential for successfully realizing an enterprise's vision and strategy.                                                                                                                                                                           |
| **Strategy Map**   | A visual tool showing the **causal relationships** among CSFs. It illustrates how an organization creates value by linking initiatives across the four perspectives.                                                                                                                                   |
| **KPI**            | **Key Performance Indicator:** A quantifiable measure to track the progress and success level of a CSF (and thus, a strategy).                                                                                                                                                                          |

**D. Four Perspectives of BSC**

The BSC manages both financial and non-financial views, with the four perspectives being organically interconnected:

1.  **Financial Perspective:** How do we look to shareholders? (e.g., profitability, revenue growth, cost reduction).
2.  **Customer Perspective:** How do customers see us? (e.g., customer satisfaction, market share, customer retention).
3.  **Process Perspective:** What must we excel at? (e.g., operational efficiency, quality, innovation, timely delivery).
4.  **Learning & Growth Perspective:** How can we sustain our ability to change and improve? (e.g., employee skills, IT capabilities, organizational culture, innovation capacity).

*   **Interconnection Example:** Improving employee skills (Learning & Growth) leads to better product quality and production efficiency (Process), which increases customer satisfaction (Customer), ultimately resulting in improved financial performance (Financial).

## Pages 115-119


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: Performance Evaluation Techniques

This guide covers financial performance evaluation, the Balanced Score Card (BSC) technique, IT-BSC, Key Performance Indicators (KPIs), and Management by Objectives (MBO).

---

### 1. Financial Performance Evaluation Techniques

These techniques assess investment feasibility and returns.

*   **Return on Investment (ROI)**
    *   **Definition:** Ratio of net financial effect to total cost.
    *   **Use:** Assesses investment feasibility.
    *   **Limitation:** Cannot estimate the time an investment needs to yield net income.

*   **Net Present Value (NPV)**
    *   **Definition:** Expresses the relationship between the cost and effect of a currency's present value, considering its discount rate.
    *   **Reflects:** Accurate future net profits and monetary value over time.
    *   **Note:** Risks associated with the payback period must be considered separately.

*   **Internal Rate of Return (IRR)**
    *   **Definition:** Revenues generated from investments against cash flows.
    *   **Expresses:** Expected annual revenues to judge risk reduction.
    *   **Limitation:** Does not consider investment size or payback period.

*   **Payback Period (PP)**
    *   **Definition:** The time it takes for cumulative effect to exceed cumulative cost and reach the break-even point.
    *   **Expresses:** Point of transition to surplus or visible success.
    *   **Shows:** *When* revenue is generated, but not *how much*.

---

### 2. Balanced Score Card (BSC) Technique

A performance management system that evaluates both financial and non-financial performance.

#### A) Overview of BSC

*   **What it is:** A balanced performance evaluation technique.
*   **Introduced by:** Robert Kaplan and David Norton in 1992.
*   **Why it's needed:** Traditional systems relied too heavily on financial indicators, making strategy execution difficult. BSC addresses this by incorporating non-financial evaluations.
*   **Purpose:** Balances indicators, concretizes and links strategies, and improves internal communication.

#### B) Characteristics of BSC

*   **Balance between indicators:**
    *   Approaches performance from multiple perspectives (not just financial).
    *   Balances short-term and long-term views.
    *   Balances leading (predictive) and trailing (result-oriented) indicators.
*   **Concreteness of strategy:**
    *   Secures strategy clarity through Key Performance Indicators (KPIs).
    *   Aims for company-wide optimization, not just partial.
    *   Aligns strategies with correct business directions.
*   **Connectivity of strategy:**
    *   Establishes causal relationships between strategies.
    *   Links core strategies after focused selection.
*   **Internal communication tool:**
    *   Builds executive capability using detailed KPIs.
    *   Serves as a common language across the organization.

#### C) Component Elements of BSC

BSC evaluates performance from four perspectives and includes elements to manage and achieve enterprise goals.

*   **Perspective:** The four viewpoints from which performance is evaluated (Finance, Customer, Process, Learning & Growth).
*   **Critical Success Factor (CSF):** Factors essential for successfully realizing the enterprise's vision and strategy.
*   **Strategy Map:** A visual representation showing the causal relationships among CSFs, illustrating how an organization creates value.
*   **Key Performance Indicator (KPI):** An indicator to measure and manage the level and success of a CSF.

#### D) Four Perspectives of BSC

These perspectives are organically interconnected, managing both financial and non-financial views.

1.  **Financial Perspective**
    *   **Focus:** Shareholder value, financial evaluation.
    *   **Key Items:** Revenue, net profits, cost reductions.
    *   **Key Indicators:** Cash flow, inventory, bonds, operating profit ratio.
    *   **Example:** Shareholder dividend income.

2.  **Customer Perspective**
    *   **Focus:** Customer satisfaction and loyalty.
    *   **Key Items:** Increase customer loyalty, enhancement of customer satisfaction.
    *   **Key Indicators:** Customer satisfaction, on-time supply rate.
    *   **Example:** Customer satisfaction and delivery time compliance.

3.  **Internal Process Perspective**
    *   **Focus:** Optimization of internal processes, efficiency.
    *   **Key Items:** Optimization of processes, removal of process bottlenecks.
    *   **Key Indicators:** Process cycle time, product unit cost.
    *   **Example:** Product quality and production efficiency improvements.

4.  **Learning and Growth Perspective**
    *   **Focus:** Employee development, innovation, organizational capacity.
    *   **Key Items:** Employee learning efforts, measurement of performance gains by enhancing skill levels.
    *   **Key Indicators:** Employee satisfaction, number of newly developed products.
    *   **Example:** New product development.

---

### 3. Balanced IT Performance Evaluation Technique (IT-BSC)

IT-BSC adapts the BSC concept to evaluate IT investment performance.

#### A) Overview of IT-BSC

*   **What it is:** A performance management tool to achieve enterprise goals by applying BSC concepts to IT investment evaluation.
*   **Why it's needed:** Traditional finance-based techniques struggle to quantify intangible IT investments. IT-BSC provides a systematic way to evaluate IT's growing importance.

#### B) Component Elements and BSC Link Structure

IT-BSC has four perspectives, linked to the enterprise's overall BSC, providing a balanced view for IT performance.

1.  **Business Value Perspective**
    *   **Measurement:** Create enterprise value from IT investments.
    *   **BSC Link:** Financial perspective.

2.  **User Perspective**
    *   **Measurement:** Maximize the value of IT service providers and users.
    *   **BSC Link:** Customer perspective.

3.  **Operational Process Perspective**
    *   **Measurement:** Ensure efficient delivery of IT products and services.
    *   **BSC Link:** Internal process perspective.

4.  **Future-Oriented Perspective**
    *   **Measurement:** Provide IT service and technology development support for continuous development.
    *   **BSC Link:** Learning and growth perspective.

---

### 4. Management of Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)

KPIs are quantifiable indicators derived from Critical Success Factors (CSFs) to measure goal achievement.

#### A) Overview of KPI

*   **What it is:** Key Performance Indicator (KPI) – a quantifiable indicator of an organization's Critical Success Factors (CSFs).
*   **Purpose:** Measures the achievement of goals.
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   Must accurately reflect organizational goals.
    *   Must be critical for realizing those goals.
    *   Can be "means" (drivers of victory) or "ends" (results of strategy).
    *   Influence employee behavior.
*   **Importance:** Widely used in performance evaluations.

#### B) KPI Establishment Procedure

KPIs should align with vision, act as strategic drivers, and provide guidance for the entire organization.

1.  **Definition of the KPI Area**
    *   **Activities:** Specify characteristics of the organization/operational unit, select participants.
    *   **Output:** KPI establishment plan, organizational chart.
2.  **Collect Data**
    *   **Activities:** Collect/review vital documents, develop interview questions, execute interview plan.
    *   **Output:** Interview questionnaire, KPI portfolio.
3.  **Analyze**
    *   **Activities:** Create activity descriptions, analyze affinity, develop topics.
    *   **Output:** Job-KPI affinity analysis chart.
4.  **Derive KPIs**
    *   **Activities:** Derive, refine, classify, and integrate KPIs.
    *   **Output:** KPI list, KPI derivation.
5.  **KPI Verification**
    *   **Activities:** Establish comparison criteria, develop a comparison matrix, compare associative relations, set targets.
    *   **Output:** KPI verification matrix.

#### C) Precautions When Deriving KPIs

1.  **Strategic Support of Top Management is Essential:** KPI management should be a top management responsibility to ensure KPIs reflect the organization's strategic vision. Avoid delegating solely to middle management.
2.  **Use Reference Models, but Don't Imitate:** KPIs must be unique to an enterprise's specific goals and strategies. A great company's KPIs may not suit another.
3.  **KPI Derivation is Continuous Improvement:** Start with a balanced set and evolve them gradually. KPIs must be modifiable to respond to changes in the business environment.

---

### 5. Goal Management System

#### A) Key Perspectives of MBO

*   **What it is:** Management by Objectives (MBO) – a system for managing organizational goals.
*   **Purpose:** A business management technique for setting goals and controlling/managing the path to meet those goals, ultimately improving individual performance and capabilities.

---

## Pages 118-122


Here's a simplified learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## **IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide**

### **1. IT-BSC and BSC Link Structure**

**Purpose:**
*   Help managers make decisions.
*   Provide a balanced view of IT performance evaluation.
*   Link IT performance to financial indicators.

**BSC Link Structure of IT-BSC:**

| Perspective             | Measurement Focus                                                      | BSC Link (Traditional)    |
| :---------------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------ |
| **Financial/Enterprise** | Create enterprise value from IT investments.                           | Financial perspective     |
| **User**                | Maximize value for IT service providers and users.                     | Customer perspective      |
| **Operational Process** | Ensure efficient delivery of IT products and services.                 | Internal process perspective |
| **Future-Oriented**     | Provide IT service/technology development support for continuous growth. | Learning and growth perspective |

### **2. Key Performance Indicators (KPI)**

#### **A) Overview of KPI**

*   **Definition:** A quantifiable indicator that measures achievement of a goal and contains a Critical Success Factor (CSF).
*   **Purpose:**
    *   Accurately reflect organizational goals.
    *   Selected from elements critical to realizing goals.
    *   Determine success in competition and strategy.
*   **Importance:** Widely used in performance evaluations; influences employee behavior.

#### **B) KPI Establishment Procedure**

KPIs should align with organizational vision and objectives, act as strategic drivers, and provide organization-wide guidance.

1.  **Define KPI Area:**
    *   Specify characteristics of the organization/operational unit.
    *   Select participants.
    *   *Output:* KPI establishment plan, organizational chart.

2.  **Collect Data:**
    *   Collect and review vital documents.
    *   Develop interview questions and execute interviews.
    *   *Output:* Interview questionnaire, KPI portfolio.

3.  **Analyze:**
    *   Create activity description sheets.
    *   Analyze affinity (relationships).
    *   Develop topics.
    *   *Output:* Job-KPI affinity analysis chart.

4.  **Derive KPIs:**
    *   Derive the initial KPIs.
    *   Refine, classify, and integrate them.
    *   *Output:* KPI list, KPI derivation.

5.  **Verify KPIs:**
    *   Establish criteria for comparison.
    *   Develop a comparison matrix.
    *   Compare associative relations.
    *   Set targets.
    *   *Output:* KPI verification matrix.

#### **C) Precautions for Deriving KPIs**

1.  **Top Management Support:** KPIs require strategic support from top management to ensure they reflect the organization's strategic vision. Don't delegate solely to middle management.
2.  **Don't Imitate:** KPIs must be unique to your enterprise, matching its specific goals and strategies. A great company's KPIs might not work for another.
3.  **Continuous Improvement:** KPI derivation is an ongoing process. Start with a balanced set, evolve them gradually, and be prepared to modify them to respond to business environment changes.

### **3. Goal Management System (MBO)**

#### **A) Key Perspectives of MBO**

*   **Definition:** Management by Objective (MBO) is a system for managing organizational goals. It's a business management technique for setting, controlling, and managing goals to improve individual performance and capabilities.
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   Employees set their own quantitatively measurable goals.
    *   Goals are set in a "bottom-up" fashion, then finalized through discussions with supervisors to align with enterprise goals.
    *   Meeting individual goals positively contributes to achieving corporate goals.

#### **B) Main Reasons for Adopting MBO**

| Reason                 | Description                                                                                                                                              |
| :--------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Goal Alignment**     | Systematically links overall enterprise goals with individual goals to improve both individual and enterprise performance.                                 |
| **Motivation Driver**  | Employees are motivated by voluntarily and creatively setting and working towards their goals, contributing to enterprise goal achievement.                  |
| **Organizational Integration** | Develops employee abilities and improves job performance, creating a unified direction for all employees. |

*   **Caution:** MBO goals may not align with enterprise goals if guidelines are absent. Also, conflicting individual goals can lead to disputes. Careful implementation is crucial.

#### **C) Component Elements of MBO**

| Component Element  | Description                                                                                                                                                            |
| :----------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Setting Objectives** | Objectives must be: <br/>- Measurable, specific, and achievable. <br/>- Established in a direction that allows for continuous yearly improvement. <br/>- Within the organization's overall goals and capabilities. |
| **Participation**  | Encourages interaction among employees (especially supervisors and subordinates) during goal setting and execution to align with enterprise strategies.                 |
| **Feedback**       | Requires continuous feedback (evaluations and encouragement) throughout the evaluation period to help employees continuously improve their performance.                 |

### **4. Recent IT Business Trends and Key Issues**

*   **Rapid Transformation:** The IT business environment is rapidly changing, driven by smart mobile technology.
*   **IT as a Business Core:** IT is no longer just a support function; it now leads business as the core service in many new business models.
*   **Accelerated Transformation:** The combination of mobile, open-source, and social services with infrastructure like cloud, big data, IoT, and AI is accelerating business environment transformation.

#### **Learning Objectives:**

1.  Explain the trend in the transformation of the IT business environment.
2.  Explain enterprise activities for responding to transformations of the IT business environment.

#### **Keywords:**

*   Disruptive innovation
*   Crowd sourcing
*   Open innovation
*   Business platform
*   API economy
*   Servitization

---

# Learning Guide: Understanding the IT Business and Ethics

This guide summarizes essential information on IT business trends, transformations, and enterprise responses.

---

## Section 1: Introduction to IT Business & Key Concepts

### 1.1 The Evolving Role of IT
*   **Shift in IT's Role:** IT is no longer just a support function; it now **leads business** as a core service.
*   **Driving Factors:** This transformation is accelerated by the combination of:
    *   Mobile, open-source, and social services.
    *   Infrastructure technologies like Cloud, Big Data, Internet of Things (IoT), and Artificial Intelligence (AI).

### 1.2 Learning Objectives
After studying this section, you should be able to:
1.  Explain the trends transforming the IT business environment.
2.  Describe how enterprises respond to these IT business transformations.

### 1.3 Key Terminology
Understanding these terms is crucial for the IT business environment:
*   Disruptive Innovation (explained further in Section 3)
*   Crowd Sourcing
*   Open Innovation
*   Business Platform
*   API Economy
*   Servitization

---

## Section 2: Trends of Change in the IT Business Environment

### 2.1 Rapid Transformation Overview
The IT business environment is changing rapidly due to global economic shifts and technological advancements.

#### A) Global Economic Imbalance & Its Impact
*   **Demand Side Issues:**
    *   Declining purchasing power.
    *   Changing global consumption patterns.
    *   Weakening economic growth in developed countries.
*   **Supply Side Issues:**
    *   Rising wages in developing countries (e.g., China, India).
    *   Increased pressure in developed countries to create local jobs.
*   **Enterprise Impact:**
    *   Companies face difficulties from long global economic downturns and low growth.
    *   Increased operating costs and a complex business environment (market opening, currency fluctuations).
    *   **Enterprise Responses:** Companies implement strategies like expanding global sourcing and entering the service industry (especially manufacturing firms).

#### B) Characteristics of IT Business Environment Transformation
Companies are adapting by diversifying and creating new business models to gain a competitive edge.

*   **New Business Model Approaches:**
    *   Specialization
    *   Modularization
    *   Scaling up
    *   Internationalization
    *   Networking
*   **Main Drivers:**
    *   Rapid development of IT technology.
    *   The emergence of the "smart era."
*   **Key Changes Accelerating Business:**
    *   Continuously evolving IT.
    *   Shifting consumption patterns.
    *   Diversification of platforms.
    *   Increased demand for innovation from companies.
*   **Blurring Business Boundaries:**
    *   Traditional competitive boundaries are disappearing (e.g., offline companies entering online markets, growth of mobile businesses, convergent businesses).
    *   **Result:** Diversified business channels (like online markets), new opportunities to connect with diverse customers, and create synergies.
*   **Emergence of New Business Concepts:**
    *   SNS-based smart shopping.
    *   Growth of one-person Internet companies.
    *   Crowd sourcing.
*   **Shifts in Marketing and Value:**
    *   Increased focus on customer-oriented marketing.
    *   More free services offered to customers.
    *   Growth of value-oriented businesses (e.g., social work businesses contributing to sustainability).

#### C) Summary of Key Corporate Innovation Areas
*   **IT Evolution:**
    *   Rapid technical changes (convergence/integration).
    *   Shift from single to integrated/bi-directional platforms.
*   **Consumption Patterns:**
    *   Consumer trends are subdividing (personalization, customization).
*   **Business Value Reorientation:**
    *   Shift from technology/quantity-focused to emotion/quality-focused.
*   **Enterprise Innovation & New Trends:**
    *   Diversification of business channels (Internet, mobile, convergence).
    *   New business concepts (smart shopping, 1-person companies, crowd sourcing).
    *   Evolution of revenue models (internet/mobile advertising, cross-media).
    *   Spread of value-oriented businesses (customer-oriented marketing, social contribution).

**Overall Message for Enterprises:** Businesses must proactively respond to these trends and strengthen their IT capabilities to provide a wider range of products and services.

---

## Section 3: Enterprise Responses to IT Business Changes

### 3.1 IT Business Innovation Activities

#### A) Disruptive Innovation
Disruptive innovation is a key solution for addressing slow growth and market depression.

*   **Definition:** A technique that destroys existing markets and simultaneously creates entirely new ones.
*   **Core Strategy:**
    *   Dominate the market through technological innovation or price disruption.
    *   Aim to outperform existing market leaders.
*   **Impact:**
    *   Changes the competitive hierarchy within industries.
    *   Can affect other industries significantly.
    *   Generates new markets and businesses by altering consumer behaviors and thinking.
*   **Example:** Smartphones, which rapidly surpassed existing mobile technologies in the late 2000s, exemplify disruptive innovation.

---

## Practical Example: Amazon's Kiva Robots (IT for Operational Efficiency)

*   **Scenario:** Amazon, a large global company, operates many delivery centers.
*   **Solution:** Amazon acquired and deployed Kiva warehousing robots.
*   **Results:**
    *   Reduced shipping center operating costs by **20%**.
    *   Over **15,000 robots** deployed.
    *   Saved approximately **KRW 990 billion** in human labor costs.
*   **Lesson:** This demonstrates how IT technology can significantly maximize operational efficiency within a business.

---

## IT Business Trends & Innovation: A Learning Guide

This guide covers key changes in the IT business environment and how enterprises are responding.

---

### Section 1: Understanding the IT Business Environment

The IT business environment is undergoing rapid transformation, driven by global shifts and technological advancements.

#### 1.1 Rapid Transformation Drivers

*   **Global Imbalance:**
    *   Declining purchasing power globally.
    *   Slow growth in developed countries.
    *   Reduced opportunities for new tech businesses.
    *   Shifting global cost structures (e.g., rising wages in China/India).
    *   Increased demand in developed countries for local job creation.
*   **Economic Downturn:** Prolonged global economic downturn leads to difficulties for companies.
*   **Increased Costs:** Companies face rising costs from slower domestic growth and increased overseas investments.
*   **Market Complexity:** Market opening and currency fluctuations complicate the business environment.

#### 1.2 Enterprise Responses to Transformation

Companies are adapting by:
*   **Diversifying Businesses:** To gain competitive advantage.
*   **New Business Models:** Employing strategies like specialization, modularization, scaling up, internationalization, and networking.

#### 1.3 Characteristics of IT Business Environment Transformation

*   **Accelerated Change:** Internal and external environments are evolving rapidly.
*   **Evolving IT:** Constant technological advancements.
*   **Changing Consumption Patterns:** New demands from consumers.
*   **Platform Diversification:** Growth of various technology platforms.
*   **Increased Calls for Innovation:** Companies are pressured to innovate.
*   **Blurring Business Boundaries:**
    *   Offline companies entering online markets.
    *   Growth of mobile businesses.
    *   Emergence of convergent businesses (combining sectors).
    *   **Impact:** Diversified business channels (e.g., online markets), opportunities for diverse customers, creation of new synergies.
*   **Emergence of New Business Concepts:**
    *   SNS-based smart shopping.
    *   Growth of one-person Internet companies.
    *   Crowdsourcing.
*   **Customer-Oriented Marketing:** Increased focus on customer needs and free services.
*   **Value-Oriented Businesses:** Growth of businesses focused on social work and sustainability.

**Key Takeaway:** The smart society is driving rapid business transformation. Enterprises must proactively strengthen their IT business capabilities to offer a broader range of products and services.

---

### Section 2: Enterprises’ Response to Changes

Companies are innovating through disruptive strategies and leveraging collective intelligence.

#### 2.1 Disruptive Innovation

**Definition:** A strategy that destroys existing markets and creates new ones, often by dominating with technological innovation or price destruction, aiming to beat market leaders. It alters industry competition and consumer behavior.

**Key Concepts:**
*   **Sustaining Innovation:**
    *   **Goal:** Continuously improve existing products for key customers.
    *   **Method:** Gradual improvements, high value at a high price.
    *   **Outcome:** Retains existing market share.
*   **Disruptive Innovation:**
    *   **Goal:** Create new markets or radically change existing ones.
    *   **Method:** Low-priced but good-quality products through simplified functions and enhanced convenience, often targeting overlooked segments.
    *   **Outcome:** Can instantly surpass existing technologies (e.g., smartphones replacing traditional mobile phones).
*   **Overshot Customers:** Customers who are unwilling to pay for high-end features they don't need or fully utilize. Disruptive innovation often targets these customers.

**Two Approaches to Disruptive Innovation:**

1.  **Low-End Disruption:**
    *   **Target:** Overserved customers in the low-end market.
    *   **Strategy:** Provide low-priced products that perfectly match customer satisfaction levels by resolving product complaints and leveraging a new, lower-cost business model (low margin, high resource utilization).
2.  **New Market Disruption:**
    *   **Target:** Non-customers (who reject existing products) or dissatisfied customers.
    *   **Strategy:** Launch innovative new products using new technologies, often simple and convenient, to build a presence in niche segments or create entirely new markets for previously unaffordable/inaccessible solutions.

**Example: Smartphones**
*   **Market Shift:** From voice-centered to data-serviced industry; from hardware-centered to platform-based.
*   **Market Obliteration:** Replaced MP3 players, digital cameras, game consoles, car navigation, tablet PCs.
*   **New Market Creation:** App stores, location-based services, SNS, social commerce, social games, Big Data, smart services.

**Latest Technologies Driving Disruptive Innovation:**

| Area        | Technology                  | Description                                                              | Predicted Change                                                                            |
| :---------- | :-------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Electronics** | **Wearable Computer**       | Computer devices worn on the body or clothing.                           | High-tech textile industry growth, machine-dependent healthcare growth.                     |
|             | **3D Printing**             | Prints 3D shapes layer by layer.                                         | Personalized manufacturing, applications in nano/bio/aerospace.                             |
| **Telecom/Services** | **Situation Awareness Technology** | Automatically performs functions based on user's situation.                      | Refined target marketing, accelerated paradigm shift to predictive responses.                |
| **Automobile** | **Self-Driving Cars**       | Controls speed/steering by sensing position/situation without driver input. | Effective road infrastructure, reduced accidents (lower insurance/hospitalizations), rental service growth. |
| **Material** | **Ultra-Lightweight Material** | Strong, lightweight materials (e.g., micromaterials).                    | Expanded applications (aerospace to transportation), reduced energy consumption/prices.     |
| **Bio/Medicine** | **Genetic Therapy**         | Cures diseases by replacing faulty genes with normal ones.               | Changes in medical expense payment, preventive health insurance, growth of beauty/anti-aging industry. |
| **Energy**  | **Post Battery**            | Flexible, high-density, low-price batteries.                             | Popularization of wearable devices, IoT device industry growth, expanded electric vehicles/power storage. |

**Enterprise Strategy:** Enterprises planning disruptive innovations must clearly define their target technology and application area, and seek outside resources to dominate market opportunities.

#### 2.2 Crowdsourcing

**Definition:** A composite word combining 'crowd' and 'outsourcing.' It's the concept of opening various phases of an enterprise's operations to participation from consumers and the general public. Participants share in revenues if their contributions lead to improvements.

**Key Aspects:**
*   **Rise:** Gained traction with the development of SNS, allowing companies to tap into collective intelligence for ideas.
*   **Benefits for Enterprises:**
    *   Generates creative ideas.
    *   Solves enterprise issues (e.g., product development, problem-solving).
    *   Saves time and labor costs.
*   **Example: Dell Computers**
    *   Collected 10,000 ideas in 18 months via a consumer blog for business-related technologies.
*   **Business Model:**
    1.  **Problem Presentation:** Companies post problems/tasks online.
    2.  **Solution Generation:** The crowd (consumers, specialists, public) provides solutions.
    3.  **Compensation:** Successful solution providers receive compensation from the company.
*   **Ecosystem:** Crowdsourcing services often partner with professional technology brokerage firms to complete diverse projects, building a positive, self-reinforcing system.
*   **Synergy with IT:** Rapid advancements in Information Technology (IT) have made crowdsourcing a crucial element for business success by enabling direct public participation.

---


---


## Pages 127-131


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: Disruptive Innovation, Collaborative Business Models, and IT Integration

This guide covers key concepts in modern business strategy, focusing on how companies innovate, collaborate, and leverage IT to compete in dynamic markets.

---

### **1. Disruptive Innovation**

Disruptive innovation involves introducing new products or services that challenge existing markets by targeting underserved customers or creating entirely new customer segments.

**1.1 Types of Disruptive Innovation:**

*   **New Market Disruption:**
    *   **Targets:** Non-customers who reject existing products or dissatisfied customers.
    *   **Strategy:** Launches innovative products using new technologies, focusing on niche segments.
    *   **Characteristics:** Low-feature, simple, convenient, low-priced, often mass-produced in smaller volumes. Makes products affordable or accessible to those who couldn't purchase before.
*   **Low-End Disruptive Innovation:**
    *   **Targets:** Customers who are "overserved" by existing, expensive products.
    *   **Strategy:** Leverages new processes and financial approaches (e.g., low margins, high resource utilization) to offer discounted prices.

**1.2 The Smartphone as an Example of Disruptive Innovation:**

*   **Market Shift:** Transformed the industry from voice-centered to data-serviced, and from hardware-centered to platform-based.
*   **Market Disruption:** Decimated markets for MP3 players, digital cameras, game consoles, car navigation, and tablet PCs.
*   **New Market Creation:** Spawned new markets and business models like app stores, location-based services, social networks (SNS), social commerce, social games, Big Data, and smart services.

**1.3 Key Technologies Driving Disruptive Innovation:**

| Area                 | Technology                 | Description                                                                 | Predicted Changes                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| :------------------- | :------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Wearable             | Wearable Computer          | Computer devices worn on the body or clothing.                              | High-tech driven textile industry; growth of machine-dependent healthcare.                                                                                                                                            |
| Electronics          | 3D Printing                | Builds three-dimensional shapes layer by layer.                             | Personalized manufacturing; used in nano, bio, and aerospace.                                                                                                                                                         |
| IT Technology        | Situation Awareness Tech   | Automatically performs functions appropriate to a user's situation.         | Refined, detailed target marketing; accelerated shift to predictive response paradigms.                                                                                                                              |
| Automobile           | Self-driving Cars          | Controls speed and steering without driver input.                           | Effective road infrastructure; reduced accidents (lower insurance/hospitalizations); growth of rental services.                                                                                                       |
| Material             | Ultra-lightweight Material | Lightweight yet strong materials (e.g., microratis).                        | Expanded applications (aerospace to transportation); reduced energy consumption/prices.                                                                                                                               |
| Bio/Medicine         | Genetic Therapy            | Replaces faulty genes to cure diseases.                                     | Changes in medical expense payment standards; introduction of preventive health insurance; growth of beauty and anti-aging industry.                                                                                    |
| Energy               | Post Battery               | Flexible, high-density, low-price batteries.                                | Popularization of wearable devices; growth of IoT device industry; expanded base of electric vehicles and power storage systems.                                                                                      |

**1.4 Strategy for Disruptive Innovation:**

*   **Purpose:** Overcome technological barriers and reshape future industries.
*   **Approach:** Clearly specify target technology and application area, seek external resources to establish market dominance.

---

### **2. Crowdsourcing**

**2.1 Definition:**

*   A combination of 'crowd' and 'outsourcing'.
*   Opening up an enterprise's operations (including R&D, problem-solving, product development) to participation from consumers and the general public.
*   Profits/revenues are shared with participants if the company's activities or revenues improve.

**2.2 How it Works:**

*   Leverages social networks and communication channels to generate ideas from a large group of people (the "masses").
*   **Business Model:** Companies post problems/tasks online; the crowd (specialists, scientists, public) provides solutions; compensation is given to successful solution providers.

**2.3 Benefits:**

*   Generates creative ideas for enterprise issues.
*   Reduces time and labor costs.
*   Provides insights into consumer needs in a rapidly changing market.
*   Helps ascertain demand for products/services through early adopter feedback.

**2.4 Example:**

*   Dell Computers collected 10,000 ideas in 18 months by creating a blog for consumers to exchange business-related technologies.

---

### **3. Open Innovation**

**3.1 Definition:**

*   An enterprise innovation method where the research, development, and productization processes are opened up to outside experts.
*   Outside experts share their ideas and knowledge.

**3.2 Purpose:**

*   Reduce costs.
*   Increase the likelihood of innovation success.

**3.3 Shift from Traditional R&D:**

| Feature         | Traditional R&D                                       | Open Innovation                                                                                                    |
| :-------------- | :---------------------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Approach**    | Internal focus; augmenting R&D manpower and tech; kept development output sealed. | Collaboration with outside experts, institutions, organizations with core capabilities.                              |
| **Limitations** | Slow response to market; difficulty launching products on time; high investment, small success chance, increasing risks. | Leverages diverse external sources (venture companies, SMEs, research institutes, universities) to accelerate improvements. |
| **Value**       | Internal-driven value.                                | External connections create greater value, including licensing, spin-offs, new market entry.                       |

**3.4 Types of Open Innovation:**

*   **Inward Open Innovation:**
    *   **Focus:** Obtaining know-how or ideas *from* external sources.
    *   **Forms:** Technology purchase, joint research, sub-contracted research, establishment of joint ventures, venture investment, acquisition.
*   **Outward Open Innovation:**
    *   **Focus:** Sending internal knowledge or ideas *to* the outside world for commercialization through other business models.
    *   **Forms:** Technology sale, spin-off.

**3.5 Importance:**

*   Rapid IT advancements and convergence make it difficult for companies to keep pace with market changes through internal R&D alone.
*   Strengthens innovation capabilities and is crucial for company growth in a structurally transforming technological and business landscape.

---

### **4. IT Business Integration & Expansion**

**4.1 Business Platform**

**4.1.1 Definition:**

*   A basic structure commonly used to produce or sell various products.
*   A key strategy for securing a competitive edge in corporate ecosystem competition.
*   Acts as a foundation for creating and delivering value to participating companies, determining the fate of the enterprise ecosystem.

**4.1.2 Major Functions:**

*   **Promote Exchanges:** Provides locations for stakeholders to connect.
*   **Reduce Costs:** Offers time-consuming and costly functions on the platform.
*   **Increase Trust:** The platform's brand offers a sense of safety and trust to users.
*   **Create Advertising Revenues:** Provides services to broadcasters, magazines, etc., developing consumer points of contact.
*   **Provide Third-Party Services:** Facilitates exchanges between different groups.

**4.1.3 Example: Apple vs. Nokia:**

*   **Nokia (Symbian OS):** Entered smartphone market earlier. Platform failed due to complex development environment geared for enterprise, creating high entry barriers for developers.
*   **Apple (iOS/App Store):** Emphasized entertainment functions, built an online content-centered ecosystem (App Store), attracting numerous developers.
*   **Key Lesson:** Apple's platform successfully connected and complemented the values produced by stakeholders, leading to market dominance.

**4.1.4 Types of Business Platforms:**

| Type                  | Definition                                          | Purpose                                                                                                 | Scope (Typical)       | Examples                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| :-------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | :-------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Product Platform**  | Universal components used in a broad range of products. | Cost savings (reduced development costs, additional models); diversified product lineup.                 | In-house              | **Nokia:** Launched ~10 platforms (e.g., Series C.E.N.X) producing ~135 phone models in 2009, based on common parts.                                                                                                                            |
| **Customer Platform** | Core customer group targeted by a company.          | Increased revenues; customer solidification; expansion of market position.                                | Outside the company   | **Woongjin Coway:** Established a home visit service network with its water purifier rental service in 1998, expanding to air purifiers, bidets, etc., leveraging its core customer base.                                                  |
| **Transaction Platform** | Infrastructure for doing transactions with outside suppliers. | Increased revenues from market partnerships; industry leadership through cooperative relationships. | Outside the company   | **Apple (iTunes Store):** Acquired 14 million songs and 300,000 apps from outside content providers, becoming a leading digital content marketplace.                                                                                         |

**4.1.5 Future Outlook:**

*   Companies will increasingly create diverse business models and stable business ecosystems based on their own platforms.
*   The platform market is expected to expand and grow rapidly.

**4.2 API Economy**

**4.2.1 Definition:**

*   A company discloses its internal business assets or services to third parties in the form of **Application Programming Interfaces (APIs)**.
*   Additional business value is created through the production of new assets and consumption by these third parties.

**4.2.2 Importance:**

*   Enables companies to apply composable/assemblable business models across all channels.
*   Improves operational and business agility, allowing effective response to market demands.
*   Provides a "platform-neutral environment" where various businesses can connect and create value.

---


---


## Pages 130-134


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Key Concepts

This guide covers essential concepts in IT business strategy, focusing on how companies innovate, integrate, and expand in today's digital landscape.

---

### 1. Open Innovation

**Definition:** Open innovation involves an enterprise collaborating with external entities to enhance its innovation capabilities. It's crucial because rapid IT advancements and convergence make it hard for companies to rely solely on internal R&D.

**Types of Open Innovation:**

1.  **Inward Open Innovation:** Obtaining knowledge or ideas from outside sources (companies, research centers, universities) during research, development, and commercialization.
    *   **Forms:**
        *   Technology Purchase
        *   Joint Research
        *   Sub-contracted Research
        *   Joint Venture Establishment
        *   Venture Investment
        *   Acquisition
2.  **Outward Open Innovation:** Sending a company's knowledge or ideas to the outside world for commercialization through other business models.
    *   **Forms:**
        *   Technology Sale
        *   Spin-off

---

### 2. IT Business Integration and Expansion

#### A. Business Platform

**Definition:** A basic structure (ecosystem) used to produce or sell various products and services. In today's market, competition is often between *corporate ecosystems*, making platforms a key strategy for competitive advantage.

**Role of a Platform:**
*   Foundation for creating and delivering value to participating companies.
*   A medium that connects and complements values produced by stakeholders.

**Key Functions:**
*   **Promote Exchanges:** Provides spaces for stakeholders to connect.
*   **Reduce Costs:** Offers time-consuming or costly functions on the platform.
*   **Increase Trust:** The platform's brand offers a sense of safety and trust to users.
*   **Create Advertising Revenue/Contact Points:** Services for broadcasters, magazines, etc.
*   **Provide Third-Party Services:** Facilitates exchanges between different groups.

**Example (Apple vs. Nokia):**
*   **Nokia (Symbian OS):** Focused on enterprise, complex development, high barriers for developers. Failed to become a standard, lost market share despite early entry.
*   **Apple (iOS):** Emphasized entertainment, built a content-centered ecosystem (App Store), attracted numerous developers. Successfully connected stakeholders and created value.

**Types of Business Platforms:**

| Type                 | Definition                                      | Purpose                                                    | Scope                 | Example                                     |
| :------------------- | :---------------------------------------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------- | :------------------------------------------ |
| **Product Platform** | Universal components for a broad range of products | Cost savings (reduced development/production costs)        | In-house              | Nokia (various phone series components)     |
| **Customer Platform**| Core customer group targeted by a company         | Increased revenue (customer solidification, diversified products) | Outside the company   | Woongjin Coway (home visit service network)|
| **Transaction Platform**| Infrastructure for transactions with external suppliers| Industry leadership (market position through partnerships) | Outside the company   | Apple (iTunes Store for 3rd party content)  |

**Future Outlook:** Business models will expand, and the platform market will continue to grow, likely at an accelerated pace.

---

#### B. API Economy

**Definition:** A business model where a company exposes its internal business assets or services to third parties as **Application Programming Interfaces (APIs)**. This creates new business values through the production and consumption of new assets.

**Why it's Important:**
*   Allows companies to respond effectively to market demands.
*   Enables "assemblable" business models across channels.
*   Improves operational and business agility.
*   APIs provide a **platform-neutral environment** for application connections.
*   Facilitates sharing of customer data and marketing insights among member companies.

**Benefits:**
*   **For App Developers:** Utilize API open data to build new applications and offer customized services.
*   **For Companies:**
    *   Generate revenue by releasing data/services (e.g., Amazon, Twitter, Google).
    *   Maximize internal/external efficiencies by sharing core assets.
    *   Enhance service quality and stability (e.g., E*Trade's stock trading API).

**Challenges:**
*   Developing and managing APIs is complex.
*   Essential management tasks: account management, authentication, security.
*   Requires systemized management due to increasing number and diversity of APIs.

**API Value Chain:**
The flow of value from API providers to end-users:
1.  **Business Assets:** Company's core data/services.
2.  **Web APIs:** Assets exposed through APIs.
3.  **Developers:** Use APIs to build innovative applications.
4.  **Apps:** Applications built using APIs.
5.  **End Users:** Use apps based on customer insights, leading to increased sales for the original business.

**Strategic API Management:**
*   Companies providing APIs must understand the needs of both developers and end-users.
*   Implement systems for monitoring and managing released APIs.
*   Provide clear documentation and communication channels for external developers.
*   Crucial for managing diverse customer contact points in the mobile-centric era.

---

#### C. Servitization

**Definition:** A fundamental business model transformation where a product evolves into a **service bundle** that continuously delivers value throughout the customer experience lifecycle. This shifts competition towards services, where revenue is linked to the availability, reliability, and performance of a company's assets.

**Trends:**
*   Accelerating in traditional manufacturing sectors.
*   Companies are moving away from product-only sales models.
*   Increased focus on differentiating through combining products with software.

**SW (Software) Convergent Models for Products:**

1.  **Product-Centered Model:** Strengthens service elements without sacrificing the sales-oriented product model.
2.  **Usage-Based Model:** Producer retains ownership but sells the *right to use* the product (e.g., subscription, pay-per-use).
3.  **Additional Sales-Oriented Model:** Producer sells diverse value-added services based on an already sold product.

**Why it's Important:**
*   Companies strengthen software convergence capabilities to be flexible and competitive.
*   Software convergence is a key factor in determining product value and corporate performance.
*   Optimizes business models for rapidly changing consumer environments.

**Examples of Convergent Products and Services:**

| Industry       | Company     | Description                                                                                             |
| :------------- | :---------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Electronics    | Apple       | Built a service ecosystem using iTunes, App Store.                                                       |
| Electronics    | Xerox       | Transformed from a facsimile manufacturer to a supplier of document management systems.                     |
| Electronics    | Philips     | Acquired Health Watch (2006) to venture into the healthcare service market.                               |
| Automobile     | GM          | Acquired 5.5 million customers through OnStar (telematics services subsidiary).                         |
| Heavy Industry | Caterpillar | Provides remote management service for excavators (GPS-based analysis, parts, fuel efficiency, monitoring).|
| Infrastructure | Vinci       | Airport/road/parking operation services account for 56% of operating profits despite 14% of total revenue. |

---

---

## Learning Guide: Understanding IT Business & Ethics

This guide covers key concepts in modern IT business, focusing on Servitization, major IT trends, and foundational web/mobile technologies.

---

### Section 1: Servitization

**What is Servitization?**
*   A business model transformation where a **product evolves into a service bundle**.
*   Focus shifts from selling products to **delivering continuous value** throughout the customer lifecycle.
*   Revenue generation is tied to the **availability, reliability, and performance** of a company's assets.

**Why is it Important?**
*   Traditional product sales models are becoming less effective.
*   Companies find it hard to **differentiate products based on merits alone**.
*   Servitization, especially by **combining products with software**, offers a path to differentiation and competitive edge.
*   Software convergence capabilities are now crucial for product value and corporate performance.

**Three Software-Convergent Models for Servitization:**

1.  **Product-centered model:** Strengthens service elements *without* abandoning the core product sales model.
2.  **Usage-based model:** Producer retains ownership but sells the *right to use* the product (e.g., subscription, pay-per-use).
3.  **Additional sales-oriented model:** Producer sells diverse *value-added services* based on an already sold product.

**Examples of Servitization:**

*   **Apple:** Built a service ecosystem (iTunes, App Store).
*   **Xerox:** Transformed from facsimile manufacturer to document management systems supplier.
*   **Philips:** Acquired Health Watch to enter healthcare service.
*   **GM (OnStar):** Provides telematics services (e.g., navigation, emergency assistance).
*   **Caterpillar:** Offers remote management for excavators (analysis, parts, fuel efficiency, monitoring).
*   **Vinci:** Airport/road/parking operation services generate a disproportionately high percentage of operating profits compared to total revenues.

---

### Section 2: Recent Trends & Key IT Issues

**Impact of IT:**
*   Rapid IT network and infrastructure development drives **IT-based innovations across all industries**.
*   Existing products gain new value through **convergence with IT**.
*   Previously overlooked technologies gain relevance through **integration**.
*   **Smart infrastructures** improve public service efficiency.
*   **Latest IT business services and technologies** are foundational to these market changes and paradigm shifts.

**Key IT Concepts/Keywords (Important to Know):**

*   **Web & Mobile Services:**
    *   **HTML5:** Next-gen web standard.
    *   **SNS:** Social Networking Service.
    *   **Responsive/Adaptive web:** Websites adjusting to screen sizes.
    *   **Open API:** Application Programming Interface allowing software components to interact.
    *   **Semantic web:** Web data linked and understood by computers.
    *   **OSS (Open Source Software):** Software with publicly available source code.
    *   **MEAP (Mobile Enterprise Application Platform):** Platforms for building mobile apps for businesses.
    *   **MDM (Mobile Device Management system):** Software for managing mobile devices in an organization.
    *   **Mobile commerce:** E-commerce on mobile devices.
    *   **LBS (Location Based Service):** Services using location data.
*   **Infrastructure & Emerging Tech:**
    *   **IoT (Internet of Things):** Network of physical objects embedded with sensors, software for connecting and exchanging data.
    *   **Cloud computing service:** On-demand delivery of computing services over the internet.
    *   **Virtualization service:** Creating a virtual version of a resource (e.g., server, OS).
    *   **Blockchain:** Distributed, decentralized ledger technology.
    *   **Smart City/Grid/Education/Healthcare:** Applications of smart technology in various sectors.
*   **Data & AI:**
    *   **Open data:** Data freely available to everyone.
    *   **Linked data:** Structured data linked to other data.
    *   **AI (Artificial Intelligence):** Machine intelligence.
    *   **Fintech:** Financial technology.
    *   **Big Data:** Extremely large data sets analyzed for patterns/trends.
    *   **O2O (Online to Offline) / O4O (Online for Offline):** Strategies connecting online and physical channels.
    *   **Virtual currency:** Digital currency.
*   **Advanced Hardware/Manufacturing:**
    *   **3D printing:** Additive manufacturing.
    *   **Self-driving cars:** Autonomous vehicles.
    *   **Smart machines:** Machines with AI capabilities.
    *   **Wearable devices:** Electronic devices worn on the body.
    *   **Drones:** Unmanned aerial vehicles.

---

### Section 3: AlphaGo Case Study (AI Impact)

*   **Event:** March 2016 Go match between Lee Sedol (human champion) and AlphaGo (AI).
*   **Significance:** AlphaGo defeated Lee Sedol, demonstrating **AI's ability to surpass human learning and skills** that evolved over thousands of years.
*   **Lesson:** A clear sign of the growing power and potential of artificial intelligence.

---

### Section 4: Latest Web & Mobile Services

#### A) Latest Web Technologies

**1. HTML5**
*   **Definition:** Next-generation HTML standard, overcoming limitations of previous HTML versions.
*   **Key Benefit:** Allows rich web applications (video, voice, 2D graphics) *without requiring separate plug-ins* (like Flash or ActiveX).
    *   *Example:* Accessing Kakao Talk or using word processors/games directly via a web browser without installation.
*   **Overcomes:** Problems associated with older plug-in solutions (e.g., functional expansion through CSS3 and JavaScript APIs).
*   **Design Principles:** Compatibility, practicality, interoperability, and universal access.
*   **New Features:**
    *   **Semantic Markup:** 26 new markups for clearer semantic representation than HTML4.
    *   **APIs:** New functions like `web form`, `canvas`, and `web socket` for web-based application development.
*   **Advantages:**
    *   Less JavaScript code needed for the same functionality compared to HTML4.
    *   Better for mobile environments (sensitive to network speed).
    *   Maximizes scalability and efficiency for corporate business solutions.

**2. Responsive Web / Adaptive Web**
*   **Problem Solved:** Users want consistent web content quality across various devices (desktops, tablets, smartphones) despite different screen sizes and specifications. Developing a separate web version for every device is impossible.
*   **Definition (Responsive Web):** A web design approach that creates an **optimal user environment by adapting to different devices and screen sizes**.
    *   The website's layout and content **automatically change size and arrangement** to fit the user's device.
*   **Current Trend:** Mobile web users now exceed regular internet web users, making responsive design essential.

## Pages 136-140


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# IT Business & Ethics: Learning Guide (Pages 136-140)

## Introduction: The Power of AI

*   **AlphaGo's Impact:** In 2016, Google's AI, AlphaGo, defeated Go world champion Lee Sedol.
*   **Significance:** This event demonstrated that Artificial Intelligence (AI) can surpass human learning abilities developed over thousands of years.

---

## 01. Latest Web and Mobile Services

### A) Latest Web Technologies

#### 1. HTML5

*   **What it is:** The next-generation standard for HTML.
*   **Key Advantage: No Plugins Needed**
    *   Eliminates the need to install separate programs or browser plugins (like ActiveX) for services (e.g., KakaoTalk, word processors, games can run directly in a web browser).
    *   Overcomes limitations of previous HTML by supporting rich web applications (video, voice, 2D graphics) natively.
*   **Design Principles:** Compatibility, practicality, interoperability, universal access.
*   **Improved Semantics:** Adds 26 new markups for clearer meaning representation than HTML4.
*   **API Support:** Introduces new API functions (e.g., web form, canvas, web socket) for web-based application development.
*   **Efficiency:** Uses less JavaScript code than HTML4 for similar functions, making it better for mobile environments.
*   **Business Adoption:** Increasingly used for corporate solutions to maximize scalability and efficiency.

#### 2. Responsive Web / Adaptive Web

*   **The Problem:** Users want consistent web content quality across various devices (desktops, tablets, smartphones) despite different screen sizes and specifications.
*   **Responsive Web:**
    *   **Approach:** A web design method where the website's layout and style automatically adjust to fit *any* device screen size, providing an optimal user experience.
    *   **Focus:** Often emphasizes adapting content from a "mobile-first" perspective.
*   **Adaptive Web:**
    *   **Approach:** A server-based or client-based technology that *detects* the accessing device.
    *   **How it works:** Delivers content (e.g., images) specifically *tailored* for that device, ensuring high-speed access, especially on mobile.

#### 3. Semantic Web

*   **What it is:** A "smart" web that enables intelligent data processing and knowledge building.
*   **How it Works:**
    *   Defines and structures data using **ontology** (a formal representation of knowledge).
    *   Links structured data, allowing computers to understand the *meaning* (semantics) and relationships between web resources.
*   **Why it's Needed:** Traditional HTML only displays documents; computers cannot understand the semantic meaning or efficiently process vast, unstructured web information.
*   **Application Areas:**
    *   **e-commerce:** Connecting to frameworks like ebXML.
    *   **Data Mining:** Web mining across the entire web (e.g., e-CRM, e-MarketPlace).
    *   **Knowledge Processing:** Collecting and distributing large volumes of knowledge.
    *   **Web Service:** Linking with enterprise business service components.

#### 4. SNS (Social Network Service)

*   **Definition:** Online services that help people maintain existing personal relationships or establish new ones.
*   **History:** Evolved from early online communities (e.g., "The Well" in 1985).
*   **Main Functions:**
    *   **Relationship Forming:** Allows users to define and manage their connections.
    *   **Profile:** Register personal information (hometown, interests, occupation).
    *   **Communication:** Provides tools like chatting, messages, email, video chat.
    *   **Content Production:** Tools for creating and sharing photos, videos, and text.
    *   **Network Utilization:** Allows users to recommend or distribute profiles and content.
*   **Scale:** Global platforms like Facebook and WhatsApp have billions of monthly users (as of 2017).

#### 5. Open API (Open Application Programming Interface)

*   **Definition:** A free, publicly available API that users and developers can use without restriction.
*   **Impact:** Empowers users to move beyond just *consuming* services to *developing their own* new services using existing APIs.
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   Provides access to specific functions of a website or service.
    *   Enables creation of new services by combining multiple APIs.
    *   Key to the development of **mashup sites**.
    *   Transforms users into potential service providers.
*   **Component Elements:**
    *   **Services Provided:** Weather data, traffic info, public information, maps, etc.
    *   **Technologies Used:** XML, SOAP (server-side), JavaScript, AJAX (client-side).

#### 6. REST (Representational State Transfer) API

*   **Prevalence:** Currently the most widely used type of Open API.
*   **Architecture:** A network-based architecture designed by Roy Fielding (an HTTP author) to leverage the strengths of the Web (HTTP).
*   **Components:** Based on Resource Oriented Architecture (ROA), composed of:
    *   **HTTP URI:** Specifies the target resource (e.g., a specific piece of data).
    *   **HTTP Method:** Designates the action to be performed on that resource.
*   **Common REST API Methods:**
    *   **POST:** Creates a new resource.
    *   **GET:** Retrieves (searches and extracts) information about a resource.
    *   **PUT:** Corrects or updates an existing resource.
    *   **DELETE:** Removes a resource.

### B) Mobile Services

#### 1. Location Based Service (LBS)

*   **Growth:** Rapidly expanded since 2010 due to the surge in smartphone use ("mobile Big Bang").
*   **Evolution:** Merged location information with commerce and entertainment to become a broad category of services.
*   **Enabling Factors:**
    *   Increased availability of devices capable of location detection.
    *   Opening of location determination platforms.
*   **How it Works (Smartphones):** Combines various location detection technologies:
    *   **Base Stations (Cell-ID):** Uses cellular tower signals.
    *   **GPS:** Global Positioning System.
    *   **Wi-Fi:** Uses Wi-Fi network signals.
    *   **Motion Sensors:** Provides precision navigation.
*   **Integration:** Adoption of mapping services like Google Maps and Apple Maps made LBS widely accessible and usable for general purposes.

**Mashup Site:** A website that combines APIs (e.g., product information, maps) from different sources (like Microsoft, Google, Yahoo) with its own user interface to create new, integrated services.
