## Pages 139-143


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT ESSENTIALS: Online Services & Mobile Technologies

This guide covers key concepts in online social interaction, software integration, and mobile services.

### 1. Social Network Service (SNS)

**Definition:**
*   Online platform for people to maintain existing relationships or form new ones.
*   Began as early online communities (e.g., "The Well" in 1985).

**Main Functions:**
*   **Forming Relationships:** Set connections with others.
*   **Profile Management:** Register personal info (hometown, interests, occupation).
*   **Communication:** Chat, messages, email, video calls.
*   **Content Production:** Create and share photos, videos, texts.
*   **Network Utilization:** Share profiles and content with others.

**Scale:**
*   Global SNS sites have billions of monthly users (e.g., Facebook, WhatsApp).

### 2. Open API (Open Application Programming Interface)

**Definition:**
*   A free, public API that allows anyone (users, developers) to access website functions.
*   Enables users to move beyond consuming services to developing and using their own.

**Characteristics:**
*   **Access Website Functions:** Allows external applications to interact with a website's features.
*   **New Service Design:** Multiple APIs can be combined to create novel services.
*   **Mashup Sites:** A key enabler for mashup sites (websites that combine data/functions from multiple sources, e.g., combining map data with real estate listings).
*   **User Empowerment:** Transforms users into potential service providers.

**Component Elements:**
*   **Open API Service:** The actual functionality provided (e.g., weather data, traffic info, maps).
*   **How to 'Open' an API:** Technologies used for communication (e.g., XML, SOAP on server-side; XML, JavaScript, AJAX on client-side).

#### REST (Representational State Transfer) API

**Definition:**
*   Currently the most widely used type of Open API.
*   A network-based architecture for web services, designed by Roy Fielding in 2000.
*   Based on Resource-Oriented Architecture (ROA), utilizing HTTP methods.

**Structure:**
*   **HTTP URI (Uniform Resource Identifier):** Specifies the target resource (e.g., a user profile, a product).
*   **HTTP Method:** Specifies the action to be performed on that resource.

**Common REST API Methods:**
*   **POST:** Creates a new resource.
*   **GET:** Searches for and retrieves information about a resource.
*   **PUT:** Corrects/updates an existing resource.
*   **DELETE:** Removes a resource.

### 3. Mobile Services

The "Anytime, Anywhere, Any Device" nature of mobile technology drives mobile commerce, entertainment, communication, and location-based services.

#### A. Location Based Service (LBS)

**Definition:**
*   Services that merge location information with commerce, entertainment, and other applications.
*   Has grown exponentially with the smartphone market.

**Key Drivers:**
*   Widespread availability of location-detection devices (smartphones).
*   Open location determination platforms.
*   Integration with mapping services (e.g., Google Map, Apple Map).

**Location Detection Mechanisms (Smartphones):**
*   Combines technologies like:
    *   **Cell-ID:** Uses cellular base station location and distance.
    *   **GPS:** Global Positioning System.
    *   **Wi-Fi:** Uses Wi-Fi access points.
    *   **Motion Sensors:** For precise navigation.

**Network-Based Location Determination Technologies:**
*   **Cell ID/Sector ID:** Calculates device location by measuring distance to a base station.
*   **AoA (Angle of Arrival):** Uses the angle of signals arriving from at least two base stations.
*   **TDoA (Time Difference of Arrival):** Uses the time difference of signals arriving from at least three base stations.
*   **Fingerprint/Pattern Matching:** Uses base station location and radio signal intensity patterns.

**Evolution of Location Determination:**
*   **2G Era:** Simple cell-based positioning.
*   **3G Era:** Adopted GPS.
*   **4G Era:** Highly precise, overcoming weaknesses of base stations (high error) and GPS (indoor issues, impediments). Wi-Fi also enabled location determination where access points exist.

#### B. Mobile Commerce (M-Commerce)

**Definition:**
*   Business transactions (trading goods, services, information) conducted using mobile devices like smartphones and tablets.

**M-Commerce vs. E-Commerce Comparison:**

| Feature               | E-Commerce                         | M-Commerce                                  |
| :-------------------- | :--------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------ |
| **Network**           | Fixed (high-speed line)            | Mobile (relatively lower speed line)        |
| **User Experience**   | Rich applications                  | Simplified user experience                  |
| **Communication**     | Stable quality                     | Relatively unstable quality                 |
| **Screen Size**       | Big screen                         | Relatively small screen                     |
| **Device Resources**  | High memory, high speed processing | Lower memory, lower speed processing        |
| **Input/Output**      | Convenient (keyboard, mouse)       | Often unnecessary (touch, voice)            |
| **Location**          | Home or office                     | User's location often determined/relevant   |
| **Usage Context**     | Personal or public                 | Typically personal                          |

**Key Technologies of Mobile Commerce:**
*   **Wireless Communication:** Technologies like 3G, 4G (LTE), 5G for voice/data/video.
*   **Mobile Security:** Core functions like certification, confidentiality, integrity, and non-repudiation (e.g., encryption, public key security).
*   **Mobile Payment:** Methods for direct payment, banking system integration, third-party services, simplified payments, and electronic wallets.
*   **Mobile Application Server:** Software platform for developing and operating application services in wireless environments.

#### C. MEAP (Mobile Enterprise Application Platform)

**Definition:**
*   A platform designed to support a wide range of diverse mobile device environments.
*   Enables sharing and reuse of applications across different devices and operating systems.

**Why MEAP is Needed (Benefits):**
*   **Reuse:** Allows the same code to be used across various smartphone OS, hardware, and service provider environments.
*   **Cost Savings:** Shared platform reduces the need for duplicate infrastructure and middleware, saving development and operational costs.
*   **Screen Support:** Helps develop mobile screens optimized for different device types.
*   **Testing & Interworking:** Provides support for testing applications and ensuring they work together across systems.

**Components:**
MEAP covers the entire lifecycle of mobile development, execution, and operation:
*   **Development Environment:**
    *   Integrated Development Environment (IDE) for coding, testing (simulators).
*   **Execution Environment:**
    *   Mobile Framework (middleware for platform-independent code execution).
    *   Distribution Management (app distribution, version control).
*   **Operations Environment:**
    *   Mobile Device Management (MDM) (for device and security management).
    *   Backend Integrated Interface (standard interface for existing systems).
    *   Service Operations and Management (monitoring).

#### D. MDM (Mobile Device Management)

**Definition:**
*   A solution for efficiently managing diverse mobile devices and applications used within an enterprise.
*   Allows remote management (Over-The-Air, OTA), provided devices are powered on.

**Main Functions:**
*   **Device Management:** Collects device info, manages distribution, identifies device IDs.
*   **Registration & Tracking:** Registers, approves, and recalls mobile devices; can freeze lost/stolen devices.
*   **Security Policy Enforcement:** Integrates with company directories (e.g., Active Directory) to establish and enforce security policies.
*   **Software Distribution:** Pushes applications and updates to devices based on policies.

---


## Pages 142-146


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business & Ethics (Mobile Commerce, M2M, IoT)

### 1. Key Technologies of Mobile Commerce

**A. Wireless Communication**
*   **Purpose:** Sending/receiving voice, data, video.
*   **Technologies:** GSM, IMT-2000, 3G, 4G (LTE), 5G.

**B. Mobile Security**
*   **Core Functions:** Certification, confidentiality, integrity, denial prevention.
*   **Methods:** Encryption-based security, Public key-based security.

**C. Mobile Payment**
*   **Methods:**
    *   Direct payment between parties.
    *   Payment via banking system.
    *   Payment via independent 3rd party.
*   **Features:** Simplified payment, Electronic wallet.

**D. Mobile Application Server**
*   **Purpose:** Software platform for developing and operating application services in both fixed-line and wireless environments.

---

### 2. MEAP (Mobile Enterprise Application Platform)

*   **Definition:** A platform supporting diverse device environments, allowing application sharing and reuse.
*   **Main Reasons for Need:** Reuse and cost savings.
*   **Benefits:**
    *   Reuse same code across different smartphone OS, hardware, and service provider environments.
    *   Save money by sharing a common platform (reduces duplicate infrastructure/middleware costs).
    *   Support developing mobile screens for various device types.
    *   Support for testing and interworking.
*   **Components (Covers entire lifecycle: development to execution & operation):**
    1.  **Integrated Development Environment (IDE):** For project setup, coding, and testing (simulators).
    2.  **Mobile Framework (Execution Environment):** Provides a meta (abstraction) layer for "one source, multi-use," acting as middleware to execute platform/device-independent code and offer device API wrappers.
    3.  **Distribution Management (Execution Environment):** Manages mobile app distribution and versioning.
    4.  **Back-end Integrated Interface (Execution Environment):** Standard interface for integrating with and reusing existing legacy systems.
    5.  **Mobile Device Management (MDM) (Operations Environment):** For device management, app management, security management, access control, and lost device management.
    6.  **Service Operations and Management (Operations Environment):** Integrated interface monitoring and management.

---

### 3. MDM (Mobile Device Management)

*   **Definition:** A solution for efficiently managing diverse mobile devices and applications within an enterprise. It enables management anytime, anywhere via Over-The-Air (OTA) transmissions (device must be on).
*   **Main Functions:**
    *   **Device Management:** Collects device info, manages distribution, identifies device IDs.
    *   **Registration & Tracking:** Registers, approves, recalls devices; freezes device use if lost/stolen.
    *   **Security Policy:** Establishes and enforces security policies based on company/group rules, integrates with internal active directory.
    *   **Software Distribution:** Manages and distributes software updates.
    *   **Authentication:** Authenticates devices.
*   **Component Elements & Roles:**
    *   **MDM Gateway Server:**
        *   Located in DMZ (screened subnet).
        *   Authenticates connections between internal network and mobile devices.
        *   Facilitates communication (e.g., direct push updates).
    *   **MDM Device Management Server:**
        *   Manages and operates mobile devices.
        *   Distributes group policies and software.
        *   Communicates with other enterprise infrastructures.
    *   **MDM Enrollment Server:**
        *   Assigns authentication to recalled devices or upon certification requests.
        *   Uses One-Time Password (OTP) for device certification.
    *   **Databases:** Stores management, configuration, work, and setup data for MDM Device Management and Enrollment Servers.
*   **Deployment Effects (Benefits):**
    *   Increased flexibility and expandability.
    *   Ability to connect to diverse services.
    *   PC-level device management.
    *   Consistent security enforcement.
    *   Easy remote support and troubleshooting.
    *   OS, language, and system support.

---

### 4. Smart Business Infrastructure

**A. Convergent Infrastructure**

**B. M2M (Machine-to-Machine)**
*   **Definition:** Communication directly between machines.
*   **Purpose:** Integrates information to network/platform to monitor object status, control situations, and send information to users or intelligent devices.
*   **Typical Service Types:**
    *   **Remote Monitoring:** Environment monitoring, remote metering.
    *   **Remote Control:** Remote control of assets, m-POS (mobile point-of-sale).
    *   **Asset Management:** Security systems, vending machines, fleet management, delivery management.
*   **Reasons for M2M Growth:**
    1.  **Expanding Wireless Networks:** Increased coverage and stability.
    2.  **Declining Telecommunication Module Prices:** Lower costs, rapid market penetration.
    3.  **Declining Sensor Prices:** More sophisticated sensors at lower costs, enabling sensing-based services.
*   **M2M Device Components:**
    *   **Module:** Contains a mobile chipset. Crucial for purpose-built devices and standardization.
    *   **Chipset:** The core processing unit.
    *   **Sensor/Input & Output Unit:** Acquires data.
    *   **Data Processing Unit:** Processes acquired data.
    *   **Communication Module:** Sends processed data (e.g., via RS-232, USB).
*   **Standardization:** Crucial for market growth; current top-down approach (service layer defining lower layers) hinders public sharing and standardization.

**C. IoT (Internet of Things)**
*   **Definition:** Creates an environment where *everything* (people, objects, spaces) is connected to the Internet to create, collect, share, and utilize information.
*   **Evolution:** The idea has existed and evolved over time, not a sudden phenomenon.
*   **IoT vs. M2M:**
    *   **M2M:** Often specialized and siloed within specific industry sectors.
    *   **IoT:** Connects these disparate M2M technologies under a universal communication network (the Internet) to offer more diverse and dynamic services. IoT is a broader concept encompassing M2M.
*   **Examples of Services:**
    *   **M2M Roots:** Barcodes, RFID, Process Control.
    *   **IoT Evolution:** Sensor Networks, Big Data, Connected Cars, Smart Grid, NFC/iBEACON, Device-to-Device (D2D).
    *   **Internet of Everything (IoE):** Distributions, Mobile Cloud, Big Data.
*   **Market Outlook:**
    *   **Phase:** Currently in introduction/early growth.
    *   **Growth:** Expected to grow >20% annually, reaching $1.2 trillion by 2022.
    *   **Value Creation:** Reduces transaction costs between physical and digital worlds, improves productivity, creates new markets.
    *   **Trends:** Mobile-centric networks, integration with Big Data, shift from supplier to buyer's market.
*   **Functions Driving Growth:**
    *   Optimization.
    *   Integration with other social infrastructures (cross-industry).
    *   Social infrastructure management.
*   **Social Benefits:** Improves efficiency of social infrastructure, responds to societal needs (broader impact beyond personal convenience).

## Pages 145-149


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: M2M, IoT, Cloud Computing, & Virtualization

### 1. Machine-to-Machine (M2M) Communication

**What is M2M?**
M2M involves direct communication between devices, enabling automation and data exchange without human intervention.

**Why is M2M Spreading?**
1.  **Expanding Wireless Networks:** Increased coverage and service stability.
2.  **Declining Module Prices:** Telecommunication module market growing with falling prices and rising availability.
3.  **Declining Sensor Prices:** More sophisticated sensors becoming cheaper, leading to diverse applications (monitoring, fault detection, asset management, customer usage).

**How M2M Devices are Built:**
*   Starts with developing a module containing a mobile chipset.
*   The device is then built using this module.
*   **Main Parts of an M2M Device:**
    1.  **Sensor/Input & Output Unit:** Acquires data.
    2.  **Data Processing Unit:** Processes acquired data.
    3.  **Communication Module:** Sends processed data (often using RS-232 or USB to connect to the processing unit).

**Challenges & Requirements for M2M:**
*   Need the right device and standardized modules for wider adoption.
*   Require a universal platform and established access protocols for large-scale rollout.
*   Identification systems and security functions are crucial for public/private sector object communication.

**Standardization Importance:**
*   A top-down approach (service layer defining lower layers) can hinder standardization and market growth.
*   Standardization of the M2M environment is critical for market expansion.
*   M2M services currently use 2G, 3G networks.

### 2. Internet of Things (IoT)

**What is IoT?**
IoT is an environment where communication connects everything – people, objects, and spaces – to the Internet to create, collect, share, and utilize information.

**IoT vs. M2M:**
*   **M2M:** Often specialized within specific industries.
*   **IoT:** An effort to connect these disparate M2M technologies under the universal Internet network to offer more diverse and dynamic services. IoT represents a broader, more interconnected vision evolving from M2M.

**IoT Market & Future:**
*   Currently in introduction/early growth phase, expected to grow over 20% annually to $1.2 trillion by 2022.
*   Creates value by reducing transaction costs between the physical and digital worlds.
*   Will improve productivity and create new markets.
*   **Trends:**
    *   **Mobile-Centric:** Driven by network speed and mobile device penetration.
    *   **Big Data Integration:** Applied to processing and analyzing large datasets.
    *   **Buyer's Market:** Market shifts from supplier to buyer influence due to increased product knowledge and usage.

**Key Functions Driving IoT Growth:**
1.  **Optimization:** Improving efficiency.
2.  **Integration with Social Infrastructures:** Connecting across industries.
3.  **Management of Social Infrastructures:** Enhancing public services and responsiveness.

### 3. Cloud Computing

**What is Cloud Computing?**
Cloud computing allows users to access IT resources (networks, servers, storage, applications) over the Internet as a service, on demand, without owning the underlying infrastructure. It's like a rental business for IT.

**Origins:**
*   An old concept that gained market interest due to global economic recession and the need for cost reduction.
*   Improved virtualization technology made it possible to integrate distributed IT resources into a single system for service.

**Characteristics of Cloud Computing:**
*   **On-Demand Self-Service:** Users can provision computing capabilities (e.g., server time, network storage) as needed, automatically, without human interaction with each service provider. Minimal infrastructure investment for customers.
*   **Scalability:** Resources can be rapidly provisioned or released to meet changing demands.
*   **Broad Network Access:** Services are available over the network and accessed through standard mechanisms (e.g., thick/thin clients).
*   **Resource Pooling:** The provider's computing resources are pooled to serve multiple consumers using a multi-tenant model, with resources dynamically assigned and reassigned based on demand.
*   **Measured Service:** Resource usage is monitored, controlled, and reported, providing transparency for both providers and consumers (pay-as-you-go).

**Cloud Computing Stakeholders:**
1.  **Vendors:** Provide hardware, solutions, and applications to cloud service providers.
2.  **Providers:** Offer cloud services to users (e.g., Amazon, Salesforce, Google).
3.  **Users:** Individuals or corporations who actually use cloud services, paying only for what they use and scaling resources in real-time.

**Cloud Service Technologies (Hierarchy):**
*   **Cloud Client:** Technologies for utilizing cloud services (e.g., lightweight terminals, mobile cloud tech).
*   **Cloud Service & Applications:** Technologies for delivering various cloud services as software or applications.
*   **Cloud Platform:** Technologies providing the basic functional environment for easily developing services (e.g., PaaS).
*   **Cloud Infrastructure:** Technologies providing fundamental resources like servers, storage, and networks as services (e.g., IaaS).

**Standardization & Quality:**
*   Standardization focuses on cloud security, clients, and platform virtualization to ensure compatibility.
*   Guidelines for managing quality indicators (SLA) are crucial for market growth.

**Cloud Service Models (Based on IT Resources):**
1.  **SaaS (Software as a Service):**
    *   **What:** Users access applications over the Internet via a web browser.
    *   **How:** Applications are hosted and managed by the provider.
    *   **Examples:** Google Gmail, MS Office 365.
2.  **PaaS (Platform as a Service):**
    *   **What:** Providers offer an environment for developing and running web applications.
    *   **How:** Includes operating systems, programming languages, databases, web servers. App development technologies must be modularized and standardized.
    *   **Examples:** Salesforce.com's Force.com, Google App Engine.
3.  **IaaS (Infrastructure as a Service):**
    *   **What:** Providers offer virtualized computing resources like servers, storage, and networks.
    *   **How:** Users manage operating systems, applications, and sometimes middleware. Requires significant infrastructure (data centers, capital, power).
    *   **Examples:** Amazon EC2 & S3.

**Cloud Service Deployment Models (Based on Configuration):**
1.  **Public Cloud:**
    *   **What:** Services shared by multiple users over the Internet.
    *   **Management:** Provided and managed by a third-party cloud service provider.
2.  **Private Cloud:**
    *   **What:** An IT environment exclusively deployed on a company's or organization's intranet.
    *   **Management:** Controlled by the company or organization itself.
3.  **Hybrid Cloud:**
    *   **What:** Combines public and private clouds, allowing data and applications to be shared between them.
    *   **Benefit:** Offers scalability and allows specialized applications to run in parallel.

**Advantages of Cloud Computing:**
*   Users can purchase, design, and install services directly without IT manager intervention.
*   Improves efficiency by sharing IT resources.
*   Avoids costs associated with owning IT resources.
*   Enables new business models by merging with different services.

### 4. Virtualization

**What is Virtualization?**
Virtualization is the abstraction of computer resources. It's a technique that hides the physical characteristics of computer resources from other systems, applications, and end-users. It allows:
*   Creating multiple logical resources from a single physical resource.
*   Creating a single logical resource from multiple physical resources.

**Types of Virtualization:**
1.  **Application Virtualization:**
    *   Users access needed applications instantly without installing them on their individual PCs.
2.  **Desktop Virtualization:**
    *   **Server-Side:** Users can virtually own a heterogeneous desktop (e.g., Windows Vista, Windows 7) from a server.
    *   **Client-Side:** Enables heterogeneous virtual desktops directly on individual PCs.
    *   **Benefit:** Allows separation of personal and corporate workspaces.

## Pages 148-152


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT Business & Ethics: Key Concepts

### 1. Cloud Computing

Cloud computing allows users to access shared IT resources over the internet, improving efficiency and reducing costs.

**1.1 Core Cloud Technologies**

*   **Cloud Client:** Technology for users to access cloud services (e.g., mobile apps, lightweight terminals).
*   **Cloud Service & Applications:** Software or applications provided as services.
*   **Cloud Platform:** Provides an environment for developing and running services.
*   **Cloud Infrastructure:** Provides fundamental resources like servers, storage, and networks as services.

**1.2 Cloud Service Models (Based on IT Resource Nature)**

*   **SaaS (Software as a Service):**
    *   **Definition:** Users access applications via the internet/web browser without installing them.
    *   **Examples:** Google Gmail, MS Office 365.
*   **PaaS (Platform as a Service):**
    *   **Definition:** Provides an environment (platform) for developers to build and run web applications. Requires modularized and standardized app development technologies.
    *   **Examples:** Salesforce.com's Force.com, Google App Engine.
*   **IaaS (Infrastructure as a Service):**
    *   **Definition:** Provides virtualized computing resources like servers, storage, and networks. Users can provision resources on demand.
    *   **Requirements:** Large data centers, capital, good electrical infrastructure.
    *   **Examples:** Amazon EC2 & S3, Gabia's cloud hosting.

**1.3 Cloud Deployment Models (Based on Configuration)**

*   **Public Cloud:**
    *   **Definition:** Services shared by multiple users over the internet. Managed by a cloud service provider.
*   **Private Cloud:**
    *   **Definition:** IT environment exclusively deployed on a company's/organization's intranet. Controlled by the company.
*   **Hybrid Cloud:**
    *   **Definition:** Combines public and private cloud services, offering scalability and flexibility for specific applications.

**1.4 Benefits of Cloud Computing**

*   Users can directly purchase, design, and install IT resources without IT manager intervention.
*   Improves efficiency by sharing IT resources.
*   Avoids costs associated with owning IT resources.
*   Enables new business models by merging with different services.

### 2. Virtualization

**2.1 Definition**
Virtualization is a technique to abstract computer resources. It hides physical resource characteristics, allowing:
*   Multiple logical resources from one physical resource.
*   A single logical resource from multiple physical resources.

**2.2 Types of Virtualization**

*   **Application Virtualization:** Users access applications instantly without local installation.
*   **Desktop Virtualization:**
    *   **Server-side:** Users get virtual desktops (e.g., Windows OS) from a central server.
    *   **Client-side:** Enables virtual desktops on individual PCs.
    *   **Benefit:** Separates personal and corporate workspaces.
*   **Server Virtualization:** Consolidates multiple physical server workloads onto fewer virtual servers, improving resource utilization, reducing rack costs, and administrative efforts.
*   **Storage Virtualization:**
    *   Uses **Thin-Provisioning** to allocate only the minimum required physical space initially.
    *   Integrates heterogeneous (different types of) storage systems into a unified environment.
*   **Network Virtualization:** Network hardware (switches, firewalls) are implemented as virtual machines, allowing virtual network operation within a single shared physical environment.

**2.3 Functions of Virtualization**

*   **Sharing:** Many virtual resources use one physical resource (e.g., Virtual Machines, Virtual LANs).
*   **Aggregation:** Virtual resources span multiple physical resources, increasing overall capacity and simplifying management (e.g., Storage virtualization).
*   **Emulation:** Virtual resources appear to have functions/characteristics they don't physically possess (e.g., virtual tape storage).
*   **Insulation (Transparent Change/Failure Proof):** Allows physical resources to be replaced without affecting virtual resources or users, preventing failures (e.g., RAID storage controller).

### 3. Blockchain Service

**3.1 Definition**
Blockchain is a distributed ledger network technology. It uses a decentralized, peer-to-peer (P2P) network where data blocks are stored and linked together in chains. It's the core technology behind cryptocurrencies like Bitcoin.

**3.2 Key Characteristics of Blockchain**

*   **Decentralized:** No central server. All network nodes work together to verify and guarantee data integrity.
*   **Improved Security:** Transactions are accepted only after consent from more than half of all network nodes.
*   **Transparency:** All nodes share their ledgers, making transaction records openly disclosed.
*   **Enhanced Safety (Self-Recovery):** The distributed nature allows the network to recover easily even if some nodes experience errors.
*   **Improved Economics:** Reduces centralized management costs and financial transaction costs due to the absence of a central server.
*   **Personal Data Protection:** Reduces risks of data collection, security breaches, or leaks associated with central systems.

**3.3 Blockchain Transaction Process**

1.  User A wants to transfer money to User B.
2.  Transaction data is generated as a "block."
3.  This block is shared with all participants on the network.
4.  Participants independently validate the transaction data (cross-validation).
5.  Once validated by the majority, the block is registered and added to the existing chain.
6.  The money transfer from A to B is complete.

**3.4 Immutability**
Because all nodes are involved in block creation and verification, and transactions require majority approval, it's virtually impossible to arbitrarily modify or manipulate transactions on a blockchain.

### 4. Smart Infrastructure

**4.1 Smart City**

*   **Definition:** An urban model that uses new technologies like ICT (Information and Communication Technology) and Big Data to solve urban problems and improve quality of life.
*   **Purpose:** Addresses challenges like aging infrastructure, energy shortages, environmental pollution, and crime.
*   **Key Technologies:** AI, Big Data, 5G mobile technologies.
*   **Service Areas:** Smart traffic, smart environment, public safety, public welfare, smart energy.
*   **Role:** A leading example of smart infrastructure.

**4.2 Smart Grid**

*   **Definition:** A next-generation power system that integrates IT with existing power grids. It monitors and controls power supply and demand in real-time to match production and consumption.
*   **Contrast with Traditional Power Systems:**
    *   **Traditional:** Centralized power generation; producers unilaterally supply power. Plants are built to meet estimated maximum consumption.
    *   **Smart Grid:** Decentralized control; optimizes power generation and consumption, making the system more efficient and responsive.

## Pages 151-155


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: Modern IT Concepts

### I. Blockchain

**What is Blockchain?**
A decentralized system where transaction ledger data is recorded, managed, and verified in "blocks" across all network participants (nodes). Unlike traditional methods, there's no central server.

**Key Characteristics:**

*   **Decentralized:** No central server. All network nodes work together to prove and guarantee data integrity.
*   **Improved Security:** Transactions are accepted only after consent from over half of the network nodes, making modification/manipulation impossible.
*   **Transparency of Transactions:** All participants share ledgers, disclosing transaction details.
*   **Enhanced Safety:** The distributed nature means the network can recover even if some nodes experience errors or abnormalities.
*   **Improved Economics:** Reduces centralized management and financial transaction costs by removing the need for a central server.
*   **Protection of Personal Data:** Lessens the risk of data collection burdens, security issues, or leaks from central system errors or hacking.

**How Blockchain Transactions Work (Concept):**
1.  **Initiation:** User A wants to transfer money to User B.
2.  **Block Creation:** Transaction data is generated as a "block."
3.  **Sharing:** The block is shared with all network participants.
4.  **Validation:** Participants cross-validate the transaction data.
5.  **Registration:** Once validated (by >50% of nodes), the block is registered onto the blockchain.
6.  **Completion:** Money transfer from A to B is complete.

### II. Smart Infrastructure

#### A. Smart City

**Definition:** An urban model that solves city problems and improves quality of life by adopting new technologies like ICT (Information and Communication Technology) and Big Data.

**Purpose:** Addresses issues such as:
*   Aging infrastructure
*   Energy shortages
*   Environmental pollution
*   Crime

**Technologies Used:** AI (Artificial Intelligence), Big Data, 5G mobile technologies.

**Service Areas:** Smart traffic, smart environment, public safety, public welfare, smart energy.

#### B. Smart Grid

**Definition:** A next-generation power system that integrates IT technologies with existing power grids to monitor and control power supply and demand in real-time, matching production and consumption.

**Key Differences: Traditional Grid vs. Smart Grid**

| Feature              | Traditional Electric Power Grid      | Smart Grid                                         |
| :------------------- | :----------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------- |
| **Generation**       | Centralized power generation         | Distributed power generation                       |
| **Control System**   | Analog                               | Digital                                            |
| **Blackout Diagnosis** | Impossible                           | Self-diagnosis                                     |
| **Blackout Recovery** | Manual recovery                      | Semi-automated recovery and automatic repair       |
| **Facility Inspection** | Manual                               | Remote                                             |
| **Communication**    | One-way                              | Bi-directional (two-way)                           |
| **Power Source**     | Centralized (fossil fuel, nuclear)   | Distributed (renewable energy expansion)           |
| **Control System**   | Local area control                   | Wide area control                                  |
| **Pricing Info**     | Limited (monthly total cost)         | Real-time information available                    |
| **Pricing System**   | Fixed price                          | Real-time varying price                            |
| **Electricity Use**  | Fluctuating (demand-dependent)       | Almost uniform (price-dependent)                   |

**Benefits:**
*   Reduces greenhouse gases.
*   Induces voluntary energy savings.
*   Improves electricity quality and reliability through efficiency and distributed energy sources (e.g., renewables).

**Characteristics:**
*   Consumers can actively participate in energy management.
*   Supports diverse ways of generating and storing electricity.
*   Leads to new products, services, and markets.
*   Provides high-quality electricity.
*   Enables connection to both centralized and distributed power generation sources (e.g., renewable energy).

**Smart Grid Components:**
1.  **Smart Grid Platform:**
    *   **Core:** Intelligent devices, bi-directional communication, sophisticated control systems.
    *   **Function:** Manages distributed and intelligent power grids.
    *   **Operations:** Supports renewable energy applications, intelligent electric vehicle charging stations, smart metering, power grid monitoring, demand response.
    *   **Intelligent Devices:** Have electronic sensors and meters to monitor the grid state, capable of basic autonomous decisions.
2.  **Smart Grid Applications:** Utilize the platform for specific functions (e.g., monitoring, managing electricity grid, smart metering, V2G - Vehicle-to-Grid).

**IT Infrastructure Role:**
*   Optimizes energy efficiency.
*   Encourages consumption changes through real-time, bi-directional information exchange.
*   Requires open system networks and protocols to foster new products, services, and markets.
*   Communication infrastructure must provide reliable end-to-end services between intelligent devices.
*   Development must adhere to standards for interoperability across various interfaces.

#### C. Micro Grid

**Definition:** An extension of a smart grid. A group of interconnected consumers and Distributed Energy Resources (DERs) that can operate as a single controllable entity. It can connect to the main grid or function independently.

**Simplified View:** A local power grid connecting electricity users with distributed energy resources (like wind and solar). It can be self-sufficient but also connect to the regular grid when needed.

**Examples (South Korea):** Pilot testing in Jeju Island's smart grid complex, Gapado, Marado, and Ulleungdo.

#### D. Smart Water Grid

**Definition:** A smart technology that leverages ICT to manage water, including the essential substance itself, water supply, and sewage water.

**Purpose:** Addresses water management challenges caused by climate change.

**How ICT is Used:** Informatizes the entire water handling process:
*   Production of drinkable water.
*   Transportation of water.
*   Processing and reuse of water.
*   Integrates traditional and diverse water resources (underground, rainwater, reclaimed sewage, saline water).

## Pages 154-158


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business & Ethics (Smart Infrastructure)

This guide covers key concepts related to Smart Grids, Microgrids, Smart Water Grids, and Smart Traffic.

---

### 1. Smart Grid

**Definition & Purpose:**
*   An intelligent electricity network that optimizes energy efficiency.
*   Enables bi-directional exchange of real-time information (supply & demand) between energy producers and consumers.

**Components:**
1.  **Smart Grid Platforms:**
    *   **Core Function:** Manages distributed and intelligent power grids.
    *   **Key Technologies:** Intelligent devices, bi-directional communication, sophisticated control systems.
    *   **Applications Supported:** Renewable energy integration, intelligent electric vehicle (EV) charging, smart metering, power grid monitoring, demand response.
    *   **Intelligent Storage Devices:** Equipped with electronic sensors/meters and digital intelligence to monitor grid state and make basic decisions autonomously.
2.  **Smart Grid Applications:** (Services built upon the platform, e.g., smart metering, demand response).

**IT Infrastructure & Requirements:**
*   **Critical Role:** Acts as the essential IT elements for smart grid operation.
*   **Benefits:** Optimizes energy efficiency, facilitates real-time information exchange.
*   **Requirements:**
    *   **Open System Networks & Protocols:** Essential for creating new value-added products, services, and markets beyond just power supply.
    *   **End-to-End Communication:** Reliable and steady power supply through communication between intelligent devices.
    *   **Standard Adherence:** Supports interoperability across various interfaces.

---

### 2. Micro Grid

**Definition:**
*   An extension of a smart grid, typically for a local area.
*   **US Department of Energy (DOE):** "A group of interconnected consumers and distributed energy resources (DERs) under clearly defined electrical specifications that can be controlled as a single entity, and that could be connected to the system or made independent."

**Key Characteristics:**
*   **Local Power Grid:** Connects local electricity users with Distributed Energy Resources (DERs) like wind and solar power.
*   **Self-Sufficiency:** Can operate independently of the main electric grid, allowing grid owners to be self-sufficient in power.
*   **Grid Connection:** Can still connect to the regular grid when needed.

**Examples (South Korea):** Jeju Island's smart grid complex, Gapado, Marado, Ulleungdo.

---

### 3. Smart Water Grid

**Definition & Purpose:**
*   A smart technology that uses Information and Communication Technology (ICT) to manage water resources.
*   Covers the entire water cycle: production of drinkable water, transportation, processing, and reuse.
*   Addresses challenges related to climate change and water management.

**Reasons for Emergence:**
*   **Spread of Cloud Computing:** Enables automatic detection, cloud storage, and automated problem resolution for water systems.
*   **Intelligent Inspection Infrastructure:** Provides real-time water usage data via remote monitoring, improving fare calculation and reducing water usage.
*   **Impact of Climate Change:** Addresses agricultural water shortages, changes in river flow rates, and increased uncertainties/damage from drought/flood.
*   **Growing Global Water Demand:** Driven by increasing world population and industrialization, leading to increased interest in water resource supply.

**Key Technologies:**
*   Water resource acquisition and distribution technology.
*   Real-time and automated water supply and demand management technology.
*   Advanced ICT-convergent water management technology.

---

### 4. Smart Traffic (Intelligent Transportation Systems)

**Definition & Purpose:**
*   An intelligent transportation service that leverages information exchange.
*   **Goals:** Improve traffic safety, enhance traffic flow efficiency, and provide user convenience.
*   **Information Exchange:** Occurs between vehicles (V2V), vehicles and infrastructure (V2I), and vehicles and traffic control servers (V2N).

**Types of V2X Services (Vehicle-to-Everything):**

#### a. V2V (Vehicle-to-Vehicle) Service
*   **Mechanism:** Vehicles wirelessly exchange information with surrounding vehicles.
*   **Information Exchanged:** Vehicle positions, traffic flow details, road conditions.
*   **Communication Technology:** Primarily Wireless Access in Vehicle Environments (WAVE).
*   **Examples:**
    *   Roadside information & obstacle notification.
    *   Road construction notification.
    *   Intersection traffic signal notification.
    *   Nearby vehicle information notification.
    *   Emergency vehicle proximity notification.

#### b. V2I (Vehicle-to-Infrastructure) Service
*   **Mechanism:** Vehicles communicate with traffic support infrastructure (e.g., roadside base stations).
*   **Vehicle Component:** On-Board Unit (OBU).
*   **Communication Technologies:** WAVE, 4G LTE/5G.
*   **Process:**
    1.  Vehicles with OBUs send/receive messages to/from roadside base stations.
    2.  Base stations connect to the traffic control center's backend server.
    3.  Center system collects, analyzes vehicle/base station data, then sends traffic/road condition info back to base stations.
    4.  Base stations relay this information to vehicles.
*   **Examples:**
    *   Real-time traffic information collection & provision.
    *   Electronic toll collection.
    *   Roadside information & obstacle notification.
    *   Road construction notification.
    *   Protected zone notification.

#### c. V2N (Vehicle-to-Network) Service
*   **Mechanism:** Vehicle communicates via a network with a server (in the cloud/Internet) or a mobile device.
*   **Vehicle Component:** Telecommunication Control Unit (TCU).
*   **Process:** TCU in vehicle communicates with a backend server, which then communicates with a mobile device.
*   **Purpose:** Provides information to the user and enables vehicle control.
*   **Communication Technologies (general network types):** Mobile communication, fixed-line connections, nearfield communication.

---


---


## Pages 157-161


## Learning Guide: Smart Technologies in Business & Ethics

This guide simplifies key concepts in Smart Transportation, Smart Education, and Smart Healthcare, focusing on essential information for learning.

---

### 1. Smart Transportation

Smart transportation uses technology to improve traffic systems. It involves communication between vehicles, infrastructure, and networks.

#### 1.1. Classification of Smart Transportation Services

Smart traffic services are categorized by who communicates with whom:

*   **V2V (Vehicle-to-Vehicle) Service:**
    *   **Definition:** Vehicles wirelessly exchange information with surrounding vehicles.
    *   **Purpose:** Share data on position, traffic flow, and road conditions.
    *   **Communication:** Primarily uses **WAVE** (Wireless Access in Vehicle Environments).
    *   **Examples:**
        *   Roadside information and obstacle notifications
        *   Road construction notifications
        *   Intersection traffic signal notifications
        *   Nearby vehicle information notifications
        *   Emergency vehicle proximity notifications

*   **V2I (Vehicle-to-Infrastructure) Service:**
    *   **Definition:** Vehicles communicate with traffic support infrastructure.
    *   **How it Works:**
        *   Vehicles with **OBU** (On-Board Units) send/receive messages with roadside base stations (via WAVE, 4G LTE/5G).
        *   Roadside base stations connect to a back-end server at a traffic control center.
        *   The center collects and analyzes vehicle/base station data, then sends traffic/road condition info back to vehicles via base stations.
    *   **Examples:**
        *   Real-time traffic information collection and provision
        *   Toll collection
        *   Roadside information and obstacle notifications
        *   Road construction notifications
        *   Protected zone notifications

*   **V2N (Vehicle-to-Network) Service:**
    *   **Definition:** Vehicles communicate with a server or mobile device via a network (cloud or Internet).
    *   **How it Works:**
        *   A **TCU** (Telecommunication Control Unit) in the vehicle communicates with a back-end server.
        *   The server then communicates with mobile devices to provide user information and control the vehicle.

#### 1.2. Connected Car Service

*   **Definition:** A core technology for self-driving cars, built on advances in telematics, mobile communication, and cloud services.
*   **Functionality:** Allows cars to connect with other cars, surroundings, and infrastructure.
*   **Services Provided:**
    *   Transportation information
    *   In-car music services
    *   Information services for riders
    *   Augmented reality (AR) information services
    *   Road condition recognition and notification
    *   Fully autonomous driving and automatic parking

---

### 2. Smart Education

Smart education adapts to societal changes by leveraging digital technology for personalized and engaging learning.

#### 2.1. Driving Factors & Concept

*   **Societal Changes:**
    *   Increased cohabitation (couples living together without marriage)
    *   Declining birth rate
    *   Increased respect for individual choices
    *   Rapid aging population
*   **Government Response:** National strategy for smart education and basic plan for education informatization.
*   **Concept of Smart Education:**
    *   **Self-paced:** Learning at one's own speed.
    *   **Fun:** Engaging and enjoyable learning experiences.
    *   **Level-aligned:** Tailored to individual student levels and interests.
    *   **IT-based:** Uses information technology for learning.
*   **Development Timeline:**
    *   **1997:** Basic research began.
    *   **2006:** Digital textbook prototype produced.
    *   **2007:** Ministry of Education developed digital textbooks (Korean, English, Math).
    *   **2011:** "Smart Education Promotion Strategy" announced.

#### 2.2. Smart Classroom

*   **Definition:** A teaching environment equipped with digital devices to enhance learning.
*   **Key Components:**
    *   Projectors, TVs
    *   Large smart liquid crystal displays
    *   Electronic blackboards
    *   Wireless Internet devices
*   **Teacher Role:** Conducts classes using various digital devices and programs.

#### 2.3. Digital Textbooks

*   **Definition:** Digital versions of traditional paper textbooks, enhanced with interactive features.
*   **Key Features:**
    *   Includes videos and multimedia content.
    *   Offers interactive functions.
    *   Provides automatic scoring capabilities.
*   **Examples:** Moving images of molecular action, zoomable images (e.g., Earth from space).

#### 2.4. Smart Education Tools & Methods

Smart education uses various digital tools for different teaching activities:

*   **Production:** PowerPoint, Hangul, Google Apps, Lectora, e-textbook authoring tools, movie makers, PDF document production, SNS, Evernote, Prezi.
*   **Search:** Naver, Google, IP-TV, Fastel, YouTube.
*   **Analysis:** Fastel, Google document tools.
*   **Presentation:** Classting, Twitter, mirroring, LMS solutions, Google document tools, SNS, messengers, electronic blackboards.
*   **Evaluation:** Fastel, Google document tools, quizzes.
*   **Sharing:** Fastel, Classting, Google document tools.
*   **Communication:** SNS, LMS messaging, Twitter, Facebook, Google Drive, Classting, school website bulletin boards.

---

### 3. Smart Healthcare

Smart healthcare combines digital devices and IT with medical services, poised for significant growth through advanced technologies.

#### 3.1. Concept & Structure

*   **Definition:** The integration of 'smart' (digital/IT devices) and 'healthcare' (medical services).
*   **Future Growth:** Expected to advance significantly when combined with **4th Industrial Revolution technologies** like IoT, cloud computing, Big Data, and AI.
*   **Operational Structure:**
    1.  **Data Generation:** Consumers/patients generate health data (e.g., via wearables).
    2.  **Communication/Platform:** Data is transmitted through communication channels and data platforms.
    3.  **Data Collection/Analysis:** Specialized firms (e.g., Bio R&D, diagnosis companies) collect and analyze this data, often using Big Data techniques.
    4.  **Service Provision:** Medical institutions, pharmaceutical companies, and health management companies use these findings to provide remote or in-person health counseling, treatment, and medical care to consumers.

#### 3.2. Growth Factors

Several factors contribute to the growth of the smart healthcare industry:

*   **Technological Advances:** User growth and advancements in wireless mobile communications and mobile devices.
*   **Data Importance:** Increased importance of analysis using Big Data and the rise of a hyper-connected society.
*   **Demographic & Health Trends:**
    *   Decreased birth rates and rapid entry into an aging society.
    *   Continuous increase in new and chronic diseases.
*   **Economic & Cultural Demand:** Increased demand for healthcare due to cultural and economic development.

#### 3.3. Key Areas of Smart Healthcare

To foster technological superiority, an open ecosystem is crucial across major sectors:

*   **Digital Medical Devices:**
    *   Includes digital diagnosis and digital therapy (e.g., software for managing diabetes or asthma).
    *   Products for diagnosing, treating, and preventing diseases, or for achieving specific clinical results.
*   **Wearable Biometric Measuring Devices:**
    *   Devices designed for the consumer market to measure biological data.
*   **Remote Healthcare (Telemedicine):**
    *   Healthcare services provided remotely.
    *   Includes monitoring remote patients.
*   **Analysis & Big Data:**
    *   Involves integrating and analyzing diverse ranges of health-related data.
*   **Others:**
    *   Consumer healthcare contract management.

#### 3.4. Core Technologies

Key technologies supporting smart healthcare include:

*   Health information measurement technology.
*   Customized diagnosis and field diagnosis technology.
*   Open healthcare platform technology.
*   Remote healthcare service technology.

## IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide (Pages 160-164)

### 1. Digital Textbooks

*   **Definition:** Digital versions of traditional paper textbooks.
*   **Added Features:** Include videos, interactive functions, and automatic scoring capabilities.
*   **Examples:** Show moving images of molecular actions, or zoomable images of Earth from space.

### 2. Smart Healthcare

*   **Definition:** A field combining digital and IT devices ("smart") with medical services ("healthcare").
*   **Future Growth:** Expected to advance significantly when integrated with core 4th Industrial Revolution technologies like IoT, Cloud Computing, Big Data, and AI.
*   **Core Process:**
    1.  Consumers/patients generate or measure data (e.g., via wearables).
    2.  Specialized firms collect and analyze this data (e.g., using Big Data techniques).
    3.  Based on analysis, medical institutions provide services (e.g., counseling, treatment).
    4.  Communication/data platform companies facilitate data exchange.

#### 2.1 Growth Factors

*   **Technology:** User growth and advancements in wireless mobile communications and mobile devices.
*   **Data:** Increased importance of Big Data analysis and the rise of a hyper-connected society.
*   **Demographics:** Decreasing birth rates, rapidly aging populations, and a continuous rise in new and chronic diseases.
*   **Economy/Culture:** Increased demand for healthcare due to cultural and economic development.

#### 2.2 Key Areas

*   **Digital Medical Devices:** Products for diagnosis, treatment, and prevention of diseases (e.g., digital diagnosis, software for managing diabetes/asthma).
*   **Wearable Devices:** Biometric measuring devices developed for the consumer market.
*   **Telemedicine (Remote Healthcare):** Healthcare services provided remotely, including remote patient monitoring.

*   Customized Diagnosis and Field Diagnosis Technology

### 3. Latest IT Business Services

#### 3.1 Artificial Intelligence (AI)

*   **Definition (Modern):** The method of making computers or machines mimic human intelligence (cognition, inference, learning), or the technology researching its feasibility.
*   **Original Definition (John McCarthy, 1956):** Making a machine behave in ways that would be called intelligent if a human were so behaving.
*   **Everyday Examples:**
    *   **Translation Services:** Google Translator, Naver Translator (using artificial neural networks).
    *   **Image Classification/Machine Vision:** Kakao's flower search, Naver's smart lens, Google Lens.
    *   **Other Services:** Music recognition, watermark removal, auto-draw.

#### 3.1.1 Key AI Technologies

*   **Characteristics:** Ability to reason, generality, vastness, inaccuracy, knowledge use.
*   **Current Focus Areas:** Pattern recognition, machine learning, and deep learning.

#### 3.1.2 Pattern Recognition

*   **Definition:** The process of separating learned data into multiple groups based on specific criteria of input values.
*   **Stages:**
    1.  **Learning Stage:** Extract key information for distinguishing patterns by analyzing characteristics of a given dataset.
    2.  **Recognition Stage:** Classify and recognize new data using the patterns identified during the learning stage.

#### 3.1.3 Machine Learning

*   **Definition:** The field of developing algorithms that enable machines to learn. It's about systems autonomously improving performance using empirical data gathered through environmental interaction.
*   **Main Categories:**
    *   **1. Supervised Learning:** Learns from labeled data (input-output pairs) to predict future outcomes.
        *   **Algorithms:**
            *   **Regression Analysis:** Models relationships between data by minimizing error margins.
            *   **Decision Tree:** Generates a tree-shaped model to derive decisions based on data properties.
            *   **Artificial Neural Network (ANN):** Mimics biological neural networks (input, hidden, output layers) by updating node weights.
            *   **Bayes Theorem:** Applies Bayes theorem (assuming independence) for classification and prediction.
            *   **Support Vector Machine (SVM):** Finds the optimal decision boundary using margins.
    *   **2. Unsupervised Learning:** Learns from unlabeled data to find hidden patterns or structures.
        *   **Algorithms:**
            *   **Clustering:** Groups similar data points into clusters.
            *   **Dimensionality Reduction:** Summarizes or represents data in a lower dimension while preserving key information.
    *   **3. Semi-supervised Learning:** Combines aspects of both supervised and unsupervised learning, often using a small amount of labeled data with a large amount of unlabeled data.
        *   **Algorithms:** Often combines supervised algorithms with clustering; Expected Value Maximization for probability models with unobserved variables.

#### 3.1.4 Deep Learning

*   **Definition:** A branch of machine learning responsible for recent AI advancements. It solves problems similarly to humans using multi-layered artificial neural networks.
*   **Basis:** Human neural network theory.
*   **Key Characteristics:**
    *   **Consolidated Feature Extraction:** Pre-processing and feature extraction steps are integrated into the overall learning process.
    *   **Automatic Complex Data Information Extraction:** Reduces information loss when processing high-dimensional, complex data (e.g., images).
    *   **Efficient for High-Level Abstractions:** Improved ability to absorb large and complex datasets by scaling high-efficiency simulations.

#### 3.2 Use of Big Data

*   **Definition:** Data sets so large and complex that traditional data storage, management, and analysis methods are insufficient. They exceed the limits of general databases.
*   **Challenges:** Difficult to quantify using conventional methods due to its defining "3Vs":
    *   **Volume:** Extremely large size (e.g., petabytes, billions of records).
    *   **Variety:** Diverse data types (unstructured, non-formal, distributed data, simple correlation with plain schema).
    *   **Velocity:** Data generated at high speed and often time-sensitive (e.g., system logs, sensor data, SNS data).
*   **Representation:** Often visualized using specialized tools.
*   **Examples:**
    *   **Google "Flu Trends" (2008):** Predicted flu outbreaks by analyzing popular search queries related to flu and cold, along with user locations.
    *   **Credit Card Companies:** Analyze customer consumption and behavioral data for marketing, product development, and personalized recommendations.

## Pages 163-167

---

## Learning Guide: Modern IT & Business Concepts

### 1. Machine Learning (ML)

*   **Definition:** Algorithms that enable machines to learn and improve performance autonomously using data.
*   **Main Categories:**
    *   **Supervised Learning:** Learns from labeled data to predict outcomes.
    *   **Unsupervised Learning:** Finds patterns in unlabeled data.
    *   **Semi-supervised Learning:** Combines aspects of both (uses a small amount of labeled data with a large amount of unlabeled data).

#### Key Machine Learning Algorithms:

*   **Supervised Learning Algorithms:**
    *   **Regression Analysis:** Models relationships between data by minimizing error between given data and estimated values.
    *   **Decision Making Tree:** Creates a tree-shaped model based on data properties to make decisions.
    *   **Artificial Neural Network (ANN):** Mimics biological neural networks with input, intermediate, and output layers; updates weighted node values.
    *   **Bayes Theorem (e.g., Naive Bayes):** Applies Bayes theorem (often assuming independence between characteristics) for classification and prediction.
    *   **Support Vector Machine (SVM):** Finds the best decision boundary by defining an object function using margins.
*   **Unsupervised Learning Algorithms:**
    *   **Clustering:** Groups similar data points into "clusters" to classify data.
    *   **Dimensionality Reduction:** Summarizes or represents data in a lower dimension while retaining essential information.
*   **Semi-supervised Learning Algorithms:**
    *   Often combines supervised learning with clustering.
    *   **Expected Value Maximization (EM Algorithm):** An iterative algorithm for finding parameters in probabilistic models with unobserved (latent) variables.

---

### 2. Deep Learning (DL)

*   **Definition:** A branch of Machine Learning that uses Artificial Neural Networks (ANNs) with multiple layers to process information and solve problems, mimicking how humans learn. It's a key driver of recent AI advancements.
*   **Characteristics:**
    *   **Consolidated Feature Extraction:** Combines pre-processing and feature extraction into a single, integrated learning process.
    *   **Automatic Complex Data Information Extraction:** Efficiently extracts information from high-dimensional, complex data (e.g., images), reducing information loss.
    *   **Efficient for High-Level Abstractions:** Improved capability to absorb and summarize key content or functions from large, complex datasets.

---

### 3. Big Data

*   **Definition:** Data sets so large and complex that traditional data processing applications are inadequate. They exceed the limits of general databases.
*   **Key Characteristics (The 3 Vs):**
    *   **Volume:** Extremely large amount of data (peta bytes, trillions of records).
    *   **Variety:** Diverse data types, including unstructured (e.g., text, images, video) and non-metrical variables.
    *   **Velocity:** High speed of data generation and processing.
*   **Examples of Use:**
    *   **Google Flu Trends:** Predicted flu trends by analyzing search queries and locations.
    *   **Credit Card Companies:** Analyze customer consumption and behavior for marketing, product development, and recommendations.
*   **Detailed Characteristics:**
    *   **Data Size:** Millions/billions of users, trillions of records.
    *   **Data Structure:** Often unstructured, non-formal, large volume of distributed data; simple data correlation with plain schema.
    *   **Type of Data:** Includes time-related data and mission-critical data (e.g., system logs, sensor data, social media data, web mining data).

---

### 4. FinTech (Financial Technology)

*   **Definition:** A composite of "Financial" and "Technology," referring to services that integrate IT into traditional financial services like payments, remittances, asset management, crowdfunding, and loans.
*   **Evolution:** Originally described large vendors for financial institutions; now refers to innovative services from financial startups.
*   **Advantages over Traditional Finance:**
    *   Leverages smartphone-based mobile devices.
    *   Uses Big Data analysis for financial management and credit risk assessment at lower costs.
    *   Offers convenient and secure accessibility for payment services.
*   **Growth Factors:**
    *   Popularization of mobile services, open-source software, and cloud technology.
    *   Increasing consumer demand for new financial services.
    *   Low initial investment and labor costs due to internet-based nature.
    *   Consumer shift to faster and cheaper mobile financial transactions.
*   **Threat to Traditional Financial Companies:**
    *   **Payment & Remittance:** Easy customer acquisition and service accessibility via scalable platforms.
    *   **Lending & Investments:** High predictability provided by social and Big Data.
    *   FinTechs often use payment/remittance services as a platform to expand into other financial services (e.g., Alibaba's Alipay).
*   **Main Attributes:** Convenience, ease, and simplicity. It signifies a paradigm shift where non-financial companies with IT expertise provide financial services.

#### Types of FinTech Services:

*   **Payment Service:** Enables easy money transfer or payments, often linked with credit cards and bank accounts.
*   **Digital Currency:** Virtual currency that can be exchanged for real currency and used for payments globally (e.g., Bitcoin).
*   **P2P (Peer-to-Peer) Lending:** Connects investors directly with borrowers, offering an alternative to traditional bank loans.
*   **Financial Software:** Enhances financial convenience through Big Data analysis, proprietary algorithms, and AI.

#### Domestic Challenges (e.g., South Korea):

*   Limited scope for independent businesses without partnerships with financial institutions.
*   Extensive financial regulations hindering growth.
*   Need for government support to energize the industry and foster value creation.

---

### 5. O2O (Online to Offline) and O4O (Online for Offline)

#### O2O (Online to Offline)

*   **Definition:** Customers pay for goods or services online and then receive or consume them in an offline physical space. It's the opposite of "showrooming" (browsing offline, buying online).
*   **Examples:**
    *   **Baedal People:** Ordering and paying for food online, then receiving it offline.
    *   **Kakao Taxi:** Booking a taxi via a mobile app, then taking a physical taxi offline.
    *   **Wahome:** Paying online for house cleaning services that are performed offline.

#### O4O (Online for Offline)

*   **Definition:** An online company leverages its online strengths (data, technology, customer base) to operate or innovate an offline business, expanding its scope from online to offline.
*   **Example:**
    *   **Amazon Go:** An offline grocery store operated by Amazon. Customers use a mobile app to enter, pick items, and walk out. Their Amazon account is automatically charged, eliminating queues and cashiers. This leverages Amazon's online technology for offline customer convenience.

---

### 6. Virtual Currency, Digital Currency, and Crypto Currency

*   **Digital Currency:** The broadest term. Refers to any currency represented in electronic form, regardless of whether it's a legal tender or not.
*   **Virtual Currency:** A type of digital currency that is *not* issued or represented by a legal currency. Examples include mileage points or in-game currencies.
*   **Crypto Currency:** A specific type of virtual currency that uses distributed ledger technology (like blockchain) and cryptography (encryption) to secure transactions and verify the validity of its units. Examples include Bitcoin and Ethereum.

---

## Pages 166-170


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# IT Business & Ethics Learning Guide

## 1. Fintech

Fintech (Financial Technology) represents a shift where non-financial companies use IT to provide financial services.

### Key Attributes of Fintech:
*   **Convenience**
*   **Ease**
*   **Simplicity**

### Types of Fintech Services:
*   **Payment Service:** Enables easy money transfers and payments, often linked with credit cards and bank accounts.
*   **Digital Currency:** Virtual currency (like Bitcoin) exchangeable with real currency, accepted globally for goods/services.
*   **P2P (Peer-to-Peer) Lending:** Connects investors with borrowers, addressing limitations of traditional bank loans.
*   **Financial Software:** Enhances financial convenience using Big Data analysis, algorithms, and AI.

### Challenges for Domestic Fintech Industry:
*   Slow growth compared to overseas markets.
*   Few independent businesses without financial institution partnerships.
*   Numerous financial-related regulations.
*   **Government Role:** Needs to strengthen and impartially enforce regulations to energize the industry and generate value.

## 2. O2O (Online to Offline) and O4O (Online for Offline)

### O2O (Online to Offline)
*   **Concept:** Customers first check goods/services in offline stores (showrooming), then pay for them online.
*   **Examples:**
    *   **Baedal People:** Order and pay for food online, receive food offline.
    *   **Kakao Taxi:** Book a taxi via a mobile app, take a real taxi offline.
    *   **Wahome:** Pay online for room and house cleaning services.

### O4O (Online for Offline)
*   **Concept:** Expands business operations from online to offline. An online service provider leverages its online value to operate an offline business, driving market innovation.
*   **Example: Amazon Go**
    *   An offline mart selling groceries.
    *   **How it works:** Customers activate a mobile app, log in, take items, and leave. Amazon automatically settles the bill through their registered account (requires Amazon Prime) and sends a receipt.
    *   **Benefit:** Eliminates waiting in line at counters and the need for packing.
    *   This is a clear O4O case where an online company (Amazon) uses its strengths for offline customer convenience.

## 3. Virtual Currency

### Definitions:
*   **Digital Currency:** Any currency represented in electronic form (can include legal tender).
*   **Virtual Currency:** A digital currency *not* represented in legal currency (e.g., loyalty points, game currency).
*   **Cryptocurrency:** A method of authenticating virtual currency using a distributed ledger and encryption (e.g., Bitcoin).
*   **General Definition:** Digital or electronic currency used in a virtual network space without physical bills or coins.
*   **Expert Definition (ECB, U.S. Treasury):** A type of digital currency issued and managed by developers, not government-controlled, used for payment in specific virtual communities. Most cryptocurrencies are both digital and virtual currencies.

### Comparison with Cash and Digital Currency:

| Feature           | Cash            | Digital Currency      | Virtual Currency      |
| :---------------- | :-------------- | :-------------------- | :-------------------- |
| **Issuing Body**  | Central bank    | Financial institutions | None                  |
| **Amount Issued** | Central bank    | 1:1 with legal currency | Determined by algorithm |
| **Transaction**   | Issuing body    | Issuing body          | P2P network, DLTs     |
| **Currency Unit** | Legal currency  | Legal currency        | Independent unit      |
| **Convertibility**| Guaranteed      | Guaranteed            | Allowed, not guaranteed |
| **Price**         | Fixed           | Fixed                 | Changes (supply/demand)|

### Reasons for Virtual Currency Value Rise:
*   **Scarcity:** Fixed total issuance, and mining consumes physical resources.
*   **Network Effect:** Value increases as more people hold it simultaneously.
*   *Note:* Scarcity and network effects alone don't fully explain value.

### Is it True Currency?
*   **Currency Functions:** Storage of value, exchangeable, scale of value.
*   **Challenge:** Virtual currencies (like Bitcoin) have severe price volatility, preventing them from performing the "scale of value" function.
*   **Expert Opinion:** Virtual currency cannot displace a nation's legal currency.
*   **Beyond Payment:** Some virtual currencies (like Ethereum) can provide services beyond just payment, and the value of these services can increase the currency's price.

### Major Virtual Currencies:
*   Over 1,100 types exist, but **Bitcoin** and **Ethereum** account for over 70% of market capitalization.
    *   **Bitcoin (2009):**
        *   First distributed ledger-based virtual currency.
        *   Closed blockchain structure, mainly for transactions.
        *   Transaction time: ~10 minutes.
    *   **Ethereum (2014):**
        *   Improved organic blockchain structure (compared to Bitcoin's closed one).
        *   Supports smart contracts and other services, not just currency.
        *   Transaction time: ~10 seconds.
    *   **Ripple (2009):**
        *   Developed for bank transfers and low-cost payment services.
        *   Immediate settlement reduces risk and uses optimal currency conversion rates, reducing fees.
        *   Used by banks and companies for foreign trades.
    *   **Litecoin (2011):**
        *   Technically similar to Bitcoin but with improved speed.
        *   Up to 4 times faster transaction speed and higher maximum mining volume.

## 4. Linked Data

### Definition:
*   A structured data model that supports an interconnected Web.
*   Identifies data on the Web using individual **URI (Uniform Resource Identifier)** and assigns linked information to each URI.

### 4 Rules of Linked Data:
1.  **Use of URI:** Each individual object (not just documents) has its own URI.
2.  **Use of HTTP URI:** URIs are accessible via the HTTP protocol to enhance data access.
3.  **Use of RDF (Resource Description Framework):** Data is structured in a triple model (subject-predicate-object) to formally represent and link web data.
4.  **Assignment of Linked Information:** Makes the process of linking existing data on the Web easier.

### Usefulness of Linked Data:
*   **Reusable Data:** Data can be used via its URI, even if it's not one's own.
*   **Reduced Data Redundancy:** Helps check for existing data, eliminating duplicate information.
*   **Maximized Interoperability & Data Integration:**
    *   Issued as a semantic web standard, allowing it to be queried and used like a database.
    *   Free access and use enable data mash-ups (combining data from different sources).
*   **Network Effects:** Data expansion through linking leads to accelerated network effects.

## 5. Open Data

### Definition:
*   Data that anyone can freely use, reuse, and redistribute.

### Conditions for Open Data:
*   **Availability and Access:**
    *   Must be downloadable over the internet.
    *   Transformation of original data or production of new works should be possible at reasonable cost.
    *   Provided in a convenient, modifiable format.
*   **Reuse and Redistribution:**
    *   Must be reusable and redistributable, including when combined with other datasets.
*   **Universal Participation:**
    *   Everyone must be able to use, reuse, and redistribute the data.
    *   No restrictions on "commercial" or "non-commercial" use, or specific purposes (e.g., education).

## 6. Latest H/W-Centered IT Business Service: 3D Printing

### Definition:
*   A method of printing 3-dimensional objects using 3D digital data.
*   Also known as **additive manufacturing** because it builds structures by stacking layers of materials (powder, liquid, solid threads/wires/pellets).

### Why Manufacturers are Interested:
*   **Customized Production:** Suitable for producing small batches of diverse, customized products.
*   **Consumer Needs:** Improves manufacturing to quickly and easily customize products for diverse consumer demands.
*   **One-Person Manufacturing:** Enables individuals to make their own products.

### Impact and Benefits:
*   **Increased Individual/Small Manufacturer Share:** Increases the involvement of individuals and small manufacturers in manufacturing/distribution.
*   **Reprocessing Industry Development:** Drives the development of industries focused on commercializing 3D-printed products.
*   **Blurred Boundaries:** Collapses the traditional separation between consumption and manufacturing, meeting small, everyday manufacturing needs (e.g., 3D-printed Button 2.0 with earphone wire grooves).
