## Pages 169-173


Here's your simplified, easy-to-read learning guide for Pages 169-173:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business & Emerging Technologies

### I. Virtual Currencies

Virtual currencies are digital or virtual forms of money.

**Key Virtual Currencies:**

*   **Bitcoin (2009)**
    *   **First distributed ledger-based virtual currency.**
    *   **Structure:** Closed blockchain, blocks woven in a row.
    *   **Transaction Time:** ~10 minutes.
    *   **Primary Use:** Transaction book.
*   **Ripple (2009)**
    *   **Purpose:** Primarily for bank transfers.
    *   **Advantage:** Low-cost payment service, immediate settlement reduces risk.
    *   **Currency Conversion:** Uses best rates, reducing fees.
    *   **Users:** Many banks and companies involved in foreign trade.
*   **Litecoin (2011)**
    *   **Similarity:** Technically similar to Bitcoin.
    *   **Improvement:** Addresses Bitcoin's slow computing speed.
    *   **Performance:** Up to 4x faster transaction speed and higher maximum mining volume.
*   **Ethereum (2014)**
    *   **Structure:** Improved from closed to an organic blockchain.
    *   **Beyond Currency:** Expandable to **smart contracts** and various services.
    *   **Transaction Time:** ~10 seconds.

### II. Linked Data

**Linked data** is a structured data model that creates an interconnected Web. It identifies data on the Web using **URIs** (Uniform Resource Identifiers) and assigns linking information to each URI.

**4 Rules of Linked Data:**

1.  **Use of URI:** Each individual object in a document gets its own URI, moving beyond a URL-centered system.
2.  **Use of HTTP URI:** Proposes URIs accessible via HTTP protocol to enhance data access.
3.  **Use of RDF:** Uses data structured in a **triple model** (like RDF) for formalized representation and linking.
4.  **Assignment of Linked Information:** Makes linking existing Web data easier by assigning specific link information.

**Usefulness of Linked Data:**

*   **Reusable Data:** Data can be used via URI even if it's not one's own.
*   **Reduced Data Redundancy:** Helps identify and eliminate duplicate data.
*   **Maximize Interoperability & Consolidate Data Value:** Acts as a semantic web standard, can be queried like a database, enables "mash-ups" using data.
*   **Network Effects:** Data expansion through linking leads to network effects and acceleration.

### III. Open Data

**Open data** is data that anyone can freely use, reuse, and redistribute, provided it meets specific conditions.

**Conditions for Open Data:**

1.  **Availability and Access:**
    *   Must be downloadable over the Internet.
    *   Original data can be transformed, and new works produced, at reasonable cost.
    *   Provided in a convenient, modifiable format.
2.  **Reuse and Redistribution:**
    *   Data must be reusable and redistributable, including combinations with other datasets.
3.  **Universal Participation:**
    *   Everyone must be able to use, reuse, and redistribute the data.
    *   No restrictions on commercial/non-commercial use or specific purposes (e.g., education).

### IV. Latest H/W-Centered IT Business Services

#### A. 3D Printing

**3D Printing (Additive Manufacturing):** A method of creating 3-dimensional physical objects from 3D digital data by stacking layers of material (powder, liquid, solid).

**Why Manufacturers are Interested:**

*   **Customized Production:** Suitable for small batches of diverse, customized products.
*   **Consumer Needs:** Improves manufacturing to satisfy diverse consumer needs quickly and easily.
*   **One-Person Manufacturing:** Enables individuals to make their own products.
*   **Collapsing Boundaries:** Blurs the line between consumption and manufacturing.

**Comparison with Traditional Manufacturing:**

*   **Traditional:** Advantageous for mass production of simple-shaped products (economies of scale, low labor costs).
*   **3D Printing:** Advantageous for **small-volume, large-variety production**. One equipment can produce many product types.

**3D Printing Process Steps:**

1.  **Modeling:** Creating the product design digitally.
    *   Data can be from a 3D scanner or a 3D modeling program.
    *   **Slicer Program:** Converts 3D model data into thin layers.
2.  **Printing:** Stacking or hardening thin layers of material based on the digitized model.
3.  **Post-processing:** Polishing, dyeing, removing supports, solidifying the object.

**Core Component Technologies:**

*   **Modeling Process:** Object scanning/designing, design-to-data conversion.
*   **Printing Process:** Precise raw material spraying, energy source control for hardening.
*   **Materials:** Development of materials compatible with printing technology and product requirements (e.g., alloys, bio-materials for high value).

**Future Outlook:**
Current performance is limited, but rapid development is expected due to new technologies, material advancements, and expiring critical patents.

#### B. Wearable Devices

**Wearable Devices:** Electronic devices designed to be attached to the human body to improve convenience. They communicate with users from close proximity, offering differentiated functions in portability, ease of use, and adaptability.

**Context:** Considered the next-generation mobile technology to replace maturing smartphones.

**Applications:** Fitness, well-being, healthcare, medical care, manufacturing, military, infotainment.

**Evolution of Forms:**

*   **Accessory Type:** (e.g., smartwatches)
*   **Body Attachment Type:** (e.g., skin patches)
*   **Apparel-Integrated Type:** (e.g., smart clothing)
*   **Body Transplants:** (e.g., implanted devices)

**Types of Wearable Devices & Core Technology:**

1.  **Accessory (e.g., watches):**
    *   **Characteristics:** Ultra-small/low power systems, ergonomic design.
    *   **Core Tech:** Ultra-small sensors, high-capacity battery, low power/high-performance SoC, flexible/thin/transparent display, interaction technology.
2.  **Apparel (e.g., smart clothing):**
    *   **Characteristics:** Integrated with fabric, circuits printed on flexible fabric.
    *   **Core Tech:** Conductive thread/textile/fabric technology, fabric circuit boards, packaging, adhesive battery components.
3.  **Body Attachment (e.g., skin patches):**
    *   **Characteristics:** Systems attached to skin, using biocompatible polymers.
    *   **Core Tech:** Polymer circuit boards, electronic component packaging, antenna/communication technology, material attach/detach technology.
4.  **Body Transplant (e.g., implants):**
    *   **Characteristics:** Electronic devices inserted into the human body, biocompatible circuit boards.
    *   **Core Tech:** Biometric sensor technology, electronic tattoo/capsule development, integration with human body, low power/miniaturization technology.

**Growing Importance (due to IoT):**

*   Always connected to user's network.
*   Frees up users' hands.
*   Always close to user's view and position.
*   Enables collection of previously difficult-to-gather data.
*   Leads to customized personal content and new services.

**Challenges:**

*   Short battery life.
*   Limited content for small screens.
*   Lack of "killer content" or game-changing functions.

**Future Value & Convergence:**
Wearables will create core value by converging with IoT, cloud computing, Big Data, and mobile devices.

*   **Sensing:** Wearables gather Big Data.
*   **Cloud Analysis:** Big Data analyzed via cloud.
*   **Customized Services:** Analysis results used for personalized user services.
*   **New Business Models:** Smart home, O2O (Online to Offline) commerce, smart car services.

#### C. Self-Driving Cars

**Self-Driving Cars (Autonomous Vehicles):** Automobiles that can drive safely on their own, recognizing their environment and risks without driver intervention. They incorporate ICT (software, AI, communication, sensors) to minimize human control.

**Reasons for Emergence:**

*   **Collaboration:** IT companies and carmakers are partnering to integrate latest ICT into cars.
*   **Market Growth:** Rapid growth in electrical parts and telematics due to demand for safety and convenience.
*   **Tech Improvements:** Advanced network/internet technology allows cars to be viewed as new mobile spaces, offering new user experiences (UXs).

**Levels of Autonomous Driving:**

1.  **No Automation:**
    *   **Description:** Driver fully monitors and controls all safety-sensitive functions (brakes, speed, steering).
    *   **Sub-Functions:** Traditional car; driver must be fully aware, judge, and control driving.
2.  **Function-Specific Automation:**
    *   **Description:** Driver controls vehicle except for some functions during normal driving or imminent collision.
    *   **Sub-Functions:** Driving assistant systems that provide info, warn, and support safe driving/parking.
3.  **Combined-Specific Automation:**
    *   **Description:** Two or more controls operate harmoniously in specific driving environments. Driver retains control rights and responsibility for monitoring/safety.
    *   **Sub-Functions:** Similar to Function-Specific but with more integrated control, still requiring driver oversight.
4.  **Limited Self-Driving Automation:**
    *   **Description:** Vehicle controls all safety functions under specific traffic environments. Vehicle has monitoring authority. Driver takes over intermittently when an alarm sounds (requiring driver control).
    *   **Sub-Functions:** Infrastructure-linked autonomous driving where cars operate on roads equipped for automatic driving.

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Key Concepts

This guide covers modern IT technologies and the increasing importance of ethical responsibility in their development and use.

### 1. 3D Printing Technology

*   **Current Status:** Limited performance in some areas.
*   **Future Outlook:** Rapid development expected due to:
    *   New technology efforts.
    *   Advancements in materials.
    *   Expiration of critical patents.

### 2. Wearable Devices

**Definition:**
*   Next-generation mobile technology, replacing smartphones.
*   Electronic devices attached to the human body for convenience.
*   Communicate with users from a close proximity.
*   Offer superior portability, ease of use, and environmental adaptability compared to existing devices.
*   Applications span fitness, healthcare, manufacturing, military, and infotainment.

**Evolution & Types:**

| Category          | Definition & Characteristics                                 | Core Technologies                                            |
| :---------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Accessory**     | Like watches; utilize ultra-small/low-power systems. Ergonomic design to overcome discomfort. | Ultra-small sensors, high-capacity batteries, low power/high-performance SoC (System-on-Chip), flexible/transparent displays. |
| **Apparel**       | Integrated into textiles; systems merged with fabric, circuits printed on flexible fabric. | Conductive thread, textile/fabric technology, fabric circuit boards, adhesive battery components. |
| **Body Attachment** | Systems that attach to the skin; use flexible polymers.      | Polymer circuit boards, electronic component packaging, antenna and communication technology, attach/detach technology. |
| **Body Transplant** | Electronic devices inserted into the human body; use biocompatible circuit boards. | Biometric sensor technology, electronic tattoo/capsule development, low power/miniaturization technology, human body integration. |

**Importance & Drivers:**
*   **IoT Growth:** Expanded interconnectedness of people, objects, and devices.
*   **User Proximity:** Always connected to the user, hands-free operation, close to user's view/position.
*   **Data Collection:** Enables collection of previously difficult data.
*   **Customization:** Supports customized personal content and new services.

**Challenges:**
*   **Battery Life:** Short battery life restricts always-on use.
*   **Content Limitations:** Limited content for small screens.
*   **Lack of "Killer" Functions:** Absence of game-changing features or services.

**Future Value & Convergence:**
*   Convergence with IoT, Cloud Computing, Big Data, and Mobile Devices.
*   **Sensing:** Wearable sensors gather Big Data.
*   **Analysis:** Cloud analyzes gathered Big Data.
*   **Services:** Analysis results inform customized user services.
*   **New Markets:** Drives new business models (e.g., smart home, O2O commerce, smart car services).

### 3. Self-Driving Cars

**Definition:**
*   Automobiles that drive safely autonomously, recognizing their environment and risks without driver intervention.
*   Integrate **ICT** (Information and Communication Technology) like software, AI, communication, and sensor technologies to minimize human control.

**Emergence Factors:**
*   **Industry Collaboration:** IT companies and car manufacturers accelerate cooperation to integrate ICT.
*   **Market Growth:** Rapid growth in electrical parts and telematics markets driven by demand for safety and convenience.
*   **Network Improvements:** Advanced network and Internet tech allow cars to be recognized as new mobile spaces, offering new UX (User Experiences).

**Levels of Autonomous Driving (SAE Standard):**

| Level                        | Description                                                  | Sub Functions / Characteristics                                |
| :--------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **No Automation**            | Driver always monitors and controls all safety-sensitive functions (brakes, speed, steering). | Traditional car; driver fully aware, judges, and controls.     |
| **Function-Specific Automation** | Driver controls most of the vehicle, but some functions are automated during normal driving or collision threats. | Driving assistant system providing info, warnings, and control support for safe driving/parking. |
| **Combined-Specific Automation** | Two or more controls operate harmoniously. Driver still monitors, can override, and is responsible for safety. | Driver assist systems that combine multiple functions (e.g., adaptive cruise control with lane keeping). |
| **Limited Self-Driving Automation** | Vehicle controls all safety functions under specific traffic environments. Vehicle has monitoring authority; driver takes over intermittently when an alarm sounds. | Infrastructure-linked autonomous driving, enabling autonomous operation on roads equipped with specific infrastructure. |
| **Full Self-Driving Automation** | Vehicle controls all safety functions and monitors its own condition. Driver enters destination and driving settings. System is fully responsible for safe driving. | Smart car functioning like a robot, driving autonomously to a specific destination via a specific course. |

**Key Technologies:**
*   **Core Functions:** Recognition (of surroundings), Judgment (on driving decisions), Manipulation (of vehicle controls).
*   **Integration:** These core functions integrate with:
    *   **AUTOSAR (Automotive Open System Architecture):** A global standard for automotive software architecture.
    *   **RTOS (Real-Time Operating System):** Operating systems for real-time computing tasks crucial for vehicle control.
    *   **Functional Safety Technologies:** Systems designed to prevent and mitigate risks from system failures.

### 4. Smart Machines

**Definition:**
*   Machines that act autonomously, possess intelligence and self-learning abilities.
*   Can judge and adapt to different situations.
*   Perform tasks previously thought impossible for non-humans.

**Examples:**
*   Digital voice assistants (Apple Siri, Google Home).
*   Medical advisors for diagnosis or drug use.
*   Robots performing assembly in factories.
*   Self-driving cars.
*   Expert advisors.

**Key Concepts:**
*   **Autonomous:** Learns by itself, generates rules, determines situations, makes optimal choices/judgments.
*   **Automation:** Executes pre-determined procedures based on instructions.
*   **Convergence:** Increasingly integrates with Big Data, AI, and Cloud Computing.

**Direction of Development:**
*   Evolving towards self-learning, rule creation, hypothesis validation, situational awareness, and discovering optimal solutions.
*   Approaching the true concept of a "smart machine" capable of tasks beyond human ability (e.g., analyzing vast medical/judicial records, recommending decisions, supplementing human physical or cognitive abilities).

### 5. Drones

**Definition:**
*   An unmanned aerial vehicle (UAV), aircraft or helicopter-shaped, flown by radio signals.

**Origin & Evolution:**
*   First developed for **military purposes** (e.g., target aircraft after WWII).
*   Increasingly used in the **private sector**, especially when equipped with GPS or video devices.

**Advantages:**
*   **Accessibility:** Can reach places impossible or too hazardous for humans (e.g., underwater, deep oceans, areas with dangerous gases or radioactivity).
*   **Autonomy:** Can operate in autonomous mode, recognizing surroundings and flying independently.
*   **Versatility:** No restrictions on where they can go, enabling diverse applications.

**Applications:**

| Sector             | Description & Examples                                       |
| :----------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Distribution**   | Delivery services (Amazon Prime Air for 16km within 30 min, Domino's Pizza delivery). |
| **ICT**            | Delivering Internet access in remote places (Facebook's drone concept for Wi-Fi). |
| **Disaster Relief** | Gathering data from hazardous zones (Global Hawk in Fukushima nuclear reactor) and aiding recovery efforts (Haiti earthquake, Philippines typhoon). |
| **Crime**          | Tracking stolen vehicles, investigating drug-related crimes (Seattle police). |
| **Traffic Information** | Gathering traffic congestion and road obstacle information (Renault car with integrated drone). |
| **Movies & Broadcasting** | Used for movie production and sports broadcasts (multicopters). |

### 6. Recent Trends & Major Issues: Professional Ethics

**Impact of IT Technology:**
*   Causes rapid fluctuations across all industries.
*   Maximizes convenience and efficiency in modern life.
*   Services prioritize user convenience and interests.

**Growing Concern:**
*   Enhanced software intelligence leads to increased risks of misuse, abuse, and malicious use.

**Importance of Ethics:**
*   The ethical responsibility of IT business-related developers is critically increasing.
*   It is essential to understand professional ethics in the IT business context.

**Learning Objectives (for professional ethics):**
1.  Describe the professional ethics expected of IT business workers.
2.  Explain the principles and codes of professional ethics related to IT business.

**Keywords:** Professional Ethics, Ethics, Work Ethics, Community Ethics, Ethics and Law.

---

# Learning Guide: Modern Tech & Professional Ethics

## Section 1: The Rise of Advanced Technology – Drones

Machines are advancing rapidly, capable of tasks beyond human limitations, such as analyzing vast data (medical, judicial) or supplementing human abilities (e.g., for the elderly).

### What is a Drone?
*   **Definition:** An Unmanned Aerial Vehicle (UAV) that is aircraft or helicopter-shaped, controlled by radio signals.
*   **Origin:** First developed for military purposes, later reused as target aircraft in exercises.
*   **Modern Use:** Increasingly adopted in the private sector, especially when equipped with GPS or video devices.

### Advantages of Drones
*   **Access:** Can reach places impossible or hazardous for humans (e.g., deep oceans, areas with toxic gases or radioactivity).
*   **Autonomy:** Can operate independently, recognizing surroundings and flying without human input.
*   **Versatility:** Due to their unrestricted access, drones have diverse applications.

### Key Applications of Drones
*   **Distribution:**
    *   Amazon: Plans 30-minute deliveries within a 16km radius.
    *   Domino's Pizza: Successfully delivered two large pizzas.
*   **ICT (Information and Communication Technology):**
    *   Facebook: Developing drones that hover like Wi-Fi routers to provide internet access in remote areas.
*   **Disaster Relief:**
    *   'Global Hawk' drone: Used to gather data from inside the Fukushima nuclear reactor.
    *   'Global Hawk' drone: Aided recovery efforts after the Haiti earthquake and typhoon disasters in the Philippines.
*   **Crime Prevention:**
    *   Seattle Police: Use drones for tracking stolen vehicles and investigating drug-related crimes.
*   **Traffic Information:**
    *   Renault: Introduced a car with an integrated drone to gather traffic congestion and road obstacle information.
*   **Movies & Broadcasting:**
    *   Multicopters (a type of drone): Used in movie production and sports broadcasts.

---

## Section 2: Understanding IT Business and Ethics

The rapid development of IT technology brings immense convenience and efficiency, creating user-centric services. However, this also increases the risks of misuse, abuse, and malicious use of advanced software. This highlights the growing importance of ethical responsibility in the IT sector.

### Why IT Ethics is Important
*   IT advancements create powerful tools, but also potential for harm.
*   Ensuring responsible use and development of IT is critical.

### Key Terms
*   **Professional Ethics:** A code of conduct for those in a specific job.
*   **Ethics:** Moral principles that govern a person's behavior or the conducting of an activity.
*   **Work Ethics:** Ethical principles related to one's job performance and duties.
*   **Community Ethics:** Ethical principles governing interactions and responsibilities within a professional community or workplace.
*   **Ethics and Law:** The interplay between moral standards and legal regulations.

### Case Study Example: The Cost of Lacking Ethics
*   **Incident:** In 2018, individuals leaked design drawings and key technical data for a domestic company's high-efficiency washing machine motor to a Chinese company.
*   **Motive:** Financial gain (cash, housing, vehicles).
*   **Consequence:** Theft of intellectual property, undermining years of investment and innovation.
*   **Lesson:** This case exemplifies how a lack of professional ethics, even in advanced technological fields, can lead to severe consequences, despite sophisticated technology and systems. Professional ethics remains a fundamental, timeless requirement.

---

## Section 3: Professional Ethics Explained

### What is Professional Ethics?
*   **Definition:** A set of conduct rules that individuals in a specific job must follow during their work.
*   **Scope:** It defines appropriate mindsets, attitudes, behaviors towards one's job, and how professionals interact with others in their work environment.
*   **Normative Aspect:** Includes ethical norms to be observed, rules for common behavior, and boundaries to prevent unethical actions.

### Components of Professional Ethics

Professional ethics is typically divided into two main categories:

1.  **Work Ethics:** Focuses on an individual's attitude and behavior towards their tasks.
    *   **Diligence:** Maintaining a steady and hardworking attitude in your job.
    *   **Honesty:** Acting truthfully and openly, without deceiving or hiding information.
    *   **Sincerity:** Handling tasks with dedication and wholehearted effort.
    *   **Spirit of Service:** Working hard for the benefit of the country, company, or others, rather than just personal gain.

2.  **Community Ethics:** Focuses on an individual's responsibilities and interactions within their professional community and society.
    *   **Responsibility:** Having the attitude to complete assigned tasks or commitments.
    *   **Compliance:** Obeying and following established workplace rules, policies, and norms.
    *   **Workplace Etiquette:** Displaying appropriate and polite language and behavior suitable for professional work and relationships.

### Importance of Professional Ethics
Professional ethics is crucial for individuals, companies, and society as a whole:

*   **For Individuals:**
    *   Helps fulfill responsibilities and duties as a professional.
    *   Supports self-realization based on moral values.
*   **For Organizations & Society:**
    *   **Cooperation:** Essential for community life, fostering cooperation towards common interests.
    *   **Influence:** Vocational activities significantly impact company order and societal development.
    *   **Reliability & Competitiveness:** Ethics build trust, which is a vital factor for economic competitiveness (e.g., "Ethics rather than profit makes a company of 200 years").
    *   **Prevents Self-Interest:** Prevents individuals from solely prioritizing their own interests over others.
    *   **Order & Credibility:** Ensures necessary cooperation, maintains organizational credibility, and prevents societal disorder.
    *   **National Impact:** Directly linked to national competitiveness and economic development.

### Self-Assessment
*   Various checklists exist (like Table 96 in the original text) to help professionals assess their own level of professional ethics. These tools encourage reflection on behaviors related to virtue, ethical codes, diligence, honesty, responsibility, and commitment to collective interests.

---

# IT Business and Ethics: A Learning Guide

This guide covers professional ethics, its importance, specifically within the IT business, and key ethical principles from recognized codes.

---

## 1. Understanding Professional Ethics

### 1.1 Definition & Scope

*   **Professional Ethics:** A code of conduct individuals should follow in their job.
*   It encompasses:
    *   **Mindset & Attitudes:** How professionals approach their work.
    *   **Behaviors:** Actions taken in a professional context.
    *   **Relationships:** Interactions with colleagues, clients, and the public.
*   **Normative Aspect:** It includes ethical norms to observe, common behavior rules, and limits on unethical actions.

### 1.2 Sub-Elements of Professional Ethics

Professional ethics is broadly divided into two areas:

*   **Work Ethics:** Focuses on individual work qualities.
    *   **Diligence:** Maintaining a steady, hardworking attitude.
    *   **Honesty:** Acting truthfully and without deceit.
    *   **Sincerity:** Handling tasks with dedication.
    *   **Spirit of Service:** Working for the greater good (country, company, others) beyond personal interest.
*   **Community Ethics:** Focuses on interactions and responsibilities within a professional community.
    *   **Responsibility:** Owning and completing assigned or chosen tasks.
    *   **Compliance:** Obeying workplace rules and norms.
    *   **Workplace Etiquette:** Showing appropriate and polite language and behavior in professional relationships.

### 1.3 Importance of Professional Ethics

Professional ethics is vital for:

*   **Individual Professionals:** Fulfilling duties, realizing self-worth, and upholding moral values.
*   **Organizational Reliability:** Building trust and competitiveness. "Ethics rather than profit makes a company of 200 years."
*   **Societal Order & Development:** Vocational activities significantly influence society.
*   **Consequences of Low Ethics:**
    *   Individuals prioritize self-interest.
    *   Lack of cooperation and interaction.
    *   Loss of organizational credibility.
    *   Disruption of societal order.
    *   Negative impact on national competitiveness and economic development.

---

## 2. Professional Ethics in the IT Business

### 2.1 Why IT Ethics Are Critical

*   **Rapid Development & Impact:** IT business evolves quickly, profoundly affecting global quality of life.
*   **High Risks:** Lack of professional ethics in IT workers (e.g., software developers) leads to:
    *   Safety accidents.
    *   Information security breaches.
    *   Cyber-crimes.
*   **Expanding Negative Impact:** These accidents cause significant social and economic losses, highlighting the crucial need for IT professional ethics.

### 2.2 Key Ethical Focus Areas in IT

While there's no single global standard, common themes in IT professional codes include:

*   **Moral Responsibility for Public Safety:** Ensuring technology implementation doesn't harm society.
*   **Privacy Protection:** Safeguarding personal information.
*   **Information Protection:** Securing data and systems.

### 2.3 Examples of IT Professional Codes

*   **ACM (Association for Computing Machinery) Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct**
*   **IEEE-CS (Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers - Computer Science) Software Engineering Code**
*   **NSPE (National Society of Professional Engineers) Code of Ethics for Engineers**

### 2.4 Ethics for Software Developers (Pete Goodliffe's Perspective)

Pete Goodliffe, a programmer and columnist, emphasizes ethical consciousness for developers:

*   **Pledge to Do No Harm:**
    *   Do not misuse code, ethics, or business for personal gain.
    *   Faithfully perform tasks and build team harmony.
    *   Be honest, aiming for efficient and valuable projects/teams.
*   **Ethical Dilemmas:** Developers must grapple with questions like:
    *   The ethics of creating wealth-generating software at others' expense.
    *   Compliance with open-source licenses (e.g., GPL) vs. company code.
    *   Reporting unethical behavior of colleagues.
    *   The role of software patents.
    *   How passion for development affects ethical behavior.
*   **Guidance in Complexity:** Professional ethics provides a sense of duty and responsibility, guiding judgments in moral dilemmas within a fast-paced environment where understanding all code uses and risks is challenging.

---

## 3. Ethical Principles: The ACM Code of Ethics

The ACM Code is a widely recognized framework, structured into General Principles, Professional Responsibilities, and Professional Leadership Principles.

### 3.1 Article 1: General Ethical Principles

These are foundational principles for computing professionals:

1.  **Contribute to Society and Human Well-being:** Acknowledge all people as stakeholders in computing.
2.  **Avoid Harm:** Prevent harm, and if accidental, try to reverse or recover. Report systemic risks immediately.
3.  **Be Honest and Trustworthy.**
4.  **Be Fair and Nondiscriminatory.**
5.  **Respect Work on New Ideas, Inventions, and Creative Works:** This includes respecting copyrights, trade secrets, patents, licenses, and open-source terms.
6.  **Respect Privacy.**
7.  **Honor Confidentiality.**

### 3.2 Article 2: Professional Responsibilities

These outline the duties of computing professionals in their work:

1.  **Strive for High Quality:** In both processes and products.
2.  **Maintain High Standards:** Of professional competence, conduct, and ethical practice.
3.  **Know and Respect Rules:** Pertaining to professional work.
4.  **Accept and Provide Appropriate Professional Review.**
5.  **Give Comprehensive Evaluations:** Of computer systems and their impacts, including risk analysis.
6.  **Perform Work Only in Areas of Competence.**
7.  **Foster Public Awareness and Understanding:** Of computing technologies and their consequences.
8.  **Access Resources Only When Authorized:** Or when compelled by public good.
9.  **Design and Implement Robustly and Usably Secure Systems:** Prepare for accidents, abuse, manipulation, and paralysis from malicious intent.

### 3.3 Article 3: Principles of Professional Leadership

These guide those in leadership roles in computing:

1.  **Ensure Public Good is the Central Concern:** In all professional computing work.
2.  **Articulate, Encourage, and Evaluate Social Responsibilities:** By members of the organization or group.
3.  **Manage Personnel and Resources:** To enhance the quality of working life.
4.  **Articulate, Apply, and Support Policies:** That reflect the Code's principles.
5.  **Create Opportunities for Professional Growth:** For team members.
6.  **Use Care When Modifying or Retiring Systems.**
7.  **Recognize and Take Special Care of Systems Integrated into Society's Infrastructure:** (e.g., Social Media, Cloud).

---

## Pages 181-185


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# Professional Ethics in Computing and Engineering

This guide covers essential ethical principles and codes for professionals in software development, IT, and engineering.

## 1. Professional Ethics for Software Developers

**Core Idea:** Software developers need a strong ethical consciousness. It's often hard to predict how code will be used or its risks, and fast-paced environments make ethical judgments difficult. Professional ethics provide guidance and a sense of duty.

### Pete Goodliffe's "Ethical Programmer Pledge"

*   **Do No Harm:** Avoid harming code, ethics, or business for personal/professional gain.
*   **Be Faithful:** Perform tasks diligently and foster team harmony.
*   **Be Honest:** Work towards efficient and valuable projects/teams.

### Why Ethical Reflection Matters

Developers face dilemmas. For example:
*   Creating software that benefits a few at others' expense.
*   Violating open-source license terms (e.g., GPL) by not disclosing required code.
*   Reporting unethical behavior of colleagues, especially if it impacts employment.
*   Navigating software patents.
*   Balancing passion with ethical considerations.

## 2. Key Ethical Principles and Industry Codes

### A) ACM (Association for Computing Machinery) Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct

*   **Focus:** Social responsibility and professional leadership in computing.
*   **Structure:** General Principles, Professional Responsibilities, Professional Leadership Principles, and Compliance.

#### Article 1: General Ethical Principles

1.  **Contribute to Society:** Benefit human well-being, recognizing all people are stakeholders.
2.  **Avoid Harm:** Prevent harm and, if accidental, reverse/recover it. Report systemic risks immediately.
3.  **Be Honest & Trustworthy.**
4.  **Be Fair:** Avoid discrimination.
5.  **Respect Intellectual Property:** Honor copyrights, trade secrets, patents, licenses, and open-source terms.
6.  **Respect Privacy.**
7.  **Honor Confidentiality.**

#### Article 2: Professional Responsibilities

1.  **High Quality Work:** Strive for excellence in processes and products.
2.  **Maintain High Standards:** Uphold professional competence, conduct, and ethics.
3.  **Respect Rules:** Know and adhere to relevant professional regulations.
4.  **Professional Review:** Accept and provide constructive feedback.
5.  **Thorough Evaluations:** Assess computer systems and their impacts, including risks.
6.  **Competence:** Work only within your areas of expertise.
7.  **Public Awareness:** Educate the public about computing and its consequences.
8.  **Authorized Access:** Use computing resources only when authorized or for the public good.
9.  **Secure Systems:** Design and implement robust and usable security (prepare for abuse/accidents).

#### Article 3: Principles of Professional Leadership

1.  **Public Good:** Prioritize the public good in all computing work.
2.  **Social Responsibility:** Encourage and evaluate social responsibilities within organizations.
3.  **Quality of Working Life:** Manage resources to improve work-life quality.
4.  **Ethical Policies:** Support and apply policies reflecting the Code's principles.
5.  **Professional Growth:** Create opportunities for professional development.
6.  **System Care:** Exercise caution when modifying or retiring systems.
7.  **Societal Infrastructure:** Recognize and care for systems integrated into society's infrastructure (e.g., social media, cloud).

#### Article 4: Compliance with the Code

1.  **Uphold & Promote:** Support and respect the Code's principles.
2.  **Address Violations:** Treat Code violations as inconsistent with ACM membership.

### B) NSPE (National Society of Professional Engineers) Code of Ethics for Engineers

*   **Focus:** Ethical standards for engineers regarding the public, customers, and employers. Emphasizes honesty, impartiality, fairness, equity, and public health/safety/welfare.

#### Fundamental Canons (Key Duties)

1.  **Public Welfare First:** Hold paramount the safety, health, and welfare of the public.
2.  **Competence:** Perform services only within your area of expertise.
3.  **Truthful Statements:** Issue public statements objectively and truthfully.
4.  **Loyalty to Employer/Client:** Act as faithful agents or trustees.
5.  **Avoid Deception:** Do not engage in deceptive acts.

### C) ACM/IEEE-CS Code of Ethics for Software Engineers

*   **Focus:** A standard for software education and practice, promoting software engineering as a beneficial and respected profession, prioritizing public health, safety, and well-being.

#### Eight Ethical Principles (Summary)

1.  **Public:** Act consistently with the public interest.
2.  **Client & Employer:** Act in their best interest, *consistent with the public interest*.
3.  **Product:** Ensure products meet the highest professional standards.
4.  **Judgment:** Maintain integrity and independence in professional judgment.
5.  **Management:** Promote ethical approaches to software development management.
6.  **Profession:** Advance the integrity and reputation of the profession.
7.  **Colleagues:** Be fair to and supportive of colleagues.
8.  **Self:** Engage in lifelong learning and promote ethical practice within the profession.

### D) ISACA (Information Systems Audit and Control Association) Code of Professional Ethics

*   **Focus:** Guidance for professional and personal conduct in information systems audit and related roles.

#### Key Principles

1.  **Support IT Governance:** Encourage compliance with standards for IT governance and management (audit, control, security, risk management).
2.  **Objectivity & Care:** Perform duties with objectivity, due diligence, and professional care.
3.  **Stakeholder Interest:** Serve stakeholders lawfully, maintain high conduct, and uphold the profession's reputation.
4.  **Privacy & Confidentiality:** Maintain confidentiality of information unless legally required; do not use for personal gain or release to inappropriate parties.
5.  **Competency:** Maintain expertise and only undertake tasks you can complete competently.
6.  **Transparent Reporting:** Inform relevant parties of work results, disclosing all significant facts that could distort findings.
7.  **Educate Stakeholders:** Support education to enhance understanding of IT governance and management.

### E) The Korean Institute of Electrical Engineers (KIEE) Code of Professional Ethics

*   **Focus:** For electrical engineering professionals, emphasizing technology's impact on life, cultural traditions, honesty, fairness, and upholding dignity.

#### Key Pledges/Principles

1.  **Social Responsibility:** Contribute to society and peace, make decisions for public safety/well-being, and take responsibility.
2.  **Principles of Faith:** Keep business information confidential and protect trust (unless public interest is harmed).
3.  **Conflicts of Interest:** Disclose and objectively deal with any conflicts that arise.
4.  **Material Honesty:** Base conclusions on engineering data; do not use false data or plagiarize.
5.  **Compliance with Laws:** Strictly follow laws, regulations, and contracts; refuse bribery.
6.  **Respect for Intellectual Property:** Respect others' copyrights and patents, and fairly acknowledge their achievements.
7.  **Fair Assessment:** Accept fair technical assessments, correct errors promptly, and fairly evaluate others.
8.  **Non-Discrimination:** Reject prejudice and discrimination based on gender, race, age, background, or disability.
9.  **Professional Development:** Develop professional knowledge and skills to advance the field.
10. **Eco-friendly & Sustainable Technologies:** Recognize the need for and promote efforts toward sustainable and eco-friendly technologies.

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business & Ethics - Understanding Personal Information

This guide extracts essential information on professional ethics and the critical aspects of personal information in the IT business.

---

### Section 1: IT Professional Ethics Codes

Ethical codes guide professionals in the IT field to maintain integrity, responsibility, and public trust.

#### A. IEEE-CS/ACM Software Engineering Code of Ethics (Continued)

*   **Management:** Promote and practice ethical software development and maintenance.
*   **Profession:** Advance the integrity and reputation of the profession, aligning with public interest.
*   **Colleagues:** Be fair and supportive of fellow professionals.
*   **Self:** Commit to lifelong learning and ethical practice within the profession.

#### B. ISACA (Information Systems Audit and Control Association) Code of Professional Ethics

Professionals should:

1.  **Support Standards:** Encourage compliance with standards for IT governance (audit, control, security, risk management).
2.  **Professional Conduct:** Perform duties with objectivity, diligence, and professional care.
3.  **Stakeholder Interest:** Act lawfully in stakeholders' interest, upholding high standards of conduct.
4.  **Confidentiality:** Maintain privacy and confidentiality of information, unless legally required to disclose. Do not use for personal gain.
5.  **Competency:** Stay competent in their field; only undertake tasks they can complete with necessary skills.
6.  **Transparency:** Inform parties of work results, disclosing significant facts that could distort reporting if withheld.
7.  **Education:** Support education for stakeholders to enhance their understanding of IT governance and management.

#### C. The Korean Institute of Electrical Engineers (KIEE) Code of Professional Ethics

KIEE members value electrical engineering's impact on life, harmony, and act with a high sense of ethics. They pledge:

1.  **Social Responsibility:** Contribute to social development and make decisions prioritizing public safety and well-being.
2.  **Principles of Faith:** Keep business/occupational information confidential and protect organizational trust, provided public interest is not harmed.
3.  **Conflicts of Interest:** Disclose and objectively manage all interests that may affect judgment in business conflicts.
4.  **Material Honesty:** Base conclusions on engineering data honestly, avoiding false data or plagiarism.
5.  **Compliance:** Strictly follow laws, regulations, contracts, and standards; refuse all bribery.
6.  **Intellectual Property Rights:** Respect others' IP (copyrights, patents) and fairly disclose achievements.
7.  **Fairness (Self):** Accept fair technical assessments and correct errors promptly.
8.  **Fairness (Others):** Reject prejudice and discrimination based on gender, race, age, background, or disability.
9.  **Specialized Fields:** Develop professional knowledge to contribute to their specialty.
10. **Eco-friendly Technologies:** Recognize and promote eco-friendly, sustainable technologies to preserve Earth's capacity.

---

### Section 2: Personal Information: Key Concepts and Importance

**Recent Trends and Major Issues:**

*   **Proliferation:** Various personal data (network, biometric, location) is widespread across industries.
*   **Asset Shift:** Personal information is now a valuable asset for companies and countries.
*   **High Risk:** Leakage is common due to unauthorized use, careless management, internal breaches, and hacking.
*   **Severe Consequences:** Leaks damage corporate image, cause financial losses, and can even harm national branding.

**Learning Objectives:**

*   Understand the concept and types of personal information.
*   Understand policies related to personal information.

**Key Terms:**

*   **Personal Information:** Any data that identifies a living individual.
*   **De-identified Personal Information:** Data processed so that a specific individual cannot be identified without additional information.
*   **GDPR (General Data Protection Regulation):** A key data protection law (EU-centric, but with global impact).

---

### Section 3: Real-World Impact: Personal Information Leaks

**Case Study Example: Accommodation App Leak**

*   **Incident:** A hacker infiltrated an accommodation app, leaking personal information from 8 companies.
*   **Data Leaked:** Website IDs, names, dates of birth, emails, phone numbers, addresses, passport numbers, accommodation reservations.
*   **Regulatory Action:** The Korea Communications Commission imposed significant penalties (fines, correction orders, disciplinary actions) for "severe violations" of personal information protection measures (e.g., access control, encryption) under the "Network Act."
*   **Takeaway:** Data breaches are serious, frequent, and result in substantial penalties and reputational damage.

**Past Leak Examples (Key Themes):**

*   Numerous past incidents in domestic companies show recurring violations involving unauthorized access, hacking, and improper data provision to third parties.
*   These incidents consistently lead to large numbers of victims and severe administrative sanctions (large fines, corrective orders).

---

### Section 4: Understanding Personal Information in Detail

#### A. Concept of Personal Information

**Definition (from Personal Information Protection Act, Article 2):**

"Personal information" means any information relating to a **living individual** that:

*   **Directly identifies** them (e.g., full name, resident registration number, image).
*   **Can be easily combined with other information** to identify a particular individual, even if it doesn't identify them by itself.

#### B. Types of Personal Information (Examples)

<br>

| Type                | Examples of Personal Information                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| :------------------ | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Identification**  | Name, resident registration number, address, hometown, phone number, date/place of birth, email, family relations.                                                                                                            |
| **Physical**        | **Biometrics:** Face, fingerprint, iris, voice, genetic info, height, weight. <br> **Medical/Health:** Health status, medical records, physical disability, medical history.                                                       |
| **Mental**          | **Preferences:** Rental/purchase records, magazine subscriptions, website search history. <br> **Inner Secrets:** Thoughts, creeds, religion, values, political affiliations.                                                      |
| **Property**        | **Financial:** Income, credit card number, bank account number, movable/immovable property holdings, savings details. <br> **Credit:** Credit rating, loan/collateral records, credit card records.                               |
| **Social**          | **Educational:** Education, grades, attendance, certificates, reward/punishment records, school records. <br> **Legal:** Criminal records, trial records, penalty payment details. <br> **Labor:** Workplace, employer, work experience, job evaluation. <br> **Military:** Military service status, number, rank, unit. |

## Pages 187-191


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# Personal Information Protection: A Learning Guide

## 1. Introduction to Personal Information Security

### 1.1 Why Personal Information Protection Matters
Recent incidents highlight the critical need for personal information protection. Hackers have leaked millions of individuals' data, including:
*   Website IDs, names, dates of birth, emails, phone numbers, addresses, passport numbers.
*   Accommodation reservations and member information.

These breaches lead to severe penalties, such as large fines and corrective orders, for companies violating personal information protection laws like the **Act on Promotion of Information and Communication Network Utilization and Information Protection, Etc. (Network Act)**. Violations include failures in access control, record preservation, encryption, and data expiration.

## 2. Understanding Personal Information

### 2.1 Definition of Personal Information
**Personal Information** is any information relating to a **living individual** that identifies them (e.g., name, resident registration number, image). It also includes information that, even if not identifying by itself, can be **easily combined** with other data to identify an individual.

*   **"Easily combined with other information"** means there's a high and possible chance of obtaining and combining additional information to identify someone.

### 2.2 Types of Personal Information
Personal information encompasses various categories:

*   **Identification:** Name, ID numbers, address, phone, email, date/place of birth, family details.
*   **Physical:** Biometrics (face, fingerprint, iris, voice, genetic info), height, weight. Medical/Health status, records, disabilities.
*   **Mental:** Preferences (rental/purchase history, website searches), inner secrets (thoughts, beliefs, religion, values, political views).
*   **Property:** Real estate, savings, income, credit card numbers, bank accounts. Credit rating, loan/collateral details.
*   **Social:** Education (grades, attendance, certificates), legal (criminal record, trial record), labor (workplace, experience, job evaluations), military service.
*   **Others:** Phone call history, website access history, emails/messages, GPS location data.

### 2.3 What is NOT Considered Personal Information
*   Information on deceased persons, corporations, groups, or objects.
*   Group statistics (aggregated data).
*   Information where it's difficult to identify a specific individual.

## 3. Key Terms in Personal Information Processing

*   **Information Subject:** The individual who can be identified by the collected and processed information.
*   **Processing:** Any act involving personal information, including collection, creation, storage, use, provision, disclosure, destruction, etc.
*   **Personal Information File:** Systematically arranged personal information for easy searching.
*   **Personal Information Processor:** Public institutions, corporations, organizations, businesses, or individuals who process personal information (themselves or via others) for business purposes.
*   **Privacy Policy:** A document outlining how an entity processes and protects personal information. It must detail processing purpose, retention period, data items, third-party provision, security measures, and the Personal Information Protection Officer.
*   **Personal Information Leakage:** Occurs when:
    *   Documents, storage devices, or computers with personal information are lost or stolen.
    *   Unauthorized persons access a personal information processing system/database.
    *   Personal information is incorrectly transmitted to unauthorized persons (intentional or negligent).
    *   Personal information is transferred to unauthorized persons or access is permitted to the processing system.
*   **Personal Information Exposure:** When general internet users can obtain others' personal information during normal internet use, without special methods like hacking.
*   **Permission to Access Personal Information:** The right of the personal information controller to access, view, record, correct, and delete personal information within the processing system.

## 4. Basic Principles of Personal Information Protection Act

*   **Scope:** Applies to all personal information processors (public and private sector). Covers handwritten documents and computer-processed information.
*   **Processing Restrictions:**
    *   Generally **prohibited** (unless the information subject consents or legal basis exists).
    *   **Sensitive information** (e.g., ideology, beliefs, health, sex life, criminal history) and **unique identification information** (e.g., resident registration number) require specific safety measures like encryption due to higher risks.
*   **Leakage Notification:** Mandatory notification of personal information leakage.
*   **Dispute Resolution:** Provides for a group dispute mediation system and group lawsuits.
*   **Committee:** Presidential Personal Information Protection Committee.

## 5. Personal Information Processing Procedure & Guidelines

The Personal Information Protection Act outlines obligations at each stage:

### 5.1 Stages of Processing

1.  **Collection and Use:**
    *   **Restriction:** Only collect the minimum personal information required.
    *   **Management:** Strict restrictions on sensitive and unique identification information.
    *   **Website Membership:** Offer alternative sign-up without resident registration numbers.
    *   **Image Data:** Install/operate processing equipment, disclose management policies.
    *   **Management:** Designate Personal Information Protection Managers, implement safety measures.
2.  **Provision:**
    *   **Limitation:** Do not provide personal information to third parties or for unintended purposes without proper consent.
    *   **Outsourcing/Transfer:** Follow rules for outsourcing processing or transferring data during business changes.
3.  **Destruction:** Destroy personal information when no longer needed.
4.  **Reporting:** Report personal information leakage and damage.
5.  **Guarantee of Rights:**
    *   **Information Subjects' Rights:** Right to access, request correction, deletion, and destruction of personal information.
    *   **Dispute Resolution:** Utilize the Personal Information Dispute Mediation Committee.
    *   **Legal Action:** Class action lawsuits to suspend infringements.
6.  **Penalty and Transition Measures:** Penalties apply for violations.

### 5.2 Guidelines for Personal Information Agreement (Privacy Policy Development)

When collecting or providing customer personal information, companies and public institutions must follow government guidelines for obtaining consent. Information should be presented clearly for users to understand.

#### 5.2.1 Preparation Stage for Policy Development

1.  **Identify Required Personal Information:**
    *   Determine the **minimum personal information** needed for a task.
    *   Check for **unique identification information** (resident registration, driver's license, passport, alien registration numbers) or **sensitive information** (ideology, beliefs, health, sex life, criminal history), as these require separate processing and consent.
2.  **Identify Retention Period:**
    *   Confirm the retention period via privacy policy guidelines or relevant laws.
    *   Set the minimum necessary retention period if not specified.
3.  **Confirm Consent Requirement for Collection & Use:**
    *   **Generally, consent from the information subject is required** for collection and use.
    *   **Exceptions (consent NOT needed for collection/use):**
        *   Public institutions performing statutory duties.
        *   Legal obligations or specific statutory provisions.
        *   Inevitably necessary for executing a contract with the data subject.
        *   Manifestly necessary to protect life, body, or property from imminent danger (and consent can't be obtained).
        *   Necessary for the legitimate interests of the controller, clearly superior to data subject's rights.
        *   For information and communication services, if difficult to get consent normally due to economic/technical reasons, or for service charge payment.
    *   **Special Consent for Sensitive/Unique ID:** Requires **separate consent** (unless laws specifically require or permit processing without it). Processing resident registration numbers is highly restricted to specific legal requirements or imminent danger situations.
    *   **Children Under 14:** Consent of a legal representative is required.
4.  **Identify if Personal Information is Provided to a Third Party:**
    *   **Generally, separate consent is required** to provide personal information to a third party.
    *   **Checklist for Third-Party Provision (to be disclosed):**
        1.  Recipient of personal information.
        2.  Purpose of recipient's use.
        3.  Specific items of personal information provided.
        4.  Recipient's retention and use period.
        5.  The data subject's right to deny consent and any disadvantages.
    *   **Exception (consent NOT needed for third-party provision):** If provided within the scope of original collection purposes under certain legal conditions (similar to collection/use exceptions above).

## 6. Personal Information Protection Management Levels

Public institutions undergo a "Diagnosis of Personal Information Protection Management Levels" to continuously improve their protection standards.

## Pages 190-194


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business, Ethics & Personal Information Protection

This guide summarizes key aspects of personal information protection, focusing on Korean regulations and international guidelines.

### 1. The Personal Information Protection Act (PIPA) - Korea

The **Personal Information Protection Act (PIPA)** is the primary law governing personal information.

#### 1.1. Basic Principles

*   **Scope:** Applies to all personal information processors in public and private sectors.
*   **Information Covered:** Includes physical documents (handwritten) and electronically processed data.
*   **Processing Rule:** Generally prohibited without the data subject's consent or a legal basis.
*   **Unique Identification Information (e.g., resident registration number):** Requires specific safety measures like **encryption** to prevent loss, theft, or damage.
*   **Data Breach Notification:** Mandatory to notify individuals of personal information leakage.
*   **Dispute Resolution:** Includes a group dispute mediation system and group lawsuits.
*   **Oversight:** Presidential Personal Information Protection Committee.

#### 1.2. Personal Information Processing Procedure & Obligations

Companies and public institutions must follow specific rules at each stage of processing personal information:

1.  **Collection & Use:**
    *   Collect only the **minimum necessary** personal information.
    *   Strict restrictions on collecting **sensitive information** and **unique identification information**.
    *   Provide alternative sign-up methods (e.g., without using a resident registration number).
    *   Install and operate **image data processing equipment** (e.g., CCTV) with disclosed management policies.
    *   Designate **Personal Information Protection Managers**.
    *   Implement **safety measures** for personal information.

2.  **Provision to Third Parties / Outsourcing:**
    *   Limit provision for purposes other than the original intended one.
    *   Specific rules apply when outsourcing personal information processing or transferring data due to business transfer.

3.  **Destruction:**
    *   Personal information must be destroyed when no longer needed.

4.  **Data Breach:**
    *   Mandatory notification and reporting of personal information leakage or damage.

5.  **Guarantee of Rights:**
    *   Individuals have the right to access their personal information.
    *   Right to request correction, deletion, or destruction of their personal information.
    *   Supported by the Personal Information Dispute Mediation Committee and class-action lawsuits.

6.  **Penalty & Transition Measures:**
    *   Legal penalties for non-compliance.

### 2. Privacy Policy Guidelines: Key Steps & Consent

Organizations must develop privacy policies that are clear and transparent to users.

#### 2.1. Preparation Stage for Policy Development

1.  **Identify Required Information:**
    *   Determine the **minimum personal information** needed for a task (e.g., name, phone number).
    *   Check for **unique identification information** (e.g., resident registration number, driver's license) or **sensitive information** (e.g., ideology, health, criminal history) as these require separate, stricter processing.
2.  **Identify Retention Period:**
    *   Confirm the legal or policy-defined retention period.
    *   Set the **minimum necessary retention period** if not specified by law.
3.  **Confirm Consent Requirements:**

    *   **Consent is generally required** to collect and use personal information.
    *   **Exceptions (when consent is NOT required):**
        *   Public institution's statutory duties.
        *   Existing special legal provisions or unavoidable legal obligations.
        *   Necessary to execute/perform a contract with the data subject.
        *   Urgent necessity to protect life, body, or property from imminent danger (and consent cannot be obtained).
        *   When justifiable interests of the controller outweigh data subject's rights.

    *   **Special Consent Rules:**
        *   **Sensitive Information or Unique Identification Information:** Requires **separate consent** from the data subject, unless statutes specifically require or permit processing.
        *   **Resident Registration Number:** Generally prohibited, except when specific laws require or permit it, or for urgent protection of life/property.
        *   **Children Under 14:** Requires consent from their **legal representative**.

4.  **Identify Third-Party Provision:**
    *   If personal information will be provided to a third party, **separate consent is required**.
    *   **Third-party provision checklist (must be provided to data subject):**
        1.  Recipient of personal information.
        2.  Purpose of use by the recipient.
        3.  Specific data to be provided.
        4.  Retention period by the recipient.
        5.  Right to deny consent and any resulting disadvantages.

### 3. Managing Personal Information Protection in Public Institutions

Public institutions undergo a national-level **Diagnosis of Personal Information Protection Management Levels**. This evaluates their management systems and infringement prevention activities, influencing institutional evaluations to encourage improvement.

#### 3.1. Key Diagnostic Areas & Indicators (Summary)

1.  **Laying the Foundation:**
    *   Dedicated organization and manpower for personal information protection.
    *   Budget allocation for protection activities.
2.  **Protection in Consignment Processing:**
    *   Understanding legal obligations for outsourced processing.
    *   Education and supervision for entrusted parties.
3.  **Establishment & Operation of Protection System:**
    *   Annual training plans and implementation for all staff (officers, handlers, general staff).
    *   Role of the Personal Information Protection Officer (management, supervision, improvement).
4.  **Establishment & Implementation of Protection Measures:**
    *   Collecting minimum necessary information and proper consent procedures.
    *   Procedures for using/providing information for non-intended purposes.
    *   Conducting **Personal Information Impact Assessments (PIA)** for new or modified systems that might infringe on privacy.
    *   Operating **Image Information Processing Devices** (e.g., CCTV) with disclosed policies and management registers.
    *   Measures to prevent leakage/exposure on webpages, systems, business computers, and mobile devices.
5.  **Establishment & Implementation of Infringement Countermeasures:**
    *   Procedures for responding to infringement incidents and emergencies.
    *   Policies for managing access rights to personal information processing systems and auditing access records.
    *   Understanding and encrypting unique identification information.

### 4. Key Definitions

*   **Sensitive Information:** A broad category of personal information requiring strict protection, including ideas, beliefs, trade union/political party membership, political opinions, health, sex life, genetic information, criminal history data.
*   **Unique Identification Information:** Information that uniquely identifies an individual, such as resident registration number, passport number, driver's license number, alien registration number.
*   **Personal Information Impact Assessment (PIA):** An evaluation system to analyze risk factors and derive improvements when new or modified personal information files might lead to infringement.
*   **Image Information Processing Device:** Devices (e.g., CCTV) installed in a space to record images of people or objects and transmit them. Operators must have and disclose a management policy.
    *   **Required items for Image Information Management Register:** Classification of use, provision, reading, destruction; date/time; file name/type; person in charge; purpose/reason; third party for data use/provision/reading; grounds for use/provision; type of use/provision; period.

### 5. Domestic Legal Landscape Comparison (Korea)

| Classification | Information & Communications Network Act (ICNA) | Personal Information Protection Act (PIPA) |
| :------------- | :---------------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------------- |
| **Governing Law** | Act on Promotion of Information and Communication Network Utilization and Information Protection, Etc. | Personal Information Protection Act |
| **Scope**        | When information communications service providers collect user personal information. | When any personal information controller collects personal information of a data subject. |
| **Subject**      | Information & communication service providers, broadcasting service providers, trustees. | Offline business owners, workers, non-profit organizations, **all personal information controllers**. |
| **Collection**   | Notification of purpose and prior consent required. Restrictions on collecting resident registration numbers. | Notification of purpose and prior consent required. |
| **Use/Provision** | Prohibition of use for other purposes or provision to third parties without consent. | Prohibition of use for other purposes or provision to third parties without consent. |

### 6. International Guidelines: OECD Privacy Guidelines

The **OECD Privacy Guidelines** (officially, "Recommendation Concerning Guidelines Governing the Protection of Privacy and Transborder Flows of Personal Data") were established in 1980. They serve as a fundamental basis for personal information laws globally.

#### Key Principles:

*   **Collection Limitation Principle:**
    *   Limits on personal data collection.
    *   Data must be obtained lawfully and fairly, ideally with data subject consent.
*   **Data Quality Principle:**
    *   Personal data must be relevant to its purpose.
    *   Data should be accurate, complete, and kept up-to-date for those purposes.

## Pages 193-197


This guide summarizes essential information from the provided text (Pages 193-197) to help you learn about personal information protection, focusing on key concepts, regulations, and practical measures.

---

## Personal Information Protection: Learning Guide

### 1. Key Concepts & Definitions

*   **Sensitive Information:** A broad category of personal data including ideas, beliefs, trade union/political party membership, political opinions, health information, genetic information, criminal history, etc.
*   **Unique Identification Information:** Data used to identify an individual, such as resident registration number, passport number, driver's license number, or alien registration number.
*   **Personal Information Impact Assessment (PIIA):** An evaluation system to analyze risks and find improvements when new personal information files are introduced or existing ones modified, especially if infringement concerns exist.
*   **Image Information Processing Device:** A device (e.g., CCTV) installed in a space to capture or transmit images of people or objects. Operators must establish and disclose a policy for its operation and management.

### 2. Personal Information Management Areas (Checklist Summary)

Public institutions (and generally all organizations) should ensure the following:

*   **Personal Information Impact Assessment (PIIA):**
    *   Conduct PIIAs when information is subject to assessment.
    *   Establish and implement a PIIA plan.
*   **Image Information Processing Device Protection:**
    *   Establish and disclose operational and management policies, reflecting all legal obligations.
    *   Record and manage use, provision, access, and destruction of personal image information in a ledger.
        *   **Required Register Items:** Classification (use, provision, reading, destruction), date/time, file name/type, person in charge, purpose/reason, third party for data use/provision/reading, grounds for use/provision, type of use/provision, period.
*   **Leakage and Exposure Prevention:**
    *   Operate systems to prevent leakage on webpages and personal information processing systems.
    *   Operate systems to prevent leakage on business computers and mobile devices.
*   **Infringement & Emergency Response:**
    *   Establish and disseminate procedures for responding to personal information infringement incidents.
    *   Establish and disseminate emergency response procedures.
*   **Personal Information Processing System Management:**
    *   Establish and implement policies for managing access rights.
    *   Perform checks and follow-up measures for access records.
*   **Unique Identification Information Restrictions:**
    *   Understand the processing status of unique identification information.
    *   Implement encryption for unique identification information.

### 3. Domestic Laws (Korea) for Personal Information Protection

| Feature             | Information Communications Network Utilization Act | Personal Information Protection Act (PIPA)                  |
| :------------------ | :------------------------------------------------ | :---------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Governing Law**   | Act on Promotion of Information and Communication Network Utilization and Information Protection, Etc. | Personal Information Protection Act                         |
| **Scope**           | When information communications service providers collect user personal information. | When any personal information controller collects personal information of a data subject. |
| **Subject**         | Information & communication service providers, broadcasting service providers, trustees. | Offline businesses/workers, non-profit organizations, all personal information controllers. |
| **Collection**      | - Notification of purpose & prior consent. <br> - Restrictions on collecting resident registration numbers. | - Notification of purpose & prior consent. <br> - Restrictions on collecting resident registration numbers. |
| **Use/Provision**   | - Prohibition of use for other purposes or provision to third parties without consent. | - Prohibition of use for other purposes or provision to third parties without consent. |

### 4. International Personal Information Protection Policies

#### A. OECD Privacy Guidelines

*   **Official Name:** Recommendation Concerning Guidelines Governing the Protection of Privacy and Transborder Flows of Personal Data.
*   **Purpose:** Established in 1980 as guidelines for cross-border transfer of personal data; now a global standard for developing personal information laws.
*   **Core Principles:**
    1.  **Collection Limitation:** Limits on data collection; data must be obtained lawfully, fairly, and with consent (where appropriate).
    2.  **Data Quality:** Personal data should be relevant, accurate, complete, and up-to-date for its intended use.
    3.  **Purpose Specification:** Purposes for data collection must be specified; subsequent use limited to those purposes.
    4.  **Use Limitation:** Data should not be disclosed or used for unspecified purposes without consent or legal authority.
    5.  **Security Safeguards:** Reasonable security measures must protect data against unauthorized access, destruction, modification, etc.
    6.  **Openness:** General policy of transparency regarding personal data; means to identify data controller readily available.
    7.  **Individual Participation:** Individuals have the right to confirm, erase, rectify, or amend their data.
    8.  **Accountability:** Data controller is accountable for complying with these principles.

#### B. EU General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR)

*   **What it is:** A unified rule by the European Parliament to strengthen the privacy of EU citizens.
*   **Timeline:** Promulgated in 2016, effective May 25, 2018.
*   **Scope & Compliance:**
    *   Applies to all companies processing personal information of EU citizens.
    *   Even companies without an EU establishment must comply if they offer goods/services to EU residents.
    *   Violations require notification to the supervisory authority within 72 hours.
*   **Main Contents:**
    *   Expands application to all companies processing personal information.
    *   Enhances data subjects' rights.
    *   Strengthens data controllers' responsibilities.
    *   Generally prohibits international transfer of personal information abroad.
    *   Requires privacy protection from the processing design stage ("privacy-by-design").
*   **Key Entities in GDPR:**
    *   **Data Subject:** The 'living natural person' who creates personal information and holds rights to it.
    *   **Controller:** Responsible for processing personal information; determines purpose and means of processing.
    *   **Processor:** An individual, corporation, or public institution entrusted by the Controller to process personal information according to the Controller's directions.
*   **Enhanced Data Subject Rights:**
    1.  **Right to be Informed:** Individuals must be informed about data collection and use.
    2.  **Right of Access:** Individuals can access their personal data.
    3.  **Right to Rectification:** Individuals can have inaccurate data corrected.
    4.  **Right to Erasure (Right to be Forgotten):** Individuals can request their data be deleted under certain conditions.
    5.  **Right to Restrict Processing:** Individuals can limit how their data is used.
    6.  **Right to Data Portability:** Individuals can obtain and reuse their personal data across different services.
    7.  **Right to Object:** Individuals can object to certain types of data processing.
    8.  **Rights in relation to Automated Decision Making and Profiling:** Individuals have rights regarding decisions made solely by automated means (e.g., marketing profiling based on hobbies/location) and must be notified and allowed to decide if their information is used.
*   **GDPR Penalty Calculation Criteria:**
    *   Factors considered include: nature, gravity, and duration of infringement; intentional/negligent character; mitigation actions; controller/processor responsibility; previous infringements; cooperation with authority; categories of data affected; notification; supervisory authority measures; adherence to codes; financial benefits gained/losses avoided.
    *   **Maximum Fines:** Up to 20 million EUR, or 4% of the total worldwide annual turnover of the preceding financial year (whichever is higher) for an undertaking.

#### C. US Consumer Privacy Bill of Rights

*   **Core Principles:**
    *   **Individual Control:** Right of the data subject to control their personal information.
    *   **Transparency:** Transparency in accessing information.
    *   **Respect for Context:** Right to know the context and reason for data collection, use, and disclosure.
    *   **Security:** Strengthened security for personal information.
    *   **Access and Accuracy:** Right to access personal information and ensure its accuracy.
    *   **Focused Collection:** Limits on personal information collected and held by businesses.
    *   **Accountability:** Data collecting agencies must comply with legislation and act accordingly.

### 5. Proactive Measures for Personal Information Controllers

*   **Technical/Administrative Protection:** Implement robust technical and administrative safeguards for personal information.
