## Pages 196-200


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Data Protection & Privacy

### 1. General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR)

The GDPR is the EU's data protection law, strengthening data subject rights.

#### 1.1 GDPR Structure (Key Chapters)
*   **Chapter 1:** General Provisions
*   **Chapter 2:** Principles
*   **Chapter 3:** Rights of the Data Subject
*   **Chapter 4:** Controller and Processor
*   **Chapter 5:** International Data Transfers
*   **Chapter 6:** Independent Supervisory Authorities
*   **Chapter 7:** Co-operation and Consistency
*   **Chapter 8:** Remedies, Liability and Sanctions
*   **Chapter 9:** Specific Data Processing Situations
*   **Chapter 10:** Delegated Acts and Implementing Acts
*   **Chapter 11:** Final Provisions

#### 1.2 Key Rights of Data Subjects under GDPR
The GDPR reinforces existing rights and introduces new ones:
*   **Right to be Informed:** Know when and why data is collected.
*   **Right of Access:** Obtain confirmation of processing and access personal data.
*   **Right to Rectification:** Correct inaccurate personal data.
*   **Right to Erasure (Right to be Forgotten):** Request deletion of personal data. (Renamed from previous draft)
*   **Right to Restrict Processing:** Limit how data is used.
*   **Right to Data Portability:** Receive personal data in a structured, commonly used, machine-readable format and transmit it to another controller. (Reinforced)
*   **Right to Object:** Object to processing of personal data.
*   **Rights in relation to Automated Decision Making and Profiling:**
    *   Right to be notified when personal information (e.g., occupation, hobbies, location) is automatically collected and used for marketing or automated decision-making.
    *   Right to decide whether their information will be used in such processes.

#### 1.3 GDPR Penalty Calculation Criteria
Administrative fines for GDPR infringements are based on:
*   Nature, gravity, and duration of infringement.
*   Intentional or negligent character.
*   Actions taken by the controller/processor to mitigate damage.
*   Degree of responsibility (considering technical/organizational measures).
*   Any relevant previous infringements.
*   Cooperation with the supervisory authority.
*   Categories of personal data affected.
*   Whether the infringement was notified.
*   Prior supervisory authority measures on the same subject.
*   Adherence to approved codes of conduct/certification.
*   Financial benefits gained or losses avoided from the infringement.

#### 1.4 GDPR Penalties
*   **Maximum Fine:** Up to 20 million Euros.
*   **For Undertakings:** Up to 4% of the total worldwide annual turnover of the preceding financial year.

### 2. US Consumer Privacy Bill of Rights

This framework outlines key principles for consumer data privacy:
*   **Individual Control:** Right to control personal information.
*   **Transparency:** Openness in information access.
*   **Respect for Context:** Right to know the context and reason for data collection, use, and disclosure.
*   **Security:** Strong security for personal information.
*   **Access and Accuracy:** Right to access and ensure accuracy of personal information.
*   **Focused Collection:** Right to control the personal information businesses collect and hold.
*   **Accountability:** Data collecting agencies must comply with legislation and act accordingly.

### 3. Personal Information Infringement: Response Methods

#### 3.1 Proactive Measures for Personal Information Controllers

**A) Technical/Administrative Protection of Personal Information**

*   **Administrative Protection:**
    *   Establish and implement an internal management plan for personal information processing.
    *   Control personal information access (make it harder to access than general data).
    *   Grant differential access rights to personal information.
    *   Promptly change or cancel access authority to personal information processing systems if the controller changes (record details, keep for ≥ 3 years).
*   **Technical Protection:**
    *   Implement access control and security measures for networks.
    *   Install and operate access control systems (intrusion prevention/detection/blocking).
    *   Apply encryption to personal information databases (DB).
    *   Store access records and prevent forgery/alteration.
    *   Install and operate security programs.

#### 3.2 Characteristics & Causes of Personal Information Infringement

| Sector     | Characteristics                                            | Causes                                                      | Occurrence                                                                  |
| :--------- | :--------------------------------------------------------- | :---------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Individual** | - Recognizes personal info as assets/goods.              | - Desire to use others' info.                               | - Theft of personal info (e.g., resident registration number).              |
|            | - Provision of info essential for cyber anonymity.       | - Increased public sharing (Web 2.0).                       | - Customer info hacking & voice transaction.                               |
|            |                                                            |                                                             | - Personal info leakage in P2P.                                             |
| **Business** | - Target marketing, CRM utilization.                     | - Negligence and carelessness.                              | - Exposure of personal info (e.g., resident registration number).           |
|            | - Securing personal info is key to competitiveness.      | - Conventionalized collection of resident registration number.| - Leakage from internal employees/branches.                                 |
|            | - Saturated communications market, overheated competition. | - Illegal collection and provision of personal information. |                                                                             |
| **Public** | - Exposure of personal info through service enhancement. | - Negligence and carelessness.                              | - Exposure of personal information.                                         |
|            | - Collection/use of personal info similar to private companies. | - Climate where unauthorized use of personal info is not an issue for service efficiency. | - Data spills by internal handlers. |

### 4. De-identification Process of Personal Data

**De-identification:** Processing personal information with alternative methods (e.g., pseudonymization, aggregation, deletion, categorization, data masking) to remove elements that can identify an individual, making it impossible to link data to a specific person. This is crucial for businesses wanting to process information for data analysis.

#### 4.1 De-identification Standards

*   **Identifiers:**
    *   As a rule, identifiers in datasets should be deleted.
    *   If absolutely needed for data use, they must be de-identified.
*   **Attribute Values:**
    *   Remove attribute values irrelevant to data use.
    *   Strict de-identification for unique attributes (e.g., rare diseases, unique professional experiences) as they carry a high risk of re-identification.

#### 4.2 De-identification Process Flow
1.  **Personal Information:** Start with identifiable data.
2.  **De-identification:** Apply de-identification methods.
3.  **Evaluation:** Assess if the de-identification is adequate.
4.  **Adequacy Check:**
    *   **Yes (Adequate):** Information is deemed non-privacy, elements removed.
    *   **No (Inadequate):** Re-identify, re-process, or block if identification of a particular individual (or easy combination with other info) is still possible.

#### 4.3 Examples of Personal Information Identifiers

**A) Attribute Values (General Characteristics)**
*   **Personal:** Gender, age, nationality, hometown, city/county, zip code, military service, marital status, religion, hobbies, clubs, smoking, drinking, vegetarianism, concerns.
*   **Physical:** Blood type, height, weight, waist circumference, blood pressure, eye color, medical examination results, disability type/level.
*   **Credit:** Tax payment, credit rating, donation, health insurance premiums, income quintile, medical aid beneficiaries.
*   **Educational/Career:** School name, department, grade, academic background, career, job type, company name, department, position, former workplace.
*   **Electronic:** Cookie information, access/visit date, service use record, internet access records, mobile phone usage records, GPS data.
*   **Family:** Spouse, children, parents, siblings, legal representative information.

**B) Unique Identifiers (Directly Identifying Information)**
*   **Unique Identification Info:** Resident registration number, passport number, alien registration number, driver's license number.
*   **Name:** Chinese/English name, pen name.
*   **Detailed Address:** Address up to the district (gu) unit.
*   **Date Information:** Birthday (solar/lunar), anniversary (marriage, first birthday, sixtieth birthday), certificate dates.
*   **Phone Number:** Mobile, home, company, fax numbers.
*   **Medical/Health Info:** Medical record number, health insurance number, welfare recipient number.
*   **Account/Card Number:** Account number, credit card number.
*   **Qualifications/Licenses:** Various qualification and license numbers.
*   **Vehicle/Device Numbers:** Vehicle number, registration number, serial number of various devices.
*   **Photos:** Still photos, videos, CCTV footage.
*   **Body Identification Info:** Fingerprint, voice, iris.
*   **Email/Network Address:** Email address, IP address, Mac address, homepage URL.
*   **Identification Code:** ID, employee number, customer number.
*   **Other Unique Numbers:** Military serial number, business registration number (sole proprietorship).

#### 4.4 Methods of De-identification
Various methods can be used individually or combined. The choice depends on data usage purpose and method strengths/weaknesses.

**Examples of De-identification Methods:**
*   **Pseudonymization:** Replacing direct identifiers with artificial identifiers.
    *   **Example:** "Hong Gil-dong, 35, Seoul, Korea University" -> "Lim Kkeokjeong, 30s, Seoul, International University".
    *   **Technologies:** Heuristic pseudonymization, encryption, hashing, wrapping.
*   **Aggregation:** Combining data to prevent individual identification.
    *   **Example:** Individual heights (180cm, 170cm, 160cm, 150cm) -> "Sum of height among physics major students: 660cm, average height: 165cm."
    *   **Technologies:** K-anonymity, L-diversity, T-closeness, micro-aggregation, rounding.
*   **Data Reduction (Suppression/Deletion):** Removing or reducing parts of the data.
    *   **Example:** Resident registration number "901206-71234567" -> "90's born, male."
    *   **Example:** Date information (e.g., date of final pass) processed annually instead of specific dates.
    *   **Technologies:** Rearrangement, identifier deletion (complete/partial), reducing records.

## Pages 199-203


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text (Pages 199-203).

---

## Learning Guide: Personal Information De-identification and Protection

This guide summarizes essential concepts, methods, and systems related to protecting personal information, focusing on de-identification and management systems.

---

### 1. De-identification of Personal Information

**Purpose:** To prevent the identification of an individual while still allowing the use of data for its intended purpose.

**1.1. De-identification Standards**

*   **Identifiers:**
    *   **Rule:** Delete identifiers from datasets.
    *   **Exception:** If absolutely essential, de-identify the identifier before use.
*   **Attribute Values:**
    *   **Rule:** Remove attribute values irrelevant to the data's purpose.
    *   **Strict De-identification:** Apply to unique values (e.g., rare disease, unique professional experiences) that could easily identify an individual.

**1.2. De-identification Process**

1.  **Personal Information:** Raw data containing identifiers.
2.  **De-identification:** Apply various methods to transform the data.
3.  **Evaluation:** Assess if the de-identification is adequate.
    *   **Adequate:** Data is anonymized (re-identification risk is low).
    *   **Inadequate:** Re-identification is possible; repeat de-identification or remove data.

**1.3. Examples of Personal Information Identifiers & Attributes**

These are examples of data that may need de-identification:

*   **Unique Identifiers:** Resident registration number, passport, driver's license, name, detailed address, specific dates (birthday, anniversary), phone numbers, medical/health insurance numbers, account/credit card numbers, vehicle numbers, photos, body identification (fingerprint, voice), email, IP/MAC address, URL, ID/employee/customer numbers, military serial number.
*   **Personal Characteristics:** Gender, age, nationality, hometown, marital status, religion, hobbies, smoking/drinking habits.
*   **Physical Characteristics:** Blood type, height, weight, medical exam results, disability type/level.
*   **Medical Information:** Disease name, injury/medication codes, treatment history.
*   **Credit Characteristics:** Tax payment, credit rating, donations, health insurance premiums, income quintile.
*   **Educational/Career Characteristics:** School, department, grade, career, job type, company, position, former workplace.
*   **Electronic Characteristics:** Cookie info, access/visit dates, service use records, internet/mobile usage, GPS data.
*   **Family Characteristics:** Spouse, children, parents, siblings, legal representative information.

**1.4. Methods of De-identification**

Methods can be used individually or in combination.

*   **Pseudonymization:** Replacing direct identifiers with artificial identifiers (pseudonyms).
    *   **Examples:** Heuristic pseudonymization (e.g., "Hong Gil-dong" -> "Lim Kkeokjeong"), Encryption, Swapping (exchanging values between records).
*   **Aggregation:** Summarizing data to remove individual details.
    *   **Examples:** Micro Aggregation (grouping similar records), Rounding (e.g., average height instead of individual heights).
*   **Data Reduction:** Removing or simplifying parts of the data.
    *   **Examples:** Rearrangement, Identifier deletion, Identifier partial deletion (e.g., "901206-7..." -> "90's born, male"), Reducing records, Complete deletion of identifiers.
*   **Data Suppression:** Hiding or omitting certain data points.
    *   **Examples:** Suppression (e.g., "35 years old" -> "30-40 years old"), Random rounding, Data ranging, Controlled rounding.
*   **Data Masking:** Obscuring data with random or fake values.
    *   **Examples:** Adding random noise, Blank and impute (e.g., "Hong Gil-dong" -> "Hong OO").

**1.5. De-identification Examples in Action**

| Original Data                                         | Data Deletion (Resident Reg. No.)                 | Data Masking (Reg. No., Hospitalization Date), Aggregation (Age) |
| :---------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------ | :--------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `770914-1234567` Male 2015/06/23 39 Flu                | Male 2015/06/23 39 Flu                            | `********-*******` Male 2015/*/** 35 Flu                       |
| `850930-1234567` Male 2015/10/01 31 Flu                | Male 2015/10/01 31 Flu                            | `********-*******` Male 2015/*/** 35 Flu                       |
| `710119-2345678` Female 2014/01/21 45 High blood pres. | Female 2014/01/21 45 High blood pres.             | `********-*******` Female 2014/*/** 35 High blood pres.         |
| ...                                                   | ...                                               | ...                                                              |
| *(Note: Age is averaged to 35 across records)*         | *(Note: Resident registration numbers are removed)* | *(Note: Dates are masked, and age is aggregated)*               |

---

### 2. Personal Information Protection Management System (ISMS-P)

**Purpose:** A certification system to establish and verify systematic and continuous protection of personal information.

**2.1. Obligated Entities for ISMS-P Certification**

*   **ISPs:** Internet Service Providers in Seoul and metropolitan cities.
*   **Integrated Information & Communication Facility Operators.**
*   **Companies with annual sales/revenue of 150 billion KRW or more AND meeting *any* of the following:**
    *   Superior General Hospitals.
    *   Higher Education Act schools with over 10,000 enrolled students.
    *   Information & Communication service sector sales of 10 billion KRW or more in the previous year.
    *   Over 1 million daily users of information & communication services in the 3 months prior to the previous year.
*   **Voluntary Applicants:** Companies not meeting criteria can still apply.

**2.2. ISMS-P Management System Structure**

The system objectively examines whether institutions systematically and continuously perform protection tasks, granting certification upon meeting standards.

**Key Requirements:**

1.  **Establishment and Operation of Management System (16 items)**
    *   1.1 Establishment of management system
    *   1.2 Risk management
    *   1.3 Operation of management system
    *   1.4 Inspection and improvement of management system
2.  **Requirements for Protection Measures (64 items)**
    *   2.1 Policy, organization, asset management
    *   2.2 Personal security
    *   2.3 External security
    *   2.4 Physical security
    *   2.5 Certification and authority management
    *   2.6 Access control
    *   2.7 Encryption application
    *   2.8 Information system introduction and development security
    *   2.9 System and service operation management
    *   2.10 System and service security management
    *   2.11 Accident prevention and response
    *   2.12 Disaster Recovery
3.  **Requirements for each stage of personal information processing (22 items)**
    *   3.1 Protection measures for collection of personal information
    *   3.2 Protection measures for possession and use of personal information
    *   3.3 Protection measures for provision of personal information
    *   3.4 Protection measures in case of destruction of personal information
    *   3.5 Protection of data subject rights

---

### 3. Follow-up Measures for Personal Information Controllers

**3.1. Response to Personal Information Leakage**

*   **Mandatory Obligation:** If personal information of more than 1,000 data subjects is leaked.
*   **Immediate Actions:**
    *   Notify affected data subjects.
    *   Confirm facts of the leakage.
    *   Block affected websites.
    *   Notify users to change passwords.
*   **Legal Implications:** Victims may file collective dispute mediation or lawsuits.

**3.2. Notification of Personal Information Leakage**

*   **Who to Report:** Ministry of Security and Public Administration, Korea Internet & Security Agency (KISA).
*   **When to Report:** Within 5 days (this includes notifying data subjects and reporting response measures).
*   **How to Report:** Email, fax, or website. For urgent or special circumstances, report by phone followed by a written report.
*   **What to Report:**
    *   Institution name
    *   Status of notification to data subjects
    *   Items and scale of leaked personal information
    *   Time and course of leakage
    *   Measures taken to minimize damage and results
    *   Methods for data subjects to minimize damage and remedy procedures
    *   Contact information of the department in charge

---

## IT Business and Ethics: Learning Guide

### I. Personal Information Protection

#### A. Obligated Persons for Information Protection
Certain entities are legally required to manage and protect personal information. You are an **obligated person** if you meet any of these criteria:

*   **Internet Service Providers (ISPs):** Those providing information and communication network services in Seoul and all metropolitan cities.
*   **Integrated Information and Communications Facility Operators (IOCs):** As per Article 46 of the Telecommunications Business Act.
*   **Large Organizations (Annual Sales ≥ 150 Billion Won) that are:**
    *   Superior General Hospitals.
    *   Schools with over 10,000 enrolled students (as of Dec 31 of previous year).
*   **Information and Communications Service Sector Companies:** With sales of 10 billion won or more in the previous year.
*   **High-Traffic Service Providers:** Those with more than 1 million daily users of information and communications services in the 3 months preceding the previous year.

**Voluntary Applicants:** Companies not meeting the criteria can voluntarily establish an information/personal information protection management system and apply for certification.

#### B. Personal Information Protection Management System (PIPMS)
The PIPMS objectively examines whether institutions and companies have a system to systematically and continuously perform personal information protection tasks, granting certification upon satisfaction of standards.

**PIPMS Structure (Key Components):**

1.  **Establishment & Operation of Management System:**
    *   1.1 Establishment of management system
    *   1.2 Risk management
    *   1.3 Operation of management system
    *   1.4 Inspection and improvement of management system
2.  **Requirements for Protection Measures (e.g., Security Aspects):**
    *   2.1 Policy, organization, asset management
    *   2.2 Personal security
    *   2.3 External security
    *   2.4 Physical security
    *   2.5 Certification and authority management
    *   2.6 Access control
    *   2.7 Encryption application
    *   2.8 Information system introduction and development security
    *   2.9 System and service operation management
    *   2.10 System and service security management
    *   2.11 Accident prevention and response
    *   2.12 Disaster Recovery
3.  **Requirements for Each Stage of Personal Information Processing:**
    *   3.1 Protection measures for collection of personal information
    *   3.2 Protection measures for possession and use of personal information
    *   3.3 Protection measures for provision of personal information
    *   3.4 Protection measures in case of destruction of personal information
    *   3.5 Protection of data subject rights

#### C. Handling Personal Information Leakage

**1. Immediate Response (Mandatory for >1,000 data subjects leaked):**
*   Notify affected data subjects immediately.
*   Initiate actions: confirm facts, block website, advise password changes.
*   Be prepared for dispute mediation or lawsuits from victims.

**2. Reporting Leakage to Authorities:**
*   **Who to report to:** Ministry of Security and Public Administration, Korea Internet & Security Agency (KISA).
*   **When to report:** Within 5 days (after notifying data subjects and completing initial response).
*   **How to report:** Via email, fax, or website. Phone reporting is allowed in special circumstances, followed by a report submission.
*   **What to report:** Institution name, notification status, leaked items & scale, time & course of leakage, damage minimization measures & results, victim self-protection methods, remedy procedures, contact info for the department in charge.

**3. Examples of Past Breaches (Domestic Companies):**
*   **Mar 2017:** Accommodation reservation hacking, 3.24M cases, 970k victims. Sanctions: 310M won penalty, 25M won fine.
*   **Aug 2016:** Personal info provided to third-party insurance companies, 180k cases, 29k victims. Sanctions: 180M won penalty, 20M won fine.
*   **May 2016:** Hacking, 25.4M cases, 20.51M victims. Sanctions: 4.48B won penalty, 25M won fine.
*   **Sep 2015:** Hacking, 1.95M cases, 1.95M victims. Sanctions: 102M won penalty, 15M won fine.
*   **May 2015:** Unauthorized use of prepaid phones for foreigners, 870k cases, 780k victims. Sanctions: 360M won penalty.

#### D. Why Personal Information Protection is Essential

*   **Ubiquity of Personal Data:** Used in nearly all public and private IT services.
*   **Corporate Asset:** Personal information is a valuable asset for companies across various sectors (finance, healthcare, education, etc.).
*   **Crime & Fraud Prevention:** Prevents illegal trafficking, impersonation, and other criminal abuse.
*   **Mitigate Corporate Losses:** Reduces financial and reputational damage from leakage incidents and class-action lawsuits.
*   **National & Social Safety:** Contributes to overall national and social security.
*   **Global Trend & Growth Engine:** Aligns with international privacy standards and drives national development.
*   **Industry Importance:** A critical issue impacting all industries.
*   **Cross-border Exchange:** Essential for safe international data exchange due to FTAs.
*   **Public Trust & National Brand:** Impacts public administration credibility and national image.

---

### II. Intellectual Property Rights (IPR)

#### A. Introduction to Intellectual Property Rights (IPR)
IPR encompasses all property rights arising from intellectual activities. It includes:
*   **Industrial Property Rights:** For industrial development (e.g., patents, trademarks).
*   **Copyrights:** For cultural development (e.g., literary, artistic works).

IPR are crucial corporate assets, with increasing transactions and new forms emerging due to technological advancements. Understanding them is vital in the IT business.

#### B. Key Concepts & Learning Objectives
*   **Keywords:** Intellectual property rights, copyrights, author's rights, industrial property rights, new intellectual property rights, business works, software copyrights, prevention of unfair competition, trade secret protection, patent rights.
*   **Learning Objectives:**
    1.  Explain copyrights and copyright infringement prevention.
    2.  Explain intellectual property rights and industrial property rights.

#### C. Trade Secret Protection

**1. Importance and Risks:**
*   Leakage of trade secrets allows competitors to easily replicate products, engage in dumping, leading to business crises and intensified competition.

**2. Definition of a Trade Secret:**
*   According to the "Act on the Prevention of Unfair Competition and Protection of Trade Secrets," a **trade secret** is information (e.g., production methods, sales methods, useful technical or business information for business activities) that:
    *   Is not publicly known.
    *   Is subject to reasonable efforts to maintain its secrecy.
    *   Has independent economic value.

**3. Causes of Leaks:**
*   Surveys show that the majority of trade secret leaks are caused by **internal staff**, often during **employee turnover**.

**4. Legal Penalties for Trade Secret Violation:**
*   **Criminal Penalties:**
    *   Up to 5 years imprisonment for domestic cases.
    *   Up to 10 years imprisonment for overseas cases.
    *   Fines are also imposed along with imprisonment.
*   **Attempted/Conspiracy:** Even attempting, intending, or conspiring to commit a crime related to trade secrets is punishable.

**5. The Human Factor in Protection:**
*   Even with reinforced security technologies, trade secrets are frequently leaked by people. Therefore, comprehensive measures addressing human factors are essential.
*   A key reason for inadequate protection systems is that executives and employees often lack exact knowledge of the "Unfair Competition Prevention and Trade Secret Protection Act."

## Pages 205-209


Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text, focusing on essential information and a study-friendly format.

---

## Intellectual Property Rights (IPR) Learning Guide

### 1. Introduction to Intellectual Property Rights (IPR)

**What are IPRs?**
*   Rights over creations of the mind.
*   Includes **Industrial Property Rights** (for industrial development) and **Copyrights** (for cultural development).
*   **Key Concept:** IPRs are important corporate assets, and their transactions are increasing rapidly.

**Why is it important in IT Business?**
*   Understanding IPR is crucial for anyone working in the IT field to protect valuable intellectual assets.

**Key Learning Points:**
*   Understand copyrights and how to prevent infringement.
*   Understand intellectual property rights and industrial property rights.

**Keywords to Know:**
*   **Intellectual property rights:** Legal rights over intellectual creations.
*   **Copyrights:** Rights for literary, artistic, and scientific works.
*   **Author's rights:** Rights belonging to the creator of a work (part of copyrights).
*   **Industrial property rights:** Rights for industrial inventions (patents, trademarks).
*   **New intellectual property rights:** IPRs emerging in new fields due to technological/social changes.
*   **Business works:** Works created in a business context.
*   **Software copyrights:** Copyrights specifically for computer programs.
*   **Prevention of unfair competition:** Laws to prevent dishonest business practices.
*   **Trade secret protection:** Legal measures to safeguard confidential business information.
*   **Patent rights:** Exclusive rights granted for an invention.

---

### 2. Trade Secret Protection

**Importance of Trade Secrets:**
*   Company trade secrets are valuable. Leaks can lead to competitors producing products easily, causing business crises and intensifying competition.

**Trade Secret Leakage Facts (2017 Survey):**
*   67.4% of leaks occurred during **employee turnover**.
*   81.4% were caused by **internal staff**.
*   **Key Takeaway:** Trade secret protection systems are often underutilized because employees lack knowledge of relevant laws.
*   Security technologies alone are insufficient; human factors must be addressed.

**Definition of "Trade Secret"** (as per "Act on the Prevention of Unfair Competition and Protection of Trade Secrets"):
Information (e.g., production methods, sales methods, technical/business info) that:
1.  Is **not publicly known**.
2.  Is subject to **reasonable efforts to maintain its secrecy**.
3.  Has **independent economic value**.

**Penalties for Trade Secret Violation:**
*   **Criminal Offense:** Subject to imprisonment and fines.
*   **Domestic Cases:** Up to 5 years imprisonment.
*   **Overseas Cases:** Up to 10 years imprisonment.
*   **Attempts/Conspiracy:** Even attempts or intentions to commit the crime are punishable.

---

### 3. Understanding Intellectual Property Rights (IPR)

**General Definition:**
*   Rights to intellectual property recognized or protected by laws/treaties.
*   Covers knowledge, information, technology, expressions of ideas, business representations, varieties of living organisms, and other intangible assets with realizable property value.

**Types of Intellectual Property Rights:**

1.  **Copyright:**
    *   Exclusive rights for academic research findings or literary/artistic creations.

2.  **Industrial Property Rights:**
    *   Rights for new industrial inventions, practical inventions, product forms, or trademarks.

3.  **New Intellectual Property Rights:**
    *   Rights for intellectual property emerging in new fields due to economic, social, cultural, or scientific/technological changes.

---

### 4. Understanding Copyright

**Definition of Copyright:**
*   An exclusive right granted by law to the **author** (creator) of a work.
*   Arises automatically upon creation of the work.
*   **Non-Formality Principle:** Automatically generated without formal requirements or registration procedures.

**Classification of Copyrights:**

1.  **Moral Rights:**
    *   **Nature:** Non-monetary, non-transferable rights.
    *   **Purpose:** Protect the author's honor and character.
    *   **Examples:**
        *   **Right of Attribution:** To be acknowledged as the author.
        *   **Right to Anonymity/Pseudonymity:** To publish a work anonymously or under a pseudonym.
        *   **Right to Integrity:** To prevent unauthorized alterations to the work.

2.  **Author's Economic Rights:**
    *   **Nature:** Monetary, transferable rights.
    *   **Purpose:** Relate to the financial aspects of using the work.
    *   **Examples:**
        *   Right of **Reproduction**
        *   Right of **Performance**
        *   Right of **Broadcasting**
        *   Right of **Transmission**
        *   Right of **Exhibition**
        *   Right of **Distribution**
        *   Right of **Rental**
        *   Right of **Production of Derivative Works**

3.  **Neighboring Rights:**
    *   **Nature:** Rights given to "neighbors" of authors (performers, record producers, broadcasters).
    *   **Purpose:** Secondary rights to create added value by using the original work. More restrictive than author's rights.
    *   **Examples of Holders and their Rights:**
        *   **Performers:** Rights related to performance, reproduction, distribution, etc.
        *   **Record Producers:** Rights related to reproduction, distribution, rental, transmission, etc.
        *   **Broadcasters:** Rights related to reproduction, performance, simultaneous broadcasting.

**Permissions & Licensing:**
*   Copyright holders can grant others permission to use their work within specified methods and conditions.
*   A licensed work **cannot be transferred** to another person without the copyright holder's consent.

**Presumption of Copyright Holder (When Author is Unknown):**
*   **If a name is indicated:** The person whose real name or well-known pseudonym is displayed on the work (or during public performance/transmission) is presumed to be the author.
*   **If no name is indicated:** The publisher, public performer, or person making the work public is presumed to hold the copyright.

**Key Copyright-Related Terms:**
*   **Public Performance:** Presenting works/performances to the public (acting, music, screening, etc.).
*   **Public Transmission:** Making works/performances available to the public by wire/wireless means for reception or access.
*   **Publication:** Reproducing and distributing works/phonograms to meet public demand.
*   **Making Works Public:** Opening works to the public via public performance, transmission, exhibit, or publication.

---

### 5. Types of Copyrightable Works

**Definition of a "Work":**
*   A creative production expressing human thoughts and emotions.
*   Requires **originality** (unique creation) and **externality** (tangible expression).

**Recognized Types of Works:**

*   **Literary Works:** Novels, poems, theses, lectures, speeches, plays, written works, oral works.
*   **Musical Works:** Compositions, lyrics, etc. (Note: The original text contained a redundant definition for this category).
*   **Theatrical Works:** Dramas, choreographies, pantomimes (body movements).
*   **Artistic Works:** Paintings, calligraphy, sculptures, printmaking, crafts, applied art (aesthetic expression in shapes/colors).
*   **Architectural Works:** Buildings, architectural models, design drawings.
*   **Photographic Works:** Creative expressions with original and aesthetic elements.
*   **Cinematographic Works:** Moving images (movies, dramas) reproducible by mechanical/electronic devices.
*   **Diagrammatic Works:** Maps, charts, design drawings, models (expressed by figures).
*   **Computer Program Works:** Series of instructions/commands for devices to process information and obtain results.
*   **Derivative Works:** Creative works produced by translating, arranging, altering, dramatizing, or cinematizing an original work. Protected as independent works.
*   **Compilation Works:** Creative compilations (selection/arrangement of materials), including databases (systematically organized data for search).

---

### 6. Works Made for Hire

**Definition:**
*   A work created by an **employee** of a legal person (e.g., company, organization) during the course of their duties and at the **initiative** of that legal person.

**Authorship:**
*   Unless otherwise specified in a contract or work regulation, the **legal person (employer)** is considered the author if the work is made public under their name.

**Requirements for a Legal Person to be the Author:**
1.  The work must be **initiated by the legal person**.
2.  It must be written by a **person engaged in business** for that legal person.
3.  It must be a work written **for business purposes**.
4.  It must be **publicized in the name of the legal person**.
5.  There must be **no contrary stipulations** in the contract or work rules.

---


---


## Pages 208-212


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

## **Understanding Copyright and Software Ethics**

### **1. Copyright and Related Rights**

Copyright protects original works of authorship. It has two main components:

*   **Moral Rights:**
    *   **Nature:** Personal, mental, non-monetary, non-transferable.
    *   **Purpose:** Protects the author's personal connection to their work.
    *   **Examples:** Right of attribution (being named), right to publish anonymously/pseudonymously, right to integrity of the work (preventing distortion).

*   **Economic Rights:**
    *   **Nature:** Property-based, monetary, transferable.
    *   **Purpose:** Allows the author to profit from their work.
    *   **Examples:** Right of reproduction, performance, broadcasting, exhibition, distribution, rental, and production of derivative works.

**Neighboring Rights:**
These rights are granted to those who "create added value" to a work, but are not the original author.
*   **Performers:** Rights like attribution, integrity, reproduction, distribution, performance, broadcasting.
*   **Record Producers:** Rights of reproduction, distribution, rental.
*   **Broadcasters:** Rights of reproduction, performance, simultaneous broadcasting.

### **2. Copyright Authorship Presumption**

If the actual creator of a work is hard to identify, copyright law provides presumptions:

*   **Author Presumed If:**
    *   Their **real name or well-known pseudonym** is indicated on the original/copies of the work in a usual manner.
    *   Their **real name or well-known pseudonym** is indicated during a public performance or transmission of the work.
*   **If no author name is indicated:** The **publisher, public performer, or person making the work public** is presumed to have the copyright.

### **3. Key Copyright Terms**

*   **Public Performance:** Presenting works (e.g., acting, singing, screening) to the public.
*   **Public Transmission:** Making works available to the public via wired or wireless means (e.g., internet).
*   **Publication:** Reproducing and distributing works to meet public demand.
*   **Making Works Public:** Opening works to the public through public performance, transmission, exhibition, or publication.

### **4. Types of Copyright-Protected Works**

A "work" is a creative production expressing human thoughts and emotions, possessing **originality** and **externality**.

*   **Literary Works:** Novels, poems, theses, lectures, speeches, plays, written & oral works (books, magazines).
*   **Musical Works:** Compositions (music, lyrics).
*   **Theatrical Works:** Dramas, choreographies, pantomimes (expressions through body movements).
*   **Artistic Works:** Paintings, sculptures, printmaking, crafts, applied art (aesthetic shapes/colors).
*   **Architectural Works:** Buildings, architectural models, design drawings.
*   **Photographic Works:** Creative expressions with original and aesthetic photographic elements.
*   **Cinematographic Works:** Movies, dramas (moving images reproducible by mechanical/electronic devices).
*   **Diagrammatic Works:** Maps, charts, design drawings, models (expressed by figures).
*   **Computer Program Works:** Series of instructions/commands applied to devices (like computers) to achieve specific results.
*   **Derivative Works:** New creative works produced by translating, arranging, altering, or adapting an original work (e.g., a movie based on a novel). Protected independently.
*   **Compilation Works:** Creative compilations of materials (e.g., selecting or arranging data), regardless of the material itself. Includes databases (systematically organized data searchable by information processing devices).

### **5. Works Made for Hire**

*   **Definition:** A work created by an employee for a legal entity (e.g., company, organization) during their duties and at the entity's initiative.
*   **Authorship:** The **legal entity** is considered the author, unless a contract or work regulations state otherwise.
*   **Requirements for Legal Entity to be Author:**
    1.  The work was **initiated by the legal entity**.
    2.  It was **written by an employee** engaged in the entity's business.
    3.  It was a work **written for the entity's business**.
    4.  It was **publicized in the name of the legal entity**.
    5.  There are **no contrary stipulations** in the contract or work rules.

### **6. Computer Program Works & Software Licensing**

*   **Software Definition:** A collection of instructions and commands that enable equipment (computers, communication devices) to process information, interact, and perform tasks. Includes related data and descriptions used to prepare them.
*   **Computer Program Work:** The program itself and its descriptive language.
*   **What is Protected by Copyright:**
    *   **Source code** and **object code** (compiled source code).
    *   **Program structure** and **arrangement method**.
*   **What is NOT Protected by Copyright:**
    *   Programming languages (e.g., C, Java).
    *   Protocols.
    *   Algorithms.
    *(These are considered ideas or tools, not the specific creative expression of a program).*
*   **Software Licensing:**
    *   The software author typically holds exclusive rights (use, copy, distribute, modify).
    *   A **license** is an agreement where the author grants specific permissions (rights) to others.
    *   License agreements define terms to prevent disputes, covering aspects like purpose, definitions, royalties, and contract duration.

### **7. Open Source Software (OSS) Copyright**

*   **Definition:** Software where anyone can freely use, copy, distribute, and modify its source code.
*   **Examples:** Apache web server, Firefox Web Browser, Linux Kernel.
*   **Common Open Source Licenses:**
    *   **BSD (Berkeley Software Distribution License):**
        *   Highly permissive.
        *   No obligation to disclose source code.
        *   No copyright notice or warranty liability required when distributing.
    *   **Apache License 2.0:**
        *   No obligation to disclose source code.
        *   If modified and distributed, must include the Apache License 2.0 and disclose its Apache Foundation origin.
    *   **GPL 2.0/3.0 (GNU General Public License):**
        *   Created by the Free Software Foundation (FSF).
        *   Most widely adopted.
        *   **Stricter obligations (copyleft):** Requires derivative works to be distributed under the same GPL license, meaning their source code must also be made available.
    *   **GNU LGPL 2.1 (Lesser GPL):**
        *   Designed for libraries.
        *   Less strict copyleft than GPL. Allows linking to simple libraries/modules without forcing the entire linked application to be LGPL. No obligation to provide source code for simply linking.
    *   **MPL (Mozilla Public License):**
        *   Separates copyright for source code and executable files.
        *   Executable files can sometimes be distributed under an exclusive license.
        *   **File-level copyleft:** Modifications to MPL-licensed files must remain MPL, but it allows linking with proprietary code.
*   **Basic Requirements for Most OSS Licenses:**
    1.  Indicate developer/contributor and copyright information on the product.
    2.  If the source code is modified, include information about the modification (who, when).
    3.  Attach a copy of the license when distributing the software.
*   **Copyleft:** A clause in some open source licenses that requires derivative works (or modified versions) to be distributed under the same license, including providing the source code.

### **8. Works Not Protected by Copyright Law**

The following types of works are generally *not* protected by copyright:

*   **Laws & Government Documents:**
    *   Constitutions, Acts, treaties, decrees, municipal ordinances and rules.
    *   Bulletins, public notifications, directives issued by central or local government.
    *   Compilations or translations of works produced by central or local government.
*   **Judicial & Administrative Decisions:**
    *   Judgments, decisions, orders, adjudications of courts.
    *   Rulings and decisions made through administrative appeals or similar procedures.
*   **Simple Facts:**
    *   Current news reporting that delivers simple facts (e.g., headlines, raw data).

---


---


## Pages 211-215


Here's a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide extracted from the provided text:

---

## Learning Guide: IT Business & Ethics

This guide covers essential concepts related to computer program works, copyright, open source software, and industrial property rights.

---

### 1. Computer Program Works & Copyright

#### 1.1 What is Software?
*   **Software** refers to collections of instructions and commands (including audio/visual info) that allow equipment (computers, communications apparatus, automation equipment) to perform tasks like command, control, input, process, save, output, and interact. It also includes descriptions used to prepare them and related data.

#### 1.2 What is a Computer Program Work?
*   A **computer program work** is a general term for a computer program and its descriptive language.
*   **Includes:** Programming languages (C, Java), protocols, algorithms, source code, object code, and program structure/arrangement.
*   **Copyright Protection:**
    *   **Protected:** Source code, object code, program structure, and arrangement.
    *   **NOT Protected:** Programming languages, protocols, and algorithms used for programming.
    *   **In essence:** The *product* of writing software is copyrighted, but the *tools and methods* for writing it are not.

#### 1.3 Software Licenses
*   **Copyright** grants the software author exclusive rights to use, copy, distribute, and modify their software.
*   A **license** is when the software author gives specific rights to others to perform certain actions with the software.
*   **License Agreements** detail contract purpose, definitions, license terms, duration, record keeping, and royalties to prevent disputes.

---

### 2. Open Source Software (OSS)

#### 2.1 What is Open Source Software?
*   **Open Source Software (OSS)** allows anyone to freely use, copy, distribute, and modify its source code.
*   **Examples:** Apache web server, Firefox Web Browser, Linux Kernel.

#### 2.2 Basic Requirements for Most OSS Licenses
*   Acknowledge the developer/contributor and copyright information on the product.
*   If source code is modified, include modification details (who, when).
*   When distributing software, attach a copy of the license.
*   **Copyleft:** Some licenses require redistribution under the *same* license, meaning the source code must also be distributed.

#### 2.3 Key Open Source Software Licenses

| License Type                  | Key Characteristics & Obligations                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| :---------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **BSD License**               | *   Very permissive. <br> *   No obligation to disclose source code. <br> *   No copyright notice or warranty liability required when distributing.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| **Apache License 2.0**        | *   Self-produced by Apache Software Foundation. <br> *   No obligation to disclose source code. <br> *   If modifying/distributing, must include Apache License 2.0 and state it's Apache Foundation software.                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| **GPL (GNU General Public License) 2.0/3.0** | *   Created by Free Software Foundation (FSF). <br> *   Most widely adopted open source license. <br> *   **Stricter obligations (strong copyleft):** Requires derivative works (works based on GPL code) to also be distributed under GPL, meaning their source code must be made available.                                                                                   |
| **GNU LGPL (Lesser GPL) 2.1** | *   Separate from GPL, for libraries. <br> *   Does **not** apply GPL's strict copyleft provisions (no obligation to provide source code for the entire linked application). <br> *   Allows linking to simple libraries and modules.                                                                                                                                                              |
| **MPL (Mozilla Public License)** | *   Developed for Netscape Browser. <br> *   Separates copyright for source code and executable files. <br> *   Allows distributing the executable file under an exclusive license, while source modifications may still need to be disclosed. (File unit copyleft – only modifications to MPL-licensed files need to be open source, not the entire linked project). |

---

### 3. Works Not Protected by Copyright Law

The following works are NOT protected by copyright:
*   Constitutions, Acts, treaties, decrees, municipal ordinances, and rules.
*   Bulletins, public notifications, directives, and similar documents issued by central or local governments.
*   Compilations or translations of works produced by central or local governments.
*   Judgments, decisions, orders, adjudications of courts, rulings, and decisions from administrative appeals.
*   Current news reporting that delivers simple facts.

---

### 4. Duration of Copyright Protection (Economic Rights)

Once the protection period expires, works can be used freely without author permission.
*   **Independent Works:** 70 years after the author's death.
*   **Joint Works:** 70 years after the death of the *last surviving* co-author.
*   **Anonymous/Pseudonymous Works:** 70 years after publication.
*   **Works Made for Hire:** 70 years after publication. If not published within 50 years of creation, then 70 years after creation.

**Note:** The duration starts from the *next year* following the event (death, publication, creation).

---

### 5. Copyright Registration

#### 5.1 What is Copyright Registration?
*   A process of officially recording facts and legal relations about a work (e.g., author's name) in a public ledger (Copyright Register) and disclosing them.

#### 5.2 What Can Be Registered?
*   Author's real name, pseudonym, nationality, domicile/residence.
*   Title, type, creation date of the work.
*   Publication status, country, and first publication date.
*   Title and author of the original work (for derivative works).
*   Information on publication medium.
*   Shares of registered rights holders (if multiple).

#### 5.3 How to Register (Documents Required)
Submit the following to the Korea Copyright Commission:
*   Copyright/Program registration application form.
*   Copyright/Program registration application statement.
*   Copies of the work (drawings, photos, electronic media). For programs, an electronic medium with a copy of the program (partial excerpt allowed if sufficient proof of creation).
*   Documents proving the reason for registration (if required).
*   List of authors/rights holders (if multiple).
*   List of works (if registering many).

*The Korea Copyright Commission issues a copyright registration certificate.*

---

### 6. Industrial Property Rights (IPRs)

#### 6.1 Concept of Industrial Property Rights
*   **Definition:** Rights protecting inventions with commercial value.
*   **Purpose:** Grant creators exclusive rights for a period to encourage technological progress and industrial development. After the period, anyone can use it.
*   **Key Types:** Patent rights, utility model rights, design rights, trademark rights.

#### 6.2 Types of Industrial Property Rights

| Classification | Content                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Duration                                        |
| :------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :---------------------------------------------- |
| **Patents**    | *   Right to an advanced invention (e.g., manufacturing methods). <br> *   Cannot be publicly known, performed, or published before filing.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | 20 years from application date                  |
| **Trademarks** | *   Right to a mark identifying one's products/services from others. <br> *   **Mark:** Symbols, letters, figures, sounds, smells, holograms, movements, colors (trade names too). <br> *   **Service Mark:** Trademark for services (academies, restaurants); website domains can be registered. <br> *   Service marks (trademarks) take precedence over registered website domains. | Virtually permanent, renewable every 10 years   |
| **Designs**    | *   Right to an aesthetically appealing design of an article's form, shape, color, font, or their compositions.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | 20 years from registration date                 |
| **Utility Models** | *   Protects practical designs of a lower technical level than patents. <br> *   Focuses on enhancing practicality by improving shape and structure of existing products.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | 10 years from application date                  |

#### 6.3 Acquisition of Industrial Property Rights
*   **Acquisition:** By registering with the Korean Intellectual Property Office.
*   **First-to-File Rule:** The first to file an application receives the right.
*   **Territorial Protection:** Rights are recognized only in the country where registered; separate applications needed for each country.

#### 6.4 Violation of Industrial Property Rights

*   **Cases of Violation (Examples of False Display):**
    *   Displaying a non-existent, non-applied, or inappropriate patent/registration number (e.g., marking a utility model as a patent).
    *   Marking a product as "patent pending" or "registered trademark" when it's not.
    *   Using false trademarks in advertisements or packaging.
    *   Theft of renowned domestic or foreign trademarks.
*   **Punishment:**
    *   Imprisonment for up to 3 years or a fine of up to 20 million won for falsely displaying intellectual property rights.
    *   This is an **offense not subject to complaint**, meaning anyone (even a third party not directly harmed) can file criminal charges with the prosecution or police.

---


---

Here is a simplified, easy-to-read learning guide based on the provided text:

---

# Intellectual Property Rights & Business Ethics: A Learning Guide

## 1. Copyright Registration Essentials

To register a copyright (or program copyright for software), you generally need:
*   **Application Statement:** Official form for copyright registration.
*   **Copies of the Work:**
    *   For general works: Drawings, photos, or electronic media.
    *   For computer programs: An electronic copy of the program.
    *   *Note:* A partial excerpt of program content may be submitted if it proves creation. This excerpt should be in program language before computer conversion.
*   **Proof of Registration Reason:** (Only if required)
*   **List of Stakeholders:** If there are multiple authors, heirs, rights holders, etc., provide a list.
*   **List of Works:** For large-quantity registrations (multiple works, neighboring works, databases).

**Outcome:** The Korea Copyright Commission issues a **Copyright Registration Certificate** upon successful application.

---

## 2. Industrial Property Rights (IPR)

**Definition:** IPRs protect inventions and creations with commercial value. They are a subset of Intellectual Property Rights.

**Types of Industrial Property Rights:**
